# 正常帝国

**作者**: Robert Chapman

---

Empire of Normality



1



Rise of the machines

机器的崛起



The most important parts of our story take place since the early nineteenth century, but it is helpful to begin with a more sweeping account that provides some broader context. Most significantly, this regards how the shift from feudalism to capitalism brought a fundamental change in how health was conceptualised.

我们故事中最重要的部分始于十九世纪初，但为了提供更广泛的背景，从更宏观的叙述开始会更有帮助。最重要的是，这涉及到从封建主义到资本主义的转变如何带来了健康概念的根本性变化。



The chapter begins by briefly looking at how health was understood as a form of harmony in Ancient Greece and elsewhere in the ancient world. This persisted until at least the seventeenth century. We then turn to the French philosopher René Descartes, whose work I take as symbolic of a broader shift in Enlightenment thinking about the body and health. For Descartes, the body was reconceptualised as a machine. In this view, health was no longer a matter of harmony, but rather a mechanistic matter of working properly. Finally, I turn to the rise of capitalism and the Industrial Revolution. I show that, far from being an inevitable scientific development, the reimagining of the body as a machine became so broadly embraced because it helped naturalise new hierarchies that emerged from capitalism itself. This overview, illustrating how capitalism brought with it a new conception and correlating science of health, will help set the stage for the following chapters on the rise of the pathology paradigm.

本章首先简要探讨了古希腊及古代世界其他地区如何将健康理解为一种和谐状态。这种观念至少延续至十七世纪。随后我们将转向法国哲学家勒内·笛卡尔，其著作在我看来象征着启蒙运动对身体与健康认知的更广泛转变。笛卡尔将身体重新构想为一台机器。在此视角下，健康不再是和谐的问题，而是机器正常运转的机械论问题。最后，我将探讨资本主义兴起与工业革命。我将论证，将身体重塑为机器的观念之所以被广泛接受，并非不可避免的科学进展，而是因为它有助于将资本主义自身催生的新等级制度自然化。这一概述揭示了资本主义如何带来新的健康观念及相应的科学体系，将为后续关于病理学范式兴起的章节奠定基础。



HEALTH AS HARMONY

作为和谐的健康



The time of the Hippocratics was the classical world of the Greek city-states where famous battles were fought, the great poets composed their epics, and Socrates argued with his fellow citizens in the marketplace of Athens. Because medicine was so basic, chronic illness and disability were widely incorporated into daily life, and there was nothing like the systemic disability segregation that came later. Archaeological evidence shows that temples, for instance, had ramps to aid access for those with impaired mobility.1 Nonetheless, there was still discrimination against disabled people. Most notably, in this context, it was widely held that illness was a punishment – or, sometimes, gift – from the gods. This ‘moral model’ of disability dates at least back to Ancient Egypt, where healing was administered by sorcerer-medics who would banish evil spirits alongside providing basic medical intervention.

希波克拉底时代是希腊城邦的古典世界，那里曾爆发著名战役，伟大诗人创作史诗，苏格拉底在雅典集市上与同胞辩论。由于医学基础薄弱，慢性疾病与残障普遍融入日常生活，不存在后来出现的系统性残障隔离。考古证据表明，例如神庙设有坡道以协助行动不便者通行。 1 尽管如此，残障人士仍遭受歧视。最显著的是，当时普遍认为疾病是神明的惩罚——有时亦是馈赠。这种残障的"道德模型"至少可追溯至古埃及，那里由巫师医师进行治疗，他们在提供基础医疗干预的同时驱逐邪灵。



Hippocrates himself was born around 460 BC on the Island of Kos, off the coast of Turkey. He was first taught by his father, a medic called Heraclides. After learning all Heraclides had to teach, Hippocrates travelled widely to learn more about medicine. While little is known for certain about his travels or later life, we do know from his contemporary Plato that Hippocrates returned to Kos and became famous for his medical work and teachings even in his own time.2

希波克拉底本人约公元前 460 年出生于土耳其沿海的科斯岛。他最初师从身为医师的父亲赫拉克利德斯。在学尽赫拉克利德斯所授知识后，希波克拉底游历四方以精研医术。虽然其游历经历与晚年生活已难考证，但我们从其同时代的柏拉图处确知：希波克拉底最终返回科斯岛，并以其医学成就与教学实践名扬当世。 2



We also know that a great many texts, known together as the Hippocratic Corpus, still survive. These were written either by Hippocrates or his followers. And from these the legacy of the Hippocratic tradition becomes clear. For while illness had traditionally been viewed through a religious lens, the Hippocratics came to understand illness naturalistically, as problems of the body or mind. They also pioneered methods of observation and record-keeping, and they came to develop complex diagnostic systems for interpreting and treating illness.

我们还知道大量被统称为《希波克拉底文集》的文献至今犹存。这些著作或出自希波克拉底本人，或由其追随者编纂。正是通过这些文献，希波克拉底学派的传承脉络得以明晰。当疾病传统上仍被置于宗教视角下审视时，希波克拉底学派已开始以自然主义视角理解疾病，将其视为身心失调的问题。他们开创了观察记录之法，并逐步建立起阐释与治疗疾病的复杂诊断体系。



In time those working in this tradition were able to treat infected wounds, build an understanding of the importance of nutrition, and to develop important surgical tools and interventions. They also saw the brain, in the words of one Hippocratic text, as ‘the seat of madness and delirium, of the fears and frights which assail us’.3 When it came to neurological disorder, they distinguished between mania, melancholy, insanity, and epilepsy, in ways not too different to the distinctions found in the works of early psychiatrists over two millennia later.4 It is thus here that we first see the recognition of specific neurological conditions as opposed to the idea that madness was inflicted by mischievous or wrathful gods.

随着时间的推移，遵循这一传统的医者逐渐能够处理感染伤口，认识到营养的重要性，并开发出重要的外科工具与治疗方法。他们还认识到，正如一部希波克拉底文献所言，大脑是“疯狂与谵妄、恐惧与惊骇侵袭我们的所在”。 3 在神经障碍方面，他们区分了躁狂、忧郁、精神错乱和癫痫，其分类方式与两千多年后早期精神病学著作中的区分并无太大差异。 4 因此，正是在这里，我们首次看到对特定神经病症的承认，而非将疯狂归咎于恶作剧或愤怒的神明。



Yet this is where the similarities with contemporary medicine end. The most important difference is that their understanding of health was wholly unlike those developed later. For today, disability and disorder are understood in relation to concepts of statistical or medical normality. Yet in fact, there was no such conception in the ancient world. While the Pythagoreans had developed the concept of the arithmetic ‘mean’ shortly prior to the birth of Hippocrates, this concept was highly abstract. As Simon Raper has written, the ‘Pythagoreans mention the arithmetic mean in the context of music and proportion, along with the geometric and harmonic means, but there is no suggestion of using it for summarising data’.5 Thus, the idea of ‘normal’ functioning – or more concretely, of the normal heart rate, normal lung capacity, normal height, normal cognitive ability, and so forth – would have been wholly alien to the medics of antiquity.

然而，这正是与当代医学相似之处的终点。最重要的区别在于，他们对健康的理解与后来发展出的观念截然不同。如今，残障与失调是相对于统计或医学上的“正常”概念来理解的。但事实上，在古代世界并不存在这样的观念。尽管在希波克拉底诞生前不久，毕达哥拉斯学派已经提出了算术“平均数”的概念，但这一概念极为抽象。正如西蒙·拉珀所写：“毕达哥拉斯学派在音乐和比例（连同几何平均数与调和平均数）的语境中提到了算术平均数，但并未提及将其用于总结数据。” 5 因此，“正常”功能的概念——更具体地说，正常心率、正常肺活量、正常身高、正常认知能力等等——对古代医学家而言是完全陌生的。



Instead, illness was defined as a disruption of bodily harmony, balance, or equilibrium. For the Hippocratics, the balance of health was primarily between what they saw as the four primary properties or ‘humours’ of blood, phlegm, yellow bile, and black bile. On this view, as the historian Andrew Scull summarises, ‘each of us is composed of four basic elements which contend for superiority’ in ways that can lead to them being more or less balanced.6 If these were in balance then the body was healthy, and different illnesses were produced by different forms of imbalance.

相反，疾病被定义为身体和谐、平衡或均衡的失调。在希波克拉底学派看来，健康的平衡主要体现在他们所谓的四种基本属性或“体液”——血液、黏液、黄胆汁和黑胆汁——之间。正如历史学家安德鲁·斯卡尔所总结的，按照这种观点，“我们每个人都是由四种基本元素构成的，它们以某种方式争夺主导地位”，这可能导致它们或多或少地保持平衡。 6 如果这些体液处于平衡状态，那么身体就是健康的；而不同的疾病则是由不同形式的失衡所导致的。



Equally, the health as harmony could be between individual and environment. For instance, the dominance of different humours was associated with different seasons, which tended to bring different illnesses. Similarly, the Hippocratics also suggested neurological functioning could be affected by things such as changes in the weather. For instance, as one Hippocratic text posits, a ‘southerly wind’ could ‘relax the brain’ and its blood vessels, while a northerly wind would ‘solidify’ parts of the brain, with each of these bringing different cognitive effects.7 If someone was ill, this was taken as a sign that there was a lack of harmony in humours or between individual and environment, and different forms of imbalance were taken to explain different medical problems.

同样，健康作为和谐也可以体现在个体与环境之间。例如，不同体液的盛行与不同季节相关，这些季节往往带来不同的疾病。类似地，希波克拉底学派也提出，神经功能可能受到天气变化等因素的影响。例如，一份希波克拉底文献假设，“南风”可能“松弛大脑”及其血管，而北风则会“固化”大脑的某些部分，每种风都会带来不同的认知影响。 7 如果有人生病，这被视为体液或个体与环境之间缺乏和谐的标志，而不同形式的不平衡则被用来解释不同的医学问题。



While our focus here will be on Western conceptions of health, it is remarkable to consider that equilibrium conceptions of bodily and mental health can also be seen in a range of traditional medical philosophies globally. These include the Ayurvedic tradition in India, Ancient Chinese medicine, Ancient Egyptian medicine, and Incan oral medical traditions.8 To be sure, each of these did differ in an array of complexities and nuances, and none used the Hippocratic concept of ‘humours’. Yet they and many other approaches did see health as, in one sense or another, a matter of harmony or equilibrium. This was either within the individual, or between individual and either the environment or their community. For instance, as Alexus McLeod summarises, those in the ancient Confucian tradition in China believed that if ‘we are in bad, vicious or unhealthy communities, our beliefs, emotions, expectations and attitudes (among other things) will be disordered in critical ways’.9

虽然我们在此主要关注西方对健康的理解，但值得注意的是，关于身心健康的平衡观念在全球多种传统医学哲学中同样可见。这些传统包括印度的阿育吠陀体系、中国古代医学、古埃及医学以及印加的口传医学传统。 8 诚然，这些传统在诸多复杂性和细微差别上各有不同，且无一采用希波克拉底的"体液"概念。然而，它们以及许多其他医学体系确实在某种意义上将健康视为一种和谐或平衡状态。这种平衡要么存在于个体内部，要么存在于个体与环境或社群之间。例如，正如亚历克修斯·麦克劳德所总结的，中国古代儒家传统认为，如果"我们身处恶劣、堕落或不健康的社会环境中，我们的信念、情感、期望和态度（以及其他方面）将在关键层面上陷入混乱"。 9



And so it was that across the ancient world, to be ill was not to have a mechanical abnormality, but to be out of balance with aspects of self, others, or environment. And far from being confined to antiquity, these traditions continued until quite recently. The humoral tradition, for instance, continued to be developed in Ancient Rome through the work of Galen, during the Islamic Golden Age by Ibn Sina, and then throughout medieval Europe. Likewise, other ancient equilibrium traditions globally continued until the modern age. Across the world the underlying equation between health and harmony, illness and imbalance, was to remain dominant until colonialism, the Enlightenment and, most of all, the rise of capitalism.

因此，在古代世界，生病并非意味着机体异常，而是指个体与自我、他人或环境某些方面失去平衡。这些传统远非仅限于古代，而是延续至相当晚近的时期。例如，体液学说传统在古罗马通过盖伦的著作得以发展，在伊斯兰黄金时代由伊本·西那继承，随后贯穿整个中世纪欧洲。同样，全球其他古老的平衡传统也一直延续到现代。在世界各地，健康与和谐、疾病与失衡之间的根本对应关系，直到殖民主义、启蒙运动，尤其是资本主义兴起之前，始终占据主导地位。



THE BODY AS MACHINE

作为机器的身体



In part the shift to a new way of understanding health concerned the new concept of ‘normality’, which I will return to in the following chapter. But it also concerned the new mechanistic understanding of the body. While there were certainly hints of this earlier, the machine metaphor was most fully and memorably proposed in the seventeenth century by the French philosopher René Descartes. Born in France in 1596 and later travelling and studying throughout Europe, Descartes developed his insights just as the Enlightenment was dawning. Over this period, a renewed focus on reason and observation, and the breaking of traditional dogmas, would bring huge advances in European philosophy, science, and technology.

部分转向理解健康的新方式涉及“正常性”这一新概念，我将在下一章中再作探讨。但这也与对身体的新机械论理解有关。虽然早期已有此迹象，但机器隐喻在 17 世纪由法国哲学家勒内·笛卡尔最全面且令人难忘地提出。笛卡尔于 1596 年出生于法国，后游历欧洲各地求学，正值启蒙运动曙光初现之际，他发展了自己的见解。在这一时期，对理性和观察的重新关注以及对传统教条的打破，将为欧洲哲学、科学和技术带来巨大进步。



While his interest in medicine arose earlier and was built on the work of his contemporaries, Descartes’ own pathbreaking work followed the death of his 5-year-old daughter Francine. Tragically, Francine had succumbed to scarlet fever in 1640, leaving Descartes deeply stricken. This seems to have led him to turn towards more universal themes such as the nature of the soul alongside the workings of the body. It is quite feasible that Francine’s tragic death influenced the suggestion he is best known for today. This was of a sharp dualism between the body and mind, whereby the mind could survive the decline of the mechanistic body, or even death itself.

尽管笛卡尔对医学的兴趣萌生得更早，并建立在同时代人的研究基础上，但他本人的开创性工作是在他五岁的女儿弗朗辛去世后才开始的。1640 年，弗朗辛不幸死于猩红热，这使笛卡尔深受打击。这似乎促使他开始转向更普遍的课题，比如灵魂的本质以及身体的运作方式。弗朗辛的悲剧性死亡很可能影响了他今天最为人所知的观点——即身心之间存在鲜明的二元对立，心灵可以超越机械身体的衰退，甚至超越死亡本身而存在。



It was in his 1641 book Meditations, written in the Netherlands shortly after Francine’s death, that Descartes outlined his understanding of the body. In particular, he suggested a number of memorable analogies between body and machine. For instance, he likened the healthy or sick body to a well-made or broken clock. He also made analogies between specific body-parts and specific machines or devices, likening the eyes, for instance, to telescopes. In this way, he wrote, we can ultimately consider ‘the body of a human being as a kind of machine made up of bones, nerves, muscles, veins, blood, and skin’.10 While his conception of the mind was more abstract and compatible with there being an immortal soul, his conception of body was wholly confined to what could be seen and studied objectively.

笛卡尔在其 1641 年出版的《沉思录》中阐述了他对身体的理解，这本书是在弗朗辛去世后不久于荷兰写成的。他特别提出了一些令人难忘的身体与机器之间的类比。例如，他将健康或生病的身体比作制作精良或损坏的钟表。他还将特定的身体部位与特定的机器或设备进行类比，比如将眼睛比作望远镜。他写道，通过这种方式，我们最终可以将“人的身体视为一种由骨骼、神经、肌肉、静脉、血液和皮肤组成的机器”。 10 尽管他对心灵的概念更为抽象，且与存在不朽灵魂的观点相容，但他对身体的概念完全局限于可以客观观察和研究的事物。



In suggesting this, Descartes was rejecting the traditional vision of the body as a dynamic organism, made up of competing humours, and always positioned in relation to different environments. Instead, for him, it was now a complex machine made up of smaller mechanistic parts that worked together to maintain health. As such, either specific parts of the body, or one’s overall bodily functioning, could be working or broken, and in turn fixed, by anyone with sufficient knowledge and resources – much like the clocks or other machines made or repaired by the great tradesmen of Descartes’ time.

笛卡尔提出这一观点时，否定了传统上将身体视为动态有机体的观念——那种认为身体由相互竞争的体液构成、始终处于不同环境关系中的看法。相反，在他看来，身体如今成了一台由更小的机械部件组成的复杂机器，这些部件协同运作以维持健康。因此，身体的特定部位或整体机能都可能运转正常或出现故障，进而也能被任何拥有足够知识和资源的人修复——就像笛卡尔时代伟大工匠制造或修理的钟表或其他机器一样。



What was so radical about this reimagining was that, in contrast to his own experience with Francine, it allowed the hope that there might come a day when any human body would be able to be fixed. And in retrospect we can see that Descartes’ hope was not unfounded. Today, scarlet fever is easily treatable with antibiotics, as are many other diseases that would have been fatal in Descartes’ time. The rise of a mechanistic medicine surely has thus saved countless others from suffering the kind of grief that Descartes held.

这种重新构想之所以如此激进，是因为与笛卡尔亲身经历弗朗辛之死的体验形成鲜明对比，它带来了希望：或许有一天，任何人的身体都能被修复。回顾过去，我们可以看到笛卡尔的希望并非空想。如今，猩红热可以通过抗生素轻松治愈，许多在笛卡尔时代致命的疾病也是如此。机械论医学的兴起无疑使无数人免于遭受笛卡尔所经历的那种悲痛。



Yet initially Descartes’s comparisons, due to prevailing religious sensibilities, were considered utterly outrageous. At the time he was writing, most doctors were still working in the humoral tradition. But by then medical thought and practice had become deeply intertwined with the dominant Christian belief system. In practice, doctors routinely relied on astrological analysis of star signs for interpretations of specific illnesses or choosing treatments. These same doctors saw new scientific approaches to medicine as a threat to not just their medical authority but also their religious worldview. Indeed, in 1643, two years after publishing his Meditations, Descartes himself was forced to flee as his philosophy was condemned as heretical.

然而最初，由于当时盛行的宗教情感，笛卡尔的类比被视为极其荒谬。在他写作的那个时代，大多数医生仍在体液学说的传统下工作。但那时，医学思想与实践已深深交织于主导的基督教信仰体系之中。实践中，医生们常依赖对星座的占星分析来解读特定疾病或选择治疗方案。这些医生将新的医学科学方法视为不仅威胁其医学权威，也威胁其宗教世界观。事实上，1643 年，即笛卡尔发表《沉思录》两年后，他本人因其哲学被谴责为异端而被迫逃亡。



Descartes did not live to see society embrace a mechanistic understanding of the body. He died in 1650, seemingly after being poisoned with arsenic by a Catholic priest in Sweden.11 Unsurprisingly, Descartes’ views remained relatively marginalised through the following century. But by the turn of the nineteenth century, it was increasingly hard to deny that the humoral approach was not just outdated, but often used to justify bizarre and unhelpful treatments. In the early eighteenth century, for instance, there had been a revival in the ancient practice of leeching, where leeches were used to suck blood from the bodies of patients to restore their humoral balance. Indeed, even as late as the early 1850s, Manchester Royal Infirmary used around 50,000 leeches a year, regardless of the lack of benefit this brought patients.12

笛卡尔未能活着见证社会接受对身体机制的理解。他于 1650 年去世，据称是在瑞典被一名天主教神父用砷毒死的。 11 不出所料，笛卡尔的观点在接下来的一个世纪里仍然相对边缘化。但到了十九世纪之交，体液疗法不仅过时，还常常被用来为怪异且无益的治疗方法辩护，这一点越来越难以否认。例如，在十八世纪初，古代的水蛭疗法曾一度复兴，即用水蛭从患者体内吸血以恢复其体液平衡。事实上，直到 1850 年代早期，曼彻斯特皇家医院每年仍使用约 5 万条水蛭，尽管这对患者并无益处。 12



By contrast, the more mechanistic understanding of the body would, as it became increasingly dominant in the latter half of the nineteenth century, come to pave the way for modern medicine to emerge. It would be here that our contemporary understanding not just of bodily anatomy and functioning, but also of germs, bacteria, viruses, and much else would begin to be developed. The Cartesian approach to the body thus helped bring a revolution in the science of medicine.

相比之下，对身体更为机械化的理解，在十九世纪后半叶逐渐占据主导地位，为现代医学的诞生铺平了道路。正是在这里，我们当代对身体解剖和功能的理解，以及对细菌、病毒等诸多事物的认识开始发展起来。因此，笛卡尔式的身体观帮助引发了医学科学的革命。



And yet despite significantly improving our understanding, the shift to the individual machine metaphor was not an inevitable and inescapable product of scientific progress. Like other metaphors used in science, it was equally a product of the historical, ideological, and technological context in which it took hold. To understand this, we need to turn to broader material and social factors that had already begun when Francine died – most importantly, the rise of the capitalist economic system.

然而，尽管这一转变极大地增进了我们的理解，但转向个体机器隐喻并非科学进步不可避免、无法回避的产物。如同科学中使用的其他隐喻一样，它同样是在其所处的历史、意识形态和技术背景下产生的产物。要理解这一点，我们需要转向更广泛的物质和社会因素——这些因素在弗朗辛去世时已经开始发挥作用，其中最重要的是资本主义经济体系的兴起。



THE TRIUMPH OF CAPITALISM

资本主义的胜利



Such a wholesale embrace of the initially outrageous machine metaphor in the nineteenth century was made possible by the shift from feudal society, through merchant capitalism, to industrial capitalism. For by the time Descartes and his contemporaries were busy theorising about the body and mind, things had already changed much. Both international domination and commerce had already been rapidly developing in ways that were growing into a new world system. This would go on to develop in ways that would allow Descartes’ initially outrageous proposal to become universally accepted across the capitalist world.

十九世纪对最初令人震惊的机器隐喻的全盘接纳，得益于从封建社会经商业资本主义向工业资本主义的转变。因为当笛卡尔及其同时代人忙于对身体和心灵进行理论化时，世界已经发生了巨大变化。国际统治和商业都已迅速发展，逐渐形成一个新的世界体系。这一体系的发展最终使得笛卡尔最初惊世骇俗的提议在整个资本主义世界被普遍接受。



To clarify this, let us start with feudalism, the economic system that flourished from roughly the ninth to fifteenth centuries. In Europe, this had developed out of the breakdown of the Roman Empire, whose growth had relied heavily on slavery. But by the fourth century, due to successive slave revolts, landlords were forced to begin giving former slaves their own land to live on with their families. At the same time, free agricultural workers increasingly needed to turn to local lords for protection, but in doing so were required to swear fealty. While slavery did still exist, in many cases both former slaves and former free workers increasingly became peasants, or serfs. They would typically be able to live and work on their own land, and have access to ‘common’ forests, meadows, and lakes, while also having duties towards the lord in exchange for protection.

为了澄清这一点，让我们从封建主义开始，这个经济体系大约在 9 世纪到 15 世纪之间繁荣发展。在欧洲，封建主义是在罗马帝国崩溃的基础上发展起来的，而罗马帝国的扩张在很大程度上依赖于奴隶制。但到了 4 世纪，由于接连不断的奴隶起义，地主们被迫开始将土地分给前奴隶，让他们和家人一起生活。与此同时，自由的农业工人越来越需要寻求当地领主的保护，但这样做需要宣誓效忠。虽然奴隶制仍然存在，但在许多情况下，前奴隶和前自由工人逐渐变成了农民，或者说农奴。他们通常可以在自己的土地上生活和工作，并有权使用“公共”的森林、草地和湖泊，同时也要对领主承担义务，以换取保护。



Beyond Europe, while the specifics were always different, we find other complex economic systems with feudal relations and pre-industrial production methods. For instance, across Africa there were a variety of complex feudalist forms of organisation based around the production of plantain bananas, cattle, and a variety of different goods. These had many similarities with European feudalism despite their religious and cultural differences. There had also been a feudal system in China that began to decline during the Ming period, which brought greater bureaucracy and central control.

在欧洲之外，尽管具体情况各异，我们同样发现了其他拥有封建关系和前工业生产方式的复杂经济体系。例如，在非洲各地，存在多种围绕大蕉、牛群及各类商品生产而形成的复杂封建组织形式。尽管在宗教和文化上存在差异，这些体系与欧洲封建制度有着诸多相似之处。中国也曾存在封建制度，该制度在明朝时期开始衰落，随之而来的是官僚体系的加强和中央集权的深化。



In this economic system populations were small and production levels were low. Most people worked from their homes or on their land, producing little more than was needed to survive. Rather than having set deadlines or quotas, they tended to work together as family units producing whatever was necessary for self-sustenance. In this context, impairment and chronic illness were more accommodated in daily life. And this was not just as medical technology was so limited, or that there were very few hospitals, which then were more just refuges for people with leprosy. It was also that the workplace had been slower, more flexible, and more self-determined. Peasants worked fewer hours and had longer breaks than those working following the Industrial Revolution. Moreover, families and communities had often worked from home and as a unit, allowing a more flexible division of labour.

在这种经济体系中，人口规模小，生产水平低。大多数人居家或在自家土地上劳作，产出仅略高于生存所需。他们没有固定的截止日期或配额，而是倾向于以家庭为单位共同劳作，生产维持生计所必需的一切。在此背景下，损伤和慢性疾病在日常生活中更容易得到包容。这不仅是因为医疗技术极为有限，或医院寥寥无几——当时的医院更像是麻风病人的收容所——也因为工作场所节奏更慢、更灵活、更自主。与工业革命后的劳动者相比，农民的工作时间更短，休息时间更长。此外，家庭和社区通常居家劳作且作为一个整体，允许更灵活的劳动分工。



When it comes to disability, this is important because it meant that people with a wider range of impairments could be – and indeed, would often have to have been – included within broader family units or communities. A deaf or blind grandmother, for instance, may have still been able to weave or cook, a man with a cognitive disability may have laboured in the fields or helped in manufacturing, and people with mobility impairments could still work from home. More generally, in this period, as people still worked more with local communities and in relation to the seasons, it made sense to think of health as harmony between these various factors. And this includes the harmony of communities, which required an acceptance of a wider range of ways of functioning than were accepted in the industrial era.

在讨论残障时，这一点至关重要，因为它意味着更多类型的损伤者能够——实际上也常常必须——被纳入更广泛的家庭单位或社区中。例如，一位聋人或盲人祖母可能仍能编织或烹饪，一位认知障碍的男性或许能在田间劳作或协助生产，而行动不便者仍可在家工作。更广泛地说，在这一时期，由于人们仍更多地与当地社区合作并顺应季节变化，将健康视为这些不同因素之间的和谐是合理的。这包括社区的和谐，它要求接受比工业时代更广泛的功能方式。



All this began to change with the rise of capitalism. In part, the shift to capitalism emerged in the context of feudalist conceptions of property, which became gradually formalised as commerce developed across a more globalised market. In this period, states increasingly needed to quantify people and their assets to collect taxes, especially following conflicts between peasants and lords that allowed more peasants to own their own land and grow their own food. In Europe, for instance, following the Black Death, wiping out up to a third of the population in the thirteenth century, workers were also able to demand better conditions, and often rebelled in demand of these. In time, this allowed some landowners to begin making high profits from selling their products, and to begin accumulating wealth that could be reinvested.

这一切随着资本主义的兴起开始改变。资本主义的转型部分源于封建主义的财产观念，随着商业在全球化的市场中发展，这些观念逐渐被形式化。在这一时期，国家越来越需要量化人口及其资产以征收税款，尤其是在农民与领主之间的冲突之后，更多农民得以拥有自己的土地并种植粮食。例如，在欧洲，黑死病在十三世纪消灭了多达三分之一的人口后，工人们也能够要求更好的条件，并经常为此反抗。随着时间的推移，这使得一些地主开始通过销售产品获得高额利润，并开始积累可以再投资的财富。



New market economies and increases in commerce can be found across the world, from Italy to China, from around the sixteenth century. Increased specialisation of labour allowed for greater production and thus a boom in population. In turn, all this required stricter forms of measurement and quantification from the state, leading to the formalisation of surnames and standard measurements for assessing harvests and profits as the population grew. Classifications relating to ability were also increasingly formalised, leading to distinctions between the ‘deserving’ and ‘undeserving’ poor. The Elizabethan Poor Law of 1601, for instance, declared that ‘Sums of Money’ for the relief of the ‘Lame, Impotent, Old, or Blind’ should be provided by the parish, while the able-bodied poor should be set to work in industry.13

从十六世纪左右开始，从意大利到中国，世界各地都出现了新的市场经济和商业增长。劳动力日益专业化促进了生产增长，从而带来了人口繁荣。相应地，随着人口增长，国家需要更严格的测量和量化形式，这导致了姓氏的规范化以及用于评估收成和利润的标准度量衡的建立。与能力相关的分类也日益规范化，导致了对“值得救济”和“不值得救济”的穷人的区分。例如，1601 年的《伊丽莎白济贫法》规定，教区应提供“金钱款项”以救济“跛足、无能、年老或失明”者，而有劳动能力的穷人则应被安排从事工业劳动。 13



Across Europe, new economic relations were further driven by the way Europeans began to colonise parts of Africa from the twelfth century, and later the Americas. Having already developed early racialised notions about the Irish and Slavs, European colonisers adapted these notions to justify their subsequent genocide and enslavement of Black and Indigenous peoples.14 This brought a new slave trade that was, if anything, much more brutal than the slavery of the Roman era. Out of this a larger, global capitalist system began to grow, with European nations, merchants, and explorers competing to colonise, murder, enslave, or trade with members of different communities across the globe. It was in this context that the Industrial Revolution would occur, making the conditions just right for Descartes’ proposal to finally begin being more widely embraced.

从十二世纪起，欧洲人开始殖民非洲部分地区，后来又殖民美洲，这进一步推动了整个欧洲新的经济关系的发展。欧洲殖民者早已对爱尔兰人和斯拉夫人形成了早期的种族化观念，他们将这些观念加以调整，以合理化随后对黑人和原住民的种族灭绝与奴役行为。 14 这催生了一种新的奴隶贸易，其残酷程度甚至可能超过了罗马时代的奴隶制。由此，一个更大规模的全球资本主义体系开始形成，欧洲各国、商人和探险家竞相在全球范围内殖民、屠杀、奴役或与不同社群进行贸易。正是在这样的背景下，工业革命发生了，为笛卡尔的提议最终开始被更广泛地接受创造了绝佳的条件。



THE PRODUCTIVE BODY

生产性身体



With this new power and the continued growth of commerce, new scientific and technological innovations were able to be developed in Europe. Interestingly, by the time Descartes proposed his mechanistic understanding of the body, there were already several workshops in Europe developing automata, where skilled workers developed expensive, self-operating machines. According to one tale, following the death of his daughter, ‘a distraught Descartes had a clockwork Francine made: a walking, talking simulacrum’.15 Yet while earlier automata may have inspired Descartes’s philosophical breakthrough, it was later technological innovations that allowed it to become widely accepted.

随着这种新权力的崛起和商业的持续扩张，欧洲得以孕育出新的科学与技术创新。有趣的是，当笛卡尔提出他关于身体的机械论理解时，欧洲已有数家工坊在研制自动机，那里技艺精湛的工匠们制造出昂贵且能自主运行的机器。据一则轶闻记载，笛卡尔在女儿去世后，“悲痛欲绝地让人制作了一个发条驱动的弗朗辛：一个能行走、会说话的仿生人偶”。 15 然而，尽管早期的自动机可能启发了笛卡尔的哲学突破，但使其观点被广泛接受的，却是后来出现的技术革新。



The first steam pump, for instance, was developed in 1698 and the first steam engine in 1712. The spinning jenny, which allowed workers to produce multiple spools of thread simultaneously, was developed in 1764, and was followed by the spinning mule and the power loom in subsequent decades. Such inventions eased processes of production and could thus be invested in to generate profit. This in turn made an even greater demand for slave labour, to produce materials such as cotton not to mention goods such as tobacco, sugar, and tea. Specialisations in divisions of labour increased further still, allowing for ever greater levels of productivity and ever higher profits.

例如，第一台蒸汽泵于 1698 年问世，第一台蒸汽机则于 1712 年诞生。1764 年发明的珍妮纺纱机让工人能够同时生产多个线轴，随后几十年又相继出现了走锭纺纱机和动力织布机。这些发明简化了生产流程，因此可以投入资金以创造利润。这反过来又进一步加大了对奴隶劳动的需求，以生产棉花等原材料，更不用说烟草、糖和茶叶等商品。劳动分工的专业化程度持续加深，使得生产力水平不断提升，利润也日益丰厚。



As merchant capitalism shifted to industrial capitalism, an ever-more powerful class of people, the bourgeoisie or capitalist class, came to rival the old powers of lords and kings. Because the bourgeoisie (by definition) owned the means of production, they could thus invest their profits and accumulate more and more capital. This small class thus became much more wealthy and influential. Everyone else, except an increasingly obsolete number of aristocrats, was either a free worker who sold their labour, an enslaved labourer forced to work, or was unemployed and thus part of a new surplus population. The work of women was also increasingly unrecognised, since they typically still worked at home while men went out to labour. For as reproductive and domestic work was not waged, it was no longer conceptualised as real work.16 This ever-more dominant system thus broke apart traditional communities and restructured populations as per their place in its new economic hierarchies at national and international levels.

随着商业资本主义向工业资本主义转变，一个日益强大的阶级——资产阶级或资本家阶级——开始与旧有的领主和国王势力分庭抗礼。由于资产阶级（根据定义）掌握着生产资料，他们能够将利润进行再投资，从而积累越来越多的资本。这个少数阶级因此变得愈发富裕且具有影响力。除了数量日益减少、逐渐过时的贵族外，其他所有人要么是出卖劳动力的自由工人，要么是被迫劳动的奴工，要么就是失业者，从而构成了新的过剩人口。女性的劳动也日益得不到承认，因为她们通常仍在家中劳作，而男性则外出工作。由于生育和家务劳动没有薪酬，这些劳动不再被视为真正的工作。 16 这种日益占据主导地位的体系因此瓦解了传统社群，并根据其在国内和国际层面新经济等级中的地位，对人口进行了重组。



When it came to health, the effects of industrial capitalism were profound. It was not just, as Marx noted, that this system and its labour relations ‘squanders human beings, living labour, more readily than does any other mode of production, squandering not only flesh and blood, but nerves and brain as well’.17 Nor was it just that the living conditions of workers, packed into the squalor and pollution of industrial cities, brought new epidemics and diseases. While this was the case, what I want to stress is that in an important sense, it was capitalism that allowed the body itself to go from being understood as a dynamic organism to being a working or broken machine. And it was not just the fact that new machines were increasingly part of daily life, making it seem natural to use machines as metaphors for the sciences of the age. It was also that the mode of production itself favoured a reduction of people to living machines, since they were seen as working or broken in relation to their productive potential.

在健康方面，工业资本主义的影响是深远的。正如马克思所指出的，这不仅是因为这种制度及其劳动关系"比其他任何生产方式都更轻易地浪费人类、活劳动，不仅浪费血肉，还浪费神经和大脑"。 17 也不仅仅是因为工人们挤在工业城市的肮脏和污染中，生活条件带来了新的流行病和疾病。虽然这些都是事实，但我想强调的是，在某种意义上，正是资本主义让身体本身从被理解为动态有机体，转变为被视为运转或损坏的机器。这不仅仅是因为新机器日益成为日常生活的一部分，使得用机器作为时代科学的隐喻显得自然而然。还因为生产方式本身倾向于将人简化为活的机器，因为人们是根据其生产潜力被看作运转或损坏的。



Most notably, in industrial England, as Vic Finkelstein has argued, as the new machines and workdays were increasingly standardised, the ideal worker was likewise standardised. Workers increasingly needed to be mobile enough to be able to travel to the factory. And they then needed to be able to work in line with the pace and production norms of the industrial workplace. At the same time, increased production of food meant that the population was able to expand. In this context, there were more and more surplus members of the workforce who had to compete against each other to gain employment. English factory workers could not, as Finkelstein writes, ‘have any impairment which would prevent him or her from operating the machine. It was, therefore, the economic necessity of producing efficient machines for large-scale production that established able-bodiedness as the norm’ in industrial England.18

最为显著的是，正如维克·芬克尔斯坦所论证的，在工业化的英格兰，随着新机器和工作日日益标准化，理想工人的形象也随之被标准化。工人越来越需要具备足够的行动能力，以便能够前往工厂。随后，他们还需要能够按照工业场所的节奏和生产规范进行工作。与此同时，粮食产量的增加使得人口得以扩张。在此背景下，劳动力中出现了越来越多的剩余人员，他们不得不相互竞争以获取就业机会。正如芬克尔斯坦所写，英国的工厂工人“不能有任何会妨碍其操作机器的损伤。因此，正是大规模生产高效机器的经济必要性，在工业化的英格兰确立了健全身体作为规范”。 18



This is not to say that disability was wholly synonymous with being unable to work in factories. In their study of disabled British coal miners in industrial England, historians Turner and Blackie stress how the ‘dynamics of inclusion and exclusion’ change ‘within particular cohorts or occupations, and in different settings’.19 In the case of coalmining, more disabled people, while encountering specific barriers and forms of discrimination, were included within the workforce. In this we see the emergence of a more general pattern, whereby disabled people and other members of the surplus class were sometimes included, if and when they are needed or can be exploited for profit. We also see how there is some fluidity between the working and surplus class, with members of either one moving into the other depending on the shifting needs of capital.

这并不是说残障完全等同于无法在工厂工作。历史学家特纳和布莱基在对工业英格兰时期英国残疾煤矿工人的研究中强调，"包容与排斥的动态"如何"在特定群体或职业内部，以及不同环境中"发生变化。 19 就煤矿开采而言，尽管面临特定的障碍和歧视形式，更多的残障人士被纳入了劳动力队伍。由此我们看到一个更普遍的模式的出现：残障人士及其他剩余阶级成员有时会被纳入，前提是当且仅当他们被需要或可以被剥削以获取利润时。我们也看到工人阶级与剩余阶级之间存在一定的流动性，任一阶级的成员都可能根据资本不断变化的需求而转入另一阶级。



We also see a more complicated situation for Black slaves. Slaves were sold on slave markets and thus their bodies and minds were commodified in ways that paid labourers were not subjected to. As Stefanie Hunt-Kennedy has detailed, since they were not paid, plantation slaves were more often required to work even despite many being disabled – which they often were due to sustaining injuries following horrific abuse at the hands of slavers. Moreover, the ‘worth’ of enslaved labourers was determined by their ‘resale value on the open market, as well as their individual output as workers’.20 Because of how racism was built into the origins of capitalism, millions of enslaved labourers were thus doubly objectified in a way that was far worse than the already bad exploitation of white workers in Europe.

对于黑人奴隶而言，情况更为复杂。奴隶在奴隶市场上被买卖，他们的身体和思想因此被商品化，这是有偿劳动者所不曾经历的。正如斯蒂芬妮·亨特-肯尼迪详细阐述的那样，由于没有报酬，种植园的奴隶即使身患残疾——这通常是由于他们在奴隶主手中遭受可怕虐待后受伤所致——也常常被迫继续工作。此外，被奴役劳动者的“价值”是由“他们在公开市场上的转售价值以及作为工人的个人产出”决定的。由于种族主义被植入了资本主义的起源之中，数百万被奴役的劳动者因此遭受了双重物化，其程度远比欧洲白人劳动者所遭受的剥削更为恶劣。



Indeed, as the research of Caitlin Rosenthal shows, it was plantation owners in the American South that pioneered the scientific management of enslaved workers. They did this, she writes, by paying ‘close attention to how efficiently enslaved men and women picked cotton, frequently experimenting with new methods for maximizing output’ recording and analysing ‘data diligently and precisely, keeping accounts and comparing them year after year’.21 In this, enslaved labourers were the first to be scientifically studied and manipulated to increase individual worker productivity in the service of capital. It was this kind of scientific management that paved the way for those methods that would later be expanded to all workers after the slave trade, and later slavery, were finally outlawed.

诚然，正如凯特琳·罗森塔尔的研究所示，美国南方的种植园主率先对受奴役的工人进行了科学管理。她写道，他们通过“密切关注被奴役的男女采摘棉花的效率，频繁尝试新方法以最大化产出”，并“勤奋而精确地记录和分析数据，逐年保存账目并进行比较”来实现这一点。 21 在此过程中，受奴役的劳动者成为首批被科学研究和操控的对象，旨在提高个体工人的生产力，服务于资本。正是这种科学管理为后来的方法铺平了道路，这些方法在奴隶贸易乃至奴隶制最终被废除后，逐渐扩展至所有工人。



While conditions thus depended on context, what is clear is that throughout the capitalist world, the body itself, including the brain, increasingly came to be judged as being working or broken in relation to the individual’s real or perceived productivity. And everyone’s output was increasingly compared with everyone else’s due to them being in competition with each other. In turn, individual productivity was increasingly observed, documented, classified, and assessed.

因此，尽管条件取决于具体情境，但显而易见的是，在整个资本主义世界中，包括大脑在内的身体本身，越来越根据个人实际或感知的生产力被评判为"正常运作"或"故障"。由于彼此竞争，每个人的产出也日益被相互比较。相应地，个人的生产力也越来越多地被观察、记录、分类和评估。



Through this period, worries regarding malingerers – people who were pretending to be ill to avoid work – continued to increase. Governmental practices to assess and distinguish the unemployed able-bodied poor from the disabled were often refined. Even as far back as 1697, for instance, the Badging Act had required everyone who relied on parish relief to wear a badge that declared their initials and pauper status. In turn, subsequent laws further constructed disability as a categorisation for state intervention, as we will return to in the following chapter.

在这一时期，对装病者——即假装生病以逃避工作的人——的担忧持续加剧。政府为评估和区分失业的健康穷人与残障人士而采取的措施也常常得到完善。例如，早在 1697 年，《徽章法案》就要求所有依赖教区救济的人佩戴一枚徽章，上面标明其姓名首字母和贫民身份。随后，后续法律进一步将残障构建为国家干预的分类范畴，我们将在下一章中再回到这一点。



In this context, Descartes’ proposal, while initially considered heretical, would come to be so widely adopted not just because it was useful for medicine. It was also enormously useful for capital, since by the nineteenth century, the industrialists, plantation owners, and other capitalists had come to see their workers as individual machines who could be working or broken. And by this time, it was the needs of the capitalists more primarily than the scriptures of the church that determined what was acceptable.

在这种背景下，笛卡尔的提议虽然最初被视为异端邪说，但后来之所以被广泛采纳，不仅仅是因为它对医学有用。它对资本也极为有用，因为到了 19 世纪，工业家、种植园主和其他资本家已经开始将他们的工人视为可以工作或损坏的个体机器。而到了这个时候，决定什么是可接受的，更多的是资本家的需求，而不是教会的经文。



So it came to be, as Karl Marx was perhaps the first to observe in 1867, that capitalism brought not just new machines, but also an ‘artificially produced’ transformation of ‘human beings into mere machines for the production of surplus-value’.22 And as we shall see in the next chapter, it was here – in these new standards of mechanistic functioning – that the emerging statistical concept of ‘normality’ would come to replace the traditional concept of equilibrium when it came to understanding health.

因此，正如卡尔·马克思在 1867 年或许首次观察到的那样，资本主义不仅带来了新机器，还带来了"人为制造的"转变，将"人类变成了仅仅生产剩余价值的机器"。 22 正如我们将在下一章中看到的，正是在这些新的机械功能标准中，新兴的"正常"统计概念将取代传统的平衡概念，成为理解健康的方式。



---

Empire of Normality



2



The invention of normality

正常性的发明



Alongside the shift from humoral to mechanistic conceptions of bodily functioning came another shift, no less important, from viewing health as harmony to viewing health as normality. It is to this shift, beginning with the story of a pioneering Belgian statistician called Adolphe Quetelet, that we now turn. What Quetelet did was propose the first science of human normality, which laid the grounds for later work in medicine, criminology, psychology, and eugenics. This made him one of the leading early social scientists, whose influence still impacts our lives today. Yet as we shall see, this was not simply a matter of scientific discovery. As with the rise of the machine metaphor, it would be a reflection of the economic and ideological shifts of the age. In part, this was the same industrialisation that led to the reinterpretation of humans as machines. But this time it was also the bourgeois revolutions in France and Belgium.

随着身体机能观念从体液论转向机械论，另一个同样重要的转变也随之而来：健康观从和谐转向正常。我们现在要探讨的正是这一转变，它始于一位名叫阿道夫·凯特莱的比利时统计学先驱的故事。凯特莱的贡献在于提出了首个关于人类正常性的科学理论，为后来的医学、犯罪学、心理学和优生学研究奠定了基础。这使他成为早期最重要的社会科学家之一，其影响至今仍渗透在我们的生活中。然而我们将看到，这并非单纯的科学发现。正如机器隐喻的兴起一样，它也是时代经济与意识形态变迁的反映。在某种程度上，这与导致人类被重新解读为机器的工业化进程同源。但这一次，它还关联着法国和比利时的资产阶级革命。



To understand Quetelet’s work, we need to first turn back to the origins of statistics that grounded his thinking. Interestingly, basic conceptions of the ‘average’ in the modern sense, associated with a summary of data, did not emerge among the medics. In fact, statistical analysis had first been developed by astronomers in the sixteenth century to predict the course of planets that could not always be observed. This then progressed in bits and pieces over the following centuries until 1801. It was in this year that the German mathematician Carl Friedrich Gauss was able to develop a formula on which he based a bell curve shaped graph, predicting the movement of a star named Ceres. This became known as the ‘error curve’, where errors were understood as deviations from the norm. It was this that opened the way for early statistical analyses of normality to be used in other fields for summarising data. It was also this that allowed the normal to be associated with correctness, and abnormality with error.

要理解凯特莱的工作，我们首先需要追溯奠定其思想基础的统计学起源。有趣的是，现代意义上与数据汇总相关的"平均值"基本概念，并非诞生于医学界。事实上，统计分析最早由 16 世纪的天文学家开创，用于预测那些无法持续观测的行星运行轨迹。此后数百年间，这项技术零散发展直至 1801 年。正是在这一年，德国数学家卡尔·弗里德里希·高斯推导出一个公式，并以此绘制出钟形曲线图，成功预测了名为谷神星的恒星运行轨迹。这条曲线后来被称为"误差曲线"，其中"误差"被理解为偏离标准值的程度。正是这项突破为早期关于正常性的统计分析开辟了道路，使其得以应用于其他领域进行数据汇总。也正是通过这一理论，"正常"开始与正确性相关联，而"异常"则被等同于误差。



In medicine, such concepts were first applied following the French Revolution, which lasted from 1789 to 1799. The revolution had attempted to free humans from religious dogma, traditional customs, and the feudal system. The new form of state that emerged required the quantification and counting of everything in standardised ways free from the taint of supernatural beliefs or provincial customs. This led to new statistical and quantitative approaches to just about everything, including the development of the metric system, the standardisation of weights, map-making surveys, and much more. These would purport to be universal and objective, allowing new ways of organising and improving society.

在医学领域，这类概念首次应用是在 1789 年至 1799 年的法国大革命之后。这场革命试图将人类从宗教教条、传统习俗和封建制度中解放出来。新兴的国家形态要求以标准化的方式对一切事物进行量化和统计，摆脱超自然信仰或地方习俗的影响。这催生了几乎涵盖所有领域的新统计与量化方法，包括公制系统的建立、度量衡的标准化、地图测绘调查等等。这些方法宣称具有普适性和客观性，为组织和改善社会提供了新的途径。



At the same time, the revolution also brought a great many injuries, deaths, and executions, which meant that physicians in Paris were free to begin documenting and experimentally applying new statistical ideas to their abundant supply of patients, bodies, and records. As the historians Cryle and Stephens have established, the term ‘normal state’ thus first appeared in French literature on comparative anatomy in around 1820 before being used in medical texts in the 1830s, although at this time it was only used in passing and had neither a clear definition nor an obvious scientific use.1

与此同时，革命也带来了大量的伤害、死亡和处决，这意味着巴黎的医生们可以自由地开始记录并将新的统计理念实验性地应用于他们丰富的病人、尸体和记录资源。正如历史学家克莱尔和斯蒂芬斯所证实的那样，“正常状态”一词因此首次出现在大约 1820 年的法国比较解剖学文献中，然后在 19 世纪 30 年代被用于医学文本，尽管当时它只是顺便提及，既没有明确的定义，也没有明显的科学用途。



Within this context, the most important early theoretical intervention came from Quetelet. Born in Ghent – then part of the French Republic – in 1796, Quetelet had studied mathematics and astronomy, receiving a doctorate from the University of Ghent in 1819. He soon became known as a talented lecturer and keen musician, who would entertain guests with recitals during dinner parties. In the 1820s Quetelet then proposed the development of a new observatory. This gained support from the government, so he travelled to France and England to learn more about the latest instruments and methods in astronomy. Guided by his new knowledge, he then returned and began constructing a new observatory of his own.

在此背景下，最早的重要理论介入来自凯特莱。他于 1796 年出生在根特——当时属于法兰西共和国——曾学习数学和天文学，并于 1819 年获得根特大学博士学位。他很快以一位才干出众的讲师和热忱的音乐家而闻名，常在晚宴上为宾客演奏助兴。19 世纪 20 年代，凯特莱提议建造一座新的天文台。这一提议得到了政府的支持，于是他前往法国和英国，学习天文学领域最新的仪器和方法。在新知识的指引下，他回国后开始着手建造属于自己的新天文台。



Quetelet’s running of the observatory was interrupted, however, by the revolution of 1830 that restored independence to Belgium. Following the disruption of the revolution – during which his observatory was occupied and used as an armoury – he became more interested in using statistics to understand and predict the social world instead of the physical world. While he published some brief articles earlier, it was his ground-breaking 1835 book The Average Man (l’homme moyen) that became an international hit and earned him his place in the history of statistics, medicine, and social science.

然而，1830 年的革命恢复了比利时的独立，打断了凯特勒对天文台的运营。革命期间，他的天文台被占领并被用作军械库。在经历了这场动荡之后，他变得更加热衷于运用统计学来理解和预测社会世界，而非物理世界。虽然他早些时候发表过一些简短的文章，但真正让他声名鹊起、并在统计学、医学和社会科学史上占据一席之地的，是他 1835 年那本开创性的著作《平均人》。



What Quetelet proposed was a radical new science of human normality. His suggestion, in his own words, was that:

凯特勒提出的，是一门关于人类正常性的全新激进科学。用他自己的话说，他的建议是：





the weight and stature of a man may be measured directly, and we may afterwards compare them with the weight and stature of another man. In comparing the different men of a nation in this manner, we arrive at average values, which are the weight and stature proper to be assigned to the average man.2

一个人的体重和身高可以直接测量，然后我们可以将其与另一个人的体重和身高进行比较。以这种方式比较一个国家中不同的人，我们就能得出平均值，这些值就是应归属于平均人的体重和身高。 2





By studying records of Scottish soldiers, he was able to make averages of height, weight, and so forth to understand and predict the nature of the typical Scotsman. Based on this, Quetelet argued that the concept of the average man would be helpful for understanding the ‘normal state’ of health. This is perhaps best exemplified by Quetelet’s development of, among much else, the very Body Mass Index, or BMI, formula that is still used today to measure whether people are under, or over, their ideal weight. This also allowed notions such as the average heart rate, or normal lung capacity, to be developed over the following century.3 This allowed human mechanistic functioning to not just be understood as working or broken, but to be assessed and ranked in ever-more fine-grained ways in relation to whatever was considered normal.

通过研究苏格兰士兵的记录，他能够计算出身高、体重等方面的平均值，以理解和预测典型苏格兰人的特征。基于此，凯特勒认为，平均人的概念将有助于理解健康的“正常状态”。这一点或许最能体现在凯特勒所发展的众多成果中，包括至今仍被用来衡量人们体重是否低于或高于理想值的身体质量指数（BMI）公式。这也使得诸如平均心率或正常肺活量等概念在接下来的一个世纪中得以发展。 3 这使得人类的机械功能不仅被理解为工作正常或故障，而且能够以越来越精细的方式，根据被认为是正常的标准进行评估和排名。



Yet like the shift to the machine metaphor, this too was not simply a matter of scientific progress. To understand it fully, we must recognise how it mirrored shifts in social and material relations. It was not just that this helped ground a mechanistic science of the body, allowing for recognition of different levels of functioning. Quetelet also posited the average man as the ideal person of post-revolution France in a way that helped create a new ideal: ‘If the average man were completely determined’, he wrote, we might ‘consider him as the type of perfection; and everything differing from his proportions or condition, would constitute’, he went on, ‘a monstrosity’.4 In making this leap, Quetelet helped solidify the association of the average man not just with health but also with moral goodness and perfection. The error curve developed to predict the course of stars now applied to human normativity, and to be abnormal was to be a mistake of nature.

然而，如同转向机器隐喻的转变一样，这也不仅仅是科学进步的问题。要完全理解这一点，我们必须认识到它如何反映了社会和物质关系的变化。这不仅有助于奠定一种机械主义的身体科学，使得不同层次的功能得以被认识。凯特勒还将平均人设定为后革命法国时期的理想人物，从而帮助创造了一种新的理想：“如果平均人被完全确定下来，”他写道，我们或许可以“将他视为完美的典范；而任何偏离其比例或状态的事物，”他继续道，“都将构成一种畸形。” 4 通过这一跨越，凯特勒不仅巩固了平均人与健康的关联，还将其与道德良善和完美联系起来。原本为预测星辰轨迹而发展出的误差曲线，现在被应用于人类的规范性，而异常则被视为自然的错误。



To understand this, it is important to bear in mind, as Allan Horwitz has noted, that, in line with the ideals of the French Revolution, Quetelet’s ‘view was radically democratic because each individual, from the most noble to the most downtrodden, had equivalent weight to every other one’ for the first time.5 Yet simultaneously, as Lennard Davis writes,

要理解这一点，重要的是要记住，正如艾伦·霍维茨所指出的，根据法国大革命的理想，凯特莱的观点是彻底民主的，因为每个个体，从最高贵到最受压迫的，首次被赋予了与其他所有人同等的权重。 5 然而与此同时，正如伦纳德·戴维斯所写，





In formulating the idea of l’homme moyen, Quetelet is also providing a justification for les classes moyens. With bourgeois hegemony comes scientific justification for moderation and middle-class ideology. The average man, the body of the man in the middle, becomes the exemplar of the middle way of life. [This ideology thus] saw the bourgeoisie as rationally placed in the mean position in the great order of things.6

在阐述“平均人”这一概念时，凯特莱也为“中产阶级”提供了合理性。随着资产阶级霸权的确立，中庸和中产阶级意识形态获得了科学上的正当性。平均人，即中间阶层的人，成为了中庸生活方式的典范。[这种意识形态因此]将资产阶级视为在万物伟大秩序中理性地处于中间位置。 6





Simultaneously, Quetelet’s ‘average man’ was also determined specifically in relation to the nation-state. The perfect man in France would be different to the perfect man from Germany, who would again be different to the perfect average in Russia. In each of these nations, those who sat further from the average man of the specific nation – consider, say, a Black man in a white majority nation – would be considered comparatively monstrous. Hence the new average man concept helped provide a way of normalising racial nationalism alongside bourgeois hegemony.

与此同时，凯特勒的"平均人"概念也明确地与民族国家相关联。法国的完美男性会不同于德国的完美男性，而后者又与俄罗斯的完美平均标准有所区别。在这些国家中，那些偏离特定国家平均标准的人——例如在白色人种占多数的国家中的黑人男性——会被视为相对而言的怪物。因此，新的平均人概念为种族民族主义与资产阶级霸权的正常化提供了一种途径。



Overall, then, the notion of the average man did not just help medicine advance. It also helped naturalise the new ideology and hierarchies that emerged as the last remnants of feudalism gave way to the dominance of capitalism in France and beyond. In European nations – where nationalism was rising as empires vied for control of colonies around the world – the average man would be a white, middle-class man of typical ability. And he, rather than, say, the king or high priest, now exemplified all that was good and proper, while those who deviated from normality were monstrous and in need of fixing.

总而言之，平均人的概念不仅促进了医学的进步。它还帮助将新兴的意识形态和等级制度自然化，这些意识形态和等级制度是在封建主义最后的残余让位于法国及其他地区资本主义统治的过程中出现的。在欧洲国家——随着帝国争夺全球殖民地的控制权，民族主义正在兴起——平均人将是一个具有典型能力的白人中产阶级男性。而他，而非国王或高级祭司，现在代表了所有美好和正当的事物，而那些偏离常态的人则是怪物，需要被纠正。



THE MEAN UNDERSTANDING

平均理解



We also see similar material forces at play in the related idea of the ‘mean understanding’. In earlier times, philosophers such as Aristotle, working in Athens, and Abu Bakr al-Razi, working in Baghdad, had written extensively on the intellect.7 But the British notion of the ‘mean understanding’ was developed for a practical purpose, initially being constructed around the notion of idiocy as capitalism dawned in England. Prior to the Enlightenment, idiocy had mainly been viewed through a religious lens. Those called idiots were sometimes seen as monstrous, but were equally often seen as vulnerable members of the community deserving of support. Indeed, some even led relatively privileged lives in court. This was because they were widely taken to have access to divine wisdom, and it was thought by some that keeping a fool would absolve one’s sins.8 More generally, in medieval and feudal societies, as the historian Roddy Sloarch details, the

我们同样在相关的“平均理解力”概念中看到了类似的物质力量在起作用。早期哲学家如雅典的亚里士多德和巴格达的阿布·巴克尔·拉齐曾对智力有过广泛论述。 7 但英国的“平均理解力”概念是为实用目的而发展起来的，最初是围绕资本主义在英国兴起时的“白痴”概念构建的。启蒙运动之前，白痴主要被置于宗教视角下审视。那些被称为白痴的人有时被视为怪物，但也同样常被视为需要社区支持的弱势成员。事实上，有些人甚至在宫廷中过着相对优渥的生活。这是因为人们普遍认为他们能接触神圣智慧，甚至有人认为豢养愚者可以赎罪。 8 更广泛地说，正如历史学家罗迪·斯洛奇详细阐述的那样，在中世纪和封建社会，





lives of people with impairments were determined by the general conditions of exploitation and oppression that obtained in these (often brutal societies). But there is no evidence of any specific, systemic discrimination levelled at them.9

残障人士的生活是由当时普遍存在的剥削与压迫条件所决定的（这些社会往往相当残酷）。但并没有证据表明他们遭受了任何特定的、系统性的歧视。 9





However, in seventeenth-century England, which was then beginning to develop into a global superpower, the concept of the ‘mean understanding’ emerged. And along with this we do precisely see new forms of discrimination.

然而，在十七世纪的英格兰——当时正开始发展成为全球超级大国——"理解力平庸"这一概念出现了。而伴随着这一概念，我们确实看到了新的歧视形式。



Interestingly, this was initially in the specific context of legal disputes relating to the inheritance of private property. The concept of the mean understanding was essentially developed to exclude people with cognitive disabilities from inheriting property, and to allow distant family members with ‘normal’ levels of understanding to be able to (usually unfairly) extract that property. We can see, for instance, how as far back as 1700 the English Lawyer John Brydall’s book Non Compos Mentis: Or, The Law Relating to Natural Fools, was full of claims such as the following:

有趣的是，这最初出现在与私有财产继承相关的法律纠纷这一特定背景下。"理解力平庸"这一概念本质上是为了将认知障碍者排除在财产继承之外，并允许那些具有"正常"理解能力的远亲（通常是不公平地）获取这些财产。例如，我们可以看到，早在 1700 年，英国律师约翰·布莱德尔的著作《精神不健全者：或关于天生愚者的法律》中就充斥着如下主张：





If a Man be of a mean understanding (neither of the wisest sort, nor of the foolish’st) but, indifferent as it were, betwixt a Wise man and a Fool, yea though he rather incline to the foolish sort, so that for his dull capacity he might worthily be termed Grossum Caput, a dull Pate, Dunce, such a one is not prohibited to make a Testament.10

若一人资质平庸（既非智者，亦非愚者），处于智愚之间，甚至更偏向愚钝，因其迟钝的悟性可被恰当地称为"Grossum Caput"（愚钝头脑）、"Dunce"（蠢材），这样的人并不被禁止订立遗嘱。 10





The proposal that such people should be prohibited from making a testament here essentially means that their testimony, and, by implication, their interests, should have no legal standing in property disputes. At the same time, the new concept of ‘natural fools’ allowed such mistreatments to be seen as part of the natural order. Hence, the concept of the ‘mean understanding’ initially took hold because it allowed cognitively enabled people to make sure they had a monopoly on property and the means of production – and to begin to frame this as part of a natural hierarchy.11

此处关于禁止此类人订立遗嘱的提议，实质上意味着他们的证词及其所代表的利益，在财产纠纷中不应具有法律效力。与此同时，"天生愚人"这一新概念使得此类不公待遇被视为自然秩序的一部分。因此，"资质平庸"这一概念最初得以确立，是因为它让具备认知能力的人得以确保自己对财产和生产资料的垄断——并开始将其塑造成自然等级体系的一部分。 11



However, early capitalist conceptions of the ‘mean understanding’ were not based on a statistical analysis, since prior to Quetelet, there were neither methods nor data to derive the mean. Soundness of mind was only very loosely determined by legal professionals who would ask questions about general knowledge or mathematics to determine legal competence. It was only following Quetelet’s influence, and in line with the start of the Industrial Revolution in England, that various attempts to apply statistical methods to the brain and mind emerged, usually in order to reify emerging hierarchical distinctions in ability, social class, gender, and race.12

然而，早期资本主义关于“平均理解力”的概念并非基于统计分析，因为在凯特勒之前，既没有方法也没有数据来推导平均值。心智健全性仅由法律专业人士非常粗略地确定，他们会询问一般知识或数学问题来判断法律行为能力。直到凯特勒的影响之后，并伴随着英国工业革命的开始，各种将统计方法应用于大脑和心智的尝试才出现，通常是为了将能力、社会阶级、性别和种族中新兴的等级差异具体化。 12



Among the most significant early examples of this is phrenology, developed by the physician Franz Gall in 1796. Back when he was a student, Gall had noticed that his classmates with larger eyes and foreheads seemed better at memorising long passages of text. He soon began to wonder whether these surface differences indicated underlying differences in brain structure and functioning. In time he came to think that mental functioning mapped onto specific brain regions which could be read through the shape of the skull. Phrenology, purported to be a new science, thus sought to link head shape with mental faculties to determine mental ability, character, and even propensity for criminality.

颅相学是最早的重要例证之一，由医生弗朗茨·加尔于 1796 年创立。早在学生时代，加尔就注意到那些眼睛和额头较大的同学似乎更擅长记忆长篇文字。他很快开始思考，这些表面差异是否反映了大脑结构与功能的深层区别。渐渐地，他形成了一种观点：心理功能对应着特定的大脑区域，而这些区域的状态可以通过颅骨的形状来解读。颅相学自诩为一门新兴科学，试图通过头型与心智能力的关联，来判定个人的智力水平、性格特征，甚至犯罪倾向。



While phrenology would later come to be seen as a pseudo-science, in industrial Britain many of its proponents believed that they could use the emerging notion of normality to ground its scientific aspirations. In 1845, for instance, James Straton, a Scottish phrenologist, explained in his book Contributions to the Mathematics of Phrenology that his aim was to develop ‘a scale, indicating the average size, the average range, and the extreme ranges of size which have been found among the various races of men’.13 For Straton, skulls and brains that were too big or small would be contrasted with what he called the ‘healthy normal structure, and competent mental capacity to fulfil the imperative duties of life’.14

尽管颅相学后来被视为伪科学，但在工业化的英国，许多支持者相信他们可以利用新兴的“正常”概念来奠定其科学抱负。例如，1845 年，苏格兰颅相学家詹姆斯·斯特拉顿在其著作《颅相学数学贡献》中解释道，他的目标是开发“一个尺度，用以指示在不同种族中发现的大脑平均大小、平均范围以及极端大小范围”。 13 对斯特拉顿而言，过大或过小的头骨和大脑将与他所谓的“健康的正常结构，以及履行生活必要职责的足够心智能力”形成对比。 14



Despite not being properly scientific, phrenology was important because it was so influential in contributing to an emerging shift in cultural understandings relating to race, cognition, and social class. By this time, it is important to remember, European empires built on genocide and colonialism encompassed most of the globe. White Europeans had come to see themselves as superior to other races, upon whose enslaved labour their power depended. The bodies of Africans and indigenous men and especially women were seen in England as monstrous and deformed, while mentally they were seen as somewhere between humans and beasts.15 The class system was also deeply entrenched, and the working classes were often seen by members of the ruling classes as having an inherently lower ability to reason.

尽管颅相学并非真正的科学，但它之所以重要，是因为它在推动文化认知关于种族、认知和社会阶级的转变中产生了巨大影响。需要记住的是，此时建立在种族灭绝和殖民主义基础上的欧洲帝国已覆盖了全球大部分地区。欧洲白人开始将自己视为优于其他种族的存在，而他们的权力正是依赖于这些被奴役的劳动力。在英格兰，非洲人和原住民的身体，尤其是女性的身体，被视为畸形和怪异的，而他们的心智则被看作介于人类与野兽之间。阶级制度也根深蒂固，统治阶级成员常常认为工人阶级天生就具有较低的理性能力。



Within this context, as Sysling details, phrenology not only ‘introduced the “average” to the masses, no matter how little factual basis it had. It provided, both in the United States and in the United Kingdom, a new way for white middle-class men and women to position themselves in an imagined statistical collective’.16 Phrenology was supported by figures ranging from the philosopher Herbert Spencer to the eminent biologist Alfred Wallace. Indeed, even Queen Victoria herself consulted a famous phrenologist, who she asked to read the heads of her children. Given its widespread support, it helped bring a mass shift in collective understanding of both ourselves and each other, and where each of us sat in a natural hierarchy of minds.

正如西斯林所详述的，在这种背景下，颅相学不仅“向大众引入了‘平均’的概念，无论其事实依据多么薄弱。它在美国和英国都为白人中产阶级男女提供了一个新的方式，让他们在一个想象的统计集合中定位自己。” 16 颅相学得到了从哲学家赫伯特·斯宾塞到著名生物学家阿尔弗雷德·华莱士等人的支持。事实上，连维多利亚女王本人也曾咨询过一位著名的颅相学家，并请他为她的孩子们解读头颅。鉴于其广泛的支持，它帮助推动了集体对我们自己以及彼此理解的巨大转变，以及我们每个人在自然心智等级中所处的位置。



Through such cultural practices the concept of the normal mind and brain merged with capitalist and colonial ideology, promising to provide a purportedly objective grounding that could naturalise the cognitive, economic and racial hierarchies that had already begun to emerge in the centuries prior. In this process, ancient conceptions of wisdom or the intellect began to be replaced by a new way of understanding, grounded in statistics. The ideal spread, and middle-class, cognitively abled white people increasingly came to see themselves as naturally closer to an idealised ‘normal’, even super-normal, way of being and thinking when compared to disabled, working-class, and Black and Brown colonised subjects. To have any kind of subnormal cognition was increasingly feared and stigmatised, especially among the upper classes in Europe as well as among white settlers around the globe.

通过这种文化实践，正常心智与大脑的概念与资本主义和殖民意识形态融合，承诺提供一种据称客观的基础，能够将此前几个世纪已开始出现的认知、经济和种族等级自然化。在这一过程中，基于统计学的全新理解方式逐渐取代了古老的智慧或智力观念。这种理想传播开来，中产阶级、认知能力健全的白人越来越将自己视为在存在与思维方式上，相较于残障者、工人阶级以及被殖民的黑人和棕色人种，天生更接近一种理想化的"正常"甚至"超常"状态。任何形式的亚正常认知都日益令人恐惧并遭受污名化，尤其是在欧洲的上层阶级以及全球各地的白人定居者中。



THE GREAT CONFINEMENT

大禁闭



All the factors detailed here and in the previous chapter did not bring a shift in understanding alone. Beyond the use of legal conceptions of the mean understanding to appropriate property from people with cognitive disabilities, a related shift that accompanied the rise of capitalism was the rise of a range of interrelated carceral systems. For those called the mad – which included the cognitively disabled – this led to what Michel Foucault, in his classic 1961 book Madness and Civilisation,17 called the ‘great confinement’. As Foucault details, in the renaissance, mad people were often depicted as having divine wisdom and were often included in the community. As with the disabled, while life was hard for them as for everyone else, they were not systematically discriminated against specifically by virtue of their madness.

本文及上一章所详述的所有因素，并不能仅凭自身带来认知上的转变。 除了利用“普通理解力”这一法律概念来剥夺认知障碍者的财产外，伴随资本主义兴起而出现的另一相关转变，是一系列相互关联的监禁体系的兴起。对于那些被称为“疯子”的人——其中包括认知障碍者——这导致了米歇尔·福柯在其 1961 年的经典著作《疯癫与文明》中 17 所称的“大禁闭”。 正如福柯所详述，在文艺复兴时期，疯子常被描绘为拥有神圣智慧，并常被纳入社区之中。与残障人士一样，尽管他们的生活像其他人一样艰辛，但并未因其“疯狂”而遭受系统性的歧视。



By contrast, as was noted above, late feudalism and then capitalism brought a boom in population density and a great increase in poverty. This generated worries about population control and productivity. In this context, alongside begging, sex work, petty crime, and other things deemed outrageous to bourgeois morality, madness came to be seen as a problem to be solved by locking people up. What each of these groups were taken to share with the others was idleness, which was at odds with the capitalist demand for productivity. The mad in particular were also seen as an affront to the Enlightenment ideal of rationality, and thus as a threat to civilisation itself.

相比之下，正如前文所述，晚期封建主义及随后的资本主义带来了人口密度的激增和贫困的大幅加剧。这引发了人们对人口控制和生产力的担忧。在此背景下，除了乞讨、性工作、轻微犯罪以及其他被资产阶级道德视为可耻的行为外，疯狂也开始被视为需要通过监禁来解决的问题。这些群体被认为共有的特点是懒惰，这与资本主义对生产力的要求相悖。特别是疯子，他们还被视为对启蒙运动理性理想的冒犯，从而对文明本身构成威胁。



While the extent of the confinement emphasised by Foucault remains controversial among historians,18 it is indisputable that asylums emerged in this period, and that the mad – including people with cognitive disability – were often chained up, isolated, and subject to physical punishments. It is also clear that by the nineteenth century, there was an ever-increasing segregation of the able poor into workhouses, the criminalised into prisons, and the mad into asylums. New legislation, most notably the New Poor Law of 1834, intended to reduce the cost of poor relief, made it mandatory for parishes to construct workhouses if they did not have one already. Thus, as capitalism further developed and the population grew, its norms hardened, with the abnormal becoming ever-more salient as more of the population fell beyond its new standards of functioning. It was this that necessitated the mass development of these new carceral systems, which, all in their own ways, imprisoned those deemed abnormal.

尽管福柯所强调的监禁程度在历史学家中仍存争议，但无可争议的是，收容所正是在这一时期出现，而疯子——包括认知残障者——常常被锁链束缚、隔离并遭受体罚。同样明显的是，到了十九世纪，健全的穷人被日益隔离于济贫院，罪犯被关入监狱，疯子则被送进收容所。新的立法，尤其是 1834 年的《新济贫法》，旨在降低济贫救济的成本，强制要求尚未建立济贫院的教区必须建造。因此，随着资本主义的进一步发展和人口增长，其规范变得更为严苛，异常者因越来越多的人无法达到其新的功能标准而愈发凸显。正是这一点促使了这些新型监禁体系的大规模发展，它们各自以不同的方式囚禁了那些被视为异常的人。



As larger state institutions were built across Europe, the confinement and management of the mad spread to the colonies of the European empires, fusing with racist ideology to delineate new discourses. Writing from Britain, for instance, the influential psychiatrist Henry Maudsley – whom the Maudsley Hospital in South London was later named after – wrote of the ‘comparative inferiority’ of the brains of indigenous ‘bushwomen’,19 when compared to white Europeans. Building on this, in sub-Saharan Africa British psychiatrists soon began pontificating on the extent to which ‘normal’ Africans had similarities to insane Europeans, on the grounds that purported ‘superstition, primitive beliefs’ and ‘incapacity for abstract thought’ manifested in both populations.20

随着欧洲各地兴建起规模更大的国家机构，对疯人的监禁与管理也蔓延至欧洲帝国的殖民地，并与种族主义意识形态相融合，催生出新的话语体系。例如，在英国颇具影响力的精神病学家亨利·莫兹利（伦敦南部的莫兹利医院后来以其命名）曾撰文称，与欧洲白人相比，土著“丛林妇女”的大脑存在“相对低劣性”。 19 在此基础上，英国精神病学家很快在撒哈拉以南非洲地区开始宣扬“正常”非洲人与欧洲疯人之间的相似程度，理由是这两类人群都表现出所谓的“迷信、原始信仰”和“缺乏抽象思维能力”。 20



Within this context, it is around the mid-nineteenth century that we finally see the birth of psychiatry as a branch of medicine. This accompanied a more general shift in the purported function of asylums. When the asylums had first emerged, they were made primarily to provide a way to keep the mad away from the rest of society. But by around 1850 – just as Quetelet’s notion of the normal state was becoming increasingly influential in a range of scientific pursuits – the emphasis was moved to viewing inmates not as threats to be contained, but as patients to be treated, or returned to normality.

正是在这一背景下，大约在十九世纪中叶，我们终于看到精神病学作为医学的一个分支诞生了。这伴随着精神病院声称的功能发生了一个更普遍的转变。当精神病院最初出现时，它们主要是为了提供一种将疯子与社会其他人隔离开来的方式。但到了大约 1850 年——就在凯特莱的常态概念在一系列科学追求中变得越来越有影响力的时候——重点转移到了将住院者不再视为需要控制的威胁，而是视为需要治疗或恢复正常状态的病人。



This came partly from the influence of earlier liberal reformers. The most notable was the influential French physician Phillipe Pinel, who sought to turn the asylums into places of what he called ‘moral therapy’ rather than imprisonment and torture. More broadly, as Andrew Scull has detailed, it was partly the role of ‘mad doctors’ in the asylums that allowed a shift from ‘the vague cultural view of madness’ into the idea that it was an identifiable and treatable condition.21 And yet equally important, Scull goes on, was that industrial capitalism had led the labour pool to be increasingly seen as:

这在一定程度上源于早期自由主义改革者的影响。其中最著名的是极具影响力的法国医生菲利普·皮内尔，他试图将精神病院转变为所谓的"道德治疗"场所，而非监禁与酷刑之地。更广泛地说，正如安德鲁·斯卡尔所详述的，精神病院中"疯人医生"的角色部分促成了从"对疯癫的模糊文化观念"向将其视为可识别、可治疗病症的转变。 21 然而斯卡尔进一步指出，同样重要的是工业资本主义导致劳动力池日益被视为：





manipulable human material whose yield could be steadily enlarged through careful management and through improvements in use and organization, rationally designed to transform its value as an economic resource.22

可操控的人力材料——通过精心管理以及合理设计的运用与组织改进，其产出可被持续提升，从而转化为更具价值的经济资源。 22





The rise of capitalism – through its colonial roots and then imperial stages – thus finally brought the modern notion that the mad need to be treated, to ease their suffering and return the idle to the workforce. It was in this new context of viewing the population as a malleable economic resource that we see the emergence of new professional roles that paved the way for early pre-paradigmatic psychiatry and related disciplines such as psychology and psychometrics to emerge. And the new mechanistic understanding of the body and mind, coupled with new conceptions of normality, brought a new way of grounding these projects. As we will see in the next chapter, this would then be combined with the emerging statistical notions of normal functioning to ground not just the rise of eugenics but also the psychiatric paradigm that still exists today – the pathology paradigm.

资本主义的崛起——通过其殖民根源及随后的帝国主义阶段——最终带来了现代观念，即精神失常者需要接受治疗，以缓解其痛苦并使闲散者重返劳动力队伍。正是在这种将人口视为可塑经济资源的新背景下，我们看到了新专业角色的出现，为早期前范式精神病学及相关学科（如心理学和心理测量学）的诞生铺平了道路。对身体和心灵的新机械论理解，加上对正常性的新概念，为这些项目提供了新的基础。正如我们将在下一章中看到的，这将与新兴的正常功能统计概念相结合，不仅为优生学的兴起奠定了基础，也为至今仍存在的精神病学范式——病理学范式——奠定了基础。



NORMALITY AND CAPITALISM

正常性与资本主义



At this point I want to pause to summarise what we have covered so far. Traditionally – across the globe – both mental and bodily health were typically conceptualised as a matter of balance or equilibrium. This was either within the body or between body and environment. But the capitalist mode of production and the Industrial Revolution began to bring a new conception of health and ability. The body and mind were increasingly seen as machines, and the new concept of normality began to be used to determine whether these machines were working or broken. And far from being a merely technical medical concept, the idea of normality began to bring a profound shift in how different individuals and classes of people came to see themselves. It also came with new forms of administration of populations. This provided white, cognitively abled, middle-class people to justify the various hierarchies that had emerged given the rise of capitalism as well as colonialism and imperialism. It also allowed cognitively abled people to begin establishing a monopoly on property and the means of production. As such, the normality concept mirrored contingent social hierarchies while at the same time framing these hierarchies as natural.

在此，我想稍作停顿，总结一下我们目前所探讨的内容。传统上——在全球范围内——无论是精神健康还是身体健康，通常都被理解为一种平衡或均衡的状态。这种平衡要么存在于身体内部，要么存在于身体与环境之间。然而，资本主义的生产方式和工业革命开始带来一种关于健康和能力的全新观念。身体和心灵日益被视为机器，而“正常”这一新概念则被用来判断这些机器是运转良好还是出了故障。远非仅仅是一个技术性的医学概念，“正常”这一观念开始深刻地改变不同个体和社会阶层如何看待自身。它还伴随着对人口管理的新形式。这使得白人、认知能力健全的中产阶级能够为资本主义、殖民主义和帝国主义兴起所带来的各种等级制度提供正当性。同时，这也让认知能力健全的人开始确立对财产和生产资料的垄断。 因此，正常性概念既反映了偶然的社会等级制度，同时也将这些等级制度框定为自然存在。



Here, then, we see the beginning of what I call the Empire of Normality. This new apparatus, made up of a complex nexus of different carceral systems, legal precedents, institutions, concepts, and practices, led to populations beginning to be systematically ranked in terms of mental and neurological ability, while positing this as part of a timeless natural order. This was not an accident, but was rather built into the logics of capitalism from the beginning. And it was in this context, as we will come to next, that a British polymath named Francis Galton developed the pathology paradigm – the precise paradigm the neurodiversity movement would later arise to name and resist.

由此，我们看到了我称之为"正常性帝国"的雏形。这个由不同监禁体系、法律先例、制度、概念和实践构成的复杂网络所组成的新机制，开始系统性地依据心智与神经能力对人群进行分级排序，同时将其标榜为永恒自然秩序的一部分。这并非偶然，而是从一开始就内嵌于资本主义的逻辑之中。正是在这样的背景下——接下来我们将要探讨——一位名为弗朗西斯·高尔顿的英国博学者发展出了病理学范式，而这一范式正是后来神经多样性运动兴起时所要命名并抵抗的精确范式。



---

Empire of Normality



3



Galton’s paradigm

高尔顿的范式



Francis Galton was born in Birmingham in 1822 to a family of bankers and gun-manufacturers. The grandson of Erasmus Darwin and half-cousin of Charles Darwin, Galton himself was a rather strange child prodigy, learning to read by the age of two and quickly excelling in his education from that time. He went on to study medicine at King’s College London and mathematics at Cambridge, just around the time that Quetelet’s pathbreaking work was being widely discussed in both fields. After his father died, the young Galton’s vast inheritance allowed him to travel, invent, write, and, in time, become among the most influential scientists of his generation.

弗朗西斯·高尔顿于 1822 年出生于伯明翰一个银行家和枪支制造商的家庭。作为伊拉斯谟·达尔文的孙子和查尔斯·达尔文的表亲，高尔顿本人是一个相当奇特的神童，两岁时就学会了阅读，并从此在学业上迅速脱颖而出。他先后在伦敦国王学院学习医学，在剑桥大学学习数学，当时凯特莱的开创性工作在这两个领域都引起了广泛讨论。父亲去世后，年轻的高尔顿凭借巨额遗产得以四处游历、发明创造、著书立说，并最终成为他那一代最具影响力的科学家之一。



To understand Galton’s work, it is important to note that he soon became obsessed with genius – a term he identified with – as well as with ranking humans in every way imaginable. This dated at least back to when, as a young man, Galton was incredibly impressed by a phrenologist he visited. While we do not know precisely what he was told, it is safe to assume that, as a Victorian gentleman, he would have been considered close to the top of their imagined statistical order. In turn, Galton became equally obsessed with heredity, hypothesising while studying at Cambridge that the fact Cambridge was full of middle-class white men might indicate that this demographic was constitutionally superior to everyone else. In this, he saw the hierarchies of the British Empire not as contingent and based on specific historical factors, but rather as an expression of natural superiority that could be scientifically verified.

要理解高尔顿的研究，必须注意到他很快就痴迷于天才这一概念——他自认与之相符——以及用尽一切可想象的方式对人类进行排序。这种倾向至少可以追溯到他年轻时拜访一位颅相学家后深受震撼的经历。虽然我们无法确切知道他当时听到了什么，但可以合理推测，作为维多利亚时代的绅士，他很可能被认为接近他们想象中的统计等级顶端。相应地，高尔顿对遗传学也产生了同等程度的痴迷，在剑桥求学时曾提出假设：剑桥大学充满中产阶级白人男性的现象，可能表明这个群体在体质上优于其他所有人。在他看来，大英帝国的等级制度并非偶然或基于特定历史因素，而是自然优越性的体现，这一点可以通过科学方法加以验证。



It was in pursuing these obsessions that Galton would go on to become an influential statistician and to help found a variety of fields, including psychometrics, behavioural genetics, and the pseudo-science eugenics (the last of these being a term he coined). It is curious that, despite his influence being acknowledged elsewhere, Galton is barely mentioned in general histories of psychiatry, whether those written by mainstream psychiatrists or anti-psychiatry critics. Yet it is my contention that he was the founder of the pathology paradigm, in the sense that he provided both its metaphysical basis and developed many of the experimental methods that provided blueprints for later researchers. And it was this – Galton’s paradigm – that would then be taken up by Emil Kraepelin, often described as the ‘father’ of modern psychiatry, and other influential clinicians and researchers across the psychological sciences. This would form the basis of the approach that has remained dominant to this very day, and which functions to naturalise and scientifically legitimise the neuronormative domination of capitalism as it continues to develop.

正是在追求这些执念的过程中，高尔顿后来成为了一位有影响力的统计学家，并帮助创立了多个领域，包括心理测量学、行为遗传学以及伪科学优生学（最后一个术语是他创造的）。奇怪的是，尽管他的影响力在其他领域得到承认，但在精神病学的一般历史中，无论是主流精神病学家还是反精神病学批评家所写的，高尔顿都很少被提及。然而，我认为他是病理学范式的创始人，因为他既提供了其形而上学基础，又发展了许多实验方法，为后来的研究者提供了蓝图。正是高尔顿的这一范式后来被埃米尔·克雷佩林（常被称为现代精神病学的“之父”）以及其他在心理科学领域有影响力的临床医生和研究者所采纳。这构成了至今仍占主导地位的方法的基础，并且随着资本主义的不断发展，它起到了将神经规范性统治自然化和科学合法化的作用。



EVOLUTIONARY RANKING

进化等级



For our purposes, a key part of Galton’s contribution was to fuse his half-cousin’s ideas about natural selection, published in On the Origin of Species in 1859,1 with Quetelet’s statistical analysis of populations, this time, in his own words, applying the ‘same law to mental faculties’.2 By bringing these together Galton began a more formal and intentional project of scientific cultural normalisation that came to impact every corner of modern society.

就我们的目的而言，高尔顿贡献的关键部分在于，他将表亲达尔文关于自然选择的思想（发表于 1859 年的《物种起源》）与凯特莱的人口统计分析相结合，用他自己的话说，这次是将“同一法则应用于心智能力”。通过将这两者结合，高尔顿开启了一个更为正式且有意为之的科学文化规范化项目，这一项目最终影响了现代社会的每一个角落。



Looking back, it is hard to understate the significance of Darwin’s impact on how humans came to understand ourselves. People had known for millennia that traits seemed to be inherited to some extent, and Darwin’s contemporaries had proposed various theories to help explain this. Yet Darwin’s theory of evolution, which suggested that natural selection occurred through a combination of random mutations and fittingness to environment, was the first to have strong evidence and explanatory force. Darwin’s own painstakingly detailed observations and explanations forced a fundamental reconsidering of the human as not just a machine, but one who shared common ancestors with other primates. As such – and in comparison to Descartes’ attempt to preserve the sanctity of the soul – the Darwinian mind was no less a product of evolutionary design, and hence nature, than the rest of the body. Darwin essentially thus provided the human and biological sciences with new levels of respectability while opening up a host of new possible developments.

回顾过去，达尔文对人类如何理解自身的影响之重大，实在难以低估。数千年来，人们早已知道特征在某种程度上似乎是遗传的，而达尔文的同时代人也提出了各种理论来解释这一点。然而，达尔文的进化论——它提出自然选择是通过随机突变与适应环境的结合而发生的——是第一个拥有有力证据和解释力的理论。达尔文本人细致入微的观察和解释，迫使人们从根本上重新思考人类不仅仅是一台机器，而是与其他灵长类动物有着共同祖先的存在。因此——与笛卡尔试图维护灵魂神圣性的努力相比——达尔文式的心灵与身体的其他部分一样，同样是进化设计乃至自然的产物。因此，达尔文实质上为人类和生物科学提供了新的尊重度，同时开启了一系列新的可能发展。



In this context, Galton saw a viable ground to move beyond Quetelet’s reliance on pre-scientific notions of human ‘perfection’ and ‘monstrosity’. What Galton took from Darwin, more specifically, was the notion that variation is ubiquitous, and in turn that different organisms will have different fitness levels given their different natural abilities. Underlying this too was the Darwinian theory of evolution, which could explain variation among different human individuals and races. For Galton, this meant that each individual could be more or less fit when compared to others, and this could be framed as a matter of evolutionary functioning or adaptiveness.

在这一背景下，高尔顿看到了超越凯特勒依赖前科学概念如人类"完美"与"畸形"的可行基础。具体而言，高尔顿从达尔文那里汲取的核心观点是：变异无处不在，且不同生物因其先天能力差异而具有不同的适应度。其深层逻辑还植根于达尔文的进化论，该理论能够解释不同人类个体与种族间的差异。对高尔顿而言，这意味着每个个体相较于他人皆存在适应度的高低差异，这可以被理解为进化功能或适应性的问题。



While he had published some briefer articles earlier, his 1869 book Hereditary Genius is notable for combining Darwin’s theory with Quetelet’s statistical methods to analyse intelligence over different generations. Thus, Galton’s proposal, in his own words, was to:

尽管他早期已发表过若干短文，但其 1869 年著作《遗传的天才》因将达尔文理论与凯特勒的统计方法相结合，用以分析跨世代智力水平而备受瞩目。因此，用高尔顿自己的话来说，他的研究方案是：





range men according to their natural abilities, putting them into classes separated by equal degrees of merit […] The method I shall employ for discovering this is an application of the very curious theoretical law of ‘deviation from the average’.3

"依据人们的先天能力进行分级，将其划分至由同等价值区间区隔的类别中……我所采用的研究方法，正是对'偏离平均值'这一奇妙理论定律的实际应用。" 3





Galton’s initial attempt was based on comparing heredity across a range of records of individuals, family trees, and races and judging them in terms of ‘eminence’. This essentially led him to rank white, upper-class Europeans, and the Ancient Greeks, at the top and Black Africans and indigenous Australians at the bottom. Women – who, Galton thought, were unlikely to be geniuses – did not even appear in his rankings. Hence his book essentially functioned to naturalise the racialised, abled, economic, and gendered hierarchies of the British Empire.

高尔顿最初的尝试基于对个人记录、家族谱系和种族遗传性的比较，并以"卓越性"为标准进行评判。这实质上导致他将白人、欧洲上层阶级和古希腊人置于顶端，而将黑非洲人和澳大利亚原住民置于底端。女性——在高尔顿看来不太可能成为天才——甚至没有出现在他的排名中。因此，他的著作本质上起到了将大英帝国种族化、能力化、经济化和性别化的等级制度自然化的作用。



Hereditary Genius was initially met with mixed reviews. On the one hand, Galton’s work was supported by Darwin, who described it as ‘interesting and original’4 and Alfred Wallace who described it as ‘ingenious’.5 Yet many others recognised that Galton’s analysis relied on a great many biased assumptions regarding the extent of heredity, the validity of judgements of ‘eminence’, and influence of social class. One reviewer, for instance, noted that Galton ascribed eminence to ‘men of very average ability, helped forward by incidental advantages’ while overlooking circumstances and early education.6

《遗传的天才》最初获得的评价褒贬不一。一方面，高尔顿的研究得到了达尔文的支持，达尔文称其为"有趣且原创" 4 ，阿尔弗雷德·华莱士也认为其"巧妙" 5 。然而，许多其他人认识到，高尔顿的分析依赖于大量关于遗传程度、"卓越性"判断有效性以及社会阶级影响的偏见假设。例如，一位评论者指出，高尔顿将"能力平平、仅凭偶然优势获得成功的人"归为卓越，却忽视了环境和早期教育的影响 6 。



Such critiques, however, did not deter Galton. His inherited wealth allowed him to continue his work, and in the following decades he went on to develop a variety of early methods for psychometric and biometric testing. These ranged from the first intelligence tests to the first biometric technology. It was these that he used in his psychological laboratory in London – the first of its kind – where he could study and record individual abilities of huge numbers of people to generate statistical norms. From this laboratory Galton pioneered new methods including psychological questionnaires alongside developing a range of devices for testing abilities such as cognitive reaction times. This led to a new notion of individual ability that was cut off from environment and reified as having its own set value. As Danziger writes

然而，这些批评并未阻止高尔顿。他继承的财富使他得以继续工作，并在接下来的几十年里，他开发了多种早期的心理测量和生物计量测试方法。这些方法从最早的智力测试到最初的生物识别技术不一而足。正是在他位于伦敦的心理实验室——世界上第一个此类实验室——中，他运用这些方法来研究和记录大量人群的个人能力，以生成统计规范。从这个实验室出发，高尔顿开创了包括心理问卷在内的新方法，同时开发了一系列用于测试认知反应时间等能力的设备。这催生了一种新的个人能力观念，这种观念脱离了环境，被物化为具有其固定价值。正如丹齐格所写





What Galton’s testing situation produced was essentially a set of individual performances that could be compared with each other [that] defined characteristics of independent, socially isolated individuals and these characteristics were designated as ‘abilities’. An ability was what a person could do on his own, and the object of interest was either the individual defined as an assembly of such abilities or the distribution of performance abilities in a population.7

高尔顿的测试情境本质上产生了一套可以相互比较的个体表现，这些表现定义了独立、社会隔离个体的特征，而这些特征被指定为"能力"。能力即个人能够独立完成之事，研究关注的对象要么是被定义为这类能力集合的个体，要么是人群中表现能力的分布。 7





Like the phrenologists who influenced him, this thus allowed Galton to locate specific individual abilities that he would rank through statistical analysis. Moreover, he sought to map this onto inherited biological traits. His method of twin studies was proposed to distinguish between ‘nature and nurture’ – another enduring phrase Galton coined – that could be used to help see to what extent ability, character, or disposition was heritable.8 This, along with seminal work on the regression of the height of sweet peas over different generations,9 allowed Galton to found the field of behavioural genetics and to suggest that a species could ‘regress’ if not properly controlled.

正如影响他的颅相学家一样，这使得高尔顿能够定位特定的个体能力，并通过统计分析进行排序。此外，他试图将这些能力映射到可遗传的生物特征上。他提出的双胞胎研究方法旨在区分"先天与后天"——这是高尔顿创造的另一个经久不衰的短语——可用于帮助观察能力、性格或倾向在多大程度上是可遗传的。 8 这项工作，连同关于甜豌豆株高在不同世代间回归的开创性研究， 9 使高尔顿得以创立行为遗传学领域，并提出物种若不受适当控制就可能发生"退化"。
