与此同时，正如我们将在后续章节中看到的，随着基本福利支持的普及以及新型精神药物的出现，关闭最后一批精神病院在经济上变得更加可行，无论可获得的社区支持或替代机构是否足以维持生存。事实上，这在 1973 年之后对各国政府尤其具有吸引力——当时资本主义周期性危机之一引发了严重的经济衰退和大规模失业。因此，诚然，随着 1960 年代末至 1970 年代反文化运动的兴起，反精神病学的批判确实使公众舆论不仅反对精神病院，也反对精神疾病这一概念本身。但在很大程度上，精神病院被逐一关闭，伴随着让患者回归社区的论调，其根本目的是削减成本。而萨斯对精神疾病真实性的怀疑，恰好为这一做法提供了正当性辩护。



SZASZ AND THE PATHOLOGY PARADIGM

萨斯与病理学范式



It should be noted here that the relationship between asylum closure, homelessness, and imprisonment is not quite as simple as it may seem. As Liat Ben-Moshe23 has convincingly argued, both homelessness and prison also generate mental illness rather than just being places where mentally ill people end up. She also notes that abolition for people with intellectual disability, which was led by different, non-Szaszian advocates, was more successful, with many more former inmates successfully returning to communities. Given this, for Ben-Moshe, we should beware of any discourse that makes it out as if the only options for people experiencing mental illness are either incarceration or homelessness. This is important, she stresses, so we can recognise that the problem was not the abolition of the state asylums as such.

这里需要指出的是，收容所关闭、无家可归与监禁之间的关系，并不像表面看起来那么简单。正如莉亚特·本-莫舍 23 所有力论证的，无家可归和监狱本身也会催生精神疾病，而不仅仅是精神疾病患者的最终归宿。她还指出，由不同的、非萨兹主义倡导者领导的针对智力障碍者的废除收容所运动更为成功，有更多的前收容者成功回归社区。鉴于此，本-莫舍认为，我们应警惕任何将监禁或无家可归描述为精神疾病患者唯一出路的言论。她强调，认识到这一点很重要，这样我们才能明白，问题本身并不在于废除公立收容所这一举措。



Yet the fact remains that the most dominant form of Anglo-American anti-psychiatry – stemming from the work of Szasz – was misguided, and its politics failed to liberate its subjects. To understand the flaws in the anti-psychiatry analysis, it is helpful to consider the Marxist psychologist Peter Sedgwick, who was anti-psychiatry’s most insightful critic at the time. For Sedgwick, a big part of the issue was that Szasz’s arguments were driven by and reproduced his hard-right libertarian politics. As Sedgwick pointed out, Szasz’s worldview was hyper-individualistic. For him, every individual had complete responsibility and freedom, and he believed the state should leave people to make their own decisions in every aspect of life. Szasz himself was quite open that this view had been a consistent driver of his work from the beginning, and he even wrote letters to the ‘father’ of neoliberalism, the economist Friedrich Hayek. In their correspondence he proudly identified as Hayek’s ‘disciple’ and emphasised how his critique of psychiatry was influenced by his Hayekian worldview.24

然而事实是，英美反精神病学运动中最具影响力的流派——源于萨斯的思想——存在方向性错误，其政治主张未能真正解放其关注的对象。要理解反精神病学分析的缺陷，不妨参考马克思主义心理学家彼得·塞奇威克的见解，他是当时对该运动最具洞见的批评者。塞奇威克指出，问题的关键在于萨斯的论点始终受其极端右翼自由意志主义政治立场的驱使与复制。在塞奇威克看来，萨斯的世界观充斥着极端个人主义色彩：他认为每个个体都拥有绝对的责任与自由，主张国家应在生活各个领域放任人们自主抉择。萨斯本人曾公开承认，这一观点自始至终驱动着他的学术工作，他甚至致信新自由主义"教父"、经济学家弗里德里希·哈耶克，在往来信件中自豪地自称哈耶克的"门徒"，并强调其精神病学批判如何深受哈耶克式世界观的影响。 24



In particular, this world view underpinned Szasz’s belief that people self-identified as ‘mentally ill’ mainly to take on a ‘sick role’ that allowed them to avoid taking personal responsibility for dealing with their problems in living. Liberal capitalists had long been worried about so-called ‘malingerers’ – people pretending to be ill to avoid responsibility – and the Hayekian philosophy perhaps entrenched this even further, as it centred the individual beyond all else. Essentially, then, Szasz saw patients as morally weak liars, pretending to be ill, rather than unwell people in need of medical assistance. For Szasz, the ‘myth’ of mental illness was as much a myth made and sustained by patients as it was made by psychiatrists. As he wrote in his 2008 book Psychiatry: Science of Lies, ‘So-called mentally ill persons’ all in fact ‘pretend to be disabled by illnesses that do not exist’.25

特别是，这种世界观支撑了萨斯的一个信念：人们自我认定为“精神疾病”患者，主要是为了扮演“病人角色”，从而避免为应对生活中的问题承担个人责任。自由派资本家长期以来一直担心所谓的“装病者”——即假装生病以逃避责任的人——而哈耶克哲学或许进一步固化了这种观念，因为它将个体置于一切之上。因此，本质上，萨斯将患者视为道德上软弱的说谎者，假装生病，而非需要医疗帮助的真正患病者。对萨斯而言，“精神疾病”这一“神话”既是精神病学家制造和维持的，同样也是患者制造和维持的。正如他在 2008 年的著作《精神病学：谎言的科学》中所写：“所谓的‘精神疾病患者’，实际上都在‘假装被不存在的疾病所困扰’。”



While many patients who were wrongly pathologised found Szasz’s analysis useful, then, the ultimate implication of accepting it was not only that state support and psychiatric diagnosis should be abolished, even for those who found them helpful. It was also that claiming to be mentally unwell was really a form of lying, to oneself and others, in order to avoid responsibility for dealing with life’s problems. More concretely, if someone commits a crime in a state of psychosis, and if the crime followed from their actions, they should be punished by community or state no less than someone who committed the same crime in a cold and calculating manner. It was not, then, an accident that Szasz’s arguments implied that the insanity defence was invalid. Rather, it was his concerns relating to individual responsibility that drove his theorising about mental illness.

尽管许多被错误病理化的患者发现萨斯分析很有用，但接受其分析的最终含义不仅是应废除国家支持和精神病学诊断——即使对那些认为这些有帮助的人也是如此。它还意味着声称自己精神不适实际上是一种对自己和他人撒谎的形式，以避免承担处理生活问题的责任。更具体地说，如果有人在精神病状态下犯罪，并且犯罪是由其行为导致的，那么他们应受到社区或国家的惩罚，其程度不应低于以冷静和算计的方式犯下同样罪行的人。因此，萨斯的论点暗示精神失常辩护无效并非偶然。相反，正是他对个人责任的关切推动了他关于精神疾病的理论化。



In this the Szaszian project would seek to go back to a pre-medical, and much more conservative, world view, where what we now call mental illness would be understood in the moral rather than medical sphere. From the Szaszian perspective, then, the shift from asylum to prison incarceration was a desired outcome, not an unfortunate side-effect. In other ways, his politics also anticipated the neoliberalism that would begin being imposed from around 1979. After all, according to Hayek modern shifts towards collectivism from the left had become soft and thus, in his own words, the virtues of ‘independence, self-reliance, and the willingness to bear risks’ were now ‘less esteemed and practiced’.26 It was, arguably, not just Hayekian neoliberalism but also such a narrative of moral decline that Szasz took up in suggesting that modern people were worse at dealing with life. It was this that allowed him to see all mental health patients as malingerers who had developed a new concept – that of mental illness – to avoid having to take responsibility for their behaviours. And part of why this was so widely attractive is that it fits with a broader form of capitalist individualism that would culminate in the global adoption of Hayek’s politics in the 1980s.

在这一萨兹式计划中，人们试图回归一种前医学的、更为保守的世界观，将我们现在所称的精神疾病置于道德而非医学领域来理解。因此，从萨兹的视角来看，从精神病院转向监狱监禁是一种期望的结果，而非不幸的副作用。在其他方面，他的政治观点也预见了自 1979 年左右开始推行的新自由主义。毕竟，根据哈耶克的观点，现代从左翼兴起的集体主义转向已变得软弱，因此用他自己的话说，“独立、自立和承担风险的意愿”这些美德如今“不再那么受推崇和实践”。 26 可以说，萨兹不仅采纳了哈耶克式的新自由主义，还采纳了这种道德衰退的叙事，暗示现代人在应对生活方面变得更糟。正是这一点使他将所有心理健康患者视为装病者，这些人发明了一个新概念——即精神疾病——来逃避对自己行为的责任。 其吸引力如此广泛的部分原因在于，它契合了一种更广泛的资本主义个人主义形式，这种形式最终在 20 世纪 80 年代促成了哈耶克政治理念在全球范围内的采纳。



Alongside this, Sedgwick also noted that Szasz and many other anti-psychiatrists relied on a depoliticising and reified notion of bodily normality in order to make their claim that psychiatry was comparatively unscientific. Szasz, most clearly, built his argument based on the assumption that bodily medicine dealt with objective abnormalities of the body, as if bodily normality were a timeless fact, which he then compared to a comparatively ‘mythical’ mental illness. Yet Sedgwick contended that conceptions of bodily illness were also no less value-laden than those of mental illness – a claim that is well supported by what we have covered in this book already in the previous chapters. It is not just that many bodily conceptions of normality are also contested – for instance, the use of Quetelet’s Body Mass Index to determine the so-called normal weight – it is also that the very idea of bodily normality, and the specific standards now used, are the product of specific social and material conditions. They are and remain intimately intertwined with racist, patriarchal, and capitalist logics. The Szaszian view, by contrast, precisely needs to downplay the ideological nature of bodily conceptions of normality, in order to be able to posit that conceptions of mental illness are so unlike those used in general medicine.

与此同时，塞奇威克还指出，萨斯和许多其他反精神病学家依赖一种去政治化且物化的身体正常性概念，以主张精神病学相对而言不够科学。最明显的是，萨斯基于一个假设构建了他的论点，即身体医学处理的是身体的客观异常，仿佛身体正常性是一个永恒的事实，然后他将此与相对"神话般"的精神疾病进行比较。然而，塞奇威克认为，身体疾病的概念同样不亚于精神疾病的概念那样充满价值判断——这一主张得到了我们在本书前几章已经涵盖的内容的有力支持。不仅许多关于身体正常性的概念存在争议——例如，使用凯特勒的身体质量指数来确定所谓的正常体重——而且身体正常性这一概念本身，以及现在使用的具体标准，都是特定社会和物质条件的产物。它们过去和现在都与种族主义、父权制和资本主义逻辑紧密交织在一起。 相比之下，萨兹派的观点恰恰需要淡化身体正常性概念的意识形态本质，以便能够断言精神疾病的概念与普通医学中所使用的概念截然不同。



In this regard, Sedgwick also critiqued what he called ‘psychomedico dualism’ underlying the Szaszian analysis. Szasz’s position was essentially Cartesianism taken to its extreme and applied to the understanding of mental health. For the precise combination of a wholly mechanistic understanding of the body as a working or broken machine, with a sharp dualism to preserve the sanctity of the mind, is unambiguously reminiscent of the distinction we have seen Descartes make in his Meditations over three centuries earlier. And just as with Descartes’ own work, Szasz’s contained both the same conceptual problems while also turning out to be incredibly useful for capital. This time, though, it was not the industrialists and slave owners of the old European empires, but the neoliberal politicians of the late twentieth century, who would find it so helpful. By the 1980s, it had become clear to critics such as Sedgwick that Szaszianism was mostly convenient for framing unwell people as work-shy malingerers, and thus for justifying cuts to services and welfare.

在这方面，塞奇威克还批判了萨兹分析背后所谓的"心理医学二元论"。萨兹的立场本质上是将笛卡尔主义推向极致，并应用于对心理健康的理解。因为将身体完全机械地理解为运转或故障的机器，同时通过尖锐的二元论来维护心灵的神圣性，这种精确组合明确让人联想到三个多世纪前笛卡尔在《沉思录》中所做的区分。正如笛卡尔本人的著作一样，萨兹的理论既存在相同的概念问题，同时也被证明对资本极其有用。不过这一次，发现它如此有用的不再是旧欧洲帝国的工业家和奴隶主，而是二十世纪末的新自由主义政客。到了 1980 年代，塞奇威克等批评者已清楚地看到，萨兹主义主要便于将患病者塑造成逃避工作的装病者，从而为削减服务和福利提供正当理由。



Finally, the basis of Szasz’s view is that the correct functioning of the mechanistic body is precisely normal functioning. For him, health was equated with the functional and structural normality of the body. As he took this to simply be an objective and natural normative standard, he fully bought into the underlying logics of the pathology paradigm. He might superficially look like he challenged it, because he proposed that mental illness was not real illness. But this is really just the most sharply dualistic manifestation of the pathology paradigm, rather than an alternative to it.

最后，萨兹观点的根基在于，机械身体的正确运作恰恰就是正常运作。对他而言，健康等同于身体功能与结构的正常。由于他将此简单地视为一种客观且自然的规范性标准，他完全接受了病理学范式的底层逻辑。他表面上看似挑战了这一范式，因为他提出精神疾病并非真正的疾病。但这实际上只是病理学范式最尖锐的二元对立表现，而非其替代方案。



Overall then – despite many anti-psychiatrists bringing important insights into how psychiatry functioned as a form of social control – the most influential anti-psychiatry analyses missed the target. Many of the anti-psychiatrists believed that the ‘myth’ of mental illness and psychiatric ‘labels’ were the core problems. They were what Marx called idealists, taking the power of psychiatric control to come from belief in the ideas of psychiatry. And so they thought that denying the reality of mental illness, reducing mental illnesses to mere ‘labels’, and closing the asylums would liberate patients. But in fact, as a materialist analysis shows, conceptions of mental illness and psychiatric diagnoses were not where the power guiding this social control lay. Rather, the ways these institutions and practices often harmed people were only specific manifestations of the broader neuronormative logics of the capitalist system. Because of this, capital was able to use anti-psychiatry’s denial of the reality of mental illness and suspicion of psychiatric diagnosis to shift the mad and disabled from one form of social control to others. These were often no less bad and were sometimes worse.

总而言之——尽管许多反精神病学运动者深刻揭示了精神病学如何作为一种社会控制形式运作——但最具影响力的反精神病学分析却偏离了靶心。许多反精神病学倡导者认为，"精神疾病"的"神话"和精神病学的"标签"才是核心问题。他们属于马克思所称的唯心主义者，认为精神病学控制的力量源于人们对精神病学理念的信仰。因此他们相信，否认精神疾病的现实、将精神疾病简化为单纯的"标签"并关闭精神病院，就能解放患者。但事实上，唯物主义的分析表明，精神疾病的概念和精神病学诊断并非这种社会控制力量的根源。相反，这些机构和实践常常伤害人们的方式，只是资本主义体系更广泛的神经规范性逻辑的具体表现。正因如此，资本得以利用反精神病学对精神疾病现实的否认和对精神病学诊断的怀疑，将疯癫者与残障者从一种社会控制形式转移到其他形式。这些新形式往往同样糟糕，有时甚至更为恶劣。



Part of what the anti-psychiatry movement shows us, looking back, is perhaps that capital requires us to recognise mental illness just enough to maintain a surplus class, but not enough for it to be forced to grant recognition and sufficient support where it is costly. And the debate between psychiatrists and anti-psychiatrists, which led to a false dichotomy between seeing mental illnesses as apolitical diseases or mere myths, helped maintain this equilibrium rather than challenging it. Thus, despite the mass energy harnessed by the anti-psychiatry movement, most of those to be locked away never really escaped, while many of those who wanted help never received it. And so capitalism and the pathology paradigm were able to continue their development relatively unhindered.

回顾反精神病学运动，它向我们揭示的一部分或许是：资本需要我们承认精神疾病，但仅止于维持一个剩余阶级的程度，而不愿在代价高昂时被迫给予充分的认可与支持。精神病学家与反精神病学家之间的辩论，将精神疾病视为非政治性疾病或纯粹神话的虚假二分法，反而助长了这种平衡的维持，而非挑战它。因此，尽管反精神病学运动汇聚了巨大的能量，大多数本应被禁锢的人从未真正逃脱，而许多寻求帮助的人也从未得到援助。于是，资本主义与病理学范式得以相对无阻地继续发展。



---

Empire of Normality



6



Fordist normalisation

福特主义的正常化



Anti-psychiatry brought two contributions. First, a seminal analysis of psychiatric social control that helped resist certain manifestations of psychiatric oppression. Second, it brought new grounds for a cultural denial of mental illness that helped provide the state with a way to save money by closing the asylums while shifting former inmates to other carceral systems. This has since had a significant and lasting impact on the politics of mental health, as will be explored in more detail below. But to understand what really happened in this period, and to see more clearly why closing the asylums did not lead to liberation for the mad and disabled, we again need to turn to the ongoing development of capitalism. After all, more general shifts in broader material conditions and technologies that were underway while Szasz was still in training were already paving the way for new neuronormative practices to take hold. This would allow an alternative field, clinical psychology, to develop new methods and techniques for care and control that purported to be more effective than anything the Freudians had to offer.

反精神病学带来了两大贡献。首先，它开创性地分析了精神病学的社会控制功能，这有助于抵制精神病学压迫的某些表现形式。其次，它为文化上否认精神疾病提供了新的依据，这有助于国家通过关闭精神病院、将前住院患者转移到其他监禁系统来节省开支。自此，这对心理健康政治产生了重大而持久的影响，下文将对此进行更详细的探讨。但要理解这一时期真正发生了什么，并更清楚地看到为什么关闭精神病院并未给疯癫者和残障者带来解放，我们仍需再次转向资本主义的持续发展。毕竟，在萨斯仍在接受培训期间，更广泛的物质条件和技术正在发生更普遍的转变，这些转变已经为新的神经元规范性实践站稳脚跟铺平了道路。这将使得另一个领域——临床心理学——得以发展出新的护理与控制方法和技术，这些方法和技术声称比弗洛伊德学派所能提供的任何方法都更有效。



Two economic factors following the Second World War are of particular importance. The first is the rise of the welfare capitalism championed by the economist Keynes, who we have already mentioned considering his role in the Eugenics Society. The second is the rise of the Fordist economic model, and with it the development of new Fordist technologies of care and control that could be used beyond the walls of the asylum. As we shall see, these broader economic shifts would bring not just new forms of intervention, but also new technologies and a tightening of neuronormativity in relation to the developing needs of capital. This would lead to a much greater portion of the population coming to be considered abnormal, far more than could be housed in state-funded asylums. They would instead be subject to new forms of intervention that extended far beyond the locked doors of the increasingly obsolete state hospitals. This would now start from the earliest years of life, and would increasingly expand through school, the workplace, and, finally, in the minds and behaviours of the population at large.

第二次世界大战后的两个经济因素尤为重要。首先是经济学家凯恩斯倡导的福利资本主义的兴起，我们之前提到过他，考虑到他在优生学会中的作用。其次是福特主义经济模式的兴起，随之而来的是新的福特主义护理和控制技术的发展，这些技术可以在精神病院之外使用。正如我们将看到的，这些更广泛的经济转变不仅带来了新的干预形式，还带来了新技术，以及神经元规范性随着资本发展需求的收紧。这将导致更大比例的人口被视为异常，远远超过国家资助的精神病院所能容纳的数量。相反，他们将受到新的干预形式的影响，这些干预形式远远超出了日益过时的国家医院紧闭的大门。现在，这种干预将从生命的最初几年开始，并逐渐扩展到学校、工作场所，最终扩展到广大民众的思想和行为中。



FORDISM

福特主义



To understand this, we need to go back to the 1910s and 1920s, when Henry Ford, an industrialist based in Detroit, had pioneered a new economic model. Born in 1863 in Michigan to a family of farmers, Ford gained a reputation as a watch repairer in his teenage years before moving to Detroit to become an apprentice machinist and then engineer while he experimented with gasoline engines in his spare time. By 1901, he was able to start his own company, the Ford Motor Company, where he would manage not just great feats of engineering but also a new model of manufacturing.

要理解这一点，我们需要回溯到 1910 至 1920 年代，当时底特律的实业家亨利·福特开创了一种新的经济模式。福特于 1863 年出生在密歇根州的一个农民家庭，少年时期就以修表技艺闻名，后来移居底特律成为一名机械学徒，继而成为工程师，并在业余时间尝试研究汽油发动机。到 1901 年，他得以创立自己的公司——福特汽车公司，在那里他不仅实现了工程上的伟大成就，还开创了一种新的制造模式。



Ford invented the assembly line, thus developing what came to be known as assembly line manufacturing. However, this work was too harrowing and alienating for workers to stay long in the job without good pay. Ford was thus forced to offer high wages and good welfare to retain the best employees. He then used these employees to mass produce standardised goods that could be sold at low prices and in large numbers. Simultaneously, he also established a monopoly in advertising in Detroit publications before doing the same nationally. This led to his Ford cars becoming the standard across the United States. This economic model went against the conventional wisdom of the capitalists of the time, who generally paid the lowest wages possible. It also went against the logic of the automobile industry, which had produced cars as luxury products to sell in small numbers at high prices.

福特发明了装配线，从而发展出了后来被称为流水线制造的生产方式。然而，这种工作对工人来说过于折磨和疏离，没有高薪很难留住他们长期工作。因此，福特被迫提供高工资和优厚福利以留住最优秀的员工。他随后利用这些员工大规模生产标准化商品，这些商品可以低价大量销售。同时，他还在底特律的出版物上建立了广告垄断，随后在全国范围内也采取了同样的策略。这使得他的福特汽车成为全美的标准车型。这种经济模式违背了当时资本家的普遍观念，他们通常支付尽可能低的工资。它也违背了汽车行业的逻辑，该行业一直将汽车作为奢侈品生产，以高价少量销售。



Yet Ford’s model turned out to be incredibly successful, making him exceptionally rich and leading to the widespread use of cars as the primary form of transport in the United States. His model was so successful, in fact, that it led to ushering in the new form of assembly line manufacturing and mass marketing that would quickly become the dominant model. It was emulated not just across the United States but far beyond. Even in Nazi Germany, for instance, after hearing about Ford’s success, Hitler personally demanded that Volkswagen find a way to mass produce affordable cars on a Fordist model. It was this that led to the development of the Volkswagen Beetle, which turned out to be even cheaper, and in time, better selling than any of Ford’s cars long after Hitler and Nazi Germany had been consigned to history. Similar innovations were quickly developed elsewhere, leading to a new form of work and the furthering of scientific work management for hard, monotonous jobs.

然而，福特的模式最终取得了惊人的成功，使他变得异常富有，并导致汽车作为主要交通工具在美国广泛使用。事实上，他的模式如此成功，以至于引领了新的装配线制造和大规模营销形式，这些形式迅速成为主导模式。不仅在美国，而且在更远的地方，人们都在效仿这一模式。例如，即使在纳粹德国，希特勒在听说福特的成功后，亲自要求大众汽车公司找到一种方法，按照福特主义模式大规模生产价格实惠的汽车。正是这一点导致了大众甲壳虫的发展，这种车型最终比福特的任何汽车都更便宜，并且在希特勒和纳粹德国被历史淘汰后，销量也超过了福特的汽车。类似的创新很快在其他地方发展起来，导致了一种新的工作形式，并为艰苦、单调的工作进一步推进了科学工作管理。



The ascent of Fordism took place alongside the adoption of Keynesian economics in the United States and the United Kingdom following the Second World War. While he was certainly no Marxist, Keynes nonetheless held that a healthy economy required not cutting and saving, but, rather, stimulating more demand and more spending. In a time where capitalist governments and policymakers were worried about communist sympathies, this approach was seen as a good way to appease the working classes and fend off the spread of communism. Keynes was a key designer of the Bretton Woods conference of 1944 where dozens of governments met to agree on a new post-war exchange system. This essentially pegged the value of gold to the US dollar, helping solidify US supremacy, and it also led to the founding of the International Monetary Fund and the World Bank. Keynesian thinking thus guided the post-Second World War trading system across much of the capitalist world.

福特主义的兴起与第二次世界大战后美国和英国采纳凯恩斯经济学同步发生。尽管凯恩斯绝非马克思主义者，但他认为健康的经济需要的不是削减和储蓄，而是刺激更多需求和支出。在资本主义政府和政策制定者担忧共产主义同情心的时代，这种方法被视为安抚工人阶级、抵御共产主义传播的有效途径。凯恩斯是 1944 年布雷顿森林会议的关键设计者，数十国政府在此会议上商定了新的战后汇率体系。该体系实质上将黄金价值与美元挂钩，有助于巩固美国的霸权地位，并促成了国际货币基金组织和世界银行的成立。因此，凯恩斯思想指导了二战后资本主义世界大部分地区的贸易体系。



In turn, during the 1950s and 1960s Keynesian government investment at the state level alongside the ascent of Fordism brought a great economic boom. States were spending more and so were workers, and a great many people could afford new goods that were previously reserved only for the wealthy. In this period, many ordinary people had high-paid jobs and were thus able to achieve a quality of life that would have been barely imaginable by their parents or grandparents. At the same time, welfare, in terms of government benefits, healthcare, and so forth, even increased for those who couldn’t work. The fusing of Fordist and Keynesian approaches thus brought about the so-called ‘Golden Age’ of capitalism, including modern welfare systems, education, and services.

相应地，在 20 世纪 50 年代和 60 年代，凯恩斯主义在州一级的政府投资与福特主义的兴起共同促成了巨大的经济繁荣。政府支出增加，工人的消费也随之增长，许多人得以负担起过去只有富人才能享有的新商品。这一时期，许多普通人获得了高薪工作，从而实现了他们的父母或祖辈几乎无法想象的生活质量。同时，对于那些无法工作的人来说，政府福利、医疗保健等方面的福利甚至有所增加。因此，福特主义与凯恩斯主义的结合催生了所谓的资本主义“黄金时代”，包括现代福利体系、教育和服务。



While this improved the lives of many, it also brought a new form of alienation relating to the capitalist manufacturing of ‘normal’ desires for consumers alongside restricted norms for employment and work. The production of false needs had already been observed by Karl Marx who had written as far back as 1857 that, to the capitalist, the ‘total mass of all workers’ appeared as potential consumers, and thus that capitalists constantly needed to search ‘for means to spur’ consumers ‘on to consumption’.1 While this had already begun in Marx’s time, the capacity for capital to manufacture desire grew significantly in the twentieth century, while the pressure to do so rose with the need to sell their wares to ever-growing numbers of consumers. After all, on the Fordist model, it no longer was the point to sell luxuries to the rich but rather to sell standardised products to the masses. This would increasingly bring the normative demands of capital out of the workplace and into individual and collective psyches.

尽管这改善了许多人的生活，却也带来了一种新的异化形式，即资本主义在为消费者制造“正常”欲望的同时，也限定了就业和工作的规范。虚假需求的产生早已被卡尔·马克思所察觉，他在 1857 年就写道，对资本家而言，“所有工人的整体”被视为潜在的消费者，因此资本家需要不断寻找“刺激”消费者进行消费的手段。 1 尽管这在马克思的时代已初现端倪，但资本制造欲望的能力在二十世纪显著增强，同时随着需要向日益增长的消费者销售商品，这种压力也随之上升。毕竟，在福特主义模式下，重点不再是向富人销售奢侈品，而是向大众销售标准化产品。这将日益将资本的规范性要求从工作场所延伸至个体和集体的心理层面。



It was Freud’s cousin Edward Bernays who most forcefully defended the adoption of these methods by governments in liberal democracies to control the desires of their populations. Building on his earlier explanation and defence of propaganda, in 1947 he published an essay titled ‘The Engineering of Consent’ in the Annals of the American Academy of Political and Social Science. Here Bernays clarified how, in his own words, ‘the engineer of consent must create news. News is not an inanimate thing. It is the overt act that makes news, and news in turn shapes the attitudes and actions of people’.2 By this time, Bernays himself had been incredibly successful at manufacturing false needs, being most well known at the time for having used such methods to help tobacco companies convince women to take up smoking in much greater numbers in a 1929 advertising campaign. But now he defended the method not just for the marketing of goods, but for the control of the populations by the state.

正是弗洛伊德的表弟爱德华·伯奈斯最有力地主张自由民主国家政府应采用这些方法来控制民众的欲望。基于他早期对宣传的解释和辩护，1947 年他在《美国政治与社会科学院年鉴》上发表了一篇题为《共识工程》的文章。伯奈斯在此阐明，用他自己的话说，“共识工程师必须制造新闻。新闻不是无生命之物。正是公开的行为制造了新闻，而新闻反过来塑造人们的态度和行动”。 2 到那时，伯奈斯本人在制造虚假需求方面已取得惊人成功，当时最为人所知的是他在 1929 年的一次广告活动中运用此类方法，帮助烟草公司说服更多女性开始吸烟。但如今，他不仅为商品营销辩护这种方法，还为国家控制民众辩护。



From a more critical perspective, the rise of such methods was examined in real time by the Frankfurt School critical theorists Max Horkheimer and Theodor Adorno in their 1946 book Dialectic of Enlightenment. As Jewish intellectuals on the left, they had fled the Nazis and emigrated to the United States in the 1940s. Yet when they arrived, they found themselves increasingly horrified at what they saw as a mass restriction on free thought that made the United States little freer than Nazi Germany. Among other factors, they argued that the mass production of false needs and desires had increased following the rise of mass media and public relations alongside standardised products. For instance, the invention of the radio, they wrote, made ‘everyone equally into listeners, in order to expose them in authoritarian fashion to the same programs put out by different stations’. This brought, they went on, ‘a cycle of manipulation and retroactive need’ to unify ‘the system ever-more tightly’.3 While the idealised average consumer did not actually exist, each person did sit closer or further to this ideal, or was thus more or less prone to adopting those desires demanded by the profit margins of new giant companies that utilised variants of the Fordist model.

从更具批判性的视角来看，法兰克福学派批判理论家马克斯·霍克海默和西奥多·阿多诺在 1946 年的著作《启蒙辩证法》中实时审视了此类方法的兴起。作为左翼犹太知识分子，他们逃离纳粹统治，于 1940 年代移民美国。然而抵达后，他们却惊恐地发现，美国对自由思想的大规模限制使其与纳粹德国相比并无更多自由。除其他因素外，他们认为，随着大众媒体、公共关系与标准化产品的兴起，虚假需求和欲望的大规模生产日益加剧。例如他们写道，收音机的发明"将所有人平等地转化为听众，以便以专制方式让他们接受不同电台播出的相同节目"。这进而带来了"操纵与追溯性需求的循环"，使"系统愈发紧密地统一起来"。 3 虽然理想化的普通消费者并不真实存在，但每个人都或多或少地接近这一理想。或者说，因此或多或少更容易接受那些由采用福特制变体模式的新兴巨头公司根据利润率所要求的欲望。



It was also this that Herbert Marcuse, one of the leading figures of the New Left, examined in his 1964 book One-Dimensional Man. For Marcuse the mass production of Fordist goods alongside new marketing techniques had brought a new form of alienation that had not been present in earlier phases of capitalism. In his own words, while ‘choice among a wide variety of goods and services’ was presented as evidence of capitalism’s deliverance of freedom to the masses, this in fact did not ‘signify freedom if these goods and services sustain social controls over a life of toil and fear – that is, if they sustain alienation’.4 In fact, for Marcuse, the monotony of Fordist work alongside the false promise of its consumerism led to psychological repression of a mass scale, unseen at any previous point in history. For him, at that time, society itself was making people psychologically unwell due to the tightness of the psychic dominance of capital and its demand for what he called ‘surplus repression’ of desires.

这也正是新左派领军人物赫伯特·马尔库塞在其 1964 年出版的《单向度的人》一书中所探讨的内容。在马尔库塞看来，福特制商品的大规模生产与新型营销技巧相结合，带来了一种资本主义早期阶段未曾出现的新型异化形式。用他自己的话说，虽然"在琳琅满目的商品和服务中进行选择"被呈现为资本主义赋予大众自由的证据，但事实上，如果这些商品和服务"维持着对劳苦恐惧生活的社会控制——即维持着异化状态"，那么这种选择就"不意味着自由"。 4 实际上，马尔库塞认为，福特制工作的单调性与其消费主义虚假承诺相结合，导致了史无前例的大规模心理压抑。在他看来，当时社会本身正使人们在心理上陷入病态，这源于资本对心理领域的严密掌控，以及资本对他所称的欲望"额外压抑"的要求。



Simultaneously, as Harry Braverman explored in his 1974 book Labour and Monopoly Capital, a range of government reports in the United States and the United Kingdom from the time found that workers were becoming increasingly unsatisfied with work, were taking more sick days, and thus production levels were decreasing. On Braverman’s analysis, the ever-increasing division of labour led to a deskilling among workers that made their jobs increasingly unfulfilling and alienating, even when compensated by better pay and increased access to new commodities. Unable to take pride in their monotonous work, people tended to feel unfulfilled despite access to a greater number of possessions than their parents and grandparents had had.

与此同时，正如哈里·布雷弗曼在其 1974 年著作《劳动与垄断资本》中所探讨的那样，当时美国和英国的一系列政府报告发现，工人对工作越来越不满意，请病假的天数增多，从而导致生产水平下降。根据布雷弗曼的分析，日益细化的分工导致工人技能退化，使得他们的工作越来越缺乏成就感和疏离感，即使有更高的薪酬和更多新商品的补偿。由于无法从单调的工作中获得自豪感，尽管拥有的财产比父母和祖父母更多，人们仍倾向于感到不满足。



Thus, while the Golden Age of capitalism did improve the lives of many people – at least those living in wealthy, Western nations – in important ways, it also hindered their thriving in other ways. During a mass drive to push each person towards an idealised norm of desires in the post-war years, many of those who adopted these new desires often felt increasingly unfulfilled and alienated despite increased consumption – and those who fell outside were increasingly stigmatised and othered. In short, neuronormativity became more restricted, changing psychological expectations in relation to the needs not of humanity, but of capital itself.

因此，尽管资本主义的黄金时代确实在许多重要方面改善了许多人的生活——至少是那些生活在富裕西方国家的人们——但它也在其他方面阻碍了他们的蓬勃发展。在战后年代，一场大规模的运动推动每个人走向理想化的欲望规范，许多采纳这些新欲望的人尽管消费增加，却常常感到越来越不满足和疏离——而那些未能达到这一标准的人则日益被污名化和边缘化。简而言之，神经规范性变得更加严格，改变了心理期望，这些期望不再关乎人类的需求，而是关乎资本本身的需求。



BEHAVIOURIST NORMALISATION

行为主义的规范化



In retrospect, we might add to Marcuse’s analysis that, by contrast, those whose minds had further proximity from fitting with this new consumer normativity – increasingly became deemed problems to be fixed. We see the combined effects of these government and commercial efforts most clearly in the rise of child psychiatry and psychology, which had barely existed before the 1940s. As Nadesan writes, during the early twentieth century, the expanding ‘interest in childhood “development” led to’ new divisions of children based on ‘their degree of apparent normality in relation to newly created and standardised developmental norms’.5 This mirrored the rise of standardised schooling – which was expanded following the Second World War – not to mention Galtonian ideas about different kinds of innate intelligence. In this context, differences in development in comparison to one’s age group became increasingly salient, and new notions of developmental ‘milestones’ brought more restricted standards of developmental normality.

回顾过去，我们或许可以在马尔库塞的分析基础上补充一点：相比之下，那些思维与这种新的消费规范相距甚远的人——逐渐被视为需要被纠正的问题。我们可以在儿童精神病学和心理学的兴起中，最清晰地看到这些政府和商业努力的共同影响，而这两个领域在 20 世纪 40 年代之前几乎不存在。正如纳迪森所写，在 20 世纪早期，对儿童“发展”日益增长的兴趣导致了基于“他们相对于新创建和标准化的发展规范的明显正常程度”对儿童进行新的划分。 5 这反映了标准化教育的兴起——二战后得到扩展——更不用说高尔顿关于不同类型先天智力的观念。在这种背景下，与同龄人相比的发展差异变得越来越突出，而关于发展“里程碑”的新概念带来了更为严格的发展正常标准。



But one reason the shift to Fordism is particularly important is that alongside restricting neuronormativity, it also brought new Fordist methods of care and control. Following the critique from anti-psychiatry, while costly psychoanalytic approaches, and the more barbaric treatments such as lobotomy, became less popular, new more economically efficient and lucrative therapeutic approaches were increasingly adopted and developed. In an important sense these would allow psychiatry and psychology to extend their reach far beyond the walls of the asylums, and into a much greater part of public and private life. Among the most important of these was behaviourism. This would be developed by psychologists, giving them increased clinical and societal influence that would in time come to match that of the psychiatrists of the asylums.

然而，福特主义转型之所以尤为关键，一个原因在于它不仅限制了神经规范性，还引入了新的福特式照护与控制方法。随着反精神病学批判的兴起，尽管昂贵的精神分析疗法以及更为野蛮的治疗方式（如脑叶切除术）逐渐失宠，但新的、经济上更高效且利润丰厚的治疗方法却日益被采纳和发展。从重要意义上讲，这些方法将使精神病学和心理学的影响力远远超出精神病院的围墙，渗透到公共和私人生活的更广泛领域。其中最为重要的便是行为主义。这一理论由心理学家发展起来，使他们逐渐获得了与精神病院的精神病医生相匹敌的临床和社会影响力。



Pioneered by the psychologist John Watson, born in South Carolina in 1848, American behaviourism sought to overcome the divide between the mind and body that dated back at least to the work of Descartes, who had proposed a dualism between the soul and the mechanistic body. While the Cartesian tradition had left the mind unobservable and thus hard to study scientifically, by the 1910s Watson proposed the revolutionary idea that psychological science should focus only on what could be objectively observed: behaviour. By attending to behaviour alone he sought not only to provide psychology with new levels of respectability, but also to revolutionise the way psychologists carried out clinical work.

美国行为主义由心理学家约翰·沃森开创，他于 1848 年出生于南卡罗来纳州，旨在克服至少可追溯至笛卡尔工作的身心二元论。笛卡尔曾提出灵魂与机械身体之间的二元对立，而笛卡尔传统使得心灵无法被观察，因而难以进行科学研究。到了 1910 年代，沃森提出了革命性的观点，认为心理科学应仅关注可被客观观察的对象：行为。通过专注于行为本身，他不仅试图为心理学赢得新的尊重，还旨在彻底改变心理学家进行临床工作的方式。



When it came to clinical intervention, Watson was inspired by the research of the Russian psychologist Ivan Pavlov. In the 1890s, Pavlov had found that dogs began salivating whenever they heard the footsteps of research assistants who routinely brought them their food.6 Because of this, Pavlov had suggested that dogs could develop a ‘conditioned’ response, whereby they learned to react in a certain way to familiar stimuli based on past experiences. It was this that Watson believed could be applied to understanding and treating humans. In time, he came to believe that our behaviours such as speech, emotional responses, and so forth were simply the combination of our innate tendencies combined with repeated exposure to stimuli that then conditioned typical responses. As we will return to later, having been the first Russian Nobel laureate in 1904, Pavlov was praised by Lenin himself following the Russian revolution. As we will return to later, this combined with a new form of what Lenin called ‘state capitalism’ in Soviet Russia, which paralleled the rise of behaviourism in market capitalist societies.

在临床干预方面，沃森受到了俄罗斯心理学家伊万·巴甫洛夫研究的启发。19 世纪 90 年代，巴甫洛夫发现，每当听到定期给它们送食物的研究助理的脚步声时，狗就会开始流口水。 6 因此，巴甫洛夫提出，狗可以形成一种“条件性”反应，即它们学会根据过去的经验对熟悉的刺激做出某种反应。沃森认为，这可以应用于理解和治疗人类。随着时间的推移，他开始相信，我们的行为，如言语、情绪反应等，只不过是我们天生的倾向与反复接触刺激后形成的典型反应相结合的结果。正如我们稍后将再次提到的，巴甫洛夫在 1904 年成为首位俄罗斯诺贝尔奖得主，并在俄国革命后受到列宁本人的赞扬。正如我们稍后将再次提到的，这与列宁在苏维埃俄国所称的“国家资本主义”新形式相结合，与市场资本主义社会中行为主义的兴起相呼应。



In the West, Watson’s theoretical work was incredibly influential, being championed by philosophers such as Bertrand Russell as well as inspiring psychologists and sociologists dissatisfied with Cartesianism. But it was his proposal that he could change behaviours through operant conditioning that had by far the greatest impact. In his influential 1924 book, simply titled Behaviourism, he wrote:

在西方，华生的理论工作极具影响力，不仅得到伯特兰·罗素等哲学家的推崇，也激励了那些对笛卡尔主义不满的心理学家和社会学家。然而，他提出的通过操作性条件反射改变行为的观点，其影响最为深远。在他 1924 年出版的影响深远的著作《行为主义》中，他写道：





Give me a dozen healthy infants, well-formed, and my own specified world to bring them up in and I’ll guarantee to take any one at random and train him to become any type of specialist I might select – doctor, lawyer, artist, merchant-chief and, yes, even beggar-man and thief, regardless of his talents, penchants, tendencies, abilities, vocations and the race of his ancestors.7

给我一打健康、发育良好的婴儿，让我在我设定的特定世界里养育他们，我保证可以随机挑选任何一个，把他训练成我选定的任何类型的专家——医生、律师、艺术家、商人首领，是的，甚至乞丐和小偷，不论他的天赋、爱好、倾向、能力、职业以及他祖先的种族如何。 7





In other words, Watson suggested that, regardless of heredity, he could mould infants to become certain kinds of people, or even to fit specific job roles. The potential of behaviourism thus lay in its promise to be able to mould individuals in line with the needs of the society and economy.

换句话说，沃森认为，无论遗传因素如何，他都能塑造婴儿成为特定类型的人，甚至适应特定的工作岗位。因此，行为主义的潜力在于其承诺能够根据社会和经济需求来塑造个体。



Influenced by Watson, a massive shift towards increasingly ambitious behaviourist research programmes soon began. By the 1930s, the Harvard psychologist B. F. Skinner began using behaviourist principles to mimic evolutionary selection pressures to change behaviours, including in those deemed mentally ill. Skinner’s approach, as detailed in his 1938 book The Behavior of Organisms, used punishments or rewards as ‘reinforcers’ to make people better fit current societal requirements.8 This grounded what he thought of as ‘behavioural engineering’, which could, he proposed, be used on a mass scale to produce desirable citizens. Indeed, a whole ‘culture’, he wrote in his later book Beyond Freedom and Dignity, ‘is very much like the experimental space used in the analysis of behaviour. Both are sets of contingencies of reinforcement’. Given this, Skinner went on, designing ‘a culture is like designing an experiment’.9 By the same token, he claimed, improving a culture can be achieved through ‘piecemeal’ operant conditioning of its people to fit the needs of society at large.

受华生影响，一场大规模转向日益雄心勃勃的行为主义研究计划的浪潮很快兴起。到了 20 世纪 30 年代，哈佛大学心理学家 B.F.斯金纳开始运用行为主义原理，模仿进化选择压力来改变行为，包括那些被视为精神疾病患者的行为。斯金纳的方法，正如他在 1938 年出版的《有机体的行为》一书中详细阐述的那样，使用惩罚或奖励作为“强化物”，使人们更好地适应当前的社会要求。 8 这奠定了他所谓的“行为工程学”的基础，他提出，这种行为工程学可以大规模应用，以培养理想的公民。事实上，他在后来的著作《超越自由与尊严》中写道，整个“文化”非常类似于行为分析中使用的实验空间。两者都是一系列强化条件的集合。因此，斯金纳继续写道，设计“一种文化就像设计一个实验”。 9 同样地，他声称，改善一种文化可以通过对其人民进行“渐进式”的操作性条件反射来实现，以适应整个社会的需求。



This was important because it meant that Darwinists and policy makers, deprived of widespread support for Galtonian eugenics, now saw a new method for normalising populations. But this time it sought to mimic evolutionary pressures in childhood development rather than through control of hereditary traits across generations. In this context, as Harvard historian Rebecca Lemov has detailed,10 large American philanthropic organisations such as the Rockefeller Foundation, which had previously funded Nazi eugenics, began lavishly funding new behaviouralist research. Most notably, this included the work of Elton Mayo, who sought to ‘adapt industrial workers to their tasks by deradicalizing them through psychological counselling’.11 This would formalise and update the kinds of scientific management that had been pioneered on slave plantations to manage the psyches of modern workers. Over this period, as Lemov writes, while the staff and trustees of such foundations ‘had no dire or secret plan to rest democratic freedom-of-action or freedom-of-thought from average Americans’, they nonetheless ‘believed that the outside imposition of policies and of normality itself was necessary for the smooth functioning of any social system’.12 As such, they saw investment in new forms of behavioural control as vital for the functioning and survival of American democracy itself.

这一点至关重要，因为它意味着达尔文主义者和政策制定者在失去对高尔顿优生学的广泛支持后，看到了一个使人口正常化的新方法。但这一次，它试图通过模仿童年发展中的进化压力，而不是通过控制跨代遗传特征来实现。正如哈佛历史学家丽贝卡·莱莫夫所详述的那样，在这种情况下，像洛克菲勒基金会这样曾资助纳粹优生学的大型美国慈善组织开始大量资助新的行为主义研究。最引人注目的是，这包括埃尔顿·梅奥的工作，他试图通过心理辅导“去激进化”，使产业工人适应他们的任务。这将使那些最初在奴隶种植园开创的科学管理方式正式化并更新，以管理现代工人的心理。 在此期间，正如莱莫夫所写，尽管这些基金会的员工和受托人“并没有剥夺普通美国人民主行动自由或思想自由的险恶或秘密计划”，但他们仍然“相信，任何社会系统的平稳运行都需要外部强加政策以及常态本身”。 12 因此，他们认为投资于新形式的行为控制对于美国民主本身的运行和生存至关重要。



Newer combinations of Freudianism and behaviourism became particularly influential during the Cold War, which began in 1945, as capitalist governments worried about how to stop people from sympathising with the other side. In the United States, for instance, Members of the Central Intelligence Agency were deeply concerned by reports that Maoist communists in the Far East had developed techniques of ‘brainwashing’ to make people support their cause. This had first been reported by the anti-communist journalist Edward Hunter in a 1950 article in Miami News, which had the terrifying headline: ‘Brain Washing Tactics Force Chinese into Ranks of the Communist Party’.13 While there was little substance to Hunter’s reports, the United States – terrified of communism spreading – soon began investing heavily in research into the uses of behaviourism, seeking to reverse engineer the so-called brainwashing techniques of the communists. Their basic idea, as Lemov writes, was to ‘quantify and control the internal arena of the personal self – its urges and wants, its worries and fears’ so governments could ‘regulate human beings in tune with the needs, demands, desires, and models of the social order’.14 In other words, the CIA and American government hoped that the techniques they believed were being used to increase sympathy for revolutionary communism could be co-opted and adapted to support the victory of capitalism. And the techniques they believed were being used were precisely the methods that had been developed by the behaviourists.

弗洛伊德主义与行为主义的新结合在 1945 年开启的冷战期间变得尤为盛行，当时资本主义政府担忧如何阻止民众同情对立阵营。例如在美国，中央情报局成员对远东地区毛泽东主义共产主义者研发出"洗脑"技术以争取民众支持的报道深感忧虑。这一说法最早由反共记者爱德华·亨特在 1950 年《迈阿密新闻》的文章中提出，其骇人标题为《洗脑策略迫使中国人加入共产党行列》。 13 尽管亨特的报道缺乏实质依据，但对共产主义蔓延深感恐惧的美国很快开始大量投资行为主义应用研究，试图逆向解析所谓共产主义者的洗脑技术。 正如莱莫夫所写，他们的基本理念是“量化并控制个人自我的内在领域——其冲动与欲望、忧虑与恐惧”，以便政府能够“根据社会秩序的需求、要求、欲望和模式来调节人类”。 14 换句话说，中央情报局和美国政府希望，那些他们认为被用来增强对革命共产主义同情的技巧，可以被吸纳并改造，以支持资本主义的胜利。而他们认为正在被使用的技巧，正是行为主义者所开发的方法。



Simultaneously, especially since the Fordist period was defined by stable manufacturing and technical jobs, the role of behaviourism was increasingly seen to consist in how children might be shaped to fit one economic role they would keep for life. Importantly, it was not just psychologists who believed in such uses, but also industrialists including Henry Ford II, the grandson of Henry Ford I and the president and CEO of Ford Motor Company from the mid-1940s. As the sociologist and critic of behaviourism Daniel Bell observed in 1947,

与此同时，尤其是在福特主义时期以稳定的制造业和技术工作为特征的背景下，行为主义的作用越来越被视为如何塑造儿童以适应他们将终身从事的经济角色。重要的是，不仅仅是心理学家相信这种用途，还包括实业家，如亨利·福特一世的孙子、自 20 世纪 40 年代中期起担任福特汽车公司总裁兼首席执行官的亨利·福特二世。正如社会学家和行为主义批评家丹尼尔·贝尔在 1947 年所观察到的，





The Ford Motor Company announced a short while ago that it was setting aside $500,000 for research into ‘human relations’. The company, Henry Ford II said, felt that it could go no further in the direction of technological rationalization of machines, and that the next step in engineering would have to be the raising of the level of ‘human achievement’.15

福特汽车公司不久前宣布，将拨出 50 万美元用于"人际关系"研究。亨利·福特二世表示，公司认为在机器技术合理化方面已无法更进一步，工程领域的下一步必须提升"人类成就"的水平。 15





Indeed, beyond the factories, Skinner even proposed that mass implementation of behaviourist principles could solve what he saw as the ‘serious’ issues of young people being reluctant to join the armed forces or of them wanting to work ‘as little as possible’.16

事实上，在工厂之外，斯金纳甚至提出，大规模实施行为主义原则可以解决他所认为的"严重"问题——年轻人不愿参军或希望"尽可能少工作"。 16



This approach was built on how psychotherapeutic models had been used in the post-war Child Guidance Movement, which was led by eugenicists such as Cyril Burt, who we mentioned in Chapter 4. Proponents of the Child Guidance Movement had posited ‘a spectrum of normalcy and the point at which any child might be located’17 and had framed the childhood mind as uniquely susceptible to intervention that would aid workplace adjustment later in life. While this was initially built on more Galtonian assumptions, by the 1960s, such efforts had blended with the philosophy of the behaviourists, and thus behaviourism had started being used to enforce conformity for children who were considered pathologically subnormal.

这种方法建立在战后儿童指导运动中运用的心理治疗模式之上，该运动由优生学家如西里尔·伯特领导（我们在第四章中提到过他）。儿童指导运动的支持者提出了“一个正常性的谱系以及每个孩子可能位于其中的位置” 17 ，并将儿童心智描述为特别容易受到干预，这种干预有助于他们日后适应工作环境。虽然最初这更多是基于高尔顿式的假设，但到了 20 世纪 60 年代，这些努力与行为主义哲学相结合，因此行为主义开始被用来强制那些被认为在病理上低于正常标准的孩子遵守规范。



Perhaps the most notable example of this is the method of Applied Behaviour Analysis, developed by Ivar Lovaas at the University of California in the 1960s. Lovaas agreed with Szasz that the concept of mental illness mainly functioned to help people evade responsibility. Instead of trying to heal people from ‘illness’, he thus instead sought to discipline them for what he saw as abnormal behaviours. His method used a harsh punishment and reward system to normalise ‘abnormal’ children. Autistic children were punished by Lovaas and his team through electric shocks or slaps every time they behaved in ways that seemed to reflect abnormal desires. As Life Magazine reported in a widely-read profile on Lovaas in 1965, the idea was to use operant conditioning on autistic children to ‘push the child toward normality’.18 Lovaas then used the same technique in the 1970s on boys considered too ‘feminine’, who were presumed to have ‘homosexual’ tendencies.19 This was essentially a form of conversion therapy, which was initially thought to be successful but in fact led to long-term trauma.

其中最引人注目的例子或许是应用行为分析法，该方法由加州大学的伊瓦尔·洛瓦斯于 20 世纪 60 年代创立。洛瓦斯赞同萨斯关于精神疾病概念主要功能是帮助人们逃避责任的观点。因此，他并未试图"治愈"人们的"疾病"，而是针对其眼中的异常行为进行规训。该方法通过严苛的惩罚与奖励机制来"矫正"异常儿童。每当孤独谱系儿童表现出反映异常欲望的行为时，洛瓦斯团队就会实施电击或掌掴作为惩罚。正如《生活》杂志在 1965 年那篇广为流传的洛瓦斯专题报道所言，其核心理念是通过操作性条件反射"将儿童推向正常状态"。 18 洛瓦斯在 1970 年代将相同技术应用于被认为过于"女性化"的男孩身上，这些男孩被假定具有"同性恋"倾向。 19 这实质上是一种转化治疗形式，初期被认为卓有成效，实则造成了长期创伤。



Throughout this period, then, new norms of childhood reflected a broader shift derived both from the perceived capacity to work as well as the perceived ability to exhibit the correct desires and behaviours as consumers. Normality is restricted even further in relation to the shifting needs of capital, alongside other intersecting pressures from gender norms and heteronormativity. Thus in the post-war decades, it was not just that new forms of production brought new career prospects for aspirational workers: it was also that the production of normal children itself became a goal for aspirational and worried parents.

在此期间，儿童的新规范反映了一种更广泛的转变，这种转变既源于人们感知到的工作能力，也源于作为消费者展现正确欲望和行为的能力。随着资本需求的不断变化，以及性别规范和异性恋规范等其他交叉压力的影响，正常性的定义被进一步限制。因此，在战后的几十年里，不仅是新的生产形式为有抱负的工人带来了新的职业前景，而且培养正常的孩子本身也成为有抱负且忧心忡忡的父母的目标。



It is true that this development did certainly have its critics at the time. According to Bell, for instance, the new approaches pioneered by the likes of Elton Mayo, ‘adjusted men to machines’ in ways that ‘introduced without any consideration of their ultimate and far-reaching effects’ to humanity. But despite these critics, it was from this basis that behaviourism would go on to increasingly be embraced in a wide range of other areas, for instance in business to increase employee performance or in fitness industries to build desired eating and exercise habits, for instance, to push people towards Quetelet’s notion of the ideal weight. It would also increasingly come to be combined with cognitive and psychoanalytic approaches to provide new targeted forms of intervention. This was much as the likes of Watson and Skinner had envisioned and would equally be in line with Kraepelin’s notion of a ‘mass psychiatry’ he had proposed back in 1908.

诚然，这一发展在当时确实遭到了批评。例如，根据贝尔的说法，像埃尔顿·梅奥等人开创的新方法，以"不考虑其最终和深远影响"的方式"将人调整到机器上"。但尽管有这些批评，行为主义正是基于这一基础，在众多其他领域被越来越广泛地接受，例如在商业中用于提高员工绩效，或在健身行业中用于建立理想的饮食和运动习惯，例如推动人们达到凯特莱的理想体重概念。它也越来越与认知和精神分析方法相结合，提供新的有针对性的干预形式。这与沃森和斯金纳等人所设想的非常相似，也符合克雷佩林早在 1908 年提出的"大众精神病学"概念。



FORDIST PHARMACEUTICALS

福特主义制药



When it came to therapeutic intervention, an equally relevant major product of the Fordist era was the discovery and mass production of psychopharmacological drugs. This began in the 1950s and rapidly expanded in ways that radically changed how depression, anxiety, and psychosis were understood. As Robert Whitaker summarises, during this period:

在治疗干预方面，福特主义时代同样重要的一个主要成果是精神药理药物的发现和大规模生产。这始于 20 世纪 50 年代，并迅速扩展，从根本上改变了人们对抑郁症、焦虑症和精神病的理解方式。正如罗伯特·惠特克所总结的，在这一时期：





Thorazine, Miltown, and Marsilid were all derived from compounds that had been developed for other purposes – for use in surgery or as possible ‘magic bullets’ against infectious diseases. Those compounds were then found to cause alterations in mood, behavior, and thinking that were seen as helpful to psychiatric patients. The drugs, in essence, were perceived as having beneficial side effects. [Seeing a new opportunity] psychiatry then reconceived the drugs as ‘magic bullets’ for mental disorders, the drugs hypothesized to be antidotes to chemical imbalances in the brain.20

氯丙嗪、眠尔通和异烟酰异丙肟都是从为其他目的开发的化合物中衍生出来的——用于外科手术或作为对抗传染病的可能“神奇子弹”。随后发现这些化合物会引起情绪、行为和思维的变化，这些变化被认为对精神病患者有帮助。本质上，这些药物被认为具有有益的副作用。[看到新的机会]精神病学随后将这些药物重新构想为精神障碍的“神奇子弹”，假设这些药物是大脑化学失衡的解药。 20





In fact, studies of the drugs only evidenced limited efficacy and did not sufficiently document potential risks. Neither was there any evidence of a chemical imbalance underlying clinical depression or anxiety. Nonetheless, the drugs were easy to mass produce, and enough people found them useful for them to catch on. Indeed, anecdotally, many found and still find them literally lifesaving.

事实上，针对这些药物的研究仅显示出有限的疗效，且未能充分记录潜在风险。同时，也没有任何证据表明临床抑郁症或焦虑症存在化学失衡的基础。尽管如此，这些药物易于大规模生产，并且有足够多的人发现它们有用，从而使其流行起来。确实，根据轶事证据，许多人过去和现在都认为这些药物确实能救命。



These new drugs were thus mass marketed to make increasingly huge profits for pharmaceutical companies and to provide support for struggling people. By 1954, 2 million Americans were taking chlorpromazine alone.21 Following this, the numbers of psychiatric medications increased year after year, leading to a significant change in how depression and melancholy were understood. No longer were they reactions to traumatic events primarily treatable by expensive, personalised talking therapy; rather, they stemmed more from so-called ‘chemical imbalances’ – a vague term that allowed a great variety of interpretations, including for those marketing them – treatable by new standardised pharmaceuticals.

因此，这些新药被大规模推向市场，为制药公司带来了日益巨大的利润，并为困境中的人们提供了支持。到 1954 年，仅氯丙嗪就有 200 万美国人在服用。 21 此后，精神科药物的数量逐年增加，导致人们对抑郁和忧郁的理解发生了重大变化。它们不再被视为对创伤事件的反应，主要依靠昂贵、个性化的谈话疗法治疗；相反，它们更多地源于所谓的“化学失衡”——这是一个模糊的术语，允许各种解释，包括那些营销它们的人——可以通过新的标准化药物来治疗。



It should again be stressed that for some these new interventions were helpful, especially those who found the new drugs helped them manage psychosis, depression, or anxiety. Thus, in some instances, in the post-war decades, psychiatric and psychological interventions helped people suffering from mental health problems. But for many others, new forms of Fordist intervention brought new forms of social control. After all, the new drugs were mass-produced standardised products, and were not adapted to the specific needs, problems, and contexts of any individual’s life. If the meds didn’t work, patients would often be prescribed a heavier dose or a second medication, despite the increased risk of side effects and, in many cases, limited efficacy of this intervention. Because human neurodiversity and complexity were not accounted for by the logics of this approach, it could be experienced as a form of control in some cases even while it was experienced as vital care in others.

必须再次强调，对某些人而言，这些新型干预措施确实有所帮助，尤其是那些发现新药物能帮助自己控制精神病、抑郁或焦虑症状的人。因此，在战后的数十年间，精神病学和心理学干预在某些情况下确实帮助了受心理健康问题困扰的人们。但对许多其他人来说，福特主义式的新型干预手段带来了新的社会控制形式。毕竟，这些新药是批量生产的标准化产品，并未针对任何个体生活的具体需求、问题及背景进行调整。如果药物无效，患者往往会被开具更大剂量或第二种药物，尽管这会增加副作用风险，且在许多情况下此类干预的疗效有限。由于这种方法论的逻辑未能考量人类的神经多样性与复杂性，它在某些情况下可能被体验为一种控制形式，而在另一些情境中却被视为至关重要的关怀。



This further helps us understand the limitations of not just biomedical psychiatry, but also the anti-psychiatry movement of the 1960s. As we saw in the previous chapter, while the asylums closed, new forms of normalisation expanded out into the community or shunted them towards the prison system or nursing homes. But as we have seen, just as importantly, for others still, they were controlled beyond the walls of any carceral system, by new Fordist technologies of normalisation. Thus, in the majority of cases, closing the asylums and ending psychoanalytic hegemony would not have liberated the mad or mentally ill as the anti-psychiatrists had hoped even if they had not been put in alternative carceral systems instead.

这进一步帮助我们理解，不仅生物医学精神病学存在局限，20 世纪 60 年代的反精神病学运动同样如此。正如前一章所见，尽管精神病院关闭了，新的规范化形式却扩展至社区，或将患者推向监狱系统或养老院。但同样重要的是，正如我们所看到的，对于其他人而言，他们被新型福特主义规范化技术所控制，这种控制超越了任何监禁系统的围墙。因此，在大多数情况下，关闭精神病院和结束精神分析霸权，即使没有将患者置于替代性的监禁系统中，也无法如反精神病学家所希望的那样解放疯子或精神病患者。



For in the Fordist period, society itself became both a laboratory and asylum for new behavioural and psychopharmacological interventions. And as the Freudian psychiatrists lost influence, the power vacuum left by them was filled by the new behaviourist psychologists intervening in childhood development right from the beginning of life, through education, and then in the workplace. For those who were harmed by this, the walls that trapped them were not made of brick and mortar but were psycho-technological, imposed by the increasingly strict behavioural reinforcers used by governments, psychologists, and public relations professionals. The anti-psychiatrists were, then, right that psychiatry often functioned as a form of social control. But in viewing the problem as relating to belief in the reality of mental illness, and in the abuses specific to the psychiatric asylums, it had missed the target. These were not in fact the core problems, but just one of the ways in which underlying problems often manifest. The true issue was not the mere concept of mental illness, but rather how increasingly restrictive conceptions of normality were produced and reproduced in line with shifting material conditions and relations. Despite the huge energy of the anti-psychiatry movement, capitalism was thus nonetheless able to continue its growth, and tighten its neuronormative grip, relatively undisturbed. It was in this context that Galtonian psychiatry would come to be reborn anew.

因为在福特主义时期，社会本身变成了新行为和心理药理学干预的实验室与收容所。随着弗洛伊德学派的精神科医生失去影响力，他们留下的权力真空被新的行为主义心理学家填补，这些心理学家从生命之初就通过教育干预儿童发展，随后又介入工作场所。对于那些因此受到伤害的人来说，困住他们的围墙并非砖石所筑，而是心理技术性的，由政府、心理学家和公共关系专家使用的日益严格的行为强化手段所强加。反精神病学运动认为精神病学常常充当社会控制的一种形式，这一点是正确的。然而，将问题归结为对精神疾病真实性的信仰，以及精神病院特有的滥用行为，却未能切中要害。这些实际上并非核心问题，而只是潜在问题常常显现的方式之一。 真正的问题并非仅仅是精神疾病这一概念，而是关于日益严苛的常态观念如何随着物质条件和关系的变迁而被不断塑造与复制。尽管反精神病学运动声势浩大，资本主义却依然能够相对不受干扰地持续扩张，并强化其神经规范性掌控。正是在这样的背景下，高尔顿式精神病学将迎来新生。



---

Empire of Normality



7



The return of Galtonian psychiatry

高尔顿式精神病学的回归



On a hot day in mid-July of 1990, United States President George H. W. Bush proclaimed the beginning of the ‘Decade of the Brain’. For Bush, a ‘new era of discovery’ was dawning, whereby, in his words, ‘Powerful microscopes, major strides in the study of genetics, and advances in brain imaging devices are giving physicians and scientists ever greater insight into the brain’. He went on to triumphantly espouse the merits of American psychiatry and neuroscience, before ending with a call for ‘all public officials and the people of the United States to observe that decade with appropriate programs, ceremonies, and activities’.1

1990 年 7 月中旬一个炎热的日子里，美国总统乔治·H·W·布什宣布“脑的十年”正式开启。对布什而言，一个“探索的新纪元”正在破晓，用他的话来说，“强大的显微镜、遗传学研究的重大进展以及脑成像设备的进步，正让医生和科学家对大脑有了前所未有的深刻洞察”。他接着热情洋溢地颂扬美国精神病学和神经科学的成就，最后呼吁“所有公职人员和美国人民通过适当的项目、仪式和活动来纪念这十年”。 1



This moment did not come out of nowhere. To understand it, we need to turn back to consider one final major impact of the anti-psychiatry movement. This concerns the very concept of mental illness, which towards the end of the 1970s sharply shifted away from Freudian models and back towards biocentric models. This had in part been a response to critiques from anti-psychiatry critics. But a related crisis arose from what was then called ‘homosexuality’. The pathologisation of queerness had initially been proposed long before, by the German psychiatrist Richard von Krafft-Ebing in his 1886 book Psychopathia Sexualis, which drew on Darwin to frame homosexuality as a form of psychopathology. Because reproduction was associated with fitness, same-sex attraction was seen as an impediment to natural functioning. Given the increasingly homophobic culture of the early twentieth century, and despite Freud himself seeing ‘homosexuality’ as non-pathological, this framing caught on.

这一时刻并非凭空而来。要理解它，我们需要回溯审视反精神病学运动的最后一个重大影响。这关乎精神疾病这一概念本身——在 1970 年代末期，它急剧地偏离了弗洛伊德模式，重新回归生物中心模型。这一转变部分是对反精神病学批评者质疑的回应。但另一场相关危机则源于当时所谓的“同性恋”问题。对酷儿群体的病理化早在更早时期就已提出：德国精神病学家理查德·冯·克拉夫特-埃宾在其 1886 年著作《性精神病态》中，借鉴达尔文理论将同性恋框定为一种精神病理形态。由于繁殖能力与适应度相关联，同性吸引被视为自然功能的障碍。鉴于二十世纪初日益恐同的文化氛围，尽管弗洛伊德本人认为“同性恋”不具有病理性，这种病理化框架仍得以广泛传播。



At the same time, the American government had increasingly been collecting statistics on people with psychiatric conditions, to help with the social administration of populations. This programme had massively grown during the Second World War, when many military personnel were deeply traumatised only to be given overly vague and general diagnoses, while the government worried about malingerers. Early manuals developed by the US military to provide greater precision eventually were developed into the American Psychiatric Association’s diagnostic bible, the Diagnostic and Statistical Manual of Mental Disorders or DSM, the first edition of which was published in 1952. While it only had limited impact in its first edition, its influence would increasingly grow over its many subsequent editions, and in time it would become one of the most influential books ever published.

与此同时，美国政府日益加强对精神疾病患者的统计工作，以协助人口的社会管理。这一项目在第二次世界大战期间大规模扩展，当时许多军人深受创伤，却仅被给予过于模糊笼统的诊断，而政府则担忧有人装病逃避。美国军方早期为提供更精确诊断而制定的手册，最终演变为美国精神病学协会的诊断圣经——《精神障碍诊断与统计手册》（DSM），其第一版于 1952 年出版。尽管初版影响有限，但在后续多个版本的修订中，其影响力与日俱增，最终成为有史以来最具影响力的著作之一。



In the DSM-I, which was influenced by the Freudian as well as biological approaches, ‘homosexuality’ came to be listed as a ‘sociopathic personality disturbance’.2 It was similarly included in the DSM-II, published in 1967, as a ‘sexual deviation’, around the same time Ivor Lovaas was developing his behaviourist conversion therapy already mentioned.3 Throughout this period, gays and lesbians were increasingly subjected to invasive and harmful therapies that sought to change their behaviours or psychological makeup. Within the logics of Fordist-era capitalism, queerness and other breakings of traditional gender roles were threats to the need for the social reproduction of workers in heteronormative families. In this context, queer people were not just discriminated against and wrongly pathologised, but incarcerated and tortured merely for having romantic attraction or sexual relations.

在受弗洛伊德学派及生物学方法影响的《精神疾病诊断与统计手册》第一版中，“同性恋”被列为“社会病态人格障碍”。 2 1967 年出版的《精神疾病诊断与统计手册》第二版同样将其归为“性欲倒错”，大约在同一时期，伊瓦尔·洛瓦斯正在发展前文提及的行为主义转化疗法。 3 在此期间，同性恋者日益遭受侵入性且有害的治疗，这些疗法试图改变他们的行为或心理构成。在福特主义时代资本主义的逻辑中，酷儿及其他对传统性别角色的突破，威胁到异性恋规范家庭中工人社会再生产的需要。在此背景下，酷儿群体不仅遭受歧视和错误的病理化，更仅因拥有浪漫吸引或性关系而被监禁和折磨。



By the early 1970s, however, many on the left as well as libertarian Szaszians had finally had enough of how queer people were represented and treated. Gay liberation activists were also angry and organised enough to do something about it. This culminated in gay liberation activists, backed by libertarian anti-psychiatry proponents and progressives alike, disrupting APA meetings to protest against the pathologisation of queerness.

然而，到了 20 世纪 70 年代初，许多左翼人士以及自由主义的萨兹主义者终于对同性恋者的形象和待遇忍无可忍。同性恋解放活动家们也愤怒不已，并组织起来采取行动。最终，在自由主义反精神病学支持者和进步人士的支持下，同性恋解放活动家们扰乱了美国精神病学协会的会议，以抗议将同性恋病理化。



Ultimately, this raised the question of why being gay had been pathologised in the first place, and it turned out to be far from clear why it should be. Eventually, the APA voted in 1973, almost unanimously, to demedicalise queerness. They realised that because being gay or lesbian did not cause suffering or disability, there was no clear reason to list it as a medical pathology. Yet while this was an important move in gay liberation, it did not improve the image of psychiatry in the eyes of its critics. As Richard McNally has observed, ‘the democratic process by which the APA resolved the controversy’ was taken, rightly or wrongly, to show ‘that psychiatry had no principled basis for distinguishing mental disorders from other aspects of human functioning’.4

最终，这引发了一个问题：为什么同性恋从一开始就被病理化？结果发现，很难找到明确的理由支持这一点。最终，美国精神病学协会在 1973 年几乎全票通过，决定将酷儿身份去医学化。他们认识到，由于同性恋或女同性恋身份并不会导致痛苦或残障，因此没有明确的理由将其列为医学病理。然而，尽管这是同性恋解放运动中的重要一步，但并未改善精神病学在其批评者眼中的形象。正如理查德·麦克纳利所指出的，“美国精神病学协会解决争议的民主过程”——无论对错——被视作表明“精神病学在区分精神障碍与人类其他功能方面缺乏原则性基础”。 4



It was this, in large part, that finally brought American psychiatry into full crisis, and forced it to confront and, to an extent, incorporate the Szaszian critique. To do this, psychiatrists turned back to, and rapidly expanded, Kraepelin’s more biocentric approach, which was largely consistent with Szasz’s affirmation of the objectivity of the concept of the ‘normal’ brain. While psychiatrists such as Samuel Guze had been arguing for a neo-Kraepelinian approach since the 1950s, the key psychiatrist to instigate the shift was Robert Spitzer. It was Spitzer that led the taskforce for the third edition of the DSM, which would go on to become a surprise best-seller and usher in a new age of psychiatric power.

在很大程度上，正是这一点最终使美国精神病学陷入全面危机，并迫使其面对——并在一定程度上吸纳——萨兹的批判。为此，精神病学家们重新转向并迅速扩展了克雷佩林更具生物中心主义的方法，这种方法在很大程度上与萨兹对"正常"大脑概念客观性的肯定相一致。尽管塞缪尔·古兹等精神病学家自 20 世纪 50 年代以来一直主张新克雷佩林主义方法，但推动这一转变的关键人物是罗伯特·斯皮策。正是斯皮策领导了《精神疾病诊断与统计手册》第三版的工作组，该手册后来意外成为畅销书，并开启了精神病学权力的新时代。



ROBERT SPITZER AND THE DSM-III

罗伯特·斯皮策与《精神疾病诊断与统计手册》第三版



Spitzer – born in New York in 1932 and educated at the New York University of Medicine – viewed the DSM revision process as a golden opportunity. While the previous editions did not even contain a definition of mental illness and were barely used by clinicians, Spitzer would seek to provide a firm concept of mental disorder that would allow robust scientific research to guide future practice. He would also get rid of the psychoanalytic influence, tighten up diagnostic criteria for each diagnosis to avoid misdiagnosis, and provide a firmly medical conception of mental disorder. It was this that would allow the DSM to go from a relatively minor book, not taken seriously by most clinicians, to among the most influential books in the modern world. It would not just be an international best-seller – generating huge income for the American Psychiatric Association with each new edition – but come to be used by researchers, insurance companies, and government policy makers alongside clinicians.

斯皮策出生于 1932 年的纽约，毕业于纽约大学医学院，他将 DSM 的修订过程视为一个黄金机遇。尽管之前的版本甚至没有包含精神疾病的定义，且临床医生很少使用，但斯皮策致力于提供一个坚实的精神障碍概念，以支持强有力的科学研究来指导未来的实践。他还将摆脱精神分析的影响，收紧每个诊断的标准以避免误诊，并提供一种坚定的医学化精神障碍概念。正是这一点使得 DSM 从一本相对次要、大多数临床医生并不重视的书籍，转变为现代世界最具影响力的著作之一。它不仅成为国际畅销书——每一新版都为美国精神病学协会带来巨额收入——而且被研究人员、保险公司和政府政策制定者与临床医生一同广泛使用。



To understand Spitzer’s work, recall here that Szasz had argued that psychoanalytic conceptions of illness were pseudo-scientific, and that real illness reflected abnormality of biological structure or functioning. Starting their work in 1974 against the backdrop of this critique, Spitzer’s team largely dropped the reliance on psychoanalytic theory – at least implicitly conceding to Szasz that the Freudian approach lacked evidence – and instead tried to develop purely descriptive criteria with necessary and sufficient conditions for each diagnosis. This sought to help make diagnosis reliable, with greater utility for research, and it led to expanding the number of diagnostic classifications, which were grouped into different kinds of disorders, such as developmental disorders, anxiety disorders, and so on.

要理解斯皮策的工作，需回顾萨斯曾提出的观点：精神分析对疾病的构想是伪科学的，真正的疾病反映的是生物结构或功能的异常。斯皮策团队于 1974 年在这一批评背景下展开工作，他们基本摒弃了对精神分析理论的依赖——至少默许了萨斯关于弗洛伊德方法缺乏证据的批评——转而尝试为每种诊断制定纯粹描述性的标准，包含必要且充分的条件。此举旨在提高诊断的可靠性，增强其在研究中的实用性，并导致诊断分类数量大幅增加，这些分类被归入不同类型的障碍，如发育障碍、焦虑障碍等。



The most fundamental addition, though, was the newly clarified concept of ‘mental disorder’, which was based on the notion of individual ‘dysfunction’. This new conception required there to be either biological, psychological, or behavioural dysfunction as a necessary condition for counting an ailment as a genuine disorder. The hope was to bring psychiatry more in line not just with somatic medicine and the biological and cognitive sciences – and their Darwinian notions of functioning – but also with the rising behaviourist science of biological organisms.

然而，最根本的补充是“精神障碍”这一新近明确的概念，它基于个体“功能障碍”的理念。这一新概念要求必须存在生物、心理或行为上的功能障碍，作为将某种疾病视为真正障碍的必要条件。其目的在于使精神病学不仅更符合躯体医学、生物与认知科学——以及它们基于达尔文主义的功能观念——还要与新兴的生物有机体行为主义科学保持一致。



In making this shift, Spitzer, at least implicitly, conceded to the Szaszian view that underlying dysfunction was necessary for disorder. However, he rejected Szasz’s overly rigid Cartesian binary between the psychological and the neurological, allowing that the dysfunction could be at either level, or even detected in behaviours taken to express underlying dysfunction. The term ‘disorder’ was thus adopted rather than ‘disease’ since the former leaves open whether the dysfunction is at the biological or merely psychological levels, while ‘disease’ is generally associated with biology only. If someone was shown to be, say, statistically subnormal on cognitive tests, or was consistently maladaptive in their behaviour, this could be sufficient, on the Spitzerian account, for considering there to be a mental disorder. And this was so even if a biological basis had not been verified.

在做出这一转变时，斯皮策至少含蓄地承认了萨兹的观点，即潜在的功能障碍是精神障碍的必要条件。然而，他拒绝了萨兹在心理与神经之间过于僵化的笛卡尔二元论，允许功能障碍可能存在于任一层面，甚至可以在被视为表达潜在功能障碍的行为中被检测到。因此，采用了“障碍”而非“疾病”这一术语，因为前者对于功能障碍是存在于生物学层面还是仅仅心理层面持开放态度，而“疾病”通常仅与生物学相关。如果某人在认知测试中被证明统计上低于正常水平，或者其行为持续适应不良，根据斯皮策的观点，这足以认为存在精神障碍。即使生物学基础尚未得到证实，情况也是如此。



Alongside the dysfunction criteria, Spitzer also realised that most of the mental disorders in previous editions were associated with harm as well as dysfunction. For that matter, this was true of somatic illnesses too. Importantly, Spitzer himself thought that queerness may be dysfunctional from an abstract Darwinian perspective, but even if so, it was nonetheless benign, making it different from genuine illnesses. Given this, Spitzer’s team decided to include the criteria that a condition must also be harmful to be considered a mental disorder, where ‘harm’ is conceptualised in terms of either distress or disability. Thus, the definition the DSM-III provided was, in its final form, as follows:

除了功能障碍标准，斯皮策还意识到先前版本中的大多数精神障碍都与伤害以及功能障碍相关。就此而言，躯体疾病也是如此。重要的是，斯皮策本人认为，从抽象的达尔文主义视角来看，酷儿可能具有功能障碍性，但即便如此，它仍然是良性的，这使其与真正的疾病有所区别。鉴于此，斯皮策的团队决定纳入一项标准，即一种状况还必须具有危害性才能被视为精神障碍，其中“危害”被概念化为痛苦或残障。因此，DSM-III 最终提供的定义如下：





each of the mental disorders is conceptualized as a clinically significant behavioral or psychological syndrome or pattern that occurs in an individual and that is typically associated with either a painful symptom (distress) or impairment in one or more important areas of functioning (disability). In addition, there is an inference that there is a behavioral, psychological, or biological dysfunction, and that the disturbance is not only in the relationship between the individual and society.5

每一种精神障碍都被概念化为个体身上出现的、具有临床意义的行为或心理综合征或模式，通常伴随着痛苦的症状（痛苦）或在一个或多个重要功能领域的损伤（残障）。此外，还推断存在行为、心理或生物功能失调，且这种紊乱不仅限于个体与社会之间的关系。 5





By making both harm and individual dysfunction necessary, and jointly sufficient, for ascribing mental disorder, it was hoped that the concept would be inherently defended against wrongfully pathologising social deviance or benign dysfunction – and would bring psychiatry, its research programmes, and practices, in line with the theories and practices of general medicine and frameworks for understanding cognitive disablement.

通过将伤害与个体功能失调同时设定为判定精神障碍的必要且充分条件，人们希望这一概念能够从根本上避免错误地将社会越轨或良性功能失调病理化，并使精神病学及其研究项目与实践，与普通医学的理论和实践以及理解认知残障的框架保持一致。



And yet, rather than being a new conception of mental disorder, what this signalled was a return to Galton’s paradigm. Just as Galton had thought about all mental disability, mental disorders were to become individual Darwinian dysfunctions in cognition or neurology, understood in relation to ‘normal’ functioning, and often taken to stem from hereditary dispositions that can be triggered in specific contexts. In pontificating over how to define dysfunction, Spitzer precisely associated it with lower productivity in relation to the statistical norm. In his own words, the concept of

然而，这并非对精神障碍的新理解，而是标志着向高尔顿范式的回归。正如高尔顿曾思考所有精神残障一样，精神障碍将被视为个体在认知或神经学上的达尔文式功能障碍，依据"正常"功能来理解，且常被认为源于特定情境下可能被触发的遗传倾向。在阐述如何定义功能障碍时，斯皮策明确将其与低于统计常态的生产力联系起来。用他自己的话说，





inherent disadvantage, relative to other individuals, that results from not being able to function in that area is useful. For example, an individual who is not able to test reality because of delusions or hallucinations, or an individual who is not able to function occupationally because of depression, is at a clear inherent disadvantage in efforts to satisfy basic biological and psychological needs.6

相对于其他个体，由于无法在该领域正常运作而产生的内在劣势这一概念是有用的。例如，因妄想或幻觉而无法检验现实的个体，或因抑郁而无法胜任职业功能的个体，在满足基本生物和心理需求方面显然处于内在劣势。 6





In line with such discussions, a mass new research programme arose among philosophers of science, who sought to clarify the precise nature of biostatistical dysfunction with ever greater precision. By 1975, for instance, in what would come to be among the most influential accounts of the nature of health in the late twentieth century, the philosopher Christopher Boorse had argued that dysfunction was an objective concept that referred only to statistically subnormal functioning when compared to all members of the same species, sex, and age.7 In turn, the dysfunctions that emerged through such theoretical analyses would be reified by Galtonian paradigm research, which focused on finding individual cognitive and biological deficits as compared to a neurotypical norm, albeit this time supplemented with elements of the behaviourist tradition and technology far more advanced than that which had been available in Galton’s time.

随着此类讨论的推进，科学哲学家群体中兴起了一项大规模的新研究计划，他们试图以日益精确的方式阐明生物统计功能障碍的确切本质。例如，到 1975 年，哲学家克里斯托弗·布尔斯提出了关于二十世纪末健康本质最具影响力的论述之一，他认为功能障碍是一个客观概念，仅指与同物种、同性别、同年龄的所有成员相比，统计上功能低于正常水平的情况。 7 反过来，通过这种理论分析得出的功能障碍，将被高尔顿范式研究具体化。这类研究侧重于寻找与神经典型规范相比的个体认知和生物缺陷，尽管此时已融入了行为主义传统的元素，并且技术远比高尔顿时代先进得多。



Importantly too, while there was some resistance to this pathologisation, the Szaszian anti-psychiatry analysis was not just increasingly irrelevant. If anything, it had been part of the very process that allowed the Galtonian approach to return stronger than ever. By relying on and reinforcing the idea that pathology is a matter of structural or functional ‘abnormality’, and seeing this as a simple, objective matter, Szasz and his followers fully bought into the logics of the pathology paradigm. Instead of building a new approach, they had just tried to limit the reach of the dominant paradigm from within by suggesting that mental illnesses needed to be verified as having a biological element to be deemed real maladies.

同样重要的是，尽管对这种病理化存在一些抵制，但萨兹式的反精神病学分析不仅越来越无关紧要。实际上，它恰恰是让高尔顿式方法以更强姿态回归的进程的一部分。通过依赖并强化“病理是结构或功能‘异常’的问题”这一观念，并将其视为一个简单、客观的问题，萨兹及其追随者完全接受了病理学范式的逻辑。他们并未构建新的方法，而是试图从内部限制主导范式的影响，主张精神疾病需要被证实具有生物学成分才能被视为真正的疾病。



Looked at this way Darwinian rather than Freudian conceptions of neurological abnormality were thus perfectly legitimate. All psychiatry needed to do was turn away from Freud’s equilibrium conception of health and towards a medicalised conception of normal functioning and begin researching again at the genetic and neurological levels. And so it was that anti-psychiatry helped open the door for Galtonian psychiatry and ideology to not just return but become fully hegemonic.

从这个角度来看，神经异常的达尔文式而非弗洛伊德式概念因此是完全合理的。精神病学需要做的只是摒弃弗洛伊德关于健康的平衡观念，转向医学化的正常功能概念，并重新在遗传和神经层面展开研究。正是这样，反精神病学运动为高尔顿式精神病学及其意识形态的回归打开了大门，不仅使其卷土重来，更使其完全占据了主导地位。



THE LIMITS OF BIOLOGICAL PSYCHIATRY

生物精神病学的局限



The decade following the release of the DSM-III had seen both a mass expansion of psychiatry and a turn from Freudian models to biocentric and cognitivist approaches to mental health. This meant that mental disorder came to be seen as stemming from a ‘broken brain’ or glitchy mind, and should be fixed primarily by biomedical, cognitive, or behavioural intervention. We see this shift exemplified, for instance, in the neuroscientist Nancy Andreasen’s 1984 book The Broken Brain: The Biological Revolution in Psychiatry. Andreasen positioned Kraepelin rather than Freud as the father of modern psychiatry, and was confident enough to state that psychiatric disorders were now medical conditions ‘in the same sense that cancer or high blood pressure are’.8

《精神疾病诊断与统计手册》第三版发布后的十年间，精神病学领域经历了大规模扩张，同时从弗洛伊德模式转向了以生物中心论和认知主义为主导的心理健康研究路径。这意味着精神障碍开始被视为源于“受损的大脑”或故障的思维，应主要通过生物医学、认知或行为干预进行矫正。这一转变的典型例证可见于神经科学家南希·安德里亚森 1984 年出版的《受损的大脑：精神病学的生物革命》。安德里亚森将克雷佩林而非弗洛伊德定位为现代精神病学之父，并充满信心地宣称：精神疾病如今已是“与癌症或高血压性质相同的医学病症”。 8



While this shift was led by enthusiastic neuroscientists and psychiatrists, it was embraced much more widely, and by 1990 it made sense for President Bush to declare the next ten years the ‘Decade of the Brain’. Bush’s support was also – so it was thought – supposed to be economically prudential. The hope was that, rather than expensive personal therapy or societal changes, new drugs could be developed and then mass produced to ease the suffering of psychiatric patients cheaply and efficiently. Following this, the 1990s, and then the 2000s, brought a huge increase in funding for the National Institute of Mental Health in the United States, and similar organisations elsewhere. New mental and neurological disorders were recognised, classified, and diagnosed in ever greater numbers. And new psychiatric therapies and drugs were developed and implemented to treat them.

尽管这一转变由热心的神经科学家和精神病学家引领，但它得到了更广泛的接纳。到 1990 年，布什总统宣布接下来的十年为“大脑的十年”便显得顺理成章。人们认为，布什的支持同样出于经济上的审慎考量。当时的期望是，与其投入昂贵的个人治疗或推动社会变革，不如研发新药并大规模生产，从而以低廉高效的方式缓解精神病患者的痛苦。此后，1990 年代乃至 2000 年代，美国国家心理健康研究所及世界各地的类似机构获得了大幅增长的资金支持。越来越多的新型精神与神经障碍得到识别、分类和诊断。同时，新的精神疗法和药物被开发并应用于治疗这些疾病。



In turn American psychiatry was increasingly exported around the world. In the place of the old European empires and their colonial asylums, the new psychiatric imperialism mainly came in the guise of ideas, diagnoses, and medications. As the work of Ethan Watters9 has shown, it was primarily drug companies that drove the exportation of Western diagnoses as and where the opportunity arose. This led to the erasure of local understandings in favour of biomedical narratives that were useful for American and European pharmaceutical companies to profit. While the suffering was of course real, the cultural expansion of biomedical narratives primarily followed the logic of the markets. According to these companies, these new biomedical treatments would help those experiencing mental distress or illness in ways that would far surpass those based on more local understandings.

相应地，美国精神病学日益向全球输出。取代旧欧洲帝国及其殖民地精神病院的是，新的精神病学帝国主义主要以思想、诊断和药物的形式出现。正如伊桑·沃特斯的研究所示，主要是制药公司在机会出现时推动了西方诊断的出口。这导致了对本土理解的抹杀，转而支持有利于美国和欧洲制药公司盈利的生物医学叙事。虽然痛苦无疑是真实的，但生物医学叙事的文化扩张主要遵循市场逻辑。根据这些公司的说法，这些新的生物医学治疗方法将以远超基于更本土理解的方式，帮助那些经历精神困扰或疾病的人。



And yet despite all of this, mental health did not improve. On some estimates, our collective mental health has flatlined since the 1980s, while on others, it may even have gotten worse. When it comes to the United States, this has been discussed by Robert Whitaker, a journalist and influential critic of biomedical psychiatry. As he noted in 2010: ‘In 2007 the disability rate (for mental illness) was 1 in every 76 Americans. That’s more than double the rate in 1987, and six times the rate in 1955’.10 This was despite a mass rise in the use of both new and old psychotropic medications. Indeed, these increased year on year until they were prescribed to almost a quarter of the UK population in 201811 and around 16.5% of the US population12 in 2020. While it should again be acknowledged that these did and do genuinely help some people – and even save many lives – for many they did not help, or not enough. And for others still, they made things worse.

然而，尽管有这一切，心理健康状况并未改善。根据某些估计，自 20 世纪 80 年代以来，我们的集体心理健康水平一直停滞不前，而另一些估计甚至显示情况可能变得更糟。就美国而言，记者兼生物医学精神病学领域有影响力的批评者罗伯特·惠特克曾对此进行过讨论。正如他在 2010 年指出的那样："2007 年，（精神疾病导致的）残障率是每 76 名美国人中就有 1 人。这比 1987 年的比率高出一倍多，是 1955 年比率的六倍。" 10 尽管新旧精神药物的使用量都大幅增加，情况依然如此。事实上，这些药物的使用量逐年增长，直到 2018 年，英国近四分之一的人口 11 以及 2020 年美国约 16.5%的人口 12 都在服用这些药物。虽然我们应当再次承认，这些药物过去和现在确实帮助了一些人——甚至挽救了许多生命——但对许多人来说，它们没有帮助，或者帮助不够。而对另一些人来说，它们反而让情况变得更糟。



The mass failure of this project can most starkly be seen in the words of Thomas Insel, who had led the National Institute of Mental Health between 2002 and 2015. It was in 2017 that he finally made the startling admission that:

这一项目的大规模失败，在托马斯·因塞尔的言论中体现得最为鲜明，他曾于 2002 年至 2015 年间领导美国国家精神卫生研究所。正是在 2017 年，他终于做出了惊人的承认：





I spent 13 years at NIMH really pushing on the neuroscience and genetics of mental disorders, and when I look back on that I realize that while I think I succeeded at getting lots of really cool papers published by cool scientists at fairly large costs – I think $20 billion – I don’t think we moved the needle in reducing suicide, reducing hospitalizations, improving recovery for the tens of millions of people who have mental illness.13

我在美国国家精神卫生研究院（NIMH）工作了 13 年，致力于推动神经科学和遗传学在精神疾病领域的研究。回顾这段经历，我意识到虽然我们成功推动了许多杰出科学家发表了众多精彩论文，为此投入了相当巨大的成本——大约 200 亿美元——但我认为我们在减少自杀率、降低住院率、改善数千万精神疾病患者的康复状况方面并未取得实质性进展。 13





A range of studies show that psychiatric medications, on average, tend to have at least a small positive impact despite their limited utility and risk of harmful side effects.14 So if everything else had stayed the same mental health should have improved given the increased use of medications. It may therefore be that to understand what went wrong, we must again turn to the broader social, economic, and technological changes that began around the same time Spitzer’s team was readying the DSM-III for publication.

一系列研究表明，精神科药物尽管效用有限且存在有害副作用的风险，但平均而言仍能产生至少微小的积极效果。 14 因此，如果其他条件保持不变，随着药物使用的增加，心理健康状况本应有所改善。所以，要理解问题出在哪里，我们可能必须再次审视更广泛的社会、经济和技术变革，这些变革大约始于斯皮策团队准备出版《精神疾病诊断与统计手册》第三版（DSM-III）的同一时期。



---

Empire of Normality



8



Post-Fordism as a mass disabling event

后福特主义作为大规模致残事件



In the summer of 1975, a speaker at the Conservative Research Department in Great Britain was giving a talk on how the British Conservative Party should avoid the extremes of left and right. Instead, he was arguing, they should forge a new ‘middle way’. Suddenly, he was interrupted by a woman who stood up and pulled a book from her briefcase. Brandishing the book so all could see it, she stated ‘This is what we believe’, before banging the book down on the table. The woman who had interrupted the speech was none other than the newly elected leader of the Conservative Party, Margaret Thatcher. And the book she had declared her allegiance to was titled The Constitution of Liberty, written by Thomas Szasz’s idol, the economist Friedrich Hayek.

1975 年夏天，英国保守党研究部的一位演讲者正在阐述保守党应如何避免左右两派的极端立场。他主张应当开辟一条新的"中间道路"。突然，一位女士起身打断演讲，从公文包中取出一本书。她高举书本向全场展示，宣称"这才是我们的信仰"，随后将书重重摔在桌上。这位打断演讲的女士正是新当选的保守党领袖玛格丽特·撒切尔。而她宣誓效忠的著作名为《自由宪章》，作者正是托马斯·萨斯的精神偶像——经济学家弗里德里希·哈耶克。



Four years later, in 1979, Thatcher was elected to be Prime Minister, and began ushering in Hayekian policies to the United Kingdom. Around the same time, Ronald Reagan in the United States also began implementing Hayekian policies. It is to this shift that we now turn. For the shift from Keynesian economics to Hayekian economics is vital for understanding the rising tide of mental health problems and the inability of biological psychiatry to effectively fight it.

四年后，即 1979 年，撒切尔当选首相，开始在英国推行哈耶克式的政策。大约在同一时期，美国的罗纳德·里根也开始实施哈耶克式的政策。我们现在要转向这一转变。因为从凯恩斯经济学向哈耶克经济学的转变，对于理解心理健康问题的日益严重以及生物精神病学无法有效应对这一问题至关重要。



The basic idea of neoliberalism, as summarised by David Harvey, was that ‘human well-being can best be advanced by liberating individual entrepreneurial freedoms and skills within an institutional framework characterized by strong private property rights, free markets, and free trade’.1 In practice this meant privatisation, deregulation, and austerity. Following the culture wars and economic recession of the 1970s, Thatcher and Reagan essentially sought to reverse the welfare capitalism of the earlier twentieth century. While Chile, guided by US pressure, had experimented with neoliberal policies several years earlier, it was during the early 1980s that Britain and the United States each began massively rolling back the state and diminishing the welfare system.

正如大卫·哈维所总结的，新自由主义的基本理念是：“在具有强大私有产权、自由市场和自由贸易特征的制度框架内，通过释放个人创业自由和技能，可以最好地促进人类福祉。” 1 在实践中，这表现为私有化、放松管制和紧缩政策。经历了 20 世纪 70 年代的文化战争和经济衰退后，撒切尔和里根实质上试图扭转 20 世纪早期的福利资本主义。尽管在美国的压力下，智利早在几年前就尝试了新自由主义政策，但直到 80 年代初，英国和美国才开始大规模缩减国家职能并削弱福利体系。



In the wake of changes made by Thatcher and Reagan, neoliberalism was quickly enforced across much of the rest of the world.
