It was globalised through international financial institutions such as the World Trade Organization and International Monetary Fund, and through US imperial pressure. As state communism fell, even Russia and China increasingly liberalised their economies to fit in – to at least some extent, and with mixed success – with the new global system. From around the same time, traditionally left-leaning political parties in liberal democracies, such as the British Labour Party and the Democratic Party in the United States, also shifted to the right. This was largely as organised labour was crushed by neoliberal governments and neoliberal ideology was propagated by the press. In this context, aspirational voters were choosing the ideal of individual freedom offered by neoliberalism over the progressive ideals, and higher taxes, of more collectivist politics.

随着撒切尔和里根推动的变革，新自由主义迅速在全球大部分地区得以推行。它通过世界贸易组织和国际货币基金组织等国际金融机构，以及美国的帝国压力实现了全球化。随着国家共产主义的衰落，甚至俄罗斯和中国也日益自由化其经济，以在一定程度上适应新的全球体系，尽管成效参差不齐。大约在同一时期，自由民主国家中传统上左倾的政党，如英国工党和美国民主党，也向右转。这主要是因为有组织的劳工被新自由主义政府打压，而新自由主义意识形态通过媒体广泛传播。在此背景下，有抱负的选民选择了新自由主义提供的个人自由理想，而非更集体主义政治中的进步理想和更高税收。



This was to have profound effects on pretty much every aspect of human life. Indeed, as Harvey writes, neoliberal ideology had since ‘become hegemonic as a mode of discourse’. It has, he goes on, ‘pervasive effects on ways of thought to the point where it has become incorporated into the common-sense way many of us interpret, live in, and understand the world’.2 As we will see below, our experiences and understandings of mental health were far from immune to this more general shift.

这对人类生活的几乎每个方面都产生了深远影响。事实上，正如哈维所写，新自由主义意识形态自此"作为一种话语模式变得霸权化"。他进一步指出，它"对思维方式产生了普遍影响，以至于已经融入我们许多人解释、生活和理解世界的常识方式中"。 2 正如我们将在下文看到的，我们对心理健康的体验和理解远未免受这一更广泛转变的影响。



The end of the Soviet Union, and other actually existing attempts to build communism, also brought the rise of what the social theorist Mark Fisher retrospectively called ‘capitalist realism’. This was his term for what he described as a ‘pervasive atmosphere, conditioning not only the production of culture but also the regulation of work and education, and acting as a kind of invisible barrier constraining thought and action’ that made capitalism seem like the natural and only possible way of organising the world. Within this context, class consciousness and thus the idea that capitalism could be meaningfully challenged or replaced was stifled. The harms of capitalism were recognised, but even then the possibility of imagining and fighting for a coherent alternative became less possible. All that was left was to strive for normality and wealth, in competition with all the other unwell workers.

苏联的终结，以及其他实际存在的构建共产主义的尝试，也带来了社会理论家马克·费舍尔后来所称的“资本主义现实主义”的兴起。这是他用来描述一种“弥漫的氛围，不仅制约着文化的生产，还调节着工作和教育，并作为一种无形的障碍限制着思想和行动”的术语，这种氛围使资本主义看起来像是组织世界的自然且唯一可能的方式。在这种背景下，阶级意识以及资本主义可以被有意义地挑战或取代的观念被扼杀了。资本主义的危害得到了承认，但即便如此，想象并为一个连贯的替代方案而奋斗的可能性也变得愈发渺茫。剩下的只是在与其他所有不健康的工人竞争中，努力追求正常和财富。



For Thatcher, poverty itself was seen not as a structural problem but as an individual one. People are in poverty, she stated in a 1978 interview, because they ‘don’t know how to budget, don’t know how to spend their earnings’. Ultimately, for her this came down to them having an individual ‘personality defect’3 In a later speech, she posited that ‘poverty is not material but behavioural’.4

在撒切尔看来，贫困本身并非结构性问题，而是个人问题。她在 1978 年的一次采访中表示，人们之所以陷入贫困，是因为他们"不懂如何规划预算，不知如何支配收入"。归根结底，她认为这源于个人"性格缺陷" 3 。在后续演讲中，她更断言"贫困无关物质条件，实属行为问题" 4 。



These shifts are relevant for understanding the worsening of mental health partly in connection with rising inequality. Over this period, the unfettered market allowed the rich to get richer, leading to a further accumulation of capital in the hands of a few. At the same time, workers’ rights were weakened, workers had less control over their workplaces, and they also had to work longer hours than ever before. The mental health effects of this have been detailed by Iain Ferguson in his 2017 book Politics of the Mind: Marxism and Mental Distress. Ferguson draws on Marx’s concept of alienation to argue that changes in the workplace have led to worsening mental health outcomes. On the one hand, he writes

这些转变对于理解心理健康恶化与不平等加剧的关联至关重要。在此期间，不受约束的市场使富人愈富，导致资本进一步向少数人手中聚集。与此同时，劳动者权益遭到削弱，工人对工作场所的控制力下降，工作时长却达到历史新高。伊恩·弗格森在 2017 年著作《心灵政治：马克思主义与精神困厄》中详细阐述了这种状况对心理健康的影响。弗格森援引马克思的异化理论，论证工作场所的变革导致了心理健康状况恶化。他指出，一方面





the mental health of those in employment has […] suffered as a result of the neoliberal policies of the past three decades. In 2015/2016 stress accounted for 37 percent of all work-related absences and 45 percent of all working days lost due to ill-health. The intensification of work, which has been a key element of the neoliberal project, is one reason for this epidemic of work-related stress.5

就业人群的心理健康因过去三十年的新自由主义政策而受损。2015/2016 年间，压力占所有工作相关缺勤的 37%，以及因健康问题导致的所有工作日损失的 45%。工作强度的加剧是新自由主义计划的一个关键要素，也是工作相关压力普遍蔓延的原因之一。 5





On the other hand, those in low-paid employment or unemployment experience the worst effects. For instance, one 2017 UK report Ferguson cites found mental health problems were directly linked to income and unemployment: 73 per cent of people in the lowest household income bracket experienced mental health problems in their lifetime, while 59 per cent of those in the highest bracket did. In turn, a ‘substantial majority of those currently unemployed (85 percent) report that they have experienced a mental health problem compared to 66 percent in paid employment’.6 Indeed, Ferguson further notes, austerity measures have also been associated with a huge rise in suicides. For instance, when neoliberal austerity was enforced in Greece, suicide rates shot up in line with rising levels of unemployment.

另一方面，低收入就业或失业人群承受着最严重的后果。例如，弗格森引用的一份 2017 年英国报告发现，心理健康问题与收入和失业直接相关：家庭收入最低群体中有 73%的人一生中经历过心理健康问题，而最高收入群体中这一比例为 59%。反过来，"当前失业者中绝大多数（85%）报告曾经历过心理健康问题，而在职就业者中这一比例为 66%。" 6 事实上，弗格森进一步指出，紧缩措施也与自杀率的大幅上升有关。例如，当新自由主义紧缩政策在希腊实施时，自杀率随着失业率的上升而急剧攀升。



At the same time, community care for people experiencing mental illness did not improve, and many neoliberal governments cut funding for health services. Hence in a myriad of ways the neoliberal era seems to have worsened mental health. And the biomedical approach, by only treating symptoms with blunt biomedical tools, was unable to stem the rising tide of mental illness and disablement.

与此同时，针对精神疾病患者的社区护理并未改善，许多新自由主义政府削减了医疗服务资金。因此，新自由主义时代似乎以多种方式恶化了心理健康状况。而生物医学方法仅用生硬的生物医学工具治疗症状，未能遏制精神疾病和失能状况的上升趋势。



THE NEW ALIENATION

新型异化



One way to help make sense of worsening mental health outcomes during this period is to update Marx’s notion of alienation to fit the current era. As has been noted already, alienation refers to an estrangement from self and others that increased within the conditions of labour under capitalism. For Marx, the structural arrangements of capitalism mean that workers are deprived of control of the means of production and are instead defined by their instrumental value to generate profit. Marx argued that when workers are effectively forced to sell their labour just so others could profit it is harmful to the worker, stunting both their health and growth. Moreover, less worker control meant greater estrangement from their creative activity and the products of work:

要理解这一时期心理健康状况恶化的原因，一种方法是将马克思的异化概念更新以适应当前时代。如前所述，异化指的是在资本主义劳动条件下日益加剧的自我与他人之间的疏离。对马克思而言，资本主义的结构性安排意味着工人被剥夺了对生产资料的控制权，反而被定义为创造利润的工具性价值。马克思认为，当工人实际上被迫出卖劳动力仅仅是为了让他人获利时，这对工人是有害的，阻碍了他们的健康和成长。此外，工人控制权的减少意味着他们与创造性活动及劳动产品之间的疏离感加剧：





the spontaneous activity of the human imagination, of the human brain and the human heart, operates on the individual independently of him – that is, operates as an alien, divine or diabolical activity – so is the worker’s activity not his spontaneous activity. It belongs to another; it is the loss of his self.7

人类想象力、人脑和人类心灵的自发活动，独立于个体之外作用于个体——即作为一种异己的、神圣的或邪恶的活动而运作——因此工人的活动并非其自发活动。它属于他人；这是其自我的丧失。 7





Importantly, while Marx did not use the language of mental health, the effects he indicates are precisely what would today be described in medical terminology. In being alienated, he writes, the worker ‘denies himself, does not feel content but unhappy, does not develop freely his physical and mental energy but mortifies his body and ruins his mind’.

重要的是，尽管马克思并未使用心理健康相关的术语，但他所描述的影响恰恰是当今医学语言中所指的现象。他写道，在异化状态下，工人“否定自我，感受不到满足而是不幸，无法自由发展身心能量，反而摧残身体、毁坏心智”。



It is important to stress, however, that Marx was writing during a time when workers’ alienation arose mainly in factories where material products were manufactured. To understand alienation today in post-industrial economies, several other changes accompanying the rise of neoliberalism need to be considered. The first is the mass rise of reliance on emotional labour. This regards what the sociologist C. Wright Mills termed the ‘personality market’, whereby ‘personal or even intimate traits of employees are drawn into the sphere of exchange, become commodities in the labor market’. While this has always been the case to some extent, it has become much more central in economic relations following the shift from manufacturing economies to service economies. In a modern services economy, ways of feeling and relating, for instance in kindliness and friendliness, ‘become aspects of personalized service or of public relations of big firms, rationalized to further the sale of something’.8

然而必须强调的是，马克思写作的时代，工人的异化主要发生在生产物质产品的工厂中。要理解后工业经济中的异化现象，还需考虑伴随新自由主义兴起的其他几项变化。首先是情感劳动依赖的大规模兴起。这涉及社会学家 C·赖特·米尔斯提出的“人格市场”——即“员工的个人甚至私密特质被纳入交换领域，成为劳动力市场中的商品”。虽然这在某种程度上始终存在，但在从制造业经济转向服务业经济后，它已成为经济关系中更为核心的要素。在现代服务经济中，感受与互动的方式（例如亲切与友善）“成为个性化服务或大公司公共关系的组成部分，被理性化设计以促进商品销售”。 8



While Mills documented this in the 1950s, the mental health effects of emotional labour were first properly comprehended three decades later by the US sociologist Arlie Russell Hochschild. By this time services dominated the US economy, bringing new forms of mass alienation Hochschild detailed in her 1983 book The Managed Heart: Commercialization of Human Feeling. Hochschild illustrated this with the example of a flight attendant:

虽然米尔斯在 20 世纪 50 年代就记录了这一点，但情感劳动对心理健康的影响直到三十年后才被美国社会学家阿莉·拉塞尔·霍克希尔德真正理解。此时服务业已主导美国经济，带来了新形式的大规模异化，霍克希尔德在其 1983 年出版的《被管理的心：人类情感的商业化》一书中对此进行了详细阐述。霍克希尔德以空乘人员为例说明了这一点：





For the flight attendant, the smiles are a part of her work, a part that requires her to coordinate self and feeling so that the work seems to be effortless. To show that the enjoyment takes effort is to do the job poorly. Similarly, part of the job is to disguise fatigue and irritation, for otherwise the labor would show in an unseemly way, and the product – passenger contentment – would be damaged. Because it is easier to disguise fatigue and irritation if they can be banished altogether, at least for brief periods, this feat calls for emotional labor.9

对空乘人员而言，微笑是她工作的一部分，这部分工作要求她协调自我与情感，使工作看起来毫不费力。若表现出愉悦需要费力，那就是工作失职。同样，掩饰疲劳和烦躁也是工作的一部分，否则劳动就会以不体面的方式显现，产品——乘客的满意度——就会受损。因为如果能彻底消除疲劳和烦躁（至少短暂地），掩饰它们就会更容易，这一技巧需要情感劳动。 9





In Hochschild’s account, this incurs massive emotional costs, whereby ‘the worker can become estranged or alienated from an aspect of self’.10 As workers she interviewed revealed, a key outcome of this is stress and situational depression.11 Hence already by the time she was writing in the early 1980s, telephone companies were giving their workers free drugs such as Valium or codeine in order to help them bear the costs of emotional labour to more easily allow more efficient production.12 At the same time, pharmaceuticals were increasingly prescribed year after year, in many cases to people working long hours in the new services industries. And this has only increased in the decades following Hochschild’s initial analysis.

在霍克希尔德的分析中，这带来了巨大的情感代价，即“工人可能变得与自我的某个方面疏离或异化”。 10 正如她采访的工人们所揭示的，一个关键后果是压力和情境性抑郁。 11 因此，早在 20 世纪 80 年代初她撰写此书时，电话公司就已经开始为员工提供免费的药物，如安定或可待因，以帮助他们承受情感劳动的代价，从而更轻松地实现更高效的生产。 12 与此同时，药物处方逐年增加，许多情况下是针对在新兴服务业长时间工作的人群。在霍克希尔德最初分析之后的几十年里，这一趋势只增不减。



Cognitive labour is equally important to consider alongside the services economy and rising reliance on emotion labour. Around the same period, new technological innovations, most notably, the personal computer, the internet, and the digital revolution more broadly, led to the rise of what has been termed post-Fordism or ‘cognitive capitalism’. Traditional industrial capitalism was based on ‘the accumulation of physical labour’ and material production, but since around 1975, ‘the object of accumulation consists mainly of knowledge, which becomes the basic source of value, as well as the principal location of the process of valorisation’.13

认知劳动与服务经济和日益增长的情感劳动依赖同样重要。大约在同一时期，新的技术创新，尤其是个人电脑、互联网以及更广泛的数字革命，导致了所谓的后福特主义或“认知资本主义”的兴起。传统的工业资本主义基于“体力劳动的积累”和物质生产，但自 1975 年左右以来，“积累的对象主要是知识，知识成为价值的基本来源，也是价值增值过程的主要场所”。 13



The cognitive alienation of this era and how it harms mental health has been examined by Franco ‘Bifo’ Berardi in his penetrating 2009 book The Soul at Work: From alienation to autonomy. As Berardi notes, architects, travel agents, solicitors, computer programmers, and so forth all use relatively similar machines – mostly computers, mobile phones, etc. – but have different specialist knowledges with specific cognitive contents that produce surplus value. Because of this, much capital is currently created by countless solitary individuals, sitting in front of screens, typing, scrolling, calculating, and using different cognitive contents to produce an endless variety of cognitive contents from which capital can be mined.

这个时代的认知异化及其对心理健康的危害，已在弗朗哥·“比弗”·贝拉尔迪 2009 年出版的深刻著作《工作中的灵魂：从异化到自主》中得到剖析。正如贝拉尔迪所指出的，建筑师、旅行代理人、律师、计算机程序员等，虽然使用着相对类似的机器——主要是电脑、手机等——但他们各自拥有不同的专业知识，这些知识包含特定的认知内容，能够产生剩余价值。正因如此，当前大量资本是由无数孤独的个体创造的，他们坐在屏幕前，打字、滚动、计算，利用不同的认知内容，生产出无穷无尽的认知内容，资本便从中被挖掘出来。



Within this phase of capitalism, Berardi documents the rise of a form of societal organisation he calls the ‘factory of unhappiness’. In the Fordist era, jobs had tended to be stable, and to require being one small part of a manufacturing process that could be left behind at the end of the day. The worker would then return to their private life where they could relax or pursue their personal interests. By contrast, in the post-Fordist era, distinctions between home and work, public and private, employed and unemployed collapsed as work became casualised and precarious while workers became always reachable through phones and emails.

在这一资本主义阶段，贝拉尔迪记录了一种他称之为"不幸福工厂"的社会组织形式的兴起。在福特主义时代，工作往往稳定，只需成为制造流程中的一小部分，下班后即可抛诸脑后。工人随后回归私人生活，得以放松或追求个人兴趣。相比之下，在后福特主义时代，随着工作变得临时化且不稳定，而工人又因手机和电子邮件而随时可被联系，家庭与工作、公共与私人、就业与失业之间的界限逐渐消解。



At the same time, our relationship with capital and production has increasingly spread beyond work, and into the weekend and evening, in other ways. Browsing online means being constantly bombarded with advertisements; posting on social media creates content that is then turned into profit by the owner of the site; and use of an app may be granted only after filling in a brief survey. Any moment we are online or using an ever-growing host of apps, we are constantly yet subtly guided by algorithms designed to direct our attention, document our behaviours, stoke our emotions, and influence our desires in the service of capital.

与此同时，我们与资本和生产的关系正以其他方式日益蔓延至工作之外，渗透进周末与夜晚。浏览网络意味着不断被广告轰炸；在社交媒体上发帖创造的内容随后被网站所有者转化为利润；使用应用程序可能只有在完成简短调查后才能获得许可。每当我们上网或使用日益增多的应用程序时，我们都在被算法微妙而持续地引导，这些算法旨在吸引我们的注意力、记录我们的行为、煽动我们的情绪，并影响我们的欲望，以服务于资本。



The result of these combined factors, in Berardi’s words, has been that mental health deteriorates as our ‘desiring energy is trapped in the trick of self-enterprise, our libidinal investments are regulated according to economic rules, our attention is captured in the precariousness of virtual networks: every fragment of mental activity must be transformed into capital’.14 Thus for Berardi, post-Fordism brings a new form of alienation ‘marked by the submission of the soul, in which animated, creative, linguistic, emotional corporeality is subsumed and incorporated by the production of value’.15 According to his analysis, this kind of instability and fluidity contributes to constant depression, anxiety, and panic – all problems that became increasingly prevalent towards the end of the twentieth century, and skyrocketed in post-Fordist economies following the turn of the millennium.

用贝拉尔迪的话来说，这些因素共同作用的结果是，随着"我们的欲望能量被困在自我创业的诡计中，我们的力比多投资按照经济规则被调控，我们的注意力被虚拟网络的不稳定性所捕获：精神活动的每一个片段都必须转化为资本"，心理健康状况不断恶化。 14 因此，在贝拉尔迪看来，后福特主义带来了一种新的异化形式，"其特征是灵魂的屈服，其中充满活力、富有创造力、语言性和情感性的身体性被价值生产所吸纳和整合"。 15 根据他的分析，这种不稳定性和流动性导致了持续的抑郁、焦虑和恐慌——所有这些问题在二十世纪末变得越来越普遍，并在千禧年之后的后福特主义经济中急剧飙升。



NEURODIVERGENT DISABLEMENT

神经殊异致残



If boredom was distinctive of the work of the monotonous Fordist era, anxiety and depression are distinctive of post-Fordism. But this was not the only effect of these shifts in capitalism. Just as the Industrial Revolution brought new bodily norms, so too did the digital revolution and cognitive capitalism bring newly restrictive cognitive, emotional, and attentive norms in both the classroom and the workplace. The sensory-cognitive intensification of capitalism meant that a great many more people were either shut out of education or work, at least to varying extents, and were thus harmed in a different way. Rather than being positioned as ‘ordinary’ workers with mental health problems, they were disabled, and pushed towards the surplus population, even if some did manage to work despite this. In this context, new disability diagnoses initially referred to as ‘shadow syndromes’ – milder versions of existing diagnoses – also began being increasingly applied during childhood as well as to adults. More people were harmed by, and considered unsuited to, the needs and organisation of the new economy and its sensory, cognitive, and emotional requirements.

如果说无聊是单调的福特主义时代工作的特征，那么焦虑和抑郁则是后福特主义的特征。但这并非资本主义这些转变带来的唯一影响。正如工业革命带来了新的身体规范，数字革命和认知资本主义同样在课堂与职场中引入了新近限制性的认知、情感及注意力规范。资本主义在感官与认知层面的强化，意味着更多人被不同程度地排斥在教育或工作之外，从而以另一种方式受到伤害。他们不再被定位为有心理健康问题的“普通”劳动者，而是被归为残障者，并被推向剩余人口的行列——尽管其中一些人仍设法坚持工作。在此背景下，最初被称为“影子综合征”（即现有诊断的轻微版本）的新型残障诊断，也开始越来越多地应用于儿童及成人。更多人因无法适应新经济及其对感官、认知和情感的需求与组织方式而受到伤害，并被视作不合时宜者。



One key example is definitive of our age: autism. When it comes to the requirement for sociality, hyper-flexibility, and emotional labour, it is not just that stress levels have risen among the general population. It is also that the autism diagnosis, which had previously been restricted to a relatively limited number of cases, was radically expanded.16 The broadening of autism into a spectrum was first tentatively suggested in 1979, the year Thatcher became Prime Minister, and began to expand over the following decade. Since the 1990s and 2000s especially, the spectrum has continually widened as an ever-rising percentage of the population fall short of the social, communicative, and sensory processing capabilities required by the new economy. The expansion of the autism diagnosis has been directly applied to people who are blocked from working in the services economies of the post-Fordist era. Hence, for instance, in 2021, a UK government report found that only 22 per cent of the autistic population were in employment despite many desiring to work.17

一个关键例子定义了我们这个时代：孤独症。当涉及到社交性、超强适应性和情感劳动的要求时，不仅仅是普通人群的压力水平上升了。同时，先前仅限于相对少数病例的孤独症诊断也被极大地扩展了。 16 将孤独症扩展为一个谱系的概念，最初在 1979 年——撒切尔成为首相的那一年——被试探性地提出，并在接下来的十年中开始扩展。特别是自 20 世纪 90 年代和 21 世纪初以来，随着越来越多的人无法达到新经济所要求的社会交往和感官处理能力，这个谱系的范围持续扩大。孤独症诊断的扩展，被直接应用于那些在后福特主义时代的服务经济中无法工作的人群。因此，例如在 2021 年，英国政府的一份报告发现，尽管许多孤独谱系人士渴望工作，但只有 22%的孤独谱系人群处于就业状态。 17



Highly relevant here is not just the emotional requirements of the services economy but the invasive sensory and information environments of the modern world, where economic relations require a constant bombardment of lights, advertising, screens, and so forth. In this context, high levels of anxiety in the autistic population have been associated in a variety of studies with what is framed as ‘sensory over-responsivity’.18 As one autistic person writes:

与此高度相关的不仅是服务经济的情感需求，还有现代世界侵入性的感官和信息环境，在这种环境中，经济关系需要持续不断的灯光、广告、屏幕等的轰炸。在此背景下，多项研究已将孤独谱系人群的高焦虑水平与所谓的“感官过度反应”联系起来。 18 正如一位孤独谱系人士所写：





I struggle with bright lights and noise, I hate swaying or spinning motion, I cannot cope in big crowds where there are a lot of competing noises, and my sense of smell is often overpowering […] It feels like my brain is being squeezed and all of my muscles tense up. My heart races fast and my breathing quickens. At this point, I lose the ability to think straight and my thoughts sound like they are overlapping and nonsensical.19

我难以忍受明亮的灯光和噪音，我讨厌摇摆或旋转的运动，我无法应对人群拥挤、各种噪音相互竞争的环境，而且我的嗅觉常常过于敏感……感觉就像我的大脑被挤压，全身肌肉都紧绷起来。我的心跳加速，呼吸急促。这时，我就失去了清晰思考的能力，我的思绪听起来像是重叠在一起，毫无意义。 19





Simultaneously, neoliberalism and cognitive capitalism have also brought a pace in the tempo of life that has increasingly disabled those whose cognitive processing fits a less hurried pace. As Robert Hassan writes, the Fordist era and ‘machine and factory based process had a specific tempo, and it was much slower than it is today’. By contrast, he goes on, today:

与此同时，新自由主义和认知资本主义也带来了生活节奏的加快，这日益使那些认知处理速度较慢的人处于不利地位。正如罗伯特·哈桑所写，福特主义时代以及"基于机器和工厂的流程有其特定的节奏，比今天慢得多"。相比之下，他继续写道，今天：





To be efficient is […] to be physically, cognitively, psychologically and metaphorically able to ‘move fast’ when the time comes. This may be a flexibility to change your job often, a flexibility regarding the way one does a job, a flexibility in your opinions (dogmatism is out for most of us), a flexibility with respect of your physical location, or [… to] be able to ‘synchronize’ with fast-changing scenarios and rapidly unfolding events.20

高效意味着……在时机来临时，能够在身体、认知、心理和隐喻意义上"快速行动"。这可能表现为频繁更换工作的灵活性、工作方式的灵活性、观点上的灵活性（对大多数人来说，教条主义已经过时）、地理位置上的灵活性，或者……能够与快速变化的场景和迅速展开的事件"同步"。 20





These economic requirements do not just affect adults in work, but also children, whose environments will be similarly determined by the broader social conditions of the time. With all this in mind, it is unsurprising that a diagnosis where a central criterion is ‘resistance to change’ or ‘need for sameness’ would rapidly expand from 1980 onward. Never before have humans been required to live at the velocities necessitated by the shifting and precarious post-Fordist world.

这些经济要求不仅影响工作中的成年人，也影响着儿童——他们的成长环境同样由当时更广泛的社会条件所决定。考虑到这一切，一种以"抗拒变化"或"渴求一成不变"为核心诊断标准的病症自 1980 年代起迅速蔓延，便不足为奇了。人类从未被要求以前所未有的速度适应后福特主义时代瞬息万变且充满不确定性的世界。



We also see similar dynamics with other diagnoses. Consider here how over this period attention too became increasingly scarce given the constant sensory and informational bombardments of the post-Fordist era. For instance, as Berardi stresses, in contemporary society we find

我们在其他诊断中也观察到类似的动态机制。不妨思考这一时期注意力如何因后福特时代持续不断的感觉与信息轰炸而日益稀缺。正如贝拉尔迪所强调的，当代社会中





visual and auditory messages in every inch of our visual space and every second of our time, The diffusion of screens in public spaces (railway stations, airports, city streets and squares), is an integral part of this abusive occupation […] Everywhere, attention is under siege […] A cognitive space overloaded with nervous incentives to act; this is the alienation of our times.21

视觉与听觉信息充斥着我们视野的每一寸空间与时间的每一秒钟，公共场所（火车站、机场、城市街道与广场）屏幕的泛滥正是这种侵扰性占据的组成部分……注意力无处不遭受围剿……认知空间充斥着刺激行动的神经信号：这正是我们这个时代的异化现象。 21





As the norms of cognitive attention became increasingly restrictive there came a great rise in people disenabled in such a way that came to be diagnosed as Attention Deficit Hyperactivity Disorder (ADHD). In line with Berardi’s example, research shows that more general sensory processing issues are common among children with ADHD and is associated with anxiety, interpersonal problems, and problems in educational attainment.22 Since the 1980s children and adults diagnosed with ADHD have, ever increasingly, required medication to enable functioning in line with educational and workplace demands alongside the cognitive stresses of day-to-day life. For instance, one study found that between 1992 and 2013 the prevalence of children under 16 taking medications for ADHD increased between three- and four-fold.23 Yet despite many finding medications useful, it remains the case that employees with ADHD tend to have chronic employment issues and are 60 per cent more likely to be fired when compared with the general population.24 Indeed, many of the questions on standard ADHD screening tests relate directly to work skills, including questions about trouble focusing on repetitive work or with planning and organising.

随着认知注意力的规范变得日益严苛，越来越多的人因此陷入功能障碍，最终被诊断为注意力缺陷多动障碍（ADHD）。正如贝拉尔迪所举例的那样，研究表明，更普遍的感官处理问题在患有 ADHD 的儿童中很常见，并且与焦虑、人际关系问题以及学业成就问题相关。 22 自 20 世纪 80 年代以来，被诊断为 ADHD 的儿童和成人越来越需要药物来帮助他们应对教育和工作场所的要求，以及日常生活中的认知压力。例如，一项研究发现，在 1992 年至 2013 年间，16 岁以下儿童服用 ADHD 药物的比例增加了三到四倍。 23 尽管许多人发现药物有用，但患有 ADHD 的员工往往面临长期的就业问题，与普通人群相比，他们被解雇的可能性高出 60%。 24 事实上，标准 ADHD 筛查测试中的许多问题直接与工作技能相关，包括关于难以专注于重复性工作或计划与组织方面的问题。



This is not to say these problems did not exist prior to post-Fordism, or that things like autism or ADHD are not real disabilities. They are no less ‘real’ than diabetes or dementia. But existing forms of difficulty or disablement, while to some extent grounded in atypical neurological development, were in many cases hugely amplified in this phase of capitalism. Traits that were previously relatively benign became associated with some level of disablement, while traits that might have only been minimally disabling became significantly so. This has increased as the intensification of capitalism has become so pervasive: it structures or at least taints almost every aspect of sensory experience and cognitive processing in day-to-day life, whether in work or in leisure time. It is not the technology itself that is the problem but rather that technology is primarily used in service of capital, and the various systems of domination that capitalism is intertwined with, which leave so many of us constantly fatigued, far beyond the workplace. And this increasingly stifles the development and thriving of even those who diverge in a relatively minimal way from the ever-more restrictive cognitive norms of the age.

这并不是说这些问题在后福特主义之前不存在，也不是说像孤独谱系或注意力缺陷多动障碍这样的问题不是真实的残疾。它们与糖尿病或痴呆症一样"真实"。但现有的困难或残疾形式，虽然在某种程度上源于非典型的神经发育，但在资本主义的这一阶段，许多情况下被极大地放大了。以前相对良性的特征开始与某种程度的残疾相关联，而那些可能只有轻微残疾的特征则变得显著严重。随着资本主义的加剧变得如此普遍，这种情况也在增加：它构建或至少污染了日常生活的几乎每一个感官体验和认知处理方面，无论是在工作中还是在休闲时间。问题不在于技术本身，而在于技术主要被用于服务资本，以及资本主义交织的各种统治体系，这使得我们中的许多人持续感到疲惫，远远超出了工作场所的范围。 而这种日益加剧的压抑，甚至对那些与时代日益严苛的认知规范仅有微小偏离者的成长与繁荣，也构成了阻碍。



Indeed, these forms of disablement are in significant part an extreme expression of issues faced across the general neurological spectrum of humanity. After all, the same problems affect everyone, not just those who are disabled in these conditions. In the scientific literature more generally, for instance, modern artificial lighting has been associated with depression and other health conditions;25 excessive exposure to screentime has been associated with chronic overstimulation, mental health conditions, and cognitive disablement;26 and noise annoyance has been associated with a two-fold increase in depression and anxiety, especially relating to noise pollution from aircraft, traffic, and industrial work.27 One study based on parental reports found that 5.3 per cent of playschool children now experience clinically significant levels of sensory processing disablement.28 And we have already seen how the alienation that follows intensive cognitive or emotional labour is harmful to all.

事实上，这些形式的失能状况在很大程度上是人类普遍神经谱系所面临问题的极端表现。毕竟，同样的问题影响着每个人，而不仅仅是在这些条件下失能的人。例如，在更广泛的科学文献中，现代人工照明与抑郁及其他健康问题相关； 25 过度接触屏幕时间与慢性过度刺激、心理健康问题和认知障碍相关； 26 而噪音困扰则与抑郁和焦虑的增加（尤其是与飞机、交通和工业工作产生的噪音污染相关）呈两倍增长。 27 一项基于家长报告的研究发现，目前有 5.3%的学龄前儿童经历了临床显著水平的感官处理障碍。 28 我们已经看到，高强度认知或情感劳动后的异化对所有人都是有害的。



Yet instead of being understood as relationally constituted between individual and environment, through the neo-Galtonian pathology paradigm these forms of disablement were framed as individual deficit. Interestingly, as Goldstein observed in 2012, most psychometricians ‘still appear to be working within the parameters set out around the time of Galton; typically either developing more complex modelling and analysis procedures or devising new measuring instruments’.29 When it comes to disability or disorder classification, as the psychologist Kurt Danzinger has detailed, this followed an older tradition whereby

然而，通过新高尔顿病理学范式，这些残障形式被框定为个体缺陷，而非被理解为个体与环境之间关系性构成的产物。有趣的是，正如戈尔茨坦在 2012 年所指出的，大多数心理测量学家"似乎仍在遵循高尔顿时代确立的框架工作；通常要么发展更复杂的建模与分析程序，要么设计新的测量工具"。 29 在残障或障碍分类方面，正如心理学家库尔特·丹齐格所详述的，这沿袭了一种更古老的传统，即





the Galtonian use of statistics greatly facilitated the artificial creation of new groups whose defining characteristic was based on performance on some psychological instrument, most commonly an intelligence test. A score on a mental test conferred membership in an abstract collectivity created for the purposes of psychological research. This opened up untold vistas for such research because psychologists could create these kinds of collectivity ad infinitum and then explore the statistical relationships between them.30

高尔顿式的统计学运用极大地促进了新群体的人为构建，这些群体的界定特征基于某些心理工具（最常见的是智力测试）的表现。心理测试的分数赋予了个体加入为心理学研究目的而创建的抽象集合体的资格。这为心理学研究开辟了前所未有的视野，因为心理学家可以无限地创建这类集合体，进而探索它们之间的统计关系。 30





Simultaneously, in line with Kraepelin’s 1919 proposal of a ‘mass psychiatry’ that would test ability for everything including the capacity to work, by the end of the twentieth century, psychometric testing had rapidly expanded. By this time, a dizzying array of new tests were developed and implemented in educational and workplace settings, for instance, to test employability or competence for even relatively menial roles.31

与此同时，根据克雷佩林 1919 年提出的“大众精神病学”理念——该理念主张测试包括工作能力在内的各项能力——到二十世纪末，心理测量测试已迅速扩展。此时，一系列令人眼花缭乱的新测试被开发出来，并在教育和工作场所中实施，例如，用于测试即使是相对低微职位的就业能力或胜任力。 31



In psychiatry, these new classifications were often reified through the notion of the ‘latent variable’, the assumed common cause inherent to the individual that underlay and could explain common results in psychometric testing. This allowed people with similar test results to be seen as sharing as-yet-unknown internal cognitive dysfunctions (empathy deficits, executive malfunctioning, etc.) or neurological dysfunctions (faulty mirror neurons, etc.). Biomedical researchers hypothesised that biomarkers would be found underlying these core cognitive deficiencies, leading to ever greater precision for diagnosis and treatment. The dominance of the pathology paradigm in this period allowed the idea to become wholly hegemonic that mental disorder stems from individual dysfunction.

在精神病学领域，这些新的分类常常通过"潜在变量"的概念被具体化——即假定个体内部存在某种共同的内在原因，这种原因能够解释心理测量测试中的普遍结果。这使得具有相似测试结果的人被视为共享着尚未被发现的内部认知功能障碍（如共情缺陷、执行功能失调等）或神经功能障碍（如镜像神经元异常等）。生物医学研究者假设，这些核心认知缺陷背后存在着可被发现的生物标志物，从而为诊断和治疗带来更高的精确性。在这一时期，病理学范式的统治地位使得"精神障碍源于个体功能障碍"这一观念变得完全霸权化。



NEOLIBERAL NORMALISATION

新自由主义正常化



Cultural practices of normalisation, where the divergent are changed to become more normal, also shifted following the Spitzerian revolution and the rise of neoliberalism. One place we see this regards the prison complex. During this period the numbers of people with psychiatric disabilities and learning disabilities incarcerated in the prison system continued to grow. By the beginning of the twenty-first century over 50% of prison inmates in the United States and the United Kingdom had dyslexia, while around a quarter have ADHD. Moreover ‘Some of the largest mental health centres in the United States currently operate behind bars, and 40 percent of people diagnosed with serious psychiatric disorders face arrest over their lifetimes’.32 Today, people with mental disorder diagnoses, especially Black people, are among the most likely to be arrested, be harassed by the police, or die in police custody.

在斯皮策革命和新自由主义兴起之后，旨在改变差异者使其更趋正常的文化实践也发生了转变。监狱体系便是这一现象的体现之一。在此期间，因精神障碍和学习障碍而被监禁的人数持续增长。到二十一世纪初，美国和英国监狱中超过 50%的囚犯患有阅读障碍，约四分之一患有注意力缺陷多动障碍。此外，“美国目前一些规模最大的心理健康中心设在监狱内，40%被诊断患有严重精神障碍的人一生中会面临被捕”。 32 如今，被诊断为精神障碍的人群，尤其是黑人，最有可能遭到逮捕、受到警察骚扰或在警方拘留期间死亡。



At the same time, a massively increased use of prison pharmaceuticals has been used alongside electronic tagging and biomedical risk assessment for prison inmates. Sociologist Ryan Hatch describes these as forms of ‘technocorrections’, which aim to reduce costs and subdue prison populations to make them more pliable. Thus by the year 2000 in the United States, for instance, ‘95 percent of maximum/high-security state prisons distributed psychotropics, compared to 88 percent of medium-security prisons and 62 percent of minimum/low-security prisons’.33 Liat Ben-Moshe has also emphasised how conditions in prison tend to make mental health worse and that even talking therapy often serves oppressive functions in prisons. In one scenario she describes from a US prison:

与此同时，监狱中电子监控和生物医学风险评估的使用大幅增加，伴随着药物的大量使用。社会学家瑞安·哈奇将这些称为“技术矫正”形式，旨在降低成本并压制囚犯群体，使其更易管理。例如，到 2000 年，在美国，“95%的最高/高度戒备州立监狱分发精神药物，而中等戒备监狱为 88%，最低/低度戒备监狱为 62%”。 33 利亚特·本-摩西也强调了监狱环境往往使心理健康状况恶化，即使在监狱中，谈话疗法也常常起到压迫作用。她描述了一个美国监狱的场景：





Most of the participants in this group therapy scene are black, all are men and each of them is sitting in a cage. This is not a hyperbole description but mere fact. Each of the participants in this therapy session is in a small cage with bars and locks, including chains around their ankles (where would they escape to in their tiny cage, we are not told). The presumed therapist (who looks phenotypically white) is sitting outside the cages, asking the men who are lined up in a row of cages how they are doing, how they progressed this week, inquiring about new body injuries he can observe, and so on. A guard is constantly circling the cages.34

在这场团体治疗场景中，大多数参与者是黑人，且均为男性，每个人都坐在笼子里。这并非夸张描述，而是客观事实。每位参与治疗者都被关在带铁栏和锁具的小笼中，脚踝还拴着锁链（至于他们能在狭小笼中逃往何处，文中并未说明）。那位疑似治疗师（从表型特征看像是白人）坐在笼外，向排成一列的笼中男性询问近况、本周进展，并检查他观察到的新伤情等等。一名警卫则持续在笼子周围巡视。 34





This, she notes, is the best mental health care inmates in US prisons tend to have access to.

她指出，这已是美国监狱囚犯通常能获得的最佳心理健康照护。



Outside the prison system, normalisation has increasingly been taken to be obligatory from younger and younger ages as the notion of mental disorder came to be seen as hereditary harmful dysfunction. For instance, with autism, behavioural interventions still focus on using a reward system to normalise neurodivergence. This has grown into a multi-billion-dollar industry with huge schools established, especially across the United States, to help enforce normalisation. Despite the protests of countless autistic activists who argue that such efforts are themselves a harmful and dehumanising form of conversion therapy, behavioural therapies are thus still the most widely used response in the United Kingdom and the United States and are regularly touted as the ‘gold standard’ of autism interventions.

在监狱系统之外，随着精神障碍被视为遗传性有害功能障碍，正常化要求正被施加于越来越年幼的群体。例如，针对孤独谱系的行为干预，其核心仍是通过奖励机制来"矫正"神经殊异性。这已发展成一个价值数十亿美元的产业，尤其是在美国各地建立了众多大型学校，以强制推行这种正常化。尽管无数孤独谱系活动家抗议此类干预本身就是一种有害且剥夺人性的转化治疗，行为疗法在英国和美国仍是最广泛采用的应对方式，并常被标榜为孤独症干预的"黄金标准"。



Through a similar logic, neoliberalism brought what Mark Fisher termed a ‘privatization of stress’.35 Here self-care became an ethical imperative for the individual, and a focus on self-management took over from state support, which was increasingly limited. Wellness and mindfulness industries have rapidly expanded in ways that function to help tired people adjust to increasingly long working hours and lower living conditions. In the United Kingdom, state support for anxiety or depression typically consists of a tiny number of CBT sessions, used with the explicit aim of returning people to work. This only increases alienation while leaving deeper problems and the social detriments of mental illness largely untouched. In some cases we also see a fusing of Szaszianism and neoliberal austerity politics. As Fisher drew attention to in 2009, in his discussion of the UK government benefits policy:

通过类似的逻辑，新自由主义带来了马克·费舍尔所称的“压力的私有化”。 35 在这里，自我关怀成为个人道德上的当务之急，对自我管理的关注取代了国家支持，而后者正日益受限。健康与正念产业迅速扩张，其运作方式旨在帮助疲惫的人们适应越来越长的工作时间和更低的生活条件。在英国，国家对焦虑或抑郁的支持通常只包括寥寥几次认知行为疗法（CBT）课程，其明确目标就是让人们重返工作岗位。这只会加剧异化，同时让更深层次的问题以及精神疾病的社会危害在很大程度上得不到解决。在某些情况下，我们还看到了萨兹主义与新自由主义紧缩政治的融合。正如费舍尔在 2009 年讨论英国政府福利政策时所强调的：





It is telling, in this context of rising rates of mental illness, that New Labour committed itself, early in its third term in government, to removing people from Incapacity Benefit, implying that many, if not most, claimants are malingerers.

在这种精神疾病发病率不断上升的背景下，新工党在其第三届政府任期初期就承诺要将人们从丧失工作能力福利中剔除，这暗示着许多（即使不是大多数）申领者是在装病，这一点很能说明问题。





In fact, he goes on,

事实上，他接着指出，





A significant proportion of claimants, for instance, are people psychologically damaged as a consequence of the capitalist realist insistence that industries such as mining are no longer economically viable […] Many have simply buckled under the terrifyingly unstable conditions of post-Fordism.36

例如，相当一部分申请者是在资本主义现实主义坚持认为采矿业等产业不再具有经济可行性的背景下遭受心理创伤的人……许多人仅仅是在后福特主义极其不稳定的条件下崩溃了。 36





Here we see how the culturally influential Szaszian notion that all ‘mental illness’ is really people pretending to be ill to avoid responsibility, combined with increased rates of stress, panic, and depression, feeds into neoliberal ideology. For Szasz as for the neoliberal, everyone is just an individual, fully responsible for their own positioning and their ability or inability to deal with it. Without a clearly defined and identifiable biological impairment, they are – following the influence of the Szaszian tradition and its grounding in a Hayekian worldview – considered malingerers, deemed to be pretending to suffer from false illnesses that do not really exist.

在此我们看到，文化上颇具影响力的萨兹观点——即所有“精神疾病”实际上都是人们为了逃避责任而假装生病——与日益加剧的压力、恐慌和抑郁相结合，如何助长了新自由主义意识形态。对萨兹和新自由主义者而言，每个人都只是独立的个体，完全为自己的处境以及应对（或无力应对）的能力负责。在没有明确界定和可识别的生物性损伤的情况下，他们——受萨兹传统及其哈耶克世界观基础的影响——被视为装病者，被认为是在假装患有实际上并不存在的虚假疾病。



At the same time, in an echo of the 1940s, for those disabilities that were recognised, this period was accompanied by an increased framing of what were now seen to be brain disorders as economic ‘burdens’. For instance, in a 2011 article, Gustavsson et al. wrote that:

与此同时，与 20 世纪 40 年代的情形遥相呼应，对于那些被承认的残障类型，这一时期也伴随着一种日益强化的叙事框架——将如今被视为脑部障碍的病症定性为经济"负担"。例如，古斯塔夫松等人在 2011 年的一篇文章中写道：





The total cost of disorders of the brain [in Europe] was estimated at €798 billion in 2010. Direct costs constitute the majority of costs (37% direct healthcare costs and 23% direct non-medical costs) whereas the remaining 40% were indirect costs associated with patients’ production losses […] disorders of the brain likely constitute the number one economic challenge for European health care, now and in the future.37

[欧洲]脑部障碍的总成本在 2010 年估计为 7980 亿欧元。直接成本占主要部分（37%为直接医疗成本，23%为直接非医疗成本），而剩余的 40%是与患者生产力损失相关的间接成本……脑部障碍很可能构成欧洲医疗保健当前及未来首要的经济挑战。 37





In turn, the idea that mental disorders were brain disorders that stemmed from hereditary risk factors, coupled with the rise of neoliberalism and worries about ‘production losses’, brought new forms of reproductive control. Instead of being imposed by the state, however, they are either offered as services or left to private organisations. Where prenatal tests for neurodivergent disabilities are available, such as in the case of Down’s syndrome, termination rates have rapidly increased, contributing to a decline in funding for social support and research into quality of life. In the United Kingdom, neurodivergent people have reported that private sperm banks regularly turn away donors due to diagnoses such as dyslexia or autism.38 Given the neoliberal order, in such cases these processes are not determined by authoritarian government policy but by private organisations and market forces functioning in line with hegemonic neuronormative ideals.

相应地，认为精神障碍是源于遗传风险因素的大脑障碍这一观念，加上新自由主义的兴起和对"生产损失"的担忧，催生了新的生殖控制形式。然而，这些控制不再由国家强制实施，而是要么作为服务提供，要么交由私人组织处理。在能够进行产前神经殊异残疾检测的地方，例如唐氏综合征，终止妊娠率迅速上升，导致社会支持和生活质量研究的资金减少。在英国，神经殊异人士报告称，私人精子库经常因阅读障碍或孤独谱系等诊断而拒绝捐赠者。 38 鉴于新自由主义秩序，在此类情况下，这些过程并非由威权政府政策决定，而是由遵循霸权性神经规范理想的私人组织和市场力量所主导。



By contrast, Anne McGuire has described how the child with closer proximity with neurotypicality is represented as a good investment:

相比之下，安妮·麦圭尔描述了更接近神经典型性的儿童如何被塑造成一项良好的投资：





The normative time of childhood – understood, simultaneously as a biological time of growth and development and as a sentimental/nostalgic time of innocence and hope – is precisely that time of seemingly infinite ‘laters’; the child is positioned as ‘early on’ on the (normative) biological timeline and therefore is understood as having more of that desired and desirable commodity of time, more future yet-to-be-realized. In a neoliberal regime where ‘time is money’, the child is figured as ‘time-rich’ and so represents a good investment opportunity indeed.39

童年的规范性时间——同时被理解为成长与发展的生物时间，以及纯真与希望的情感/怀旧时间——正是那看似充满无限“以后”的时期；儿童被置于（规范性）生物时间线的“早期”，因此被理解为拥有更多那种被渴望且可欲的时间商品，更多尚未实现的未来。在新自由主义体制下，“时间就是金钱”，儿童被塑造成“时间富足者”，因而确实代表着良好的投资机会。 39





In short, the world was made increasingly uninhabitable for neurodivergent people, and then individuals or private companies were left to determine whether neurodivergent life should be reproduced in a world that fails to accommodate neurodivergence.

简而言之，这个世界对神经殊异人群变得越来越不宜居，然后由个体或私营公司来决定，在一个无法适应神经殊异性的世界里，是否应该繁衍神经殊异的生命。



While each of these practices stems from a variety of different factors, part of what unites them is that each is in part predicated by Spitzer’s idea that there is something not just inherently dysfunctional but also something inherently harmful about neurodivergent disabilities. Indeed, as I will come back to, this was sometimes to the point that it is considered better for some neurodivergent people to not exist at all. With this in mind, it is also important to consider that, during this time, the reach of the Galtonian paradigm grew further still. Around the turn of the millennium, conceptions of the good human life itself were also increasingly Galtonianised.

尽管这些做法各有不同的成因，但将它们联系起来的部分原因在于，每一种做法都部分基于斯皮策的观点：神经殊异的残疾不仅本质上是功能失调的，而且本质上是有害的。事实上，正如我稍后会再次提及的，这种观点有时甚至到了认为某些神经殊异者根本不存在更好的地步。考虑到这一点，同样重要的是要认识到，在此期间，高尔顿范式的范围进一步扩大。在世纪之交前后，关于美好人类生活本身的观念也日益被高尔顿化。



Culturally, we see this in how, through the neoliberal era a kind of individualism grew whereby the majority of people in the United States, according to a number of studies, came to identify as above-average in terms of intelligence.40 Despite this being an illusion – by definition, it cannot be the case that most people are above-average – the idea that people’s economic positioning and accumulation of material goods allowed this illusion to continue. Few wanted to be abnormal – weird, strange, and so forth. Yet in line with Galtonian ideology everyone wanted to be better than normal – and most believed themselves to be so.

在文化层面，我们通过新自由主义时代看到一种个人主义的兴起，根据多项研究，美国大多数人开始认为自己的智力高于平均水平。 40 尽管这是一种错觉——从定义上讲，大多数人不可能高于平均水平——但人们的经济地位和物质财富的积累使这种错觉得以持续。很少有人愿意被视为异常——古怪、奇特等等。然而，根据高尔顿的意识形态，每个人都想比正常更好——而且大多数人相信自己确实如此。



Indeed, the Galtonianisation of the good life has occurred even among highly nuanced ethicists. For instance, in her 2006 book Frontiers of Justice, philosopher Martha Nussbaum proposed that the ‘species norm (duly evaluated) tells us what the appropriate benchmark is for judging whether a given creature has decent opportunities for flourishing’. For Nussbaum, this makes normalisation a moral imperative, not just a medical one. Hence for autism, she proposes, special efforts’ are required to help autistics ‘attain the core capabilities that form part of that species norm’.41 Such ways of thinking increasingly naturalised and individualised the harms associated with neurodivergence, and made the normative necessity of normalising neurodivergence likewise seem natural.

确实，高尔顿式美好生活的理念甚至已渗透到那些思想极为精微的伦理学家之中。例如，哲学家玛莎·努斯鲍姆在其 2006 年的著作《正义的前沿》中提出，"物种规范（经过恰当评估）告诉我们，判断一个生物体是否拥有体面的繁荣机会，其恰当的基准是什么"。对努斯鲍姆而言，这使得规范化不仅是一种医学要求，更成为一种道德律令。因此，对于孤独谱系，她主张需要"特殊努力"来帮助孤独症人士"获得构成该物种规范一部分的核心能力"。 41 这类思维方式日益将神经殊异性相关的伤害自然化和个体化，同时也使得规范化神经殊异性的规范性必要性显得同样自然而然。



Around the same time, the demand to go to therapy continued to be enforced. The neoliberal privatisation of stress coupled with the ever-growing division of labour under capitalism brought an increased pressure for individuals to outsource their emotional processing to new and expanding therapy industries. Yet this has created a pressure for busy, cash-strapped workers to pay for unaffordable therapy that might not work and could even be harmful, while allowing wealthier people to position themselves as morally enlightened given their capacity to continually outsource their emotional processing to the best therapists, who can charge hundreds of pounds or dollars an hour that is then converted into cultural capital by wealthy clients.

与此同时，接受心理治疗的要求仍在持续推行。新自由主义将压力私有化，加之资本主义下日益细化的劳动分工，促使个人将情绪处理外包给新兴且不断扩张的心理治疗行业。然而，这给忙碌且资金紧张的工薪阶层带来了压力，他们不得不支付可能无效甚至有害的、负担不起的治疗费用；而富人则因其有能力持续将情绪处理外包给最优秀的治疗师——这些治疗师每小时收费数百英镑或美元，随后被富裕客户转化为文化资本——从而得以将自己定位为道德上开明的人士。



More recently still physician-assisted suicide has been legalised, including in Canada, where it is increasingly used, as Jeremy Appel writes, ‘for people with disabilities to apply to die rather than survive on meager benefits’.42 As Appel details, while the rationale is about choice and harm reduction for people with terminal illnesses and in great pain, in practice ‘euthanasia in Canada represents the cynical endgame of social provisioning within the brutal logic of late-stage capitalism’. It begins with starving ‘you of the funding you need to live a dignified life’, and then posits the decision to then die as a matter of freedom rather than coercion. While the choice for assisted suicide can genuinely increase autonomy, when this is granted in a broader neoliberal economy it leaves many little space for autonomy in practice.

最近，医生协助自杀也已合法化，包括在加拿大，正如杰里米·阿佩尔所写，这种做法越来越多地“被残疾人用来申请死亡，而不是靠微薄的福利生存”。 42 正如阿佩尔详细说明的那样，虽然其理由是为绝症患者和极度痛苦的人提供选择和减少伤害，但实际上，“在晚期资本主义的残酷逻辑下，加拿大的安乐死代表了社会供给的愤世嫉俗的终局”。它始于剥夺“你过上有尊严生活所需的资金”，然后将选择死亡视为自由而非强迫的决定。虽然选择协助自杀确实可以增加自主权，但在更广泛的新自由主义经济中，这种做法实际上给许多人留下的自主空间微乎其微。



Hence through neoliberal ideology, and eased by the Spitzerian conception of disorder as harmful dysfunction, normalisation, and eugenic control have continued. The main difference between contemporary approaches and Galton’s is that, while Galton framed the social harmfulness of subnormal cognition more primarily at the societal level and thus a task for governmental intervention, contemporary approaches tend to frame the badness more primarily at the individual level and thus a matter of individual responsibility. On this privatisation of eugenic responsibility, no longer should neurodivergence be eliminated because it is a threat to society, but because it is inherently harmful and thus an inherent threat to its own bearer. Hence in her 2008 book The Ethics of Autism, bioethicist Professor Deborah Barnbaum argued that, once prenatal diagnostic technology is capable, there will be a moral obligation to abort autistic foetuses on the grounds that being autistic is inherently incompatible with living a good human life.

因此，通过新自由主义意识形态，并借助斯皮策将障碍视为有害功能障碍、正常化和优生控制的概念，这些做法得以延续。当代方法与高尔顿的主要区别在于，高尔顿更多地将低于正常认知的社会危害性置于社会层面，从而视其为政府干预的任务；而当代方法则更多地将这种"不良性"置于个体层面，从而视其为个人责任。在这种优生责任的私有化下，神经殊异性不再因其对社会构成威胁而被消除，而是因为它本身具有危害性，从而对其承载者构成内在威胁。因此，生物伦理学教授黛博拉·巴恩鲍姆在其 2008 年的著作《孤独症的伦理》中主张，一旦产前诊断技术成熟，就有道德义务终止孤独谱系胎儿的妊娠，理由是身为孤独谱系本质上与过上美好人生不相容。



---

Empire of Normality



9



The neurodiversity movement

神经多样性运动



In June 1997 a young woman taking a part-time sociology degree read an article in the New York Times. Written by a journalist called Harvey Blume, the article, titled ‘Autistics are Connecting in Cyberspace’, instantly stoked Judy Singer’s attention.1 Given the recent wider availability of the internet, Blume wrote, ‘many of the United States’ autistics are doing the very thing the syndrome supposedly deters them from doing – communicating’. Indeed, it was not just that they found connecting easier online than in person. More than this, Blume detailed, an increasing number of these ‘autistics are neither willing nor able to give up their own customs. Instead, they are proposing a new social compact, one emphasizing neurological pluralism’. That is, rather than giving in to pressure to act more ‘normally’, they were resisting this, and, in doing so, pushing back against the idea that autism itself was in need of fixing at all.

1997 年 6 月，一位攻读兼职社会学学位的年轻女性在《纽约时报》上读到一篇文章。这篇由记者哈维·布鲁姆撰写的文章题为《孤独谱系人士在网络空间建立联系》，立刻引起了朱迪·辛格的注意。 1 布鲁姆写道，鉴于互联网近期的普及，"美国的许多孤独谱系人士正在做着这种综合征据称会阻碍他们去做的事情——交流"。事实上，他们不仅发现在线交流比面对面更容易。更重要的是，布鲁姆详细描述道，越来越多的这些"孤独谱系人士既不愿意也无法放弃他们自己的习俗。相反，他们正在提出一种新的社会契约，强调神经系统的多元性"。也就是说，他们并没有屈服于表现得更加"正常"的压力，而是在抵制这种压力，并在此过程中，反对那种认为孤独谱系本身需要被"修复"的观念。



At that time, Singer was studying sociology at the University of Technology Sydney, in Australia. After previously dropping out of a medicine degree, Singer had turned to sociology to make sense of her political interests. One of these interests regarded the politics of disability. By the time that she read Blume’s article, Singer had already begun to identify as being on the autism spectrum – then a little-known diagnosis, mainly associated with social and communication problems alongside restricted interests and habits. Finding that many problems in her own life mirrored those of many autistic people, she had already joined various online autistic groups where she met other autistic people. What’s more, Singer had also already begun thinking about autism through the sociological lens of disability studies, which framed disablement as a societal more than an individual problem.

当时，辛格正在澳大利亚悉尼科技大学攻读社会学。此前她从医学学位辍学后，转而投身社会学，以理解自己的政治兴趣。这些兴趣之一涉及残障政治。在读到布鲁姆的文章时，辛格已经开始认同自己属于孤独谱系——当时这是一个鲜为人知的诊断，主要与社会交往和沟通问题以及受限的兴趣和习惯相关。她发现自己生活中的许多问题与许多孤独谱系群体的经历相似，因此已经加入了多个线上孤独谱系社群，并在那里结识了其他孤独谱系人士。更重要的是，辛格已经开始通过残障研究的社会学视角来思考孤独谱系，该视角将残障更多地视为一个社会问题而非个人问题。



While all this made Blume’s article pique her interest, what she related to most strongly was the ‘neurological pluralism’ that he described, and the related refusal to give up autistic customs in a neurotypical world. For more than anything else, Singer’s own emerging understanding of autistic resistance was grounded in her experience of being part of the Jewish diaspora. That is, of being part of a group of outsiders who refused to assimilate – and who therefore paid the price.2 After all, Singer herself was the daughter of a Holocaust survivor who had moved to Australia after the Second World War. And Singer herself had grown up feeling like an outsider even in the country of her birth. It was this heritage and experience, as part of a diaspora, that made her relate so strongly to this new politics of neurological pluralism and its associated refusal to give up autistic customs in the face of overwhelming societal pressure.

尽管这一切都让布卢姆的文章引起了她的兴趣，但她最为共鸣的是他所描述的“神经多样性”，以及与之相关的在神经典型世界中拒绝放弃孤独谱系习俗的立场。因为，辛格自身对孤独谱系抵抗的初步理解，更多地植根于她作为犹太流散群体一员的经历。也就是说，她属于一个拒绝同化的外来者群体——并因此付出了代价。 2 毕竟，辛格本人就是一位大屠杀幸存者的女儿，这位幸存者在二战后移居澳大利亚。而辛格自己，即使在出生国成长，也始终感觉自己像个局外人。正是这种作为流散群体一部分的传承和经历，让她对这种新的神经多样性政治及其在面对强大社会压力时拒绝放弃孤独谱系习俗的立场产生了如此强烈的共鸣。



And so it was that on reading Blume’s article, Singer quickly contacted him and signed up to become a member of this new community, based in a group called Independent Living on the Autism Spectrum. Within a year, she would not only immerse herself in this community, but go on to propose the more concise concept of ‘neurodiversity’ and provide the first sustained sociological analysis positioning these ideas in the field of disability studies. It was this that allowed her to call for a ‘politics of neurological diversity, or neurodiversity’ in a 1999 book chapter and thus, accompanied by Blume’s reporting, helped this pioneering community of autistic activists spark the rise of the neurodiversity movement across the globe.

因此，在阅读了布鲁姆的文章后，辛格迅速联系了他，并加入了这个名为“孤独谱系独立生活”的新社群。不到一年时间，她不仅深入融入了这个社群，还进一步提出了更为简洁的“神经多样性”概念，并首次在残障研究领域对这些理念进行了持续的社会学分析。正是基于此，她在 1999 年的一本书的章节中呼吁建立“神经多样性政治，或神经多样性”，并借助布鲁姆的报道，帮助这个由孤独谱系活动家组成的先驱社群在全球范围内点燃了神经多样性运动的兴起。



In this seminal work, what Singer suggested was that neurodiversity should be recognised as ‘an addition to the familiar political categories of class/gender/race’.3 By conceptualising autism as an unrecognised intersection, Singer envisioned a new civil rights movement that could lead to the development of what she called an ‘ecological’ society. For Singer, this society would view neurodiversity much in the way conservationists view biodiversity, and would thus be geared towards changing social and material conditions to accommodate and conserve autistic ways of being. This would include making policy and practices more inclusive, and constructing cognitive niches to help cultivate autistic thriving and inclusion. It would be precisely at odds with the dominant way of organising society, which segregated disabled people and routinely placed great pressure on autistics to become more ‘normal’. While the core ideas of the movement were developed communally by countless advocates and activists, Singer’s contribution was to ground these emerging ideas in the body of theory developed by disability studies. It was this that established the theoretical basis that has since guided the movement and its tactics and aspirations.

在这部开创性著作中，辛格提出应将神经多样性视为"对阶级/性别/种族等传统政治类别的补充"。 3 通过将孤独谱系概念化为未被承认的交叉维度，辛格构想了一场可能催生她所谓"生态型"社会的新民权运动。在她看来，这种社会将以环保主义者看待生物多样性的方式来看待神经多样性，从而致力于改变社会与物质条件，以接纳并保护孤独谱系的存在方式。这将包括制定更具包容性的政策与实践，构建认知生态位以促进孤独谱系者的蓬勃发展与融入。这种理念恰恰与主流的社会组织方式背道而驰——后者将残障人士隔离在外，并持续对孤独谱系者施加成为更"正常"人群的巨大压力。虽然这场运动的核心思想是由无数倡导者与活动家共同孕育的，但辛格的贡献在于将这些新兴理念植根于残障研究领域发展的理论体系之中。 正是这一点奠定了此后指导该运动及其策略与愿景的理论基础。



DISABILITY THEORY

残障理论



To understand where these ideas first came from, we have to go back a bit further. All the way back, in fact, to 1968, when a 30-year-old Vic Finkelstein entered the United Kingdom as a refugee. Finkelstein was a political activist and had been imprisoned for his work in the anti-apartheid movement. He was then banned from South Africa for five years as he was suspected of being a communist. What the authorities who imprisoned him didn’t realise is that their treatment of him would help him develop an idea that would change the world.

要理解这些思想最初从何而来，我们必须再往前追溯。事实上，要一直追溯到 1968 年，当时 30 岁的维克·芬克尔斯坦以难民身份进入英国。芬克尔斯坦是一位政治活动家，曾因参与反种族隔离运动而入狱。随后他被禁止进入南非五年，因为他被怀疑是共产主义者。监禁他的当局没有意识到的是，他们对他的对待将帮助他发展出一个改变世界的理念。



For the authorities, the issue with Finkelstein was that, after breaking his neck in an accident at 16, he had used a wheelchair ever since. This meant that the government had been forced to make adjustments to accommodate his impairment in order to imprison him. But because they found ways to accommodate his impairment when it suited them, Finkelstein began to wonder whether governments could – and, indeed, should – be pressured to make accommodations by default. During his 18-month detention, he also began to see more similarities between his experience of disability segregation and the apartheid he had been protesting. This led him to explore how disability segregation was the result of contingent historical forces, which might possibly be changed.

对当局而言，芬克尔斯坦的问题在于，他 16 岁时因事故导致颈部骨折，此后便一直使用轮椅。这意味着政府不得不为适应他的损伤而做出调整，以便将其监禁。但由于当局在方便时找到了适应其损伤的方法，芬克尔斯坦开始思考，政府是否能够——甚至是否应该——被迫默认提供便利设施。在 18 个月的拘留期间，他也开始更多地看到自己的残障隔离经历与他所抗议的种族隔离之间的相似之处。这促使他探索残障隔离是如何成为特定历史力量的结果，而这种状况或许是可以改变的。



These ideas were formalised in the 1970s by the Union of Physically Impaired Against Segregation, or UPIAS, a radical group of Marxist disability activists who used to meet in a pub in London. This group had been co-founded in 1972 by Finkelstein and another disabled activist, Paul Hunt, who had been confined in institutions across England since he was a child. Based on their combined experiences, they came to see their disablement as the product of material social factors rather than a mere problem with the body. This way of thinking was clarified in a 1975 document titled Fundamental Principles of Disability, where they proposed what came to be called the ‘social model’ of disability.

这些理念在 20 世纪 70 年代由"反对隔离的肢体残障者联盟"（UPIAS）正式提出，该组织是一个由马克思主义残障活动家组成的激进团体，他们常在伦敦的一家酒吧聚会。该组织由芬克尔斯坦和另一位残障活动家保罗·亨特于 1972 年共同创立，亨特自幼便被禁锢在英格兰各地的收容机构中。基于共同的经历，他们逐渐认识到自身的残障是社会物质因素的产物，而非仅仅是身体的问题。这种思维方式在 1975 年发布的《残障基本原则》文件中得到明确阐述，他们在其中提出了后来被称为残障"社会模式"的理论。



They compared their new model to the individual or medical model. On the medical model, disability is taken to be caused by impairment or dysfunction. The idea is that something is wrong with a person’s body, and that this causes that person to be unable to do normal things. On this traditional – and then still largely hegemonic – view, disability is a physiological tragedy that afflicts the individual. In many cases it is seen to inherently impede the possibility of living a full and good life. The best the individual can hope for is for medical treatment that minimises the disabling effects of their impairment in day-to-day life.

他们将这一新模式与个体模式或医疗模式进行了对比。在医疗模式中，残障被认为是由损伤或功能障碍引起的。其核心观点是：人的身体存在某种缺陷，导致其无法完成正常活动。在这种传统且当时仍占主导地位的视角下，残障被视为一种折磨个体的生理悲剧。在许多情况下，它被认为本质上阻碍了人们过上充实美好生活的可能性。个体所能期待的最好结果，就是通过医疗手段来尽量减少其损伤在日常生活中造成的残障影响。



UPIAS rejected almost everything about this traditional framing. The core theoretical move made by UPIAS was to reject the causal link between bodily impairment and disablement. Instead, the Union of Physically Impaired Against Segregation proposed that it is

UPIAS 几乎完全否定了这种传统框架。该联盟在理论上的核心突破，在于切断了身体损伤与残障之间的因果关系。相反，反隔离肢体损伤者联盟提出：





society which disables physically impaired people. Disability is something imposed on top of our impairments by the way we are unnecessarily isolated and excluded from full participation in society.4

是社会使肢体损伤者成为残障。残障是在我们既有损伤之上，因遭受不必要的孤立、被排斥在充分参与社会之外而强加于我们的负担。 4





In this view, material conditions and societal structures and practices, such as the lack of ramps to access buildings, ‘imposed’ disablement on people with physical impairment. This acknowledged that the impairment was real and part of the body but refused the assumption that this implied that disability is an individual tragedy. Viewed this way, the problem of disability is primarily one of marginalisation and oppression, not simply an individual medical matter. In other words, disability – or at least physical disability, since UPIAS excluded cognitive disability from their account – is no longer an individual medical problem but a problem relating to our social and material conditions.

在这种观点下，物质条件和社会结构及实践——例如建筑物缺乏无障碍坡道——对具有身体损伤的人“强加”了残障。这承认了损伤是真实存在的、是身体的一部分，但拒绝接受这意味着残障是一种个人悲剧的假设。如此看来，残障问题主要是一个边缘化和压迫的问题，而不仅仅是个人的医疗问题。换言之，残障——或者至少是身体障碍，因为 UPIAS 在其论述中排除了认知障碍——不再是一个个人的医疗问题，而是一个与我们社会和物质条件相关的问题。



While the social model is generally dated back to UPIAS, it is notable that other radical groups were developing similar insights at around the same time. For instance, as Sami Schalk has detailed, the Black Panthers, the US Black power and Marxist-Leninist organisation, had also begun seeing disabled liberation as bound up with collective liberation. Thus, by the late 1970s the Black Panthers were supporting radical disability activism. They ‘took quickly to the social model of disability because it paralleled their own understanding of race and class oppression as stemming from the biases and failures of larger society’.5

虽然社会模式通常可追溯至 UPIAS，但值得注意的是，其他激进团体在同一时期也发展出了类似的见解。例如，正如萨米·沙尔克所详述的，美国黑人权力和马克思列宁主义组织黑豹党也开始将残障解放视为与集体解放紧密相连。因此，到 1970 年代末，黑豹党已在支持激进的残障行动主义。他们“迅速接纳了残障的社会模式，因为这与他们自己对种族和阶级压迫的理解相平行——即认为压迫源于更广泛社会的偏见与缺陷”。 5



The social model and other similar analyses developed elsewhere served as the theoretical basis for the disabled persons’ movement, which mainly focused on physical disability for the first few decades. By focusing on how attitudes, physical structures, social expectations, and inadequate social support stifled the functioning and flourishing of disabled people, this movement was able to make significant gains in legal and social recognition, and in removing disabling barriers and challenging segregation. This broader movement is precisely why, today in the United Kingdom and other countries, construction routinely includes disabled car parking spaces, accessible toilets, ramps, and much more. This is because it brought about significant legal gains establishing disability rights in the United Kingdom, the United States, and elsewhere.

社会模式及其他在各地发展的类似分析，构成了残障人士运动的理论基础，该运动在最初几十年主要聚焦于身体障碍。通过关注态度、物理结构、社会期望以及不足的社会支持如何阻碍残障人士的功能发挥与蓬勃发展，这一运动在法律与社会认可方面取得了重大进展，并成功消除了致残性障碍、挑战了隔离制度。正是这一更广泛的运动，使得如今在英国及其他国家，建筑规划中常规包含残障人士停车位、无障碍卫生间、坡道等设施。这是因为它在英国、美国等地促成了确立残障权利的重大法律成果。



It was this way of thinking – rather than the Szaszian tradition – that early autistic activists drew on to begin challenging the idea that the disablement they experienced was wholly down to individual impairments. For instance, according to early autism rights advocate Jim Sinclair in a seminal 1993 article, the tragedy of autism occurred ‘not because of what we are, but because of the things that happen to us’ in a world that failed to accommodate autistic modes of processing and communication.6 Autistic activists also argued that many problems in learning and understanding were down to sensory environments not accommodating autistic sensory processing styles. If physical structure, assumptions, expectations, and norms changed, much autistic disablement would be eased. They also argued that different minds could be seen as having different specialisations, and that divergent minds were not necessarily deficient.

正是这种思维方式——而非萨兹式的传统——被早期的孤独谱系活动家所借鉴，开始挑战他们所经历的障碍完全归因于个体损伤的观点。例如，根据早期孤独症权利倡导者吉姆·辛克莱在 1993 年一篇开创性文章中的说法，孤独症的悲剧之所以发生，“并非因为我们是谁，而是因为在一个未能适应孤独谱系处理与沟通模式的世界里，发生在我们身上的事情”。 6 孤独谱系活动家还认为，学习和理解中的许多问题源于感官环境未能适应孤独谱系的感官处理方式。如果物理结构、假设、期望和规范得以改变，许多孤独谱系的障碍将会得到缓解。他们也主张，不同的心智可以被视为拥有不同的专长，而差异化的心智未必是缺陷。



It was this that led Blume to report on this emerging idea of ‘neurological pluralism’. And as Singer has noted in retrospect, it also provided the ‘intellectual framework’ for her seminal work. Part of Singer’s intervention was thus to formalise and clarify the insights of early autistic activists who applied the social model to neurological disability for the first time – and then used this as the basis for a new movement that would be part of the broader disabled persons movement.

正是这一点促使布鲁姆报道了这种新兴的"神经多样性"理念。正如辛格事后回顾所言，这也为她开创性的工作提供了"智识框架"。因此，辛格的贡献部分在于将早期孤独谱系活动家的洞见系统化与明晰化——这些活动家首次将社会模式应用于神经性残障领域，并以此为基础开创了这场新运动，使之成为更广泛的残障人士运动的一部分。



DIVERSITY

多样性



The diversity in ‘neurodiversity’ comes from two sources. The first was the shift towards celebrating other forms of human diversity – cultural, sexual, and so forth – that arose following the major civil rights and pride movements of the twentieth century. Alongside these, early neurodiversity proponents began to ask whether neurological divergence could similarly be celebrated and be a locus of pride rather than being seen as an inherently tragic deviation. It was on this basis that neurodivergent people began to reclaim diagnostic classifications – autism, dyspraxia, and so forth – to allow recognition of shared forms of disablement while resisting the idea that this disablement stemmed from individual dysfunction. Notably, this allowed them to avoid the Szaszian mistake of denying recognition of disablement, while still positioning them to collectively push back against wrongful pathologisation and control. In this it kept the benefits of anti-psychiatry while avoiding its most harmful aspects.

“神经多样性”中的“多样性”源自两个源头。其一是二十世纪主要民权运动和骄傲运动兴起后，转向颂扬其他形式的人类多样性——文化、性别等——的转变。与此同时，早期的神经多样性倡导者开始提出疑问：神经系统的差异是否同样值得庆祝，能否成为自豪感的来源，而非被视为一种固有的悲剧性偏差。正是基于此，神经殊异者开始重新主张诊断分类——如孤独谱系、发育性协调障碍等——以承认共同的障碍形式，同时抵制这种障碍源于个体功能障碍的观点。值得注意的是，这使他们避免了萨兹式的错误，即否认障碍的存在，同时仍能共同抵制错误的病理化和控制。在此过程中，它保留了反精神病学的益处，同时避免了其最具危害的方面。



The other source of the ‘diversity’ in ‘neurodiversity’, which is more relevant for understanding the most original contribution of neurodiversity theory, was the shift towards viewing biodiversity as a vital part of what sustains broader ecosystems. This had emerged in the 1960s as more scientists and activists became concerned with how capital’s need to constantly consume natural resources for profit had not just led to the depletion of finite resources but the destruction of ecological equilibrium. By the 1990s the idea that biodiversity should be valued and conserved had entered the more progressive elements of public consciousness – and it was this that Singer and Blume extended to theorise the concept of neurological diversity.

“神经多样性”中“多样性”的另一个来源，对于理解神经多样性理论最原创的贡献更为相关，是转向将生物多样性视为维持更广泛生态系统的重要组成部分。这一观点在 20 世纪 60 年代出现，当时越来越多的科学家和活动家开始关注资本为利润不断消耗自然资源的需求，这不仅导致了有限资源的枯竭，还破坏了生态平衡。到了 20 世纪 90 年代，生物多样性应被重视和保护的理念已进入公众意识中较为进步的部分——而正是这一点被辛格和布鲁姆扩展，用以理论化神经多样性的概念。



We see this when we consider how the term ‘neurodiversity’ was first used in print by Harvey Blume in 1998. (While Blume helped develop the concept in email conversations with Singer, he was able to publish first.) Blume framed the concept precisely as a challenge to the concept of the normal brain. In his words:

当我们考虑“神经多样性”一词在 1998 年首次由哈维·布鲁姆在印刷品中使用时，就能看到这一点。（虽然布鲁姆在与辛格的电子邮件对话中帮助发展了这一概念，但他得以首先发表。）布鲁姆将这一概念明确表述为对正常大脑概念的挑战。用他的话来说：





The common assumption in cognitive studies these days is that [in] the human brain […] the occasional bug is inevitable: hence autism and other departures from the neurological norm. [Autistics are suggesting] another way of looking at this. Neurodiversity may be every bit as crucial for the human race as biodiversity is for life in general. Who can say what form of wiring will prove best at any given moment?7

如今认知研究中的普遍假设是，人类大脑中偶尔出现故障是不可避免的：因此产生了孤独谱系及其他偏离神经学常态的现象。孤独谱系人士提出了另一种看待此问题的方式。神经多样性对人类的重要性，或许丝毫不亚于生物多样性对整体生命的重要性。谁能断言在特定时刻，何种神经连接方式将被证明是最优的呢？ 7





On Blume’s understanding, the shift was from viewing mental functioning as either normal or abnormal – with the norm privileged as superior – to viewing different minds as having different cognitive specialisations within a broader cognitive ecosystem. For instance, ‘computer culture’, he wrote ‘may favor a somewhat autistic cast of mind’. In stark contrast to the Galtonian tradition, the idea is that neurological diversity is vital for dealing with the complex problems that humanity will encounter in a constantly changing environment. From this view, then – even if we put aside ethical issues for a moment – it does not make sense to seek to eliminate neurodivergence, since this would impede our collective functioning.

在布鲁姆的理解中，这种转变是从将心理功能视为正常或异常——以常态为优越标准——转变为将不同的心智视为在更广阔的认知生态系统中拥有不同的认知专长。例如他写道：“计算机文化可能偏爱某种略带孤独谱系特质的心智模式。”与高尔顿传统的鲜明对比在于，这种观点认为神经多样性对于应对人类在不断变化的环境中遇到的复杂问题至关重要。因此，从这个角度来看——即便我们暂时搁置伦理问题——试图消除神经殊异性也是没有意义的，因为这会阻碍我们集体的运作能力。



It was this that “Singer’s thesis brought together with insights from autistic activists and disability studies. In her thesis she grounded the idea of neurodiversity in critiques of the notion of the ‘normal’ body as well as the social model of disability. Although the constraints of the thesis didn’t allow her to clarify the underlying theory in great detail, she suggested that the neurodiversity movement would work towards an ‘ecological’ society that would foster inclusion by constructing cognitive niches to accommodate autistic people. The more general idea was that for humanity to flourish, we need to both conserve diversity and to support divergence. Hence in stark contrast to the Galtonian tradition, which suggested the abnormal needed to be systematically pushed towards the norm, Singer sought to suggest that divergence itself was part of what constituted ‘healthy’ neurological functioning.

正是这一点，"辛格的论文将孤独谱系活动家和残障研究的洞见结合了起来。在她的论文中，她将神经多样性的理念植根于对'正常'身体概念的批判以及残障的社会模式之中。尽管论文的篇幅限制使她未能详尽阐述其背后的理论，但她提出，神经多样性运动将致力于构建一个'生态型'社会，通过营造认知环境来容纳孤独谱系群体，从而促进包容。更广义的理念是，为了让人类繁荣发展，我们既需要保护多样性，也需要支持差异性。因此，与高尔顿传统——该传统认为异常需要被系统性地推向常态——形成鲜明对比的是，辛格试图表明，差异性本身正是构成'健康'神经功能的一部分。"



While Singer’s work was seminal in helping formalise emerging autistic community theorising, it was also underdeveloped in a number of ways. There are at least two key issues worth drawing attention to here. One issue is that she limited her analysis to what she called ‘high-functioning’ autism. This left those autistic people who fall further from neuronormative standards back in an individualised medical model. In this, her analysis retained traces, to at least some extent, of the kind of ranking system definitive of the pathology paradigm. In turn, the practical implication of this is that her analysis would exclude many autistic (and otherwise neurodivergent) people who find a neurodiversity approach helpful and want to be included. Thus, her analysis did not go far enough, and if adopted may still end up reproducing rather than overcoming aspects of Galton’s paradigm.

辛格的研究在帮助新兴的孤独谱系社群理论体系化方面具有开创性意义，但在若干方面仍有待完善。此处至少有两个关键问题值得关注。其一在于，她将分析范围局限于所谓的“高功能”孤独症。这使得那些更偏离神经常态标准的孤独谱系群体，重新被置于个体化的医疗模式框架中。就此而言，她的分析至少在某种程度上，仍残留着病理学范式所特有的等级划分体系的痕迹。相应地，这种做法带来的现实影响是：许多认为神经多样性视角有益且渴望被纳入其中的孤独谱系（及其他神经殊异）群体，将被排除在她的分析框架之外。因此，她的研究尚未触及核心症结，若被采纳实施，最终可能非但未能超越高尔顿的范式，反而会复现其某些特征。



Second, it is also worth mentioning Singer’s more recent response to criticisms of neurodiversity that suggest the approach is at odds with a scientific understanding that is promoted in mainstream psychiatry.8 Singer’s retort has been to simply claim that her concept was only ever supposed to be an ‘activist’ concept rather than a scientific one.

其次，也值得提及辛格对神经多样性批评的近期回应，这些批评认为该立场与主流精神病学所推崇的科学理解相悖。辛格的反驳是，她声称自己的概念从一开始就只是一个“行动主义”概念，而非科学概念。



Her response is unsatisfactory for several reasons. First, Singer makes scientific claims that can generate testable hypotheses (such as that neurological diversity is vital for optimal functioning at the group level) while claiming that they are not scientific. This does not only seem contradictory. It also undersells the scientific and theoretical legitimacy of the neurodiversity perspective, risking making it seem as if it is closer to mere scientific sounding rhetoric rather than rigorous theory that has legitimate uses in scientific research. Second, it has become clear since Singer developed her analysis that using the neurodiversity concept to change how we approach scientific research is not just possible but also vital for neurodivergent liberation. After all, as we have seen in earlier chapters, the way knowledge has been produced under Galton’s paradigm is a big part of the problem, and hence changing how we approach the science of neurodiversity is vital. This can be seen when we consider the work of Nick Walker, and her proposal that neurodivergent liberation requires a paradigm shift. While neurodiversity theory has always been developed collectively, Walker is arguably one of the foundational neurodiversity theorists alongside Singer. Synthesising a second wave of neurodivergent community theorising, Walker clarifies the core differences between the pathology paradigm and the neurodiversity paradigm. It is thus to her work that we will now turn.

她的回应在多个方面都难以令人满意。首先，辛格提出了可产生可检验假说的科学主张（例如神经多样性对于群体层面的最佳运作至关重要），却同时声称这些并非科学论断。这不仅是自相矛盾，更低估了神经多样性视角在科学与理论层面的正当性，使其看似仅是一种披着科学外衣的修辞，而非能在科学研究中发挥实际效用的严谨理论。其次，自辛格提出其分析以来，我们已经清楚地认识到，运用神经多样性概念来改变科学研究方法，不仅是可能的，更是神经殊异群体解放的关键所在。毕竟，正如前几章所述，高尔顿范式下知识生产的方式本身就是问题的重要部分，因此改变我们研究神经多样性科学的方法至关重要。当我们审视尼克·沃克的研究时，这一点尤为明显——她提出神经殊异群体的解放需要一场范式转变。 虽然神经多样性理论一直是由集体共同发展的，但沃克可以说是与辛格并列的基础神经多样性理论家之一。她综合了神经殊异社群理论的第二波思潮，厘清了病理学范式与神经多样性范式之间的核心差异。因此，我们现在将转向她的研究。



NEURODIVERSITY AS PARADIGM

作为范式的神经多样性



It is striking that, like Singer, Walker is also a descendant of Jewish Holocaust survivors, who grew up in poverty as an undiagnosed autistic. And like Singer, Walker too would go on to make her seminal intervention not as a tenured academic but as an outsider student engaged in activist communities and online autistic groups. Unlike Singer, though, she honed her political views as a teenager involved in queer and anti-fascist activism on the American East Coast through the 1980s.

引人注目的是，与辛格一样，沃克也是犹太人大屠杀幸存者的后代，在贫困中长大，且是未被诊断的孤独谱系人士。与辛格相似，沃克后来也做出了开创性的贡献，但她并非终身教职学者，而是作为参与激进社群和在线孤独谱系团体的局外人学生。不过，与辛格不同的是，她在青少年时期就通过参与 1980 年代美国东海岸的酷儿和反法西斯激进活动，磨砺了自己的政治观点。



This was the time of the AIDS epidemic, when Ronald Reagan was presiding over the deaths of tens of thousands of people with AIDS while rolling back state welfare and ushering in the neoliberal era. Even though it followed the depathologisation of ‘homosexuality’, this period in some ways brought worsening discrimination against the queer community, who were wrongly scapegoated for the government’s failure to deal with the crisis. And so it was this that, in line with her commitment to queer politics and her mistrust of the kind of binary thinking exemplified by the high-functioning/low-functioning distinction, Walker went on to propose an expanded analysis that surpassed Singer’s work.

这是艾滋病肆虐的年代，罗纳德·里根在任期间数万艾滋病患者死亡，同时国家福利被削减，新自由主义时代拉开序幕。尽管"同性恋"已不再被视为疾病，但这一时期酷儿群体在某些方面遭受的歧视反而加剧，他们被错误地当作政府应对危机不力的替罪羊。正因如此，出于对酷儿政治的承诺以及对高功能/低功能这类二元对立思维的不信任，沃克继而提出了一种超越辛格理论的扩展分析。



To understand this, it is helpful to skip forward to 2012. By that time, Walker was a mature graduate student at the California Institute for Integral Studies. She had also settled into a late autism diagnosis and had been engaged in online neurodiversity discourse for almost a decade. The movement and its theories had also expanded considerably, being adopted and developed by people with other diagnoses such as bipolar disorder as well as by people with so-called ‘low-functioning’ autism diagnoses, most notably the late autistic writer Mel Baggs. At the same time, new terms had begun to emerge, including ‘neurodivergent’ and ‘neurominority’, as additions to the concepts of ‘neurotypicality’ and ‘neurodiversity’.

要理解这一点，不妨先跳到 2012 年。那时，沃克已是加州整合研究学院一名成熟的研究生。她也已接受了晚期的孤独谱系诊断，并参与线上神经多样性讨论近十年。这场运动及其理论也已大幅扩展，被双相情感障碍等其他诊断者以及所谓“低功能”孤独谱系诊断者采纳和发展，其中尤以已故的孤独谱系作家梅尔·巴格斯为代表。与此同时，新的术语开始出现，包括“神经殊异”和“神经少数群体”，作为对“神经典型性”和“神经多样性”概念的补充。



This all helped Walker to see that the neurodiversity concept was, in bits and pieces, and through collective effort, being expanded into a whole new ‘paradigm’. Here Walker drew on a concept the philosopher and historian Thomas Kuhn9 developed to help make sense of how sciences develop through history. A scientific paradigm, for Kuhn, is a set of assumptions and axioms that members of a scientific community share to ground their research for a given historical period. Kuhn showed that, in early historical stages scientific fields are pre-paradigmatic, but when they mature, they come to follow key prototypes and accompanying assumptions that later become adopted among the scientific community to ground their research. In turn, these paradigms can also sometimes change when the old paradigm becomes outdated and new prototypes and frameworks emerge, such as we see in the shift from Newton’s paradigm to Einstein’s paradigm.

这一切都帮助沃克认识到，神经多样性的概念正在通过集体努力，一点一滴地扩展成一个全新的“范式”。在这里，沃克借鉴了哲学家和历史学家托马斯·库恩 9 提出的一个概念，用以理解科学在历史上是如何发展的。对库恩而言，科学范式是一套假设和公理，在特定历史时期内，科学共同体的成员共享这些假设和公理，并以此为基础进行研究。库恩指出，在历史的早期阶段，科学领域是前范式的；但当它们成熟时，就会开始遵循关键的原型及相应的假设，这些后来被科学共同体采纳，作为其研究的基础。反过来，当旧范式过时，新的原型和框架出现时，这些范式有时也会发生变化，正如我们从牛顿范式向爱因斯坦范式的转变中所看到的那样。



Walker’s conception of the neurodiversity ‘paradigm’ thus indicated the need for a new general set of fundamental assumptions, axioms, or principles that could form the basis for changing how we think about, study, and respond to human neurodiversity as such. This was first published in her seminal essay ‘Throw away the master’s tools: Liberating ourselves from the pathology paradigm’, in an influential collection of autistic activist theorising titled Loud Hands: Autistic People, Speaking. It was here that Walker first argued that a new paradigm was beginning to emerge – and in turn that neurodivergent liberation would require the further development and implementation of this new paradigm.

因此，沃克提出的神经多样性"范式"概念，意味着需要一套全新的基本假设、公理或原则，作为我们从根本上改变对人类神经多样性的思考、研究和应对方式的基础。这一观点首次发表于她的开创性文章《扔掉主人的工具：从病理范式中解放自我》，该文收录于具有影响力的孤独谱系行动者理论文集《响亮的手：孤独谱系群体，口语者》。正是在这里，沃克首次论证了一种新范式正在兴起——进而指出，神经殊异者的解放将需要这一新范式的进一步发展和落实。



Walker has summarised the core differences to the Galtonian pathology paradigm as follows. On the one hand:

沃克将这一范式与高尔顿式病理范式的核心差异总结如下。一方面：





The pathology paradigm starts from the assumption that significant divergences from dominant sociocultural norms of cognition and embodiment represent some form of deficit, defect, or pathology. In other words, the pathology paradigm divides the spectrum of human cognitive/embodied performance into ‘normal’ and ‘other than normal’, with ‘normal’ implicitly privileged as the superior and desirable state.

病理学范式始于这样一种假设：认知和具身化显著偏离主导的社会文化规范，代表着某种形式的缺陷、缺损或病理。换句话说，病理学范式将人类认知/具身化表现谱系划分为“正常”与“非正常”，其中“正常”被隐含地赋予特权，被视为优越且理想的状态。





By contrast, she goes on,

相比之下，她继续说道，





The neurodiversity paradigm starts from the understanding that neurodiversity is an axis of human diversity, like ethnic diversity or diversity of gender and sexual orientation, and is subject to the same sorts of social dynamics as those other forms of diversity – including the dynamics of social power inequalities, privilege, and oppression. From this perspective, the pathologization of neurominorities can be recognized as simply another form of systemic oppression which functions similarly to the oppression of other types of minority groups.10

神经多样性范式始于这样一种理解：神经多样性是人类多样性的一个维度，就像种族多样性或性别与性取向的多样性一样，并且受到与这些其他形式的多样性相同的社会动态影响——包括社会权力不平等、特权与压迫的动态。从这个角度来看，对神经少数群体的病理化可以被视为系统性压迫的另一种形式，其运作方式类似于对其他类型少数群体的压迫。 10





In short, for Walker, if we adopt this emerging understanding, instead of dividing groups into the normal and the pathological, we can instead frame them as having closer or further proximity to the neurotypical ideal. This raises the prospect of a more general shift in our scientific and cultural representations, analogous to the shift from viewing ‘homosexuality’ as a mental disorder to reframing it as a minority sexual orientation understood through queer theory. Hence, Walker writes, for neurodiversity proponents, the long-term aim should be understood as working towards a ‘paradigm shift: a widespread supplanting of the pathology paradigm by the neurodiversity paradigm’.

简而言之，对沃克而言，如果我们采纳这种新兴的理解，便不再将群体划分为正常与病态，而是可以将其视为与神经典型理想的距离或近或远。这预示着我们的科学与文化表征可能发生更广泛的转变，类似于从将“同性恋”视为精神障碍，转变为通过酷儿理论将其理解为一种少数性取向。因此，沃克写道，对于神经多样性的支持者来说，长期目标应被理解为努力实现“范式转变：以神经多样性范式广泛取代病理学范式”。



It is my view that Walker’s concept of the neurodiversity paradigm is important – and quickly caught on among neurodivergent activists  – because it helps overcome the two key limitations of Singer’s analysis. First, it allows us to recognise how neurodiversity has begun to form the basis for a different way of generating knowledge and thus justifying new approaches to policy and practice that would be based on this knowledge. Indeed, as Walker noted in 2021, in recent years it has precisely been the case that it is not only scientific research on neurodivergence (mainly autism so far) that has begun to change by incorporating social and ecological models of functioning. Research in literary studies, psychotherapy, musicology, and many other areas has also begun to emerge based on a neurodiversity paradigm framing. This framing helps show the significance of neurodiversity as a concept with applicability to scientific research, that can produce different knowledge to that which is generated by Galton’s paradigm and hence help undo the latter’s scientific as well as cultural hegemony.

我认为沃克的神经多样性范式概念之所以重要——并迅速在神经殊异活动家中流行起来——是因为它有助于克服辛格分析的两个关键局限。首先，它使我们认识到神经多样性如何开始成为一种不同知识生成方式的基础，从而为基于这种知识的新政策与实践方法提供正当性。事实上，正如沃克在 2021 年指出的，近年来情况恰恰表明，不仅关于神经殊异性（目前主要是孤独谱系）的科学研究开始通过融入社会与生态功能模型而发生转变，文学研究、心理治疗、音乐学等众多领域也开始出现基于神经多样性范式框架的研究。这一框架有助于展现神经多样性作为一个概念对科学研究的重要意义——它能产生与高尔顿范式不同的知识，从而有助于消解后者的科学及文化霸权。



The second key benefit of Walker’s concept of the neurodiversity paradigm is that it allows us to formalise a broader analysis that goes far beyond autism.
