This has helped the framework become more inclusive, allowing people who find the paradigm helpful to adopt it regardless of what diagnosis they have. While some non-autistic people identified with the neurodiversity approach since more or less the beginning, this broader conception helped such identifications rapidly increase, expanding neurodiversity activism far beyond the autistic community.

沃克神经多样性范式的第二个关键益处在于，它使我们能够将分析框架正式扩展到远超出孤独谱系的范畴。这有助于该框架更具包容性，让任何认同此范式价值的人都能采纳它，无论其诊断为何。虽然一些非孤独谱系人士几乎从一开始就认同神经多样性理念，但这种更广泛的界定促使此类认同迅速增长，将神经多样性行动主义扩展至远超出孤独谱系群体的范围。



NEURODIVERGENT MARXISM

神经殊异马克思主义



That said, Walker only argued that the paradigm was beginning to emerge, and proposed that its consolidation should be seen as a goal for neurodiversity proponents to work towards. She didn’t claim that it was fully formed and ready to be implemented. Neither did she explore in detail exactly what it would take to change the paradigm, framing the issue as one of changing how we think. As such, our current understanding of the proposed paradigm shift is limited.

尽管如此，沃克仅主张该范式正在萌芽阶段，并提出其巩固完善应被视为神经多样性倡导者努力的目标。她并未声称该范式已完全成熟并可立即实施，也未详细探讨实现范式转变的具体条件，仅将问题框架为思维方式的变革。因此，我们对当前提出的范式转变的理解仍存在局限。



The most fundamental limitation, which I have sought to address in this book, is that neither Walker nor any other neurodiversity theorist until now has provided a historical materialist analysis of the pathology paradigm. But here, by showing how the paradigm arose and caught on specifically because it allowed the individualisation and reification of neurodivergent disablement, we can better understand the significance and power of the pathology paradigm, as well as what it might take to overcome it. Since the pathology paradigm, and the way it naturalises increasingly restricted conceptions of normality, grew precisely to mirror the needs of the capitalist economy, it is these material conditions that need to be changed, not just our thinking. While changing our thinking is vital, we are unlikely to fully supplant the pathology paradigm while the capitalist global economic order remains dominant.

我在本书中试图解决的最根本局限在于，无论是沃克还是迄今为止任何其他神经多样性理论家，都未曾对病理学范式进行历史唯物主义的分析。但在此，通过揭示该范式如何因其允许将神经殊异障碍个体化与物化而兴起并流行，我们能更深刻地理解病理学范式的意义与力量，以及克服它可能需要什么。既然病理学范式及其将日益受限的正常性概念自然化的方式，正是为了反映资本主义经济的需求而发展起来的，那么需要改变的是这些物质条件，而不仅仅是我们的思维方式。尽管改变思维方式至关重要，但在资本主义全球经济秩序仍占主导地位的情况下，我们不太可能完全取代病理学范式。



More generally, the key limitation of existing neurodiversity theory and activism is that it is more focused on changing our thinking and attitudes than on changing material conditions. To be clear, this is not to say that existing proponents ignore the material. Far from it. The embrace of the social model precisely demonstrates neurodiversity proponents’ commitment to changing the social and material world when it comes to alleviating disablement. Still, this is usually limited to the individual, institutional, and, occasionally, legal levels rather than challenging the deeper structures of the economic order. Until now, there has been little to no analysis in neurodiversity theory and activism of political economy, or of whether liberation under capitalism is even possible. It is this that I think we need to go beyond. For as we have seen, the pathology paradigm – and its scientific quest to naturalise capitalist neuronormaitivity – was a product of those material conditions. While it has now become its own, distinct problem – and certainly could persist beyond capitalism – it seems unlikely to be supplanted without changing the deeper structures of society.

更广泛地说，现有神经多样性理论与行动主义的关键局限在于，它们更侧重于改变我们的思维和态度，而非改变物质条件。需要明确的是，这并非指现有倡导者忽视了物质层面。恰恰相反。对社会模式的接纳恰恰证明了神经多样性倡导者在减轻残障问题上致力于改变社会与物质世界的决心。然而，这种努力通常局限于个人、机构乃至偶尔的法律层面，并未挑战经济秩序中更深层的结构。迄今为止，神经多样性理论与行动主义中几乎未曾对政治经济学进行过分析，也未曾探讨在资本主义制度下实现解放是否可能。我认为，这正是我们需要超越的领域。因为正如我们所看到的，病理学范式——及其将资本主义神经常态自然化的科学追求——正是那些物质条件的产物。尽管它如今已演变成一个独特的问题，并且无疑可能在资本主义之外持续存在，但若不改变社会的深层结构，它似乎不太可能被取代。



My historical analysis also allows us to see another more general problem with liberal approaches to neurodiversity theory. As we have seen, neurodiversity proponents argue that variations in mental functioning are like biodiversity, and that it takes more than just neurotypical minds for groups or even society as a whole to function. In an important sense this is a radical new idea that is the opposite of what Nazi ideology had held. The Nazi view, as we covered earlier, saw society as an organism that required uniformity of all its constituent parts. This meant that neurodivergent people had to be exterminated except to the extent they might prove useful for the economy at certain points. By contrast, neurodiversity holds that society requires diversity, and hence that divergence must be conserved. This places the demand on society to support neurodivergence rather than seeking to eliminate it.

我的历史分析也让我们看到了自由主义神经多样性理论方法中另一个更普遍的问题。正如我们所看到的，神经多样性支持者认为，心理功能的差异就像生物多样性一样，群体乃至整个社会的运作需要的不仅仅是神经典型心智。从重要意义上说，这是一个激进的新理念，与纳粹意识形态所持的观点截然相反。正如我们之前所讨论的，纳粹观点将社会视为一个有机体，要求其所有组成部分保持一致性。这意味着神经殊异者必须被消灭，除非他们在某些时候可能对经济有用。相比之下，神经多样性理论认为社会需要多样性，因此必须保护差异。这要求社会支持神经殊异性，而不是试图消除它。



Yet despite providing a stark difference to more fascistic ideologies of normality, some versions of neurodiversity theory can still be made to cohere with capitalist logics. For if the capitalists recognise that neurological diversity actually helps groups function, then capitalism can adopt a liberal neurodiversity perspective that conserves neurodivergent people as and to the extent that they are able to be mined for productivity. It will thus still have an in-group and an out-group, since this will inevitably only apply to some neurodivergent people – those with specific skills or who help group functioning – and not to others. Even while this is not, of course, something that would be endorsed by neurodiversity theorists, it is far from clear that the paradigm could truly be changed without simultaneously changing the deep structures of society. It is thus important to supplement existing neurodiversity theory with a more radical analysis.*

然而，尽管与更为法西斯式的常态意识形态形成了鲜明对比，神经多样性理论的某些版本仍可能被调整以符合资本主义逻辑。因为如果资本家认识到神经多样性实际上有助于群体运作，那么资本主义就可以采纳一种自由主义的神经多样性视角，将神经殊异者作为生产力资源加以保留，并仅限于他们能够被挖掘出生产力的程度。因此，它仍将存在内部群体与外部群体之分，因为这不可避免地只适用于某些神经殊异者——那些拥有特定技能或有助于群体运作的人——而非所有其他人。当然，这绝非神经多样性理论家会赞同的做法，但若不同时改变社会的深层结构，这一范式能否真正被改变，还远未可知。因此，用更激进的分析来补充现有的神经多样性理论至关重要。 *





* Since I submitted this manuscript for publication, new archival evidence has come to light showing that the concept of neurodiversity as described by Singer and Blume was already in use in online autistic spaces in 1996. Moreover, this came to light following a string of statements from Singer on social media that have widely been regarded as transphobic. As such, while I think it is still worth engaging with her texts – which remain seminal studies of the movement – her role in formulating the theory will, over the coming years, need to be reassessed. I will address this in future publications.

* 自从我提交这份手稿准备出版以来，新发现的档案证据表明，辛格和布鲁姆所描述的神经多样性概念早在 1996 年就已在线上的孤独谱系社群中被使用。此外，这一发现是在辛格在社交媒体上发表一系列被广泛视为恐跨的言论之后才浮出水面的。因此，虽然我认为她的文本——作为该运动的开创性研究——仍然值得探讨，但她在理论构建中的作用在未来几年内需要重新评估。我将在未来的出版物中处理这个问题。



---

Empire of Normality



10



Cognitive contradictions

认知矛盾



Over the past decade the neurodiversity movement has grown at an incredible pace. The theories discussed in the previous chapter have formed the basis for neurodivergent praxis across much of the globe. This avalanche of activity occurred because it had to: because a sizeable portion of humanity could by this point no longer function within the increasingly strict neuronormativity imposed within the Empire of Normality. Neurodiversity activism has, over this time, been incorporated into everything from street protest to political lobbying; from unionism to research; and there has even been an attempt to include a commitment to ending neurodivergent oppression in a recently proposed draft constitution in Chile.

过去十年间，神经多样性运动以惊人的速度发展。前一章讨论的理论已构成全球范围内神经殊异实践的基础。这场活动雪崩之所以发生，是因为它必须发生：因为此时已有相当一部分人类无法在"常态帝国"日益严苛的神经规范框架内正常运作。在此期间，神经多样性行动主义已渗透到从街头抗议到政治游说、从工会运动到学术研究的各个领域；智利近期提出的宪法草案甚至尝试纳入终结神经殊异压迫的承诺。



As a framework for praxis, neurodiversity theory is notable for not reproducing the old Cartesian dualism that has turned out to be, whether in its original or Szaszian form, so useful for capital and the state. Instead, the ‘neuro’ suffix emphasises the embodied nature of the mind, and that cognition is inseparable from the body, and beyond that, the world. This approach also avoids another key issue associated with the anti-psychiatry movement, which as we have seen legitimised a widespread denial of mental disability or illness. While neurodiversity proponents do challenge pathologisation in some cases, their challenge is directed more toward default pathologisation of those atypical minds considered to be unproductive, and not a blanket denial of mental illness as such. At the same time, in reclaiming disability rather than denying the fact of disability, neurodiversity proponents have been well-positioned to make demands of the state, as and where neurodivergent people find this useful.

作为一种实践框架，神经多样性理论的显著之处在于它没有复制旧的笛卡尔二元论——无论其原始形式还是萨斯式变体，这种二元论已被证明对资本和国家极为有用。相反，"神经"这一后缀强调了心智的具身性，即认知与身体密不可分，并进一步延伸至与世界不可分割。这一路径也避免了反精神病学运动相关的另一个关键问题，正如我们所见，该运动曾为广泛否认精神残障或精神疾病的现象提供了正当性。虽然神经多样性倡导者确实在某些情况下挑战病理化倾向，但他们的批判更侧重于针对那些被视为非生产性的非典型心智的默认病理化，而非全盘否定精神疾病本身。与此同时，通过主张残障身份而非否认残障事实，神经多样性倡导者得以在神经殊异者认为有益的情境中，更有力地向国家提出诉求。



A related reason this has provided a useful basis for praxis is that, as Steve Graby1 notes, since it emphasises the embodied nature of cognition alongside the reality of disability, neurodiversity theory has helped connect mental health politics with the broader politics of disablement. This has helped with the development of a broader, more unified politics linked by neurodiversity theory and activism than is possible under a more Cartesian approach that seeks to strictly distinguish mental distress from bodily illness. Neurodiversity theory has thus helped provide a more unified politics that aims for collective liberation.

这为实践提供了有用基础的另一个相关原因是，正如史蒂夫·格拉比所指出的，由于神经多样性理论强调认知的具身性以及残障的现实性，它有助于将心理健康政治与更广泛的残障政治联系起来。相较于那种试图严格区分精神困扰与身体疾病的笛卡尔式方法，这有助于发展出一种更广泛、更统一的政治，这种政治由神经多样性理论和行动主义所联结。因此，神经多样性理论有助于提供一种更统一的政治，旨在实现集体解放。



Finally, since neurodiversity theory centres disabled people as primary experts in their own experience, it provides a stark challenge to the authority of not just psychiatrists but also clinical psychologists, psychotherapists, and other clinical professions. This does not deny that members of these professions have some relevant expertise, but it both decentres that and uncovers the paradigm and ideology that has hitherto oriented, and often stifled, this expertise. Unlike the Szaszian tradition, which reproduces a medical model epistemology and thus remains led by clinical professionals, the neurodiversity movement challenges the authority of the physician and clinician class, instead orienting towards the needs of disabled and ill people more broadly.

最后，由于神经多样性理论将残障人士视为自身经验的首要专家，它不仅对精神病学家的权威构成了严峻挑战，也对临床心理学家、心理治疗师及其他临床专业人士的权威提出了质疑。这并非否认这些专业人士具备某些相关专业知识，而是既削弱了其中心地位，又揭示了迄今为止引导并常常扼杀这些专业知识的范式与意识形态。与萨兹传统不同——该传统复制了医疗模式的认识论，因而仍由临床专业人士主导——神经多样性运动挑战了医师和临床医生阶层的权威，转而更广泛地以残障人士和病患的需求为导向。



Yet despite these improvements on previous attempts, neurodiversity theory and activism has remained, for the most part, within a liberal framework. The focus has been on a rights-based approach and on changing recognition, representations, and concepts. Neurodiversity advocacy has also tended to assume, at least implicitly, that neurodivergent liberation is possible under capitalism. This can be seen in so far as most neurodiversity activism has been geared towards attaining justice within capitalism rather than directly working towards a post-capitalist future.

然而，尽管相较于之前的尝试有所改进，神经多样性理论和行动主义在很大程度上仍停留在自由主义框架内。其关注点主要基于权利路径，侧重于改变认知、表征和观念。神经多样性倡导也倾向于——至少是隐含地——假设神经殊异者的解放可以在资本主义制度下实现。这一点可以从大多数神经多样性行动致力于在资本主义内部争取正义，而非直接致力于后资本主义未来中看出。



At the same time, perhaps especially in the past five years, new neurodiversity industries have arisen, while existing industries have rapidly changed their branding to present themselves as neurodivergence-inclusive. What we are seeing is capitalism adapting to neurodivergence inclusion in so far as this can help capitalists profit. For instance, in the United Kingdom, airports now increasingly include sensory rooms, designed to make airports more accessible for children who are autistic or who have similar sensory processing disabilities, while supermarkets increasingly have ‘autism-friendly’ hours with reduced lighting. But we only see such changes in so far as they allow the consumer base to be increased. They do not lead to deep, systemic change.

与此同时，或许尤其是在过去五年间，新的神经多样性产业已然兴起，而现有产业也迅速调整品牌定位，以彰显其对神经殊异性的包容。我们所目睹的是资本主义对神经殊异性包容的适应——只要这种包容能帮助资本家获利。例如在英国，机场如今越来越多地配备了感官室，旨在让孤独谱系儿童或有类似感官处理障碍的儿童更易使用机场设施；超市也日益推行"孤独症友好"时段，在此期间调暗灯光。然而，这类改变仅出现在能够扩大消费群体的范围内，并未引发深刻、系统性的变革。



We are also seeing the increased capture of neurodiversity advocacy by elites who are invested in maintaining the dominant system. For instance, the previous Conservative Member of Parliament and Health Secretary, Matt Hancock, has recently launched a neurodiversity charity that has made headlines in major UK papers. Despite this, Hancock and the government he served in have pursued austerity policies that are exceptionally harmful to neurodivergent people. His political commitments are inherently at odds with neurodivergent emancipation.

我们也看到，神经多样性倡导正越来越多地被那些致力于维护现有体系的精英阶层所利用。例如，英国前保守党议员、卫生大臣马特·汉考克最近成立了一个神经多样性慈善机构，并登上了英国各大报纸的头条。尽管如此，汉考克及其所服务的政府却推行着对神经殊异群体伤害尤为严重的紧缩政策。他的政治立场与神经殊异群体的解放事业从根本上就是对立的。



The rise of neuro-Thatcherism, whereby neurodiversity advocacy is turned into a business-oriented programme for unearthing neurodivergent strengths or ‘super powers’ and then mining those with these strengths may be useful for those neurodivergent people it helps into jobs. One possible by-product of this worth bearing in mind is that the more neurodivergent people who are recognised as vital for the workforce, the more potential power those people will have to organise as workers in unions. This could then have some utility for a politics of neurodiversity. Yet overall, neuro-Thatcherism does nothing to fundamentally challenge the deeper structures of society I have identified throughout this book as underpinning neurodivergent oppression. What’s more, to the extent that neuro-Thatcherism becomes the dominant neurodiversity discourse, it will drown out the more radical and emancipatory modes developed by grassroots activists.

神经撒切尔主义的兴起，将神经多样性倡导转变为一种商业导向的计划，旨在发掘神经殊异者的优势或“超能力”，然后利用这些拥有优势的人。对于那些因此获得工作的神经殊异者来说，这可能是有益的。值得记住的一个可能副产品是：被认定为对劳动力至关重要的神经殊异者越多，这些人作为工人在工会中组织起来的潜在力量就越大。这可能对神经多样性的政治斗争有一定用处。然而总体而言，神经撒切尔主义根本未能挑战我在本书中始终指出的、支撑神经殊异压迫的深层社会结构。更重要的是，如果神经撒切尔主义成为神经多样性的主导话语，它将淹没基层活动家发展出的更为激进和解放的模式。



Of course, not all liberal activism coheres with the neuro-Thatcherist approach. There is a strong intersectional and more critical liberal component of the movement, especially at the grassroots level. One important development, among others, is the Disability Justice Movement in the United States. Proponents of this approach tend to demand rights while acknowledging that rights-based approaches tend to fall far short of justice, especially for multiply marginalised disabled people. Lydia X. Z. Brown and Shain M. Neumeier, for instance, have emphasised how disabled people at the margins are not protected by human rights laws. Moreover, they stress, even laws proposed to protect disabled people can end up being used to harm them, as in the case of guardianships and involuntary commitment.2

当然，并非所有的自由主义行动主义都与神经撒切尔主义路径一致。这场运动中存在着一个强大的交叉性且更具批判性的自由主义分支，尤其是在基层层面。其中一个重要的发展，便是美国的残障正义运动。这一路径的支持者倾向于在要求权利的同时，承认基于权利的路径往往远未实现正义，特别是对于遭受多重边缘化的残障人士而言。例如，莉迪亚·X·Z·布朗和谢恩·M·诺伊迈尔曾强调，处于边缘地位的残障人士并未受到人权法的保护。此外，他们还强调，即便是旨在保护残障人士的法律，最终也可能被用来伤害他们，例如监护制度和非自愿收容的情况。



In line with a disability justice approach, one of the more positive recent developments is the theory and praxis of neuroqueering. Stemming from the work of Nick Walker and Remi Yergeau, neuroqueering focuses on embracing weird potentials within one’s neurocognitive space, and turning everyday comportment and behaviour into forms of resistance.3 This has provided a new tool for combatting neuronormativity from within the constraints imposed by history and current material conditions. By queering the social world, new possibilities are carved out for the future, helping us not just challenge aspects of the current order but to start collectively imagining what a different world could be like.

与残障正义方法相一致，近期一个较为积极的进展是神经酷儿化的理论与实践。源于尼克·沃克和雷米·耶尔戈的工作，神经酷儿化聚焦于拥抱个体神经认知空间内的怪异潜能，并将日常举止与行为转化为抵抗的形式。这为在历史和当前物质条件所施加的约束下，从内部对抗神经规范性提供了一种新工具。通过酷儿化社会世界，为未来开辟了新的可能性，不仅帮助我们挑战当前秩序的某些方面，更开始集体想象一个不同的世界可能是什么样子。



Unlike some ‘class-first’ Marxists, I think these more intersectional approaches are extremely important, and provide a helpful contrast to neuro-Thatcherism. If neuronormative ideology enforces a pervasive fog, restricting our thought, agency, and action, neuroqueering prods this, helping identify its weak points. And disability justice approaches help build vital community resources and projects outside of state-sanctioned interventions. Such efforts not only change local material conditions but also allow an expansion of neurodivergent consciousness and agency at individual and collective levels. Still, even these approaches tend to avoid deeper analysis of neurodivergent oppression in relation to the political economy. Given what I have sought to show in this book, it seems worth clarifying exactly what a Marxian analysis, and lessons taken from the historical materialist perspective, might add.

与某些"阶级优先"的马克思主义者不同，我认为这些更具交叉性的方法极为重要，并为神经撒切尔主义提供了有益的对照。如果说神经规范意识形态制造了弥漫的迷雾，限制了我们的思想、能动性和行动，那么神经酷儿化则对此进行刺激，帮助识别其薄弱环节。而残障正义方法则有助于在国家认可的干预之外，建立至关重要的社区资源和项目。这些努力不仅改变了地方的物质条件，还允许在个体和集体层面扩展神经殊异的意识和能动性。然而，即使是这些方法，也往往避免对神经殊异压迫与政治经济学的关系进行更深入的分析。鉴于我在本书中试图展示的内容，似乎值得澄清马克思主义分析以及从历史唯物主义视角汲取的教训可能带来什么补充。



TURNING DISABLEMENT INTO A WEAPON

将失能转化为武器



What can we learn from the historical analysis provided here? How should we orient our organising and praxis? Let us first be clear about some key concepts and the ways they can be useful for either reproducing or challenging the dominant order. One initial insight that this historical analysis makes possible is that capital requires a certain ambiguity in beliefs about mental illness and disablement. On the one hand, it requires us to believe in mental illness and disablement just enough to justify the maintenance of a surplus class, and to be able to incarcerate divergent people who have not committed any recognised crime. This latter tendency is what the anti-psychiatrists saw and sought to challenge. But capital also requires us to be sceptical enough about the reality of mental illness and disablement so that it can get away with not providing healthcare or support for the majority of those who need it. This is where many of the anti-psychiatrists got, and get, their analysis wrong. For in seeking to render recognition of mental illness or disability invalid as such, the Szaszian anti-psychiatrists produced a discourse that is enormously helpful for capital. For a mass cultural scepticism of the reality of mental illness nicely feeds into the need of state and capital to deny help where such help would fail to maximise profit.

从这段历史分析中我们能学到什么？我们应如何定位自身的组织与实践？首先需要厘清若干关键概念及其作用机制——它们既可用来维系主导秩序，亦可成为挑战该秩序的工具。历史分析带来的首要启示在于：资本需要人们对精神疾病与残障保持某种认知上的模糊性。一方面，它要求我们足够相信精神疾病与残障的存在，以便为维持过剩阶级提供理由，并得以监禁那些未犯任何公认罪行的异见者——这种倾向正是反精神病学运动所洞察并试图挑战的。但另一方面，资本又要求我们对精神疾病与残障的真实性保持足够怀疑，从而得以逃避为大多数需求者提供医疗或支持的责任。这正是许多反精神病学理论过去及当下陷入分析误区之处：当萨兹学派的反精神病学家试图从根本上否定精神疾病或残障的认定有效性时，他们实际上构建了一套对资本极为有利的话语体系。 大众对精神疾病真实性的普遍文化怀疑，恰好迎合了国家和资本的需求——当援助无法最大化利润时，他们便拒绝提供帮助。



It is also worth mentioning contemporary ‘critical psychiatry’. This newer approach, which has become a small and relatively mainstream industry led by non-disabled clinical professionals, draws on the philosophical basis of anti-psychiatry but shifts from abolition to reformism. It mainly focuses on seeking to erase recognition of mental illness or disability, and instead frames diagnoses like ADHD or PTSD as mere ‘distress’, in a form of disability denial that is no less useful for capital than were its Szaszian predecessors. A good example of this approach is the work of James Davies. While he identifies some genuine harms of psychiatry, his own work goes back towards a moral model of disability, where distress is primarily understood as a potential for learning and growth. While suffering can of course sometimes allow growth, this orientation is a political dead end, and seems more likely to be used to justify the needs of the masses to suffer than to justify alleviating our suffering. Moreover, while Davies has correctly identified some of the harmful effects of neoliberal capitalism specifically, he still defends capitalism as such while very quickly dismissing attempts to develop communism.4 Given these practices and commitments, this clinician-led form of bourgeois reformism seems incompatible with a neurodivergent-led politics of emancipation.

同样值得提及的是当代的“批判精神病学”。这种由非残障临床专业人士主导的新兴方法已形成规模较小但相对主流的产业，它借鉴了反精神病学的哲学基础，却从废除主义转向改良主义。其主要着力于试图抹除对精神疾病或残障的承认，转而将 ADHD 或 PTSD 等诊断仅仅框定为“痛苦”，这种残障否认的形式对资本的效用，丝毫不亚于其萨兹主义先驱。詹姆斯·戴维斯的研究便是这种取向的典型例证。虽然他指出了精神病学造成的某些真实伤害，但其著作本身却回归到残障的道德模型，将痛苦主要理解为学习与成长的潜在契机。尽管苦难有时确实能催生成长，但这种导向在政治上注定走入死胡同，它更可能被用来论证大众承受苦难的必要性，而非为缓解我们的痛苦提供正当依据。 此外，尽管戴维斯准确指出了新自由主义资本主义的一些特定有害影响，他仍然为资本主义本身辩护，同时迅速否定了发展共产主义的尝试。 4 鉴于这些实践与承诺，这种由临床医生主导的资产阶级改良主义形式，似乎与神经殊异者主导的解放政治不相容。



With this in mind, it is worth considering that there are other traditions, not yet clarified here, which embraced politicised conceptions of mental illness rather than rejecting recognition of illness as such. Writing in the 1950s, for instance, Frantz Fanon saw mental illness as real illness, but also held it to be largely socially caused by inequality, colonialism, racism, and other social factors.5 He sought to develop this into anti-racist praxis, which could be usefully synthesised with neurodiversity paradigm approaches. More recent efforts to decolonise mental health continue in Fanon’s tradition. On the account of Mimi Khúc, for instance, this requires not just material decolonisation, but also a questioning and interrogation of manners in which ‘larger forces and institutions have told us what counts as mental health and what counts as suffering’.6 Decolonising efforts such as these tend to acknowledge that mental health is real but resist the imposition of hegemonic Western narratives and responses to such experiences.

考虑到这一点，值得思考的是，还存在其他尚未在此阐明的传统，它们接纳了政治化的精神疾病概念，而非拒绝承认疾病本身。例如，弗朗茨·法农在 20 世纪 50 年代撰文时，将精神疾病视为真实的疾病，但也认为它很大程度上是由不平等、殖民主义、种族主义及其他社会因素所引发的。 5 他试图将其发展为反种族主义的实践，这可以与神经多样性范式方法进行有益的综合。近期在法农传统下持续进行的心理健康去殖民化努力，如米米·库克所述，不仅需要物质层面的去殖民化，还需质疑和审视“更大的力量与制度如何定义何为心理健康、何为痛苦”。 6 此类去殖民化努力往往承认心理健康是真实存在的，但抵制将霸权式的西方叙事及应对方式强加于这些体验之上。



Beyond decolonising efforts, the radical group the Socialist Patients Collective, active in West Germany in the 1970s, also saw mental illness as an undeniable fact. But for them it was primarily caused by societal factors, and they argued that illness was the only possible way of life under capitalism. They embraced the use of certain therapies and medications, but, as Adler-Bolton and Vierkant write, ‘felt that, above all else, care should be self-directed and synergetic, a dual dialectic between doctor and patient working in collaboration and producing forms not just of care but also of solidarity’.7 Alongside this, they sought to build a ‘People’s University’ where treatments would be developed not for profit but on principles of collective self-determination. This challenge to the physician and researcher class, coupled with a commitment to ending capitalism, also provides a stark alternative to bourgeois and denialist mental health politics.

除了去殖民化的努力之外，活跃于 1970 年代西德的激进团体“社会主义患者集体”也将精神疾病视为一个不可否认的事实。但对他们而言，这主要是由社会因素造成的，他们认为疾病是资本主义下唯一可能的生活方式。他们接受使用某些疗法和药物，但正如阿德勒-博尔顿和维尔坎特所写，“他们认为，最重要的是，护理应该是自我导向和协同增效的，是医生和患者之间的一种双重辩证法，通过合作不仅产生护理形式，还产生团结形式。” 7 与此同时，他们试图建立一所“人民大学”，在那里开发治疗方法不是为了利润，而是基于集体自决的原则。这种对医生和研究者阶层的挑战，加上对终结资本主义的承诺，也为资产阶级和否认主义的精神健康政治提供了一个鲜明的替代方案。



It is also worth emphasising the significance of the British Marxist Peter Sedgwick, whose critique of Szasz we have already mentioned. In his 1982 book PsychoPolitics, Sedgwick critiqued what he rightly identified as the dualism of the anti-psychiatrists. Instead, he argued that recognising the reality of mental illness as illness was currently necessary for making demands from the state while also emphasising the need for alternative community organisation of mental health resources beyond the state apparatus. Given the failings of contemporary bourgeois critical psychiatry, there has been a resurgence of interest in Sedgwick in recent years, with two new editions of PsychoPolitics being published in the past decade. A Sedgwickian politics has recently been defended by scholar-activists such as Hel Spandler and Mark Cresswell.8 This approach also has some overlap with contemporary radical survivor groups such as Recovery In the Bin, who call for ‘a robust “Social Model of Madness, Distress & Confusion”, placing mental health within the context of social justice and the wider class struggle’.9 The radical mental health magazine Asylum has also resisted harmful binary thinking about mental health, taking a nuanced and pluralistic approach that holds space for recognition of illness and disability, consistent with the Sedgwickian tradition. Similarly, albeit more influenced by French post-structuralists, the social theorist Mark Fisher called for a politicisation of depression as a pathology definitive of the post-Fordist era.10 This alternative British tradition ultimately affirms the need for and right to treatments while simultaneously aiming at breaking the centring of the needs of capital in treatment production. It promotes a form of abolitionism, but where the abolition is of social control rather than the recognition of unwellness or the right to treatment.

同样值得强调的是英国马克思主义者彼得·塞奇威克的重要性，我们已经提到过他对萨斯（Szasz）的批判。在其 1982 年的著作《心理政治学》中，塞奇威克批判了他正确识别出的反精神病学二元论。相反，他认为，承认精神疾病作为疾病的现实性，在当前是向国家提出诉求的必要条件，同时也强调需要在国家机器之外，以替代性的社区组织形式来配置心理健康资源。鉴于当代资产阶级批判精神病学的失败，近年来对塞奇威克的兴趣有所复苏，其《心理政治学》在过去十年中已发行了两个新版本。学者兼活动家如赫尔·斯潘德勒和马克·克雷斯韦尔最近一直在捍卫塞奇威克式的政治立场。 8 这种方法与当代激进的幸存者团体（如“回收在垃圾桶里”）也有一定的重叠，他们呼吁“建立一个强有力的‘疯狂、痛苦与困惑的社会模式’，将心理健康置于社会正义和更广泛的阶级斗争的语境之中”。 9 激进心理健康杂志《避难所》同样抵制关于心理健康的有害二元思维，采取了一种细致入微且多元化的方法，为承认疾病和残障保留了空间，这与塞奇威克传统一脉相承。类似地，尽管更多地受到法国后结构主义者的影响，社会理论家马克·费舍尔呼吁将抑郁症政治化，将其视为后福特主义时代的一种决定性病理。 10 这一另类的英国传统最终肯定了治疗的必要性和获得治疗的权利，同时旨在打破资本需求在治疗生产中的中心地位。它倡导一种废除主义形式，但废除的是社会控制，而非对不适状态的承认或获得治疗的权利。



My understanding of Neurodivergent Marxism follows in these traditions, while departing on some specifics. Clearly, pathologisation can sometimes be wrongful and harmful, and in such cases should be resisted. But attempts to deny the reality of mental illness or disability as such are no less harmful. At best, they waste huge effort swapping terms (e.g. ‘illness’ for ‘distress’) without improving material conditions, while at worst they provide justification for a mass cultural denial of recognition of disablement, or state denial of the requirement to provide support. By contrast, the Socialist Patients Collective’s manifesto was titled Turn Illness into a Weapon, and they precisely called for the use of illness to demand resources and support while also calling for the ‘sick proletariat’ to fight against capitalist domination. In line with this example, Neurodivergent Marxism, as I understand it – at least at the current historical moment – seeks to turn both neurodivergent disablement and illness into sites of organisation and resistance to the system that necessitates both the production and harm of both neurodivergents and neurotypicals. In doing this, we should not seek to unwisely erase ancient concepts of mental illness, which as we have seen were recognised globally, as such. Rather, we must work towards breaking the associations between health, normality, and productivity. Challenging the biomedical and psychological understandings and their ideological functions, yet without denying the reality of mental illness or disablement, will be necessary for constructing new ways of recognising illness and disablement in such a manner that nonetheless resists eugenic ideology and pressure.

我对神经殊异马克思主义的理解遵循这些传统，但在某些具体问题上有所偏离。显然，病理化有时可能是错误且有害的，在这种情况下应当予以抵制。然而，试图否认精神疾病或残障本身的存在，其危害性并不亚于前者。往好了说，这种做法耗费巨大精力去替换术语（例如用“痛苦”替代“疾病”），却未能改善物质条件；往坏了说，它为大规模文化上拒绝承认残障，或国家拒绝提供必要支持提供了借口。相比之下，社会主义患者集体的宣言题为《将疾病转化为武器》，他们明确呼吁利用疾病来争取资源和支持，同时号召“生病的无产阶级”反抗资本主义统治。遵循这一范例，神经殊异马克思主义——正如我所理解的，至少在当前历史时刻——旨在将神经殊异残障与疾病转化为组织和抵抗的阵地，对抗那个既催生又伤害神经殊异者与神经典型者的制度。 在此过程中，我们不应轻率地抹去古老的精神疾病概念——正如我们所知，这些概念在全球范围内都曾得到承认。相反，我们必须努力打破健康、常态与生产力之间的关联。挑战生物医学和心理学的理解及其意识形态功能，同时不否认精神疾病或残障的现实，对于构建识别疾病与残障的新方式至关重要——这些新方式必须能够抵制优生学意识形态及其压力。



My understanding of Neurodivergent Marxism also sits in a realist and materialist tradition of disability studies, which sees disablement as always relationally produced between bodyminds and the world. This does not deny that there can be a pathological aspect to some forms of disability, which may require medical assistance. Indeed, it demands the right to access medical care as and where it is useful. But it resists the idea that disability is merely an individual problem, a mere mechanical breaking of the body or mind to always be mechanically fixed. As we have seen, our conceptions of ability, impairment, normality, and so forth change in different contexts. This is in part as more people actually become disabled or non-disabled, in relation to each other – compared to the norm – and to their environments. It is vital to remain realists about disability in this historical moment since just as with illness, there is a huge administrative and ideological pressure to obscure or erase recognition of disability. After all, recognising disability and how it is continually reproduced by the dominant mode of production implies recognition of the state’s responsibility to provide support, for as long as the state persists.

我对神经殊异马克思主义的理解，同样植根于残障研究的现实主义与唯物主义传统，这一传统认为残障始终是在身心与世界的互动关系中产生的。这并不否认某些形式的残障可能具有病理学层面，需要医疗辅助。事实上，它恰恰要求在有用且必要的地方，保障获得医疗服务的权利。但它反对将残障仅仅视为个体问题，仅仅看作是身体或心灵的机械性“损坏”，并总需以机械方式“修复”。正如我们所看到的，我们关于能力、损伤、正常等概念，在不同的情境下会发生变化。这部分是因为，相对于所谓的“常态”以及各自所处的环境，越来越多的人实际上在彼此参照中成为了残障者或非残障者。在这个历史时刻，对残障保持现实主义态度至关重要，因为正如对待疾病一样，存在着巨大的行政与意识形态压力，试图模糊或抹杀对残障的承认。 毕竟，承认残障以及它如何被主导的生产方式不断再生产，意味着承认国家有责任提供支持，只要国家继续存在。



On this view, neurodivergent disabilities such as autism or ADHD are not random clusters of traits, grouped together by psychiatric whim, as many liberal critical analyses of psychiatry suggest. Neither are they mere identities, as liberal neurodiversity proponents have suggested. Rather, they are what Sartre called ‘serial collectives’, that is, collectives of people that tend to share certain experiences and problems given objective relations with material conditions.11 As we have seen in this book, our current disabilities emerged, certain clusters of traits became salient as disabilities, because of objective material relations emerging from the development of the Empire of Normality. This, however, does not mean that normality and divergence are not real: it only means that their reality is socially and materially constituted, and hence can be altered only through material change.

根据这种观点，诸如孤独症或多动症等神经殊异残障，并非如许多自由主义对精神病学的批判分析所暗示的那样，是精神病学一时兴起随意归类的特质集合。它们也不仅仅是自由主义神经多样性倡导者所提出的身份认同。相反，它们是萨特所称的"序列集体"，即由于与物质条件的客观关系而倾向于共享某些经验和问题的人群集合。 11 正如我们在本书中所见，我们当前的残障之所以出现，某些特质集合之所以凸显为残障，正是因为源于"常态帝国"发展的客观物质关系。然而，这并不意味着常态与殊异不是真实的：它只意味着它们的现实是由社会和物质构成的，因此只能通过物质变革来改变。



I do not mean to suggest that this is the final analysis of these issues. These are preliminary suggestions for the current historical moment. For now, my aim is not to work out exactly which classifications are valid or where the boundary between health and illness should lie. Such boundaries are not, and cannot be, fixed. They are relative to time and place and change as people and contexts change. Neither is my aim to suggest that such boundaries should never be challenged. To the contrary, I think they constantly require challenging, when it comes to both bodily and mental illness. For disablement and pathologisation occurs through colonial and capitalist logics, and often reproduces their valuations. Our analysis will thus assume that disability and illness are facts, even if they always arise in social and ideological contexts and even if the boundaries are necessarily shifting and obscure. It is only in accepting these as real that we can begin to effectively organise to change reality as it is currently constituted.

我并非意在暗示这是对这些问题的最终分析。这些只是针对当前历史时刻的初步建议。目前，我的目标并非要精确界定哪些分类是有效的，或者健康与疾病的界限应该划在哪里。这样的界限并非，也不可能，是固定不变的。它们相对于时间和地点而存在，并随着人和情境的变化而变化。我的目标也并非暗示这些界限永远不应受到挑战。恰恰相反，我认为它们需要不断地被挑战，无论是对于身体疾病还是精神疾病而言。因为残障化和病理化是通过殖民主义和资本主义的逻辑发生的，并且常常复制了它们的价值评判。因此，我们的分析将假定残障和疾病是客观存在的事实，即使它们总是在社会和意识形态的语境中产生，即使其界限必然是变动不居且模糊的。只有接受这些是真实的，我们才能开始有效地组织起来，去改变当前构成的现实。



EXTRACTIVE ABANDONMENT

榨取性抛弃



To recap, so far, we have explicitly used two aspects of a Marxian analysis. The first is the materialist approach to history, which views human consciousness and agency as significantly constituted yet also constrained by the broader economic, social, and material conditions and relations of the specific age. This has helped us see how modern conceptions of normality and productivity have arisen and changed how we think about health. We have also drawn on and developed Marx’s conception of alienation, which shows how material conditions can be harmful to us and stratify us into hierarchies. This has helped us understand rising levels of mental illness or disablement in the modern world.

总结来说，到目前为止，我们明确运用了马克思主义分析的两个方面。首先是历史的唯物主义方法，它将人类意识和能动性视为在很大程度上由特定时代更广泛的经济、社会及物质条件和关系所构成，同时也受其制约。这帮助我们理解了现代关于正常和生产力的观念是如何兴起的，以及它们如何改变了我们对健康的看法。我们还借鉴并发展了马克思的异化概念，它揭示了物质条件如何可能对我们造成伤害，并将我们分层为等级体系。这有助于我们理解现代世界中精神疾病或残疾水平的上升。



But a Marxian analysis offers more than just materialism. Marx also saw the potential for historical change arising dialectically, from contradictions in our material relations. In the period in which he was writing, recall, the key conflict he saw was between the capitalist class and the workers. As I have noted previously, for Marx, it was in the fact that value was developed collectively by the workers, but then accumulated by a tiny number of capitalists, that the possibility of a new synthesis lay. He saw that the capitalist drive for ever-increasing expansion constantly led to the need for new machinery and technology. In turn, he suggested, this would lead to increased worker deskilling and thus increased alienation. Highlighting this was important for Marx as he believed that this was unsustainable, and that once they became more aware of their situation, workers would be more likely to organise and resist. His theory thus both began in praxis and in turn sought to help to make future praxis more efficient.

但马克思主义分析提供的远不止唯物主义。马克思还看到了历史变革的潜力，这种潜力辩证地产生于我们物质关系中的矛盾。在他写作的那个时期，请记住，他所看到的关键冲突是资产阶级与工人阶级之间的对立。正如我之前提到的，对马克思而言，价值由工人集体创造，却由少数资本家积累，这一事实蕴含着新综合的可能性。他认为，资本家对不断扩张的追求不断催生对新机器和技术的需求。反过来，他提出，这将导致工人技能退化加剧，从而加剧异化。强调这一点对马克思至关重要，因为他相信这是不可持续的，一旦工人更加意识到自己的处境，他们就更有可能组织起来进行抵抗。因此，他的理论既源于实践，又反过来致力于使未来的实践更加高效。



We can see similar contradictions when it comes to disability. In this regard, newer materialist analyses have been most notably developed by activists and scholars such as Martha Russell, Jasbir Puar, Artie Vierkant, and Beatrice Adler-Bolton. These take us far beyond the oversimplifications sometimes associated with the traditional social model. On the one hand, as Martha Russell stresses, a Marxian analysis helps us see how capital and the state need a surplus population to act as a reserve army of workers. Notably, for Marx, since capitalists compete to produce, capitalism is inherently prone to crises of overproduction. This therefore often requires pushing some of the working class into the surplus population. Moreover, increased automation, driven by the most fundamental logics of capitalism, also continually pushes more of the population into the surplus. Yet, capitalism also often has periods of growth, which requires having a surplus to draw on. This reserve army must also be ready to be called upon in times of sickness, war, and so forth.

在残障问题上，我们也能看到类似的矛盾。在这方面，玛莎·拉塞尔、贾斯比尔·普尔、阿尔蒂·维尔坎特和比阿特丽斯·阿德勒-博尔顿等行动者和学者，对更新的唯物主义分析做出了尤为显著的贡献。这些分析使我们远远超越了有时与传统社会模式相关的过度简化。一方面，正如玛莎·拉塞尔所强调的，马克思主义分析帮助我们看清资本和国家如何需要一个过剩人口来充当工人的后备军。值得注意的是，对马克思而言，由于资本家竞相生产，资本主义天生就容易出现生产过剩的危机。因此，这常常需要将一部分工人阶级推入过剩人口。此外，由资本主义最根本逻辑驱动的自动化程度提高，也在持续将更多人口推向过剩。然而，资本主义也常常有增长期，这需要有可调用的过剩人口。这支后备军也必须随时准备在疾病、战争等时期被征召。



Thus, the existence of a surplus population is no less necessary for capitalism than is the existence of workers, since capitalism both creates an ever-expanding surplus population while also relying on them to act as a reserve army. Put another way, disabled people – who make up much of the surplus – need to exist for capitalism to exist, and are hence part of what is both produced by, and sustains, the system. So it is not just that the capitalist class also often finds ways to profit off the surplus class through a variety of industries built around the management and confinement of the surplus. It is also that the capitalist class both creates the surplus, and often needs them for the possibility of growth at all. For every time there is a possibility of growth, this suddenly requires more workers, and for them to be read a surplus population has to be maintained. On this view, then, it is not just the case that certain environments, especially when driven by capitalist logics, are disabling for people with impairments. It is also that capitalist logics both produce and require disablement, which is itself primarily determined in relation to the needs of capital at any given time.

因此，剩余人口的存在对资本主义而言，其必要性不亚于工人的存在，因为资本主义既在不断创造日益扩大的剩余人口，同时也依赖他们充当后备军。换言之，构成剩余人口主体的残疾人——他们的存在是资本主义存在的必要条件，因而既是这一体系所生产的产物，也是维系该体系的一部分。所以，这不仅意味着资产阶级常常通过围绕管理和限制剩余人口建立的各种产业从剩余阶级中获利，还意味着资产阶级既创造了剩余人口，又往往需要他们来实现增长的可能性。因为每当存在增长可能时，就会突然需要更多工人，而为了随时提供这些工人，就必须维持一个剩余人口群体。由此看来，某些环境——尤其是受资本主义逻辑驱动的环境——不仅会对残障人士造成障碍。 资本主义逻辑既制造又需要残障，而残障本身主要取决于特定时期资本的需求。



The association between capitalism and health is complex, and has been further clarified by Adler-Bolton and Vierkant in their book Health Communism: A Surplus Manifesto. Here I have primarily focused on how capitalism led to a conflation of health with both normality and productivity. But there is more to say. Adler-Bolton and Vierkant emphasise how capitalism requires health, to some extent, for productivity. At the same time, it must pathologise surplus populations while mining them for productivity through industries of administration in order to extract profit from their ill health. And the central aim of this is not to improve the prospects of thriving for members of the surplus class, but rather for capitalists to profit from the ongoing maintenance of their unwellness alongside the exploitation of care workers.

资本主义与健康之间的关系错综复杂，阿德勒-博尔顿和维尔坎特在《健康共产主义：剩余宣言》一书中对此进行了深入阐释。此处我主要聚焦于资本主义如何将健康与常态及生产力混为一谈。但问题不止于此。阿德勒-博尔顿和维尔坎特强调，资本主义在某种程度上需要健康来维持生产力。与此同时，它必须将剩余人口病理化，同时通过行政管理产业榨取他们的生产力，从而从其病弱状态中牟利。这一过程的核心目标并非改善剩余阶级成员的生存前景，而是让资本家在持续维持其病弱状态的同时，通过剥削护理工作者来获取利润。



The overall disposition of the capitalist political economy of health consists in what they call extractive abandonment. That is, capitalism both creates and extracts from the surplus class while simultaneously abandoning them. This allows Adler-Bolton and Vierkant to frame the surplus population as a class (rather than a subset of the working class). Importantly, this goes beyond a social model analysis, which frames disablement as oppression imposed by barriers. More than this, a political economy characterised by extractive abandonment of the surplus class must build industries to administer surplus populations in order to mine their oppressed status for profit while also extracting surplus value from workers at these institutions. We see this, for instance, in the multi-billion dollar Applied Behaviour Analysis industry, which does little to help most autistic individuals subjected to it, and harms many, but which continues to exist and grow because so much profit is made through it. Considering how the overall disposition of the political economy is one of extractive abandonment, this helps explain why this industry has been able to continue its expansion despite mass resistance from autistic activists.

资本主义健康政治经济的总体倾向在于他们所谓的榨取式遗弃。也就是说，资本主义既创造并榨取剩余阶级，同时又遗弃他们。这使得阿德勒-博尔顿和维尔坎特能够将剩余人口框定为一个阶级（而非工人阶级的一个子集）。重要的是，这超越了社会模式分析——该分析将残障视为由障碍施加的压迫。不仅如此，以榨取式遗弃剩余阶级为特征的政治经济，必须建立产业来管理剩余人口，以便从其受压迫的状态中挖掘利润，同时从这些机构的工人身上榨取剩余价值。例如，我们在价值数十亿美元的应用行为分析产业中看到了这一点，该产业对大多数接受其干预的孤独谱系个体帮助甚微，且伤害了许多人，但它之所以持续存在并发展，正是因为通过它能够获取巨额利润。 考虑到政治经济的整体格局具有榨取性抛弃的特征，这有助于解释为何该行业能够在孤独谱系活动人士的大规模抵制下持续扩张。



TOWARDS NEURODIVERGENT POWER

迈向神经殊异力量



With the analysis presented in this book, however, I argue that we see a more specific orientation of extractive abandonment when it comes to not just neurodivergence but also neurodiversity at the group level. Consider, on the one hand, how vital neurodiversity at the group level is for production. Part of what follows from adopting a neurodiversity paradigm lens is the recognition that mental functioning and thus production emerges from our neurological diversity at the group level. No human is capable of doing much alone, or is wholly independent, and everything we do relies to varying extents on people who think differently having produced at least some part of what each of us uses. Moreover, even those most valued in the neuronormative hierarchies of capitalism cannot produce except in tandem with those less valued. At the level of the team, the company, the corporation, whole industries, nations, or the economic system itself, neurodiversity – that is, diversity in cognitive and emotional functioning – is required for capitalism to continue at all.

然而，通过本书的分析，我认为我们能看到一种更为具体的榨取性抛弃取向，这不仅针对神经殊异性，也针对群体层面的神经多样性。试想，一方面，群体层面的神经多样性对生产何其重要。采用神经多样性范式视角所带来的部分认知是：心理功能乃至生产活动，都源于我们在群体层面的神经多样性。没有谁能独自成就太多，或完全独立，我们所做的一切都在不同程度上依赖于那些思维方式不同的人，他们至少生产了我们每个人所使用的某些部分。此外，即便是资本主义神经规范等级中最受重视的那些人，也必须与那些不那么受重视的人协同合作才能进行生产。在团队、公司、企业、整个行业、国家乃至经济体系本身的层面，神经多样性——即认知和情感功能的多样性——是资本主义得以持续运行的必要条件。



This is not a mere theoretical claim. There are multiple historical and scientific studies that support this. For instance, one study found that including one person with ADHD in a group makes that group much better at creative problem-solving at the group level.12 Other studies have found that increased cognitive diversity at the group level makes groups better at adapting to changing environments.13 Marx himself noted that capitalism functioned in part by what he called ‘the general intellect’14 – the combined intellect of all humanity – and we can now add that the general intellect requires neurodiversity at the general level as well as in more local groups.

这并非仅仅是理论上的主张。有多项历史与科学研究为此提供了支持。例如，一项研究发现，在团队中加入一名患有注意力缺陷多动障碍（ADHD）的成员，能显著提升整个团队在创造性问题解决方面的集体能力。 12 其他研究也发现，团队层面认知多样性的增加，有助于团队更好地适应不断变化的环境。 13 马克思本人曾指出，资本主义的运作部分依赖于他所谓的“普遍智力” 14 ——即全人类智力的总和——而我们现在可以补充说，普遍智力不仅需要在更局部的群体中，也需要在普遍层面上具备神经多样性。



It is similarly notable that capitalism always requires surplus forms of neurodivergence ready for the cognitive requirements of tomorrow. As Marx noted, capitalism brings the constant revolution of the means of production – of technology, machinery, and so forth. But because of this, it constantly needs different kinds of minds to be ready for whatever comes next. Recall, as Harvey Blume wrote in his seminal neurodiversity article: ‘Who can say what form of wiring will prove best at any given moment? Cybernetics and computer culture, for example, may favor a somewhat autistic cast of mind’.15 While it has now become something of a stereotype to say autistic people are good with maths or computers, this is true in at least some cases. And where autistic people are not good with computers, many others provide important skills due to the various cognitive traits associated with the autistic population.

同样值得注意的是，资本主义总是需要储备过剩的神经殊异性形式，以满足未来的认知需求。正如马克思所指出的，资本主义带来了生产手段——技术、机器等等——的持续革命。但正因如此，它不断需要不同类型的心智，为即将到来的任何变化做好准备。回想一下，正如哈维·布鲁姆在其开创性的神经多样性文章中所写：“谁能断言在任何一个特定时刻，哪种形式的‘布线’将被证明是最佳的呢？例如，控制论和计算机文化，可能就偏爱某种带有孤独谱系特质的心智。” 15 虽然现在说孤独谱系群体擅长数学或计算机已经成了一种刻板印象，但这至少在部分情况下是成立的。而在孤独谱系群体不擅长计算机的领域，由于与孤独谱系群体相关的各种认知特质，许多其他人提供了重要的技能。



Yet despite capital both needing and constantly extracting from neurodivergent cognition, it simultaneously abandons neurodivergent people. This begins at birth, when neurodivergent infants are framed as tragedies, and continues in schools, which are still often based on eugenicist logics and forms of segregation. From there it continues in adulthood, whether in workplace discrimination or in the mass incarceration of neurodivergent people, in prisons and then nursing homes. This social subjugation is then reified through psychological and biomedical research, thus continually cementing the naturalisation of capitalist cognitive hierarchies.

然而，尽管资本既需要又不断从神经殊异的认知中汲取养分，它却同时抛弃了神经殊异者。这种抛弃始于出生之时，神经殊异的婴儿被塑造成悲剧，并在学校中延续——这些学校往往仍基于优生学逻辑和隔离形式。此后，这种抛弃贯穿成年期，无论是在职场歧视中，还是在监狱乃至养老院中对神经殊异者的大规模监禁中。这种社会压制随后通过心理学和生物医学研究被具体化，从而不断固化资本主义认知等级制度的自然化。



These contradictions are important to bear in mind as they help us understand how capitalism requires neurodiversity, and neurodivergence, even while devaluing and seeking to control it. To be clear, I am not in any way suggesting that we should value neurodivergence because it contributes to collective functioning. Rather, my point is that recognising these factors is helpful for starting to apprehend how capitalism devalues neurodivergence even by its own logics. It is equally useful for recognising the power neurodivergent people have if we organise in great enough numbers to resist. While we are individually disabled, we have collective cognitive power – itself a product of our neurological diversity – that could be harnessed no less than the collective power of the working class to combat the dominant order.

这些矛盾值得牢记，因为它们帮助我们理解资本主义如何既需要神经多样性与神经殊异性，同时又贬低并试图控制它们。需要明确的是，我绝非主张我们应该因为神经殊异性有助于集体运作而重视它。相反，我的观点是，认识到这些因素有助于我们开始理解资本主义如何甚至依据其自身逻辑来贬低神经殊异性。这同样有助于认识到，如果我们组织起足够庞大的力量进行抵抗，神经殊异者所拥有的力量。尽管我们作为个体是失能的，但我们拥有集体的认知力量——这本身就是我们神经多样性的产物——这种力量不亚于工人阶级的集体力量，可以被用来对抗主导秩序。



It is worth considering how the proponent of a liberal neurodiversity approach might respond to what I have just suggested. The question they might raise here regards whether, if capital does in fact need both neurodivergence and collective neurodiversity, then there could be room for neurodivergent emancipation within a capitalist framework. That is, it could be argued that since capitalism and the state currently devalue neurodivergent people even from within the logics of capitalism, then the issue is more about misrecognition than political economy. In this argument, raising awareness that capital requires neurodivergence just as it requires neurotypicality could provide grounds for developing a revaluation and new recognition of neurodivergence within a capitalist system. If this were possible, it might seem like a good basis for cultivating neurodivergent liberation without changing the deeper structures of society.

值得思考的是，自由主义神经多样性方法的支持者会如何回应我刚才提出的观点。他们可能提出的问题是：如果资本确实既需要神经殊异性，也需要集体的神经多样性，那么在资本主义框架内是否有可能为神经殊异者的解放留出空间。也就是说，有人可能会争辩，既然资本主义和国家目前甚至在资本主义的逻辑内部也在贬低神经殊异者，那么问题更多是误认而非政治经济学问题。按照这种论点，提高人们对资本既需要神经典型性也需要神经殊异性的认识，可能为在资本主义体系内重新评估和认可神经殊异性提供基础。如果这成为可能，似乎就为在不改变社会深层结构的情况下培育神经殊异者的解放提供了良好的基础。



Indeed, this seems to be precisely the implicit assumption guiding much equality, diversity, and inclusion work on neurodiversity, which focuses on recognising neurodivergent ‘strengths’ to help get more neurodivergent people into work. It is also worth noting that Singer’s concept of an ‘ecological society’ that constructs niches is, while being opposed to the ideology of normality, still perfectly compatible with capitalist logics. After all, if capital and the state can construct niches to help neurodivergent people into work, they can then extract surplus value from neurodivergent labour. As and when this is economically viable there is room for expanding capitalist neuronormativity to incorporate some minds currently positioned as neurodivergent, to bring them out of the surplus through environmental construction that enables their functioning.

的确，这似乎正是指导许多关于神经多样性的平等、多元与包容工作的隐含假设，其重点在于识别神经殊异者的"优势"，以帮助更多神经殊异者进入职场。同样值得注意的是，辛格提出的构建生态位的"生态社会"概念，虽然反对常态性的意识形态，却与资本主义逻辑完全兼容。毕竟，如果资本与国家能够构建生态位来帮助神经殊异者就业，它们就能从神经殊异者的劳动中榨取剩余价值。一旦这在经济上变得可行，就有空间扩展资本主义的神经常态性，将目前被定位为神经殊异的一些心智纳入其中，通过构建能使其发挥作用的环境，将他们从剩余状态中解放出来。



Yet I precisely do not think this will lead to liberation in any meaningful sense, at least not for any but the most privileged neurodivergent people. It is not just that this approach will inevitably exclude those with disabilities that require more immediate support, who will remain discriminated against in the surplus, segregated, and controlled. In this, it will only reform the pathology paradigm, making it marginally more inclusive, rather than overcome it. Neither is it only that capital would likely only use this to increase the administration and control of neurominorities, pushing them towards ever-more refined brain-type specific roles that would increase predetermined specialisation and thus limit freedom.

然而我恰恰认为这不会带来任何有意义的解放，至少除了最享有特权的神经殊异人群外，对其他人而言并非如此。这不仅是因为这种做法将不可避免地排除那些需要更直接支持的残障人士，他们仍将在过剩、隔离与控制中遭受歧视。就此而言，它只会改良病理学范式，使其略微更具包容性，而非克服它。这也不仅仅是因为资本很可能只会利用这一点来加强对神经少数群体的管理与控制，将他们推向日益精细化的脑型特定角色，从而加剧预定的专业化并因此限制自由。



It is also that there is a further neuronormative contradiction in capitalism that, I think, shows this will not free even those of us who are granted niches to be able to enter the workforce. For based on the historical analysis provided in previous chapters, capitalism, especially once it reaches a period where labour requires high-level cognitive or emotional processing, is increasingly disposed towards making us all, at the very least, either mentally ill or disabled. This includes those positioned as temporarily neurotypical, who it harms even if not quite so directly as neurodivergents.

此外，资本主义中还存在更深层次的神经元规范性矛盾，我认为这表明即使是我们这些被允许进入劳动力市场的人，也无法获得真正的自由。根据前几章的历史分析，资本主义，特别是当它进入劳动需要高水平认知或情感处理的阶段时，越来越倾向于使我们所有人——至少是所有人——要么精神上患病，要么身体上残疾。这包括那些暂时被视为神经典型的人，即使他们不像神经多样性者那样直接受到伤害，资本主义同样对他们造成了损害。



To understand this, consider how, as we have seen from my historical analysis, capitalism always has a neurological in-group and an out-group, the boundaries of which shift. This shifting is largely in relation to perceived productive potential, but also in relation to consumer potential and whether any given person is susceptible to adopting the desires required for the needs of capital. We have seen that this harms those in the out-group through positioning them as surplus, but it is also harmful to the in-group, as it positions them as workers to be exploited until they finally become neurodivergent through burnout, illness, or cognitive decline.

要理解这一点，不妨思考一下，正如我的历史分析所揭示的，资本主义始终存在一个神经学意义上的内群体和一个外群体，其边界是不断变动的。这种变动主要与感知到的生产潜力有关，但也与消费潜力以及特定个体是否易于采纳资本所需欲望有关。我们已经看到，这通过将外群体定位为过剩人口而伤害了他们，但同样也伤害了内群体，因为它将他们定位为可被剥削的劳动者，直至他们最终因倦怠、疾病或认知衰退而成为神经殊异者。



In this, as we see most clearly in post-Fordist economies, capitalism puts each of us between two harmful conditions. Either it ‘values’ us, in which case it makes us workers and mercilessly exploits us, making us ill through the alienation such exploitation brings. Or, it disvalues us, making us disabled and discriminating against us as part of the surplus population. This often pushes us into poverty and positions us to be treated as disposable. However each of our minds is constituted, we are caught between these two options, neither good for us, and both harmful in different ways.

正如我们在后福特主义经济中最清晰地看到的，资本主义将我们每个人都置于两种有害境地之间。要么它“重视”我们，将我们变成工人并无情地剥削，使我们因这种剥削带来的异化而患病；要么它贬低我们，将我们视为残障人士，并作为过剩人口的一部分加以歧视，这常常将我们推向贫困，使我们被当作可抛弃的对象。无论我们的心智如何构成，我们都困于这两种选择之间，两者皆非善途，且以不同方式造成伤害。



Many of us sit somewhere between these two extremes, or fall from one into the other at different points in our lives. Some enabled people in the working class become disabled and end up discarded in the surplus class. For instance, a worker who catches COVID-19 and develops Long Covid, due to their working conditions (say, an unventilated office where large numbers of workers are crammed together), may suddenly find themselves neurodivergent and disabled to the point of being unable to work. Indeed, many people temporarily shift to the surplus class simply due to burnout from overwork and stress. Others begin in the surplus class, with neurodivergent disabilities, but then find a niche job where they can thrive for a time, until alienation makes them ill. Overall the situation is one where mental health is elusive for most of us, many of us are in precarious and part-time employment, and the lines between worker and surplus become blurred.

我们许多人处于这两个极端之间，或是在人生的不同阶段从一端跌落到另一端。一些原本健全的工人阶级成员可能因故致残，最终被抛入剩余阶级。例如，一名工人因工作环境（比如通风不良、人员密集的办公室）感染新冠病毒并发展为长期新冠后，可能会突然发现自己变得神经殊异且残疾，以至于无法工作。事实上，许多人仅仅因为过度工作和压力导致的倦怠，就暂时性地转入剩余阶级。另一些人则从剩余阶级起步，本身带有神经殊异相关的残疾，但后来找到了一份能让他们暂时施展才华的合适工作，直到异化使他们再次病倒。总体而言，当前状况是：心理健康对大多数人来说遥不可及，许多人从事着不稳定或兼职的工作，工人与剩余人口之间的界限变得日益模糊。



It is important to stress how this is interlocked with the oppression of manual workers as much as cognitive workers, and that the divide is often blurred and superficial. Most importantly, cognitive and emotional exploitation in post-Fordist economies require the production and harm of disabled people in the global south. As Jasbir Puar notes, the very same technologies used in post-Fordist economies

必须强调的是，这与体力劳动者和脑力劳动者所受的压迫同样密不可分，且这种区分往往是模糊而表面的。最重要的是，后福特主义经济中的认知与情感剥削，需要以全球南方残障人士的生产与伤害为代价。正如贾斯比尔·普阿尔所指出的，后福特主义经济中使用的技术





produce vastly debilitated populations across the globe, from Chinese labourers in Apple factories who commit suicide, to wheelchair technology that enhances mobility developed in Israel […] on the backs of Palestinian oppression and immobility, to the mountains of e-waste hand-sanded by the working poor in India, to the neocolonial extraction of minerals and natural substances from resource-rich areas for the purpose of manufacturing hardware.16

在全球范围内催生了大量孱弱群体——从苹果工厂里自杀的中国劳工，到以色列基于对巴勒斯坦人的压迫与行动限制而开发的增强行动能力的轮椅技术，再到印度贫困工人手工打磨的堆积如山的电子垃圾，以及为制造硬件而从资源丰富地区进行新殖民主义的矿产与自然资源掠夺。 16





In this, the same working of the same system harms both cognitive workers in the imperial core and manual workers in the peripheries, albeit in different ways. Across the globe, even while bringing rapid progress in mechanistic medicine, capitalism is making workers ill.

由此可见，同一体系的运作以不同方式同时伤害着帝国核心的脑力劳动者和边缘地带的体力劳动者。在全球范围内，即便资本主义带来了机械医学的飞速进步，它仍在使劳动者病弱不堪。



This contradiction – being caught between alienation and disablement – does not just help clarify how liberation is impossible under the capitalist mode of production. It also shows us how the interests of the working class and the interests of the surplus class are one. Rather than the surplus being a drain on workers, as the dominant ideology suggests, the two are intimately connected, with members of each routinely having some small part in, or crossing over to, the other. Both neurodivergence and neurotypicality are a matter of proximity to a norm that changes in line with both global and local changes in the means of production, as well as any given person’s current level of ability or debility. Neurotypicality is not just a temporary phase for any individual, but a phase whose continuation becomes more unlikely with each passing year as capitalism intensifies.

这种矛盾——被困于异化与失能之间——不仅有助于阐明为何资本主义生产方式下不可能实现解放。它还向我们展示了工人阶级的利益与剩余阶级的利益是同一的。剩余阶级并非如主流意识形态所暗示的那样是工人的负担，两者实则紧密相连，每一方的成员都时常在对方中扮演微小角色，或跨越界限进入对方。无论是神经殊异性还是神经典型性，都关乎与一个规范的接近程度，而这个规范会随着生产方式的全球与地方性变化，以及任何个体当前的能力或身体失能水平而改变。神经典型性对任何个体而言都不仅是一个暂时阶段，更是一个随着资本主义日益强化、其延续性逐年递减的阶段。



---

Empire of Normality



11



After normality

常态之后



Following the October Revolution in 1917, Vladimir Lenin and the Bolsheviks began attempting to shift from a capitalist to a communist economic system. This was no easy thing. Russia was poor, in great turmoil, and under threat of invasion from Germany and other nearby nations. Neither were the Bolsheviks experienced in ruling a country. After all, they were revolutionaries, not career politicians. Their attempts thus had mixed success.

1917 年十月革命后，弗拉基米尔·列宁和布尔什维克开始尝试从资本主义经济体系转向共产主义经济体系。这绝非易事。俄国贫穷不堪，动荡不安，还面临德国等邻国入侵的威胁。布尔什维克也缺乏治国经验。毕竟他们是革命者，而非职业政客。因此他们的尝试成败参半。



Bolshevik rule improved day-to-day life for millions, bringing state healthcare and important reforms for disabled people. Yet despite their attempts to move beyond capitalism, the Bolshevik state never established communism. Rather, the Soviet Union took a form that some have called ‘state capitalism’. Marx himself had seen communism as requiring the withering away of the state, and workers in control of their own workplaces. By contrast, the workspaces of the Soviet Union were state-controlled. Lenin himself had seen this as a brief transitional stage, preferable to market capitalism but still a form of capitalist domination. But when Joseph Stalin became state leader following Lenin’s death in 1924, the new leader soon gave up on shifting beyond state capitalism. Instead, Stalin simply declared that communism had been achieved, despite this going against what Marx and Lenin had suggested.

布尔什维克的统治改善了数百万人的日常生活，建立了国家医疗体系并为残疾人推行了重要改革。然而，尽管他们试图超越资本主义，布尔什维克国家却从未建立起共产主义。相反，苏联采取了一种被某些人称为"国家资本主义"的形态。马克思本人认为共产主义需要国家逐渐消亡，并由工人掌控自身的工作场所。相比之下，苏联的工作场所却由国家控制。列宁本人曾将此视为短暂的过渡阶段，虽优于市场资本主义，但仍是一种资本主义支配形式。但当约瑟夫·斯大林于 1924 年列宁逝世后成为国家领导人时，这位新领袖很快放弃了向国家资本主义之外转型的尝试。斯大林直接宣称共产主义已经实现，尽管这违背了马克思和列宁的论述。



In this context, the emphasis on production continued. And especially given the continuation of market capitalism over much of the world, there was still an emphasis on competition, albeit this time competition with the capitalists. At the same time, as the Lithuanian Marxist Raya Dunayevskaya argued as far back as 1941, alienation was maintained within these Soviet relations of production. In her own words, the ‘determining factor in analysing the class nature of a society is not whether the means of production are the private property of the capitalist class or are state-owned’ but ‘whether they are monopolized and alienated from the direct producers’. With this in mind, she went on, in the Soviet Union ‘there exists the real economic relation of state-capitalist-exploiter to the propertyless exploited’.1

在此背景下，对生产的强调仍在继续。特别是考虑到市场资本主义在世界大部分地区的持续存在，竞争依然受到重视，尽管这次的竞争对象是资本家。与此同时，正如立陶宛马克思主义者拉娅·杜纳耶夫斯卡娅早在 1941 年所论证的那样，异化在这些苏联的生产关系中依然存在。用她的话来说，“分析一个社会阶级性质的决定性因素，不在于生产资料是资本家阶级的私有财产还是国有财产”，而在于“它们是否被垄断并与直接生产者相异化”。考虑到这一点，她进一步指出，在苏联“存在着国家资本主义剥削者与被剥削的无产者之间真实的经济关系”。 1



As it shifted into an industrial state capitalist economy, biomedicine, psychiatry, and psychology in the Soviet Union remained within the pathology paradigm, and the broader Empire of Normality persisted. It was not just that the physician class refused to give up their power, or that these professions were used to pathologise political dissidents and for social control more generally, much as in the rest of the world. It was also that the idea of individual ability as compared to the norm, and the ideology of normality, still dominated. With very limited knowledge or analysis of neurodivergent oppression among the Bolsheviks, the Empire of Normality was not recognised as something that had to be destroyed in the course of the revolution.

随着苏联转向工业国家资本主义经济，其生物医学、精神病学和心理学领域依然固守病理学范式，更广泛的"常态帝国"也持续存在。这不仅是因为医生阶层拒绝放弃权力，或是这些专业被用于将政治异见者病理化并进行更广泛的社会控制——这与世界其他地区的情况并无二致。更深层的原因在于，以个体能力对照"常态"的理念，以及常态意识形态本身，仍然占据着主导地位。由于布尔什维克内部对神经殊异群体所受压迫的认知和分析极为有限，"常态帝国"并未被视作革命进程中必须摧毁的对象。



Indeed, Pavlov himself, the father of behaviourism, was lauded by Lenin specifically for his contribution to normalisation. In 1921 Lenin declared the ‘tremendous importance’ of Pavlov’s work to the ‘working people of the world’2 and provided funding for Pavlov’s work in the hope of creating a new standardised Soviet man. In turn, Lenin embraced Taylor’s scientific management of workers, which was adopted in Soviet Russia in the 1920s. The workers of the Soviet Union were, then, while spared from the harshest inequality of market capitalism, were not only lacking control of their workspaces. They were also being actively controlled to maximise production at all costs, which would have bought compulsory neuronormativity much as was found in the United States. This as much as anything else makes it clear that this attempt to move beyond capitalism never got past state capitalism, thus maintaining neuronormative domination despite radically decreasing economic inequality.

事实上，行为主义之父巴甫洛夫本人就因其对规范化的贡献而受到列宁的特别赞扬。1921 年，列宁宣布巴甫洛夫的工作对“全世界劳动人民”具有“巨大重要性” 2 ，并为巴甫洛夫的研究提供资金，以期塑造出新型的标准化苏联人。相应地，列宁采纳了泰勒对工人的科学管理方法，该方法在 20 世纪 20 年代被苏联采用。因此，苏联的工人虽然免于市场资本主义最严重的不平等，却不仅缺乏对工作场所的控制权。他们还被积极管控，不惜一切代价最大化生产，这必然带来了强制性的神经规范性，正如在美国所见。这一点比其他任何事都更清楚地表明，这种试图超越资本主义的努力从未超越国家资本主义，因此尽管经济不平等大幅减少，神经规范性的统治依然得以维持。



A particularly memorable example of pathology paradigm ideology concerns Lenin himself. After Lenin died in 1924, Stalin commissioned the creation of the Institute of the Brain. The aim of this institute was primarily to examine Lenin’s brain with the hope of unlocking the secrets of his genius. As Victor Sebestyen details, Soviet scientists ‘began the process of comparing Lenin’s brain with those of “ordinary people”’ as well as with ‘the brains of other high achievers’.3 This went on for a whole decade, at great expense, during which time Lenin’s brain was preserved using formaldehyde and alcohol. It was chopped and sliced into parts which were then analysed in relation to the average over the following years. As it turned out, however, this project was the product of ideology, and a significant waste of resources. As the decade-long project came to an end it was reported, as Sebestyen summarises, the key finding was that ‘Lenin’s brain was fairly ordinary. An average male brain weighs between 1,300 and 1,400 grams; Lenin’s was 1,340 grams’.

一个关于病理范式意识形态的特别令人难忘的例子涉及列宁本人。1924 年列宁去世后，斯大林下令成立了大脑研究所。该研究所的主要目的是检查列宁的大脑，以期揭开他天才的秘密。正如维克多·塞巴斯蒂安详细描述的那样，苏联科学家“开始将列宁的大脑与‘普通人’的大脑进行比较”，同时也与“其他高成就者的大脑”进行比较。 3 这项研究持续了整整十年，耗资巨大，期间列宁的大脑用甲醛和酒精保存。它被切成片，然后在随后的几年里与平均水平进行分析比较。然而，事实证明，这个项目是意识形态的产物，是对资源的巨大浪费。正如塞巴斯蒂安总结的那样，当这个长达十年的项目结束时，报告的关键发现是“列宁的大脑相当普通。普通男性大脑的重量在 1300 到 1400 克之间；列宁的是 1340 克”。



This is not to say that Bolshevik and Soviet approaches to normality were identical to those seen elsewhere. Initially, there had been less enthusiasm for eugenics in Russia than in Western European nations. As Nikolai Krementsov has detailed,4 in the latter half of the nineteenth century, the Russian Empire largely lacked the socio-economic conditions, such as urbanisation, over-population, and an influential aristocracy, that had brought a growth of interest in eugenics elsewhere. In fact, eugenic research expanded in Russia only following the 1917 Revolution. Bolshevik scientists then came to distinguish between what they called ‘bourgeois’ eugenics and ‘proletarian’ eugenics. But these were relatively similar in practice, and this was in turn criticised by anti-eugenicist Marxists, who suggested the focus should be on healthcare and education rather than biological control. Overall, support for eugenics was no more or less widespread in the Soviet Union than it was elsewhere. And beyond the Soviet Union, as late as 1934 Leon Trotsky, who by then had become a fierce critic of Stalin, still stressed hope for the application of ‘genuine scientific methods to the problem of eugenics’ in the United States.5 Ultimately, much as we have seen elsewhere, in Soviet Russia, and among Marxists more broadly, it was only following the Second World War that an open commitment to eugenics became widely seen as tainted by Fascism, and thus less acceptable. But even then, the ideology has continually re-emerged on the left as elsewhere on the political spectrum, with imagined utopian futures often being based on eugenicist logics that construct the ideal as a world that reinforces rather than challenges the equation between productivity and health.

这并非意味着布尔什维克和苏联对"正常"的界定方式与其他地方完全相同。起初，俄罗斯对优生学的热情远不及西欧国家。正如尼古拉·克列缅佐夫所详述的，在十九世纪后半叶，俄罗斯帝国基本缺乏推动优生学兴趣增长的社会经济条件，如城市化、人口过剩以及有影响力的贵族阶层。事实上，优生学研究在俄罗斯的扩展是在 1917 年革命之后。布尔什维克科学家随后区分了他们所谓的"资产阶级"优生学与"无产阶级"优生学。但在实践中，这两者相对相似，这反过来遭到了反优生学的马克思主义者的批评，他们认为重点应放在医疗保健和教育上，而非生物控制。总体而言，苏联对优生学的支持程度与其他地方并无二致。 在苏联之外，直到 1934 年，当时已成为斯大林激烈批评者的列昂·托洛茨基，仍强调对美国应用“真正的科学方法解决优生学问题”抱有希望。 5 最终，正如我们在其他地方所见，在苏联俄罗斯以及更广泛的马克思主义者中，直到第二次世界大战后，公开支持优生学才被广泛视为受到法西斯主义的玷污，因而变得不那么可接受。但即便如此，这种意识形态仍不断在左翼及其他政治光谱中重新浮现，想象中的乌托邦未来往往基于优生学逻辑，这种逻辑将理想世界构建为强化而非挑战生产力与健康之间等式的世界。



It is not my aim to go into detail about the merits and limitations of Soviet policy or attempts to develop proletarian sciences. That attempt was highly complex and ambitious, and deserves much more careful attention than I can provide here. I only want to stress how just moving beyond currently dominant forms of capitalism, or just decreasing inequality, will not necessarily end the Empire of Normality. We must learn from the mistakes made by past attempts, and remember that since new economic systems grow out of the conditions imposed by older ones, it is likely that any attempt to develop towards post-capitalism will retain at least some elements of the apparatus I have called the Empire of Normality.

我无意深入探讨苏联政策的利弊或发展无产阶级科学的尝试。这一尝试极为复杂且雄心勃勃，值得比我在此所能提供的更为细致的关注。我只想强调，仅仅超越当前主导的资本主义形式，或仅仅减少不平等，未必能终结常态帝国。我们必须从过去尝试所犯的错误中吸取教训，并记住，由于新的经济体系是从旧体系所施加的条件中生长出来的，任何向资本主义后阶段发展的尝试，都很可能至少保留我称之为常态帝国的某些要素。



Indeed, many more recent speculations about the possibility of capitalism developing into a post-capitalist society – for instance through the use and democratisation of information technology – contain little or no consideration of neurodivergent oppression, or of how we might seek to minimise it in such new societal organisations. Without this, we have every reason to believe that these attempts too will retain elements of the apparatus that underpins and necessitates the production, scientific reification, and control of neurodivergence.

确实，许多关于资本主义可能发展成后资本主义社会的近期推测——例如通过信息技术的使用和民主化——很少或根本没有考虑神经殊异压迫，或者我们如何在这样的新社会组织中尽量减少它。没有这一点，我们完全有理由相信，这些尝试也将保留那些支撑并需要神经殊异性生产、科学物化及控制的机制要素。



ESCAPING NORMALITY

逃离常态



The first thing we must do to combat the Empire of Normality is to further develop an analysis of its nature and workings, and to build a critique of these into our imagining of what a post-capitalist society might look like. Our future theory and praxis must work towards this end, if we do not want neuronormative domination to persist and even worsen. After all, especially given the re-emergence of fascist governments and oligarchies across the world in recent decades, there is every possibility that whatever comes after capitalism could be even worse.

要对抗常态帝国，我们首先必须进一步分析其本质和运作方式，并将对这些的批判融入我们对后资本主义社会可能面貌的构想中。如果我们不希望神经常态统治持续甚至恶化，我们未来的理论和实践就必须朝着这个方向努力。毕竟，特别是考虑到近几十年来法西斯政府和寡头政治在全球范围内的重新抬头，资本主义之后出现的任何社会形态都有可能变得更加糟糕。



As to the possibility of a form of communism, or post-capitalism, that goes beyond the Empire of Normality, it is not yet clear what this might look like. As I have already said, I have not sought here to propose a strategy or set of policies to alleviate the current situation. At the current historical moment, it seems to me, eugenic and capitalist ideologies are still so hegemonic, we are only just beginning to be able to glimpse signposts towards possible ways out. What this will turn out to look like will only be determined through mass consciousness-raising, critique, and collective imagining. This will be a mass theoretical, scientific, political, and revolutionary project of many years or decades.

至于超越常态帝国的一种共产主义或后资本主义形式是否可能，其具体形态尚不明确。正如前文所述，我在此并未试图提出缓解当前困境的策略或政策体系。在当下的历史节点，优生学与资本主义意识形态仍占据着如此霸权地位，我们才刚刚开始窥见可能出路的零星路标。未来的具体形态唯有通过大众意识觉醒、批判实践与集体想象才能共同塑造。这将是一项需要多年乃至数十年持续推进的、集理论探索、科学研究、政治实践与革命行动于一体的大众事业。



But with what I have argued in mind, there are several things we can say, which hint at a variety of possibilities going forward. First, it is important that Marx’s own writings reveal a commitment to an ideal that is directly opposed to neuronormative domination. While some readers have interpreted him as expressing a kind of essentialism about human nature and thriving, a closer reading reveals that his conception of human nature was much more flexible, and not fixed by any clear essence. As Paul Raekstad writes,

但结合我之前的论述，我们可以得出几点看法，这些看法暗示了未来发展的多种可能性。首先，重要的是马克思本人的著作展现了一种与神经规范性支配直接对立的理想。虽然有些读者将他解读为表达了一种关于人性和繁荣的本质主义，但仔细阅读会发现，他关于人性的概念要灵活得多，并不受任何明确本质的束缚。正如保罗·雷克斯塔德所写，





Marx’s conception of human development is inherently open-ended (because it’s not evaluated in terms of any predetermined yardsticks), [and] pluralistic (because it acknowledges that there are many different valuable ways to develop, and no particular vision of full or perfect development is imposed upon anyone).6

马克思关于人类发展的概念本质上是开放式的（因为它不以任何预设的标准来评估），[并且]是多元的（因为它承认存在许多不同的有价值的发展方式，没有将任何关于完全或完美发展的特定愿景强加于人）。 6





It is notable that this is in line with the core insight from neurodiversity theory, which is that human neurological development is, at the species level, always diverse, unfinished, and open-ended. In line with this, Marx’s vision of the highest stage of communism was one where it moves from each according to their abilities to, ultimately each according to their needs. That is, the end goal is one where people are provided for and valued regardless of their individual ability. In this, there is certainly more room – and we must work on this over the coming years – to further develop a theoretical Marxism that has the insights and commitments of the neurodiversity movement built into its core.

值得注意的是，这与神经多样性理论的核心见解是一致的，即人类的神经发育在物种层面上始终是多样、未完成且开放的。与此相一致，马克思对共产主义最高阶段的设想是，从各尽所能最终过渡到各取所需。也就是说，最终目标是无论个人能力如何，人们都能得到供养和重视。在这方面，我们当然有更多空间——并且必须在未来几年致力于此——进一步发展一种将神经多样性运动的见解和承诺融入其核心的理论马克思主义。



Ultimately, we must be militant in our demand to shift towards ways of organising and living that do not value humans by individual productivity, and which do not see us as machines to be upgraded in line with the economic requirements of capital at any given time. While capitalism has brought great increases in medical understanding and technology, these have too often been used more to reify capitalist neuronormativity than to aid human flourishing in all its diversity. A neurodivergent communism would be one where we live and work together, in a shared ecology, without discriminating against individuals for being divergent or unproductive.

最终，我们必须以战斗的姿态要求转向一种组织和生活方式，这种模式不将人的价值等同于个人生产力，也不将我们视为需要根据资本在任何特定时期的经济需求而升级的机器。尽管资本主义极大地推动了医学认知和技术的进步，但这些成果往往更多地被用来固化资本主义的神经常态，而非促进人类在多样性中的繁荣发展。一个神经殊异的共产主义社会，将是我们共同生活、共同工作于一个共享生态中的社会，在那里，个体不会因为与众不同或生产力不足而受到歧视。



To begin working towards this we must work through the contradictions I have identified in capitalism, orienting our theory and praxis to the points where capital’s power ends up undermining its own future prospects. Some of this will regard work. In practice, Neurodivergent Marxism requires moving away from diversity consultants teaching companies how to exploit more neurodivergent workers, and towards neurodivergent workers organising as neurodivergents to radically change the structures and expectations of the workplace. In fact, this has already been happening more in recent years, where, anecdotally, I have been told of many emerging neurodivergent-led groups forming to change their own workplaces. Neurodivergent trade unionists such as Janine Booth have begun working on how to make unions more neurodivergence-inclusive and more directed towards focusing on the needs of neurodivergent people.7 More efforts to build neurodivergent-led cooperatives will also help build new ways and modes of working and relating, less tainted by the focus on profit over working conditions. A mass effort in this direction is important because it will not just increasingly change how work is organised and understood, but make it more open to many of those neurodivergents who are currently in the surplus, thus providing more organising power for more disabled people in the long run.

要开始朝这个方向努力，我们必须处理我在资本主义中发现的矛盾，将我们的理论和实践对准那些资本力量最终会削弱其自身未来前景的节点。其中一些将涉及工作领域。在实践中，神经殊异马克思主义要求我们远离那些教公司如何剥削更多神经殊异工人的多元化顾问，转向神经殊异工人以神经殊异者的身份组织起来，从根本上改变工作场所的结构和期望。事实上，近年来这种情况已经越来越多地发生，据传闻，我听说许多新兴的由神经殊异者领导的团体正在形成，以改变他们自己的工作场所。像贾宁·布斯这样的神经殊异工会成员已经开始研究如何使工会更具神经殊异性包容性，并更专注于关注神经殊异人群的需求。 7 更多努力去建立由神经殊异者领导的合作社，也将有助于构建新的工作和互动方式与模式，减少因过度关注利润而忽视工作条件所带来的负面影响。 朝着这个方向进行大规模努力至关重要，因为它不仅将逐步改变工作的组织方式和理解方式，还会让更多目前处于剩余状态的神经多样性群体获得参与机会，从而长远来看为更多残障人士提供更强的组织力量。



We can also already say that an integrated surplus class must organise as surplus alongside the workers of the world, and workers must orient their theory and praxis to include critique of eugenic ideology and the liberation of the surplus. It is not just that the combined forces of both will likely be necessary for realising the possibility of building a post-capitalist world. It will also be necessary for imagining one that does not just reproduce the Empire of Normality in a different way.

我们还可以断言，一个整合的剩余阶级必须与全世界的工人一起作为剩余力量组织起来，而工人也必须调整其理论和实践，以纳入对优生意识形态的批判和剩余群体的解放。这不仅是因为两者的联合力量对于实现构建后资本主义世界的可能性可能是必要的，而且对于构想一个不再以不同方式复制"常态帝国"的世界也是必要的。



A transitional politics that centres the surplus and, crucially, finds ways to empower the surplus as surplus, will need to take different forms to traditional union organising, which is based on the threat of withholding regular waged labour. This could take various forms. It may be that unions can incorporate more mechanisms to support members of the surplus who are only sporadically employed to withhold labour, as historically, for instance, striking dockworkers in Britain, who were paid by the day, managed. Alternatively, it may be that demand for the implementation of a Universal Basic Income gives those members of surplus who have never worked more economic power – primarily the power to withhold as consumers but also to organise towards direct action – regardless of whether they can withhold labour.

一种以剩余劳动力为核心，并关键性地寻求赋予剩余劳动力以其本质力量的政治过渡策略，需要采取不同于传统工会组织的形式——后者主要基于威胁停止常规有偿劳动。这种策略可以呈现多种形态。或许工会能够纳入更多机制，以支持那些仅偶尔就业的剩余劳动力成员停止工作，正如历史上英国按日计酬的码头工人成功组织罢工那样。又或者，推行全民基本收入的要求，可能赋予那些从未工作过的剩余劳动力成员更多经济权力——主要是作为消费者拒绝消费的权力，同时也为组织直接行动创造条件——无论他们是否能够停止劳动。



Equally, it is worth noting Marxist-Leninist vanguardism, where a party led by workers seeks to raise revolutionary consciousness. An interesting recent event was the short-lived organisation Red Fightback, active in the United Kingdom between 2018 and 2023. While this organisation split due to problems with several members of the leadership, it also did important community work, and it is interesting to consider it as the first Marxist-Leninist political party to have an explicit commitment to ending neurodivergent oppression. Many members of the leadership were also openly neurodivergent and queer. In this, it has at least some overlap with the Black Panthers as it developed in the 1970s, as a Marxist-Leninist party that despite initial problems, later strove to become more intersectional in its efforts. It seems likely that we will see more neurodivergent Marxist-Leninist organisations in the coming years, especially as neuronormativty continues to become increasingly restrictive. This may be key in raising the consciousness of a broader neurodivergent movement that cuts across the working and surplus classes.

同样值得注意的是马克思列宁主义的先锋主义，即由工人领导的政党致力于提升革命觉悟。近期一个有趣的事件是短暂存在的组织“红色反击”，该组织于 2018 年至 2023 年间在英国活跃。尽管这一组织因领导层若干成员的问题而分裂，但它也开展了重要的社区工作，值得关注的是，它被视为首个明确承诺终结神经殊异压迫的马克思列宁主义政党。其领导层中许多成员也公开承认自己是神经殊异者和酷儿。在这方面，它与 20 世纪 70 年代发展起来的黑豹党至少存在某些重叠之处——作为一个马克思列宁主义政党，尽管初期面临问题，但后来努力在其行动中变得更加交叉包容。未来几年，我们很可能会看到更多神经殊异的马克思列宁主义组织出现，尤其是随着神经规范性日益严苛。这对于提升一个跨越工人阶级和剩余阶级的更广泛神经殊异运动的觉悟可能至关重要。



Neurodivergent Marxism also requires building on existing elements within mental health politics. When it comes to the various psych disciplines, we should not think that the abolition of coercion is impossible just because the abolitionist attempts from the 1960s and 1970s largely failed. They failed, as we saw, because there were not usually better alternatives, leading to many former asylum inmates ending up homeless or in prison. Moreover, Szaszianism was designed to work this way, and ultimately it was the broader shift to neoliberalism that allowed Szaszianism to become dominant as a purported counter-narrative to biomedical psychiatry. Yet this does not imply that other forms of abolitionism are not worth pursuing. These, to be successful, will likely need to be based more on the approach of the Basaglians, the Sedgwickians, and the Socialist Patient’s Collective, all of which avoid the Szaszian and bourgeois critical psychiatry shift to disability denial and Hayekian moralism. We should aim to abolish coercion and harm, and the power of the physician class, while steadfastly protecting recognition of disability or illness alongside the need for housing, resources, support, and services. These services must be both radically changed and increased, in ways that centre the needs of those who need them, while mass community building must take place beyond the scope of state support.

神经殊异马克思主义同样需要在心理健康政治现有的基础上继续发展。面对各类精神学科，我们不应因为 1960 至 1970 年代废除强制医疗的尝试大多失败，就认为废除强制医疗是不可能的。正如我们所见，这些尝试之所以失败，通常是因为缺乏更好的替代方案，导致许多前精神病院患者最终无家可归或身陷囹圄。此外，萨斯主义的设计本就如此运作，而最终是新自由主义更广泛的转向，使得萨斯主义得以作为生物医学精神病学的一种所谓反叙事而占据主导地位。然而，这并不意味着其他形式的废除主义不值得追求。要想取得成功，这些尝试很可能需要更多地借鉴巴萨利亚派、塞奇威克派以及社会主义患者集体的方法，它们都避免了萨斯主义及资产阶级批判精神病学向否认残障和哈耶克式道德主义的转向。 我们应当致力于废除强制与伤害，以及医师阶层的权力，同时坚定地维护对残障或疾病的承认，并保障住房、资源、支持与服务的需求。这些服务必须进行彻底变革并大幅增加，其方式应以需求者的需求为核心，而大规模的社区建设则必须在国家支持的范围之外展开。



At the level of scientific research, the continued construction of neurodiversity paradigm science requires new methods for measurement and analysis, the centring of neurodivergent perspectives, the use of social and ecological models of functioning, and a politicised understanding of neurodivergent disablement. This science will need to be led by and for neurodivergents, especially those who are multiply marginalised. This will be vital not just for breaking the grip of the pathology paradigm, but also for constructing new knowledges that will help guide us towards new forms of societal organisation and ways of living.

在科学研究层面，神经多样性范式科学的持续构建需要新的测量与分析方法，以神经殊异者的视角为中心，采用社会与生态功能模型，并对神经殊异者的残障处境进行政治化理解。这门科学必须由神经殊异者主导、为神经殊异者服务，尤其是那些遭受多重边缘化的群体。这不仅对打破病理学范式的桎梏至关重要，也将有助于构建新的知识体系，引导我们走向新的社会组织形式与生活方式。



This also raises the importance of decolonising neurodiversity theory and research. While neurodiversity theory can certainly fit well with anti-racist politics, the perspectives that have been centred so far are of proponents (of a range of ethnicities) in the Global North. It thus reflects the perspectives and concerns of those people. In the past few years, neurodiversity theory has increasingly been adopted and adapted across much of the majority world – from Chile to Kenya – and this seems like it will continue in the coming years, since global capitalism produces similar forms of debility, disability, and illness everywhere. This will change and challenge neurodiversity theory, allowing it to further develop in new directions that are led by and reflect the needs of different people in different local contexts. The attempt to build a neurodiversity paradigm by those of us in the Global North must therefore remain open and flexible enough to be adapted or superseded by those of us in the global south.
