Our neurodivergent praxis must also be internationalist in its orientation, aiming to destroy the eugenic borders that structure and limit movement globally.

这也凸显了神经多样性理论与研究去殖民化的重要性。虽然神经多样性理论无疑能与反种族主义政治紧密结合，但迄今为止占据中心地位的仍是全球北方支持者（涵盖多种族裔）的视角。因此，它反映的是这些人群的观点与关切。过去几年间，神经多样性理论已在多数世界地区——从智利到肯尼亚——日益被采纳和改造，这种趋势在未来数年似乎仍将持续，因为全球资本主义在各地催生了相似的身体失能、残障与疾病形态。这将改变并挑战神经多样性理论，推动其沿着由不同地域人群主导、反映本土需求的新方向进一步发展。因此，我们全球北方构建神经多样性范式的尝试，必须保持足够的开放性与灵活性，以便全球南方的实践者对其进行改造或超越。我们的神经殊异实践同样需要具备国际主义导向，致力于摧毁那些建构并限制全球流动的优生学边界。



A radical politics of neurodivergent conservation is also consistent with a radical politics of environmental conservation. After all, it has been the same logics, the same system, that has ravaged the biodiversity of the planet as has sought to eliminate the neurological diversity of humanity. And neurodivergent liberation is no less intertwined with the liberation of those of us who diverge from gendered and sexual norms, those oppressed by patriarchy, and those with bodily disabilities. For the ideals of normality and supernormality, as we have seen, grew together and are intimately intertwined with not just racial capitalism but also a range of interlocking systems of domination, out of which the Empire of Normality arose. Our Neurodivergent Marxism must work towards building an understanding of all of this, for there is no liberation without collective liberation.

神经殊异保护的激进政治也与环境保护的激进政治相一致。毕竟，正是同样的逻辑、同样的系统，在蹂躏地球生物多样性的同时，也试图消除人类的神经多样性。而神经殊异的解放，与那些偏离性别和性规范的人、那些受父权制压迫的人以及那些有身体残疾的人的解放，同样是密不可分的。因为正如我们所看到的，正常性和超常性的理想是共同成长的，并且不仅与种族资本主义紧密交织，还与一系列相互关联的统治体系密不可分，正是这些体系催生了"正常性帝国"。我们的神经殊异马克思主义必须致力于构建对所有这一切的理解，因为没有集体的解放，就没有解放。



It is vital to say here that some neurodivergent disablement and illness will always exist, and that imagined worlds where they do not exist at all are fascistic fantasies. But mass neurodivergent disablement and constant, widespread anxiety, panic, depression, and mental illness, combined with systemic discrimination of neurodivergent people, is a problem specific to the current historical era. Hegemonic neuronormative domination, in other words, is a key problem of our time. For the Empire of Normality, and in turn the pathology paradigm, emerged in the context of capitalist logics, but have now become pervasive and partially distinct systems of domination in their own rights.

必须在此指出，某些神经殊异性的障碍与疾病将始终存在，而幻想它们完全消失的世界则是法西斯式的空想。然而，大规模的神经殊异性障碍、持续蔓延的焦虑、恐慌、抑郁与精神疾病，加之对神经殊异人群的系统性歧视，乃是当前历史时代特有的问题。换言之，霸权性的神经规范性支配是我们这个时代的关键问题。因为正常性帝国及其衍生的病理范式虽诞生于资本主义逻辑的语境中，如今却已演变为普遍存在且部分独立的支配体系。



I have tried to write a book that helps clarify some of the broader contexts that led to the problems so many of us continually experience. This helps us understand why the neurodiversity movement arose, and what neurodivergent liberation might require. In this, I hope to have contributed some small part to a collective project of consciousness-raising, in such a way that will help us orient our theory and praxis over the coming years. As I have acknowledged, this is of course incomplete, and is just one small step in a greater, collective march towards a new world. But what I hope to have shown, ultimately, is that at this historical moment, the collective building of a mass anti-capitalist politics of neurodiversity will be necessary for not just neurodivergent liberation but also for our broader efforts towards collective liberation.

我试图撰写一本书，以帮助阐明导致我们许多人持续面临问题的更广泛背景。这有助于我们理解神经多样性运动为何兴起，以及神经殊异解放可能需要什么。在此过程中，我希望为集体意识提升项目贡献微薄之力，以帮助我们在未来几年中定位我们的理论与实践。正如我所承认的，这当然是不完整的，只是迈向新世界的更伟大集体征程中的一小步。但最终，我希望展示的是，在这个历史时刻，构建一种群众性的、反资本主义的神经多样性政治，不仅对于神经殊异解放是必要的，也对我们更广泛的集体解放努力至关重要。



Together, then, we must work towards a future world beyond the Empire of Normality. It is true that this is not a future that we can yet properly comprehend. For ideology still hangs everywhere around us, like an all-encompassing fog that impedes our ability to think and see. Yet as our collective consciousness grows, this fog will pass. Our strength too will grow as we organise as neurodivergent workers and members of the surplus class, across borders and sites of struggle globally. Our possibilities will expand as the old world falters and its structures crumble. We will then see a clear path with signposts towards a bright future. It is up to us to get there.

因此，我们必须共同努力，迈向一个超越常态帝国统治的未来世界。诚然，这仍是一个我们无法完全理解的未来。因为意识形态仍如无处不在的迷雾般笼罩着我们，阻碍着我们的思考与视野。然而，随着集体意识的觉醒，这层迷雾终将散去。当我们作为神经殊异的劳动者和过剩阶级的成员，跨越国界、在全球各地的抗争阵地上组织起来时，我们的力量也将随之壮大。随着旧世界的动摇及其结构的崩塌，我们的可能性将不断扩展。届时，我们将看到一条通往光明未来的清晰道路，路标已然树立。抵达彼岸，责任在我们。



---

Empire of Normality

第一章

4.    They also recognised hysteria, although following earlier beliefs, this was seen as stemming not from neurological pathology, but rather from the womb ‘wandering’ around the body and upsetting its general balance. While there was no systemic oppression of disabled people as a whole, here we see an early example of patriarchal oppression through diagnosis, whereby women were prescribed marriage and regular sex as treatment for a wandering womb.

4. 他们也认识到了癔症，不过根据早期的观念，这种病症并非源于神经系统的病理变化，而是由于子宫在体内"游走"，扰乱了身体的整体平衡。虽然当时并没有对残疾人整体进行系统性压迫，但这里我们看到了一个通过诊断实施父权制压迫的早期例证——女性被建议通过结婚和规律性行为来治疗"游走的子宫"。



5.    Simon Raper. ‘The Shock of the Mean’. Significance 14, no. 6 (2017): 12. https://doi.org/10.1111/j.1740-9713.2017.01087.x

12.  Quetelet himself contributed to this shift in his writings on what he called ‘the statistics of the deranged’, and ‘diseases of the mind’. Nonetheless, while he described people with such disabilities as being ‘in a direct ratio with civilisation’, his research only included statistics about these people rather than about the nature of the normal mind as such. He charted, for instance, how many idiots made up the population of a country, the month in which they were most often born, the age of onset of insanity, and so forth. In my view, he did not, therefore, develop the concept of the normal mind, although he certainly paved the way for it.

12. 凯特莱本人在其关于所谓"精神错乱者统计"和"心智疾病"的著作中推动了这一转变。然而，尽管他将这类残障人士描述为"与文明程度呈正比"，他的研究仅包含关于这些人群的统计数据，而非关于正常心智本身的本质。例如，他统计了一个国家中白痴人口的比例、他们最常出生的月份、精神错乱发病的年龄等等。在我看来，他因此并未发展出正常心智的概念，尽管他无疑为此铺平了道路。

9.    To be sure, if underlying biological abnormality is found, Szasz was happy to say that the illness was genuine, and the pathology objective. In these cases, though, he thought that pathologisation was a purely scientific matter and that care of the now verified condition should be passed from psychiatry to neurology. Indeed, he noted, this is exactly what had tended to happen historically, such as when what had previously been known as general paralysis or paresis of the insane was found to be caused by syphilis in the 1890s. Without this, there was no justification for calling something an illness, thus placing those suffering under the power of doctors. At the time he was writing, there was also no known biological basis for any mental disorder – meaning that his argument posed a powerful challenge to the very core of psychiatry.

9. 诚然，如果发现了潜在的生物异常，萨兹乐于承认这种疾病是真实的，其病理是客观的。但在这些情况下，他认为病理化是一个纯粹的科学问题，对现已确诊的病症的护理应从精神病学转交给神经病学。事实上他指出，历史上恰恰倾向于发生这种情况，例如在 19 世纪 90 年代，当先前被称为全身性麻痹或精神错乱性麻痹的病症被发现是由梅毒引起时。如果没有这种生物基础，就没有理由称某物为疾病，从而将患者置于医生的权力之下。在他写作的时代，任何精神障碍也都没有已知的生物学基础——这意味着他的论点对精神病学的核心构成了强有力的挑战。

Empire of Normality



Acknowledgements

致谢



Given various contingent historical occurrences and bourgeois ideology, books tend to be attributed to single authors. In reality they are always the product of collective effort. This book has gone through many transformations, and along the way has been shaped, guided, and improved by a great many people.

由于各种偶然的历史事件和资产阶级意识形态，书籍往往被归功于单一作者。实际上，它们始终是集体努力的产物。本书经历了多次修改，在此过程中，众多人士对其进行了塑造、指导和改进。



Various parts of the book have, at different points, been significantly strengthened following feedback from Hane Maung, Coreen McGuire, David Batho, Koshka Duff, Shelley Tremain, Havi Carel, Jaakko Nevasto, Shona Murphy, Chris Bailey, Tuomas Pernu, Tom Whyman, John Ray, Alice McAndrew, Anton Jäger, Judy Singer, Isaac Kneebone Hopkins, and Nick Walker. At relatively late stages, extensive and invaluable feedback on the whole draft was provided by Joshua Habgood-Coote, Beatrice Adler-Bolton, David Shulman, and Hel Spandler.

本书的各个部分在不同阶段，根据 Hane Maung、Coreen McGuire、David Batho、Koshka Duff、Shelley Tremain、Havi Carel、Jaakko Nevasto、Shona Murphy、Chris Bailey、Tuomas Pernu、Tom Whyman、John Ray、Alice McAndrew、Anton Jäger、Judy Singer、Isaac Kneebone Hopkins 和 Nick Walker 的反馈，得到了显著加强。在相对较晚的阶段，Joshua Habgood-Coote、Beatrice Adler-Bolton、David Shulman 和 Hel Spandler 对整个草稿提供了广泛且宝贵的反馈意见。



I have also gained much from informal interactions with everyone already noted, but also countless others. These include Micha Frazer-Caroll, Abs Stannard Ashleigh, Monique Botha-Kite, Justin Garson, Nipper Mad Dog, Nev Jones, Virginia Bovell, Dan Degerman, David Mordecai, Alastair Morgan, Vincenzo Passantre Spaccapietra, RoseAnnieFlo, Guilaine Kinouani, Béatrice Han-Pile, Damian Milton, Sonia Soans, Steven Kapp, Jay Watts, Fergus Murray, Sonny Hallet, Abdo Abuhassan, and far too many others to mention. They will each surely disagree with me on much, but their insights permeate throughout.

除了与已提及的各位，我还从与无数其他人的非正式交流中获益良多。其中包括米卡·弗雷泽-卡罗尔、阿布斯·斯坦纳德·阿什利、莫妮克·博塔-凯特、贾斯汀·加森、尼珀·疯狗、内夫·琼斯、弗吉尼亚·博维尔、丹·德格曼、大卫·莫迪凯、阿拉斯泰尔·摩根、文森佐·帕桑特·斯帕卡皮特拉、罗斯安妮弗洛、吉莱恩·基努阿尼、贝亚特丽斯·汉-皮尔、达米安·米尔顿、索尼娅·索恩斯、史蒂文·卡普、杰伊·瓦茨、弗格斯·默里、桑尼·哈利特、阿卜杜·阿布哈桑，以及太多无法一一列举的人。他们每个人肯定在许多方面与我意见相左，但他们的见解贯穿始终。



Over the past year, I wrote much of the book while stuck in bed with Long Covid. During this time, while his editorial suggestions have been rejected, my cat Marcel has been a constant and steadfastcompanion. Special thanks also go to my editor, David Shulman, who has provided unwavering support and guidance from the moment we first spoke.

过去一年里，我因长期新冠卧床不起，在此期间完成了本书的大部分写作。这段时间里，尽管他的编辑建议被拒绝了，但我的猫马塞尔一直是我坚定而忠实的伙伴。特别感谢我的编辑大卫·舒尔曼，从我们第一次交谈起，他就给予了我不懈的支持和指导。



Finally, I would never have been able to have written this book without Alice, Jenny, Adrian, Harriet, Daniel, and Dan. I cannot thank them enough for everything they have done and continue to do.

最后，如果没有爱丽丝、珍妮、阿德里安、哈丽特、丹尼尔和丹，我绝不可能完成这本书。对于他们所做的一切以及持续的支持，我感激不尽。



---

Empire of Normality



Empire of Normality

正常帝国



‘This groundbreaking book fills a crucial gap in the discourse about neurodiversity, providing a deep history of the invention of the “normal” mind as one of the most damaging and oppressive tools of capitalism, while not succumbing to the myths of the “anti-psychiatry” movement. To read it is to see the world more clearly.’

“这本开创性的著作填补了神经多样性讨论中的一个关键空白，它深刻揭示了‘正常’心智的构建史——这一资本主义最具破坏性与压迫性的工具之一，同时并未陷入‘反精神病学’运动的神话之中。阅读此书，将使你看清世界的本质。”



—Steve Silberman, author of NeuroTribes:

——史蒂夫·西尔伯曼，《神经部落》作者：

The Legacy of Autism and the Future of Neurodiversity

《孤独症的遗产与神经多样性的未来》



‘Empire of Normality argues that a radical politics of neurodiversity needs to be central to the struggle against capitalism. Chapman explains why this is necessary, not only for neurodivergent folk, but for our collective liberation. Thought provoking, challenging and compelling.’

“《正常帝国》主张，激进的神经多样性政治必须成为对抗资本主义斗争的核心。查普曼阐释了为何这不仅是神经殊异群体的必需，更是我们集体解放的必经之路。发人深省、充满挑战且极具说服力。”



—Professor Hel Spandler, Editor, Asylum:

——海伦·斯潘德勒教授，《庇护》杂志主编：

The Radical Mental Health Magazine

《激进心理健康杂志》



‘Engaging, impeccably researched, and a vital step in the emergence of a new social paradigm. Chapman uncovers the origins of the stifling norms that limit our collective potentials, and points the way toward a better and more creative future.’

“引人入胜、研究严谨，是新兴社会范式发展中的关键一步。查普曼揭示了那些束缚我们集体潜能的压抑规范的根源，并指明了通往更美好、更具创造力未来的道路。”



—Nick Walker, author of Neuroqueer Heresies

——尼克·沃克，《神经酷儿异端》作者



‘A vital book that kindles the flames of a Marxist neurodivergent revolution. Chapman boldly challenges us to envision a world liberated from neuronormative oppression, where dismantling capitalism is central to disabled, Mad, and neurodivergent liberation – a new radical approach to neurodiversity that is explicitly anti-capitalist.’

一本至关重要的著作，点燃了马克思主义神经殊异革命的火焰。查普曼大胆地挑战我们，去构想一个摆脱神经规范性压迫的世界，在那里，瓦解资本主义是残障者、疯人及神经殊异者解放的核心——这是一种全新的、明确反资本主义的神经多样性激进路径。



—Beatrice Adler-Bolton, co-author of Health Communism

——比阿特丽斯·阿德勒-博尔顿，《健康共产主义》合著者



and co-host, Death Panel podcast

及《死亡陪审团》播客联合主持人



‘An instant seminal text, Empire of Normality takes on the huge task of crafting a coherent, radical, Marxist approach to neurodivergence. Chapman impressively and critically assembles disparate philosophical, scientific and activist currents across time to carve out a new politics that pushes beyond liberal rights-based approaches, and guides us towards a liberated future.’

一部立时成为开创性文本的著作，《常态帝国》承担起一项艰巨任务：构建一种连贯、激进、马克思主义的神经殊异性研究路径。查普曼令人印象深刻且批判性地汇集了跨越时空的、各不相同的哲学、科学和行动主义思潮，开创出一种超越自由主义权利本位路径的新政治，并指引我们走向一个解放的未来。



—Micha Frazer-Carroll, author of Mad World

——米莎·弗雷泽-卡罗尔，《疯狂世界》作者



---

Empire of Normality



Preface

前言



In this book I use neurodiversity theory as a lens for reinterpreting the past to better navigate the present. History, after all, is useful not just for allowing us to understand what has already been. It equally gives us tools to spot patterns, traps, and possibilities in the here and now. In some cases, this can help us imagine new worlds. Perhaps more rarely, it can help us see how to bring these worlds into being. In line with such possibilities, my project here looks backwards while striving forwards. It uses history to develop an understanding that may help us collectively work towards neurodivergent liberation.

本书中，我以神经多样性理论为镜鉴，重新解读历史以更好地把握当下。历史的价值不仅在于帮助我们理解过往，更在于赋予我们洞察当下模式、陷阱与可能性的工具。在某些情况下，这能帮助我们构想新世界；或许更难得的是，它能指引我们如何将这些新世界变为现实。基于这样的可能性，我的研究既回望过去，也奋力向前。通过历史梳理形成认知框架，以期助力我们共同迈向神经殊异解放之路。



While this is a scholarly work, it is also personal and political. My thinking, inevitably, has been moulded by my experience of being neurodivergent as well as of mental illness, not to mention the stigma and discrimination that accompany these. Equally, my views and commitments have been profoundly shaped by the experience of growing up in poverty, sometimes homeless, and then in foster care in the United Kingdom. And no less important has been living through constant crises of capitalism and the mental health effects of precarious employment and insecure housing through much of my adult life. Through this and so much more, I have come to see neurodivergent oppression as bound up with the malaises of advanced capitalism as well as with the other systems of domination that capital developed alongside and remains intertwined with.

尽管这是一部学术著作，它同时也是个人化的、政治化的。我的思考不可避免地受到我作为神经殊异者以及患有精神疾病的经历所塑造，更不用说随之而来的污名与歧视。同样地，我的观点和信念也深受我在英国成长于贫困之中、有时无家可归、随后进入寄养系统的经历所深刻影响。同样重要的是，在我成年后的大部分时间里，我经历了资本主义的持续危机，以及不稳定就业和缺乏保障的住房对心理健康造成的影响。通过这些以及更多的经历，我开始认识到神经殊异的压迫与晚期资本主义的弊病紧密相连，也与资本发展过程中相伴而生、至今仍相互交织的其他统治体系密不可分。



My perspective is also limited by my positionality. I am a white person born in Britain. Here I have focused most centrally on the European and North American contexts, these being the contexts I am best qualified to comment on. To an extent this is fitting as both the systems and ideas the neurodiversity movement arose to fight against, and the movement itself, are largely products of the Global North. Yet the forms of domination the movement arose to resist have had far-reaching consequences, including across much of the Global South. As I make clear throughout, the idea of the ‘normal’ person, brain, and mind has been intimately intertwined with colonialism, imperialism, and white supremacy. While I seek to make such connections salient, my analysis will still likely be of more direct relevance to those living in post-Fordist, high-tech economies. The extent to which it will be relevant to other contexts will depend on countless factors. My hope is that my argument will at least serve as a basis for building or contrasting different analyses that draw on different knowledges and for different contexts.

我的视角也受到自身立场的局限。我是一名出生于英国的白人。在此，我主要聚焦于欧洲和北美语境，这些是我最有资格评论的语境。在某种程度上，这是恰当的，因为神经多样性运动兴起所要对抗的体系与观念，以及这场运动本身，很大程度上都是全球北方的产物。然而，该运动兴起所要抵制的统治形式已产生了深远影响，波及全球南方的大部分地区。正如我在全书中所阐明的，“正常”的人、大脑和心智这一观念，与殖民主义、帝国主义和白人至上主义紧密交织在一起。尽管我试图凸显这些关联，但我的分析可能仍与生活在后福特主义高科技经济体中的人们更为直接相关。至于它在其他语境中的相关性程度，将取决于无数因素。我希望我的论述至少能作为一个基础，用以构建或对比那些汲取不同知识、适用于不同语境的分析。



Caveats aside, my aim here is to develop a more radical analysis of neurodiversity history, theory, and politics, built from a broadly Marxian perspective. This begins with a materialist interpretation of the history of neurodivergent disablement and our understanding of normality and disability. I seek to place them within the broader context of a range of interlocking systems of domination, most centrally capitalism. In turn, while I locate the origins of the problem much earlier, I suggest that especially since the mid-twentieth century, capitalism has reached a stage where neurological domination, through either disablement or alienation, has become pervasive regardless of how close or far each of us sits to the neurotypical ideal. In an important sense, what I want to show is that capitalism’s domination shifts more towards the neuronormative the further capitalism itself intensifies. Here we see a dialectical tension between the expansion of the domain of capital alongside a simultaneous restriction of neuronormativity that accompanies it.

撇开这些告诫不谈，我的目标是从广义的马克思主义视角出发，对神经多样性的历史、理论和政治进行更为激进的分析。这始于对神经殊异残障历史的唯物主义解读，以及我们对正常与残障的理解。我试图将它们置于一系列相互交织的支配体系——最核心的是资本主义——的更广泛背景中。相应地，虽然我将问题的起源追溯得更早，但我认为，特别是自二十世纪中叶以来，资本主义已进入这样一个阶段：无论我们每个人距离神经典型理想是近是远，通过残障或异化实现的神经支配已变得无处不在。从某种意义上说，我想表明的是，资本主义本身越是强化，其支配就越倾向于神经规范性。在此我们看到一种辩证的张力：资本领域的扩张与随之而来的神经规范性的同时收紧并存。



In covering this, I hope partly to show that things are as they are not due to natural necessity, but specific historical and economic conditions. By the same token, I show that things do not have to be as they are, and that by placing neurodiversity theory and praxis within broader anti-capitalist struggles, we might help make them otherwise. This is not an attempt to offer a fully developed political strategy, since I think that is something to be done collectively, and which we are only now beginning to be ready for. Rather, it is an attempt to help develop a historical neurodivergent consciousness in such a way that will make collective efforts to develop strategy more possible. The first aim of this book is thus to uncover a past that has been rendered opaque. And the second aim is to help open up a future that we cannot yet fully understand, yet which is important to try to reach for, nonetheless.

在探讨这一点的过程中，我希望部分地揭示事物之所以如此，并非出于自然的必然性，而是特定的历史与经济条件使然。同样地，我也试图说明事物并非必须保持现状，通过将神经多样性理论与实践融入更广泛的反资本主义斗争中，我们或许能推动其改变。这并非试图提供一个完全成熟的政治策略，因为我认为这需要集体努力，而我们现在才刚刚开始为此做好准备。相反，这是为了帮助发展一种历史的神经殊异意识，从而使集体制定策略的努力更具可能性。因此，本书的首要目标是揭示一个已被掩盖的过去。其次，则是帮助开启一个我们尚无法完全理解、却值得奋力追寻的未来。



---

Empire of Normality



Introduction

引言



My life has been structured by both neurodivergence and economic hardship since the beginning. This dates to my first memories, which take place during the early 1990s in London. One characteristic impression from the council flat in which we lived is of an alcoholic father furiously ranting and raging. Another is of a distraught mother, tearfully saying goodbye as she left for some unspecified period. While there were also happier memories, home life was hard. And since we never had any money and were not part of any broader community, there seemed no realistic hope of things improving.

我的生活从一开始就被神经殊异性和经济困境所塑造。这可以追溯到我最早的记忆，发生在 20 世纪 90 年代初的伦敦。我对我们居住的政府公屋公寓的一个典型印象是：酗酒的父亲愤怒地咆哮和发怒。另一个印象是心烦意乱的母亲，在她离开一段不确定的时间时，含泪道别。虽然也有更快乐的回忆，但家庭生活是艰难的。而且，由于我们从未有过任何钱，也不属于任何更广泛的社区，似乎没有现实希望情况会好转。



My impressions from school are little better. Those from the playground are mainly of bullies pointing and laughing. It was not just that I was poor and wore uncool, second-hand clothes. It was also that I was weird, quiet, and hadn’t yet developed the social fluency required to evade their efforts. I also experienced constant sensory processing problems that hindered my learning. My memories of lessons are mainly of trying to strive through sensory bombardment just to hear the teacher’s voice. Despite these efforts, I still often struggled to grasp even basic things. I was soon taken by my teachers to simply be lazy and unintelligent. In time they stopped trying to help, and I began to internalise their negative images of me.

我对学校的印象也好不到哪里去。操场上的记忆，主要是霸凌者指指点点和嘲笑。不仅仅是因为我穷，穿着不酷的二手衣服。还因为我古怪、安静，还没有发展出躲避他们欺凌所需的社交能力。我还经历了持续的感觉处理问题，这阻碍了我的学习。我对课堂的记忆，主要是努力在感官轰炸中挣扎，只为听到老师的声音。尽管付出了这些努力，我仍然常常连基本的东西都难以掌握。很快，老师们就认为我只是懒惰和不聪明。随着时间的推移，他们不再试图帮助我，我开始内化他们对我的负面看法。



Much later, I learned clinical names for these problems, and moreover, that I was far from alone in encountering them. The addiction and depression I had seen in family members, for instance, were relatively common mental health problems. I also found out that my sensory processing and social understanding issues were associated with autism, a diagnosis that had increased nationwide by 787% between 1998 and 2018.1 I likewise discovered that my early traumatic experiences led to what is often called complex Post Traumatic Stress. More generally, I learned, related experiences of anxiety2 and depression3 had risen in recent decades. And the risks of such problems were much higher for members of economically deprived and marginalised groups.4 Knowing all this would later help me begin to see that my problems were not merely individual. Rather, I was suffering from wider, more systemic problems that were affecting many of us in similar ways.

很久以后，我了解到这些问题的临床名称，并且发现远不止我一个人遇到这些问题。例如，我在家人身上看到的成瘾和抑郁是相对常见的心理健康问题。我还发现，我的感官处理和社会理解问题与孤独谱系有关，这一诊断在全国范围内从 1998 年到 2018 年增加了 787%。 1 同样，我发现我早期的创伤经历导致了通常被称为复杂性创伤后应激障碍的状况。更普遍地说，我了解到，相关的焦虑 2 和抑郁 3 体验在近几十年来有所上升。而对于经济贫困和边缘化群体的成员来说，出现此类问题的风险要高得多。 4 了解这一切后来帮助我开始明白，我的问题不仅仅是个人的。相反，我正遭受着更广泛、更系统性的问题的困扰，这些问题正以类似的方式影响着我们中的许多人。



Yet while all this helped my understanding in retrospect, as a child and teenager, I knew none of this. I did know I was different from those considered ‘normal’. But I felt too much shame to explore what this difference might consist in, or whether it was necessarily a bad thing. At the time, the disposition of my experience was largely one of confusion, anxiety, and hopelessness. In the end, stuck in poverty, alienated from both myself and the world around me, my mental health went from bad to worse. Beyond constant anxiety and hopelessness, I developed an eating disorder, experienced intrusive thoughts, and, finally, began thinking about suicide. Life was overwhelmingly bad and there seemed no other way to escape.

然而，尽管这一切在事后帮助我理解了当时的情况，但作为一个孩子和青少年，我对这些一无所知。我只知道自己与那些被认为是“正常”的人不同。但我感到太过羞耻，不敢去探究这种差异可能意味着什么，或者它是否必然是一件坏事。那时，我的体验状态主要是困惑、焦虑和绝望。最终，深陷贫困，与自我和周围世界疏离，我的心理健康状况每况愈下。除了持续的焦虑和绝望，我还患上了饮食失调，经历了侵入性思维，最后，开始考虑自杀。生活糟糕透顶，似乎没有其他逃脱的方式。



As so often happens, things only began to change for the better after hitting rock bottom. This occurred, for me, in 2005, by which time I was 15. By then, I had dropped out of school and had been sleeping on the streets for some time. I had turned my back on a world that had failed me, and was initially determined to make my own way, mainly by selling cannabis for a local dealer. Yet homelessness was hard, dangerous, and lonely. And when it finally got cold enough to snow, I knew I couldn’t survive. With nowhere else to go, and finally feeling defeated, I turned up at the local government council offices one cold winter morning. There, I explained my situation and asked if they could help. After an emergency meeting with a team of social workers, they decided I needed to enter the foster care system without delay. They soon found me a family to stay with in a tiny rural village miles away from anywhere I had ever been.

正如常有的情况，事情总是在跌入谷底后才开始好转。对我而言，这个转折点发生在 2005 年，那时我 15 岁。当时我已辍学，在街头露宿了一段时间。我背弃了这个辜负我的世界，起初决心自力更生，主要靠为当地毒贩贩卖大麻维生。然而，无家可归的生活艰难、危险且孤独。当天气冷到开始下雪时，我知道自己无法撑下去了。走投无路、最终感到挫败的我，在一个寒冷的冬日早晨来到了当地政府办公室。在那里，我说明了自己的处境，询问他们能否提供帮助。经过与社会工作者团队的紧急会议，他们决定我必须立即进入寄养系统。很快，他们为我找到了一个家庭，让我住进一个偏远的小村庄，那里离我熟悉的一切都遥不可及。



It was here that things began to change. First, I was dropped off at a beautiful old country house that seemed like it came straight out of a fairy-tale. In turn, I was warmly welcomed in by a new family, a white cat, and a black dog. It was in this context that I first came to experience uncomplicated encouragement, love, and support. Although this transition was far from easy, and while my disabilities and trauma remained an ongoing problem, I soon became part of the family.

正是在这里，一切开始发生转变。首先，我被送到一座宛如童话故事中走出的美丽古老乡间别墅。接着，我受到了一个新家庭、一只白猫和一只黑狗的热烈欢迎。正是在这样的环境中，我第一次体验到毫无保留的鼓励、关爱与支持。尽管这个转变过程远非易事，我的残疾和心理创伤也仍是持续存在的问题，但很快我便融入了这个家庭。



From this point on, old possibilities closed off as new paths began to open. Having no schoolwork and little else to do in the village, I began to read voraciously. I also began to think about options for the future. This included, for the first time, the thought of university, which, to my surprise, seemed to be considered normal in middle-class families. After trying various subjects over the next few years, and since I found the world so chaotic and confusing, I was drawn towards the study of philosophy. My hope was that analysing concepts and social theory would help me understand and navigate the strange and chaotic world I lived in. I wanted to make sense of life and all the problems I had encountered, so I could learn to live a better life than my parents.

从那时起，旧的可能性逐渐关闭，新的道路开始显现。在村里没有学业负担，也无事可做，我开始如饥似渴地阅读。同时，我也开始思考未来的选择。这其中包括了上大学的念头——这是我第一次认真考虑这个选项，令我惊讶的是，这在许多中产家庭看来似乎是理所当然的事。在接下来的几年里尝试了各种学科后，由于我发现这个世界如此混乱而令人困惑，我被哲学研究深深吸引。我希望通过分析概念和社会理论，能够帮助我理解和驾驭这个陌生而混乱的世界。我想要理解生活以及我所遇到的所有问题，从而学会过上比我父母更好的生活。



In the end, however, it took seven more years to find what I was looking for. By this time, I had received a long-awaited autism diagnosis and was studying philosophy while working factory nightshifts. Thankfully, much of what I had learned by this time really did help me make sense of some of my experiences. Most notably, as I will return to, Karl Marx and the later tradition of critical theory helped me understand economic domination both within the British class system and under capitalism more generally. I had also read much on the theory, science, and politics of mental health to try to understand my various distressing experiences. Yet while some of this was helpful to an extent, nothing I had come across fit neatly with the complex and messy forms of disablement that had structured my life since the beginning.

然而，最终我又花了七年时间才找到我所追寻的答案。那时，我已获得期待已久的孤独谱系诊断，一边在工厂上夜班，一边攻读哲学。值得庆幸的是，当时学到的许多知识确实帮助我理解了自己的一些经历。最值得一提的是——我稍后会再谈到——卡尔·马克思及其后的批判理论传统，帮助我理解了英国阶级体系内以及更广义资本主义下的经济支配现象。我还阅读了大量关于心理健康理论、科学及政治的著作，试图理解自己种种痛苦的经历。虽然其中部分内容在某种程度上有所帮助，但没有任何理论能完全契合那种自生命之初就构筑我生活的、复杂而混乱的残障形态。



On the one hand, while I had found my autism diagnosis helpful, much about it was also distressing. The dominant medicalised narrative suggested that being autistic made me somehow tragic, broken, and in need of fixing. This narrative reinforced the constant messages I had received since school, indicating that there was something inherently wrong with me. Alternatively, popular critics of psychiatric diagnosis, from the anti-psychiatry tradition, suggested things like autism and depression were merely illusory ‘labels’ rather than real medical conditions. For them, people like me were not really disabled, but just experiencing normal day-to-day problems. These two binary options seemed to offer either disability shame or disability denial, neither of which was helpful. This was why I found discovering the neurodiversity movement, which offered a different analysis, so liberating. It was this that set me on the path to writing this book.

一方面，虽然我觉得自己的孤独谱系诊断有所帮助，但其中许多内容也令人痛苦。主流的医学化叙事暗示，身为孤独谱系人士让我在某种程度上是悲惨的、残缺的，需要被"修复"。这种叙事强化了我自上学以来就不断收到的信息，即我本身存在某种问题。另一方面，来自反精神病学传统的、对精神科诊断的流行批评者则认为，像孤独谱系和抑郁症这类事物仅仅是虚幻的"标签"，而非真正的医学状况。对他们而言，像我这样的人并非真正残障，只是经历着正常的日常问题。这两种二元对立的选择似乎只提供了要么是残障羞耻，要么是残障否认，两者都无济于事。这就是为什么我发现神经多样性运动——它提供了一种不同的分析——是如此令人解放。正是这一点让我走上了撰写本书的道路。



DISCOVERING NEURODIVERSITY

发现神经多样性



The neurodiversity movement began to emerge in autistic activist groups during the 1990s, back when I was still a child struggling to process in school. At that time, autism was widely seen as an individual medical tragedy, incompatible with living a good human life. The only hope for autistic people and our families, it was thought, was that we would one day be fixed through behavioural conditioning or biomedical intervention.

神经多样性运动于 20 世纪 90 年代在孤独谱系活动家群体中开始兴起，那时我还是个在学校里苦苦挣扎的孩子。当时，孤独症被普遍视为一种个人的医学悲剧，与过上美好的人类生活不相容。人们认为，孤独谱系群体和我们家庭的唯一希望，是有朝一日能通过行为训练或生物医学干预得到"修复"。



Yet by around 1993, the wider availability of personal computers and the internet meant that autistic people were able to begin connecting online for the first time. This meeting of autistic minds brought an intense period of consciousness-raising that would challenge the dominant understanding of autism. For once they were together, these pioneering autistic activists began to realise they all experienced similar problems, including the kinds I have just noted in my own life. In turn, they began to argue that perhaps the problems they all experienced had less to do with their brains being broken, and more to do with societal failure to accommodate their neurological differences. They thus started to argue for what one 1997 report from the New York Times described as a form of ‘neurological pluralism’. This emphasised the need for the behaviours and processing styles of atypical people to be accepted and supported rather than framed as medical pathologies to be controlled, treated, and cured.

然而到了 1993 年左右，个人电脑和互联网的普及使得孤独谱系群体首次能够在线上建立联系。这场孤独谱系思想者的相遇引发了一场深刻的思想觉醒浪潮，对当时主流的孤独症认知提出了挑战。当这些开创性的孤独谱系活动家们聚集在一起时，他们开始意识到彼此都经历着相似的困境——包括我此前描述的个人遭遇。由此，他们逐渐提出一种观点：这些共同面临的难题或许并非源于大脑"故障"，而更多是由于社会未能接纳他们的神经多样性。他们开始倡导一种被《纽约时报》1997 年报道称为"神经多元主义"的理念，强调社会应当接纳并支持非典型人群的行为模式与认知方式，而非将其视为需要控制、治疗乃至根治的医学病症。



Out of this came the idea of neurodiversity, first documented by a sociology student called Judy Singer. The basic point was that we should reject the very idea of a ‘normal’ brain and of the ‘neurotypical’ as an ideal. Instead, it implied viewing mental functioning more in the way we view biodiversity. In this view, it takes all kinds of minds for society to function, and thus normality should not be assumed to be superior to divergence. Rather, there were many kinds of minds. Each was enabled or disabled in different environments, and no single one was naturally superior to all the others. The kind of sensory problems I myself had experienced, for instance, could be seen as caused by the neurotypical-biased design of schools, the workplace, and public spaces. More broadly, in this view, much autistic suffering – such as the bullying I had encountered at school – could be understood largely in the context of societal marginalisation and discrimination.

由此诞生了神经多样性的理念，这一概念最初由社会学学生朱迪·辛格记录。其核心观点在于，我们应当摒弃“正常”大脑以及将“神经典型”视为理想标准的观念。相反，它暗示我们应以看待生物多样性的方式来看待心理功能。在这种视角下，社会的运转需要各种不同的心智，因此不应假定正常状态优于差异状态。实际上，心智的种类繁多。每种心智在不同环境中都可能被赋能或受限，没有任何一种天生优于其他所有类型。例如，我自己曾经历的那种感官问题，可以被视为由学校、工作场所和公共空间偏向神经典型的设计所导致。更广泛地说，在这种观点下，许多孤独谱系人士的痛苦——比如我在学校遭遇的欺凌——在很大程度上可以被理解为社会边缘化和歧视的产物。



To remedy this, Singer and other activists thus called for a new ‘politics of neurological diversity’. For them, this would consist in a new movement that would be modelled on the earlier civil rights movements that had sought to end racial, gendered, and sexual segregation and oppression within and across borders. This new neurodiversity movement would, they hoped, supplement existing struggles by fighting for the rights of the neurologically weird and disabled. The hope was to end neurodivergent oppression everywhere by redesigning the world in ways that would cultivate neurodivergent thriving.

为此，辛格和其他活动家呼吁建立一种新的“神经多样性政治”。对他们而言，这将是一场以早期民权运动为蓝本的新运动，旨在终结跨越国界的种族、性别和性取向隔离与压迫。他们希望，这场新的神经多样性运动能够通过为神经上与众不同和残障人士的权利而斗争，补充现有的抗争。其愿景是通过重新设计世界，培育神经殊异者的繁荣发展，从而终结无处不在的神经殊异压迫。



This call for a politics of neurodiversity had a great impact, and many new advocates rallied to the cause. Yet while these early efforts had focused on autism, the framework and vocabularies that emerged from autistic spaces were quickly adopted by a great many others. First, this was among those with other developmental disabilities such as Attention Deficit Hyperactivity Disorder (ADHD) or dyspraxia. In turn, the neurodiversity framing began to be adopted by those with other diagnoses such as bipolar disorder and borderline personality disorder, not to mention those with no official diagnosis at all.

这一呼吁神经多样性政治的行动产生了巨大影响，许多新的倡导者纷纷投身于此项事业。然而，尽管早期的努力主要聚焦于孤独谱系，但从孤独谱系社群中诞生的框架与语汇，很快就被众多其他群体所采纳。首先，这包括了那些患有其他发展性障碍的人群，例如注意缺陷多动障碍（ADHD）或发育性协调障碍。随后，神经多样性的框架开始被其他诊断群体所采用，比如双相情感障碍和边缘型人格障碍，更不用说那些根本没有正式诊断的人群了。



The breadth of this expansion is captured in Kassiane Asasumasu’s coining of ‘neurodivergent’ in the early 2000s. For her, this refers to any kind of neurological functioning that is considered ‘divergent from typical’,5 whether mere differences are disabled by an unaccommodated society or medical conditions such as epilepsy. Asasumasu wrote that the concept was ‘specifically a tool of inclusion’, available for any neurologically atypical person who found it useful. While this expansion raised questions about the scope and limits of the neurodiversity framework, it was important as it helped more people gather under the neurodiversity banner. At the same time, as Steve Graby6 has observed, while the anti-psychiatry proponents had emphasised that they were unlike people with bodily disabilities – and that psychiatrised people were not really disabled – the neurodiversity perspective embraced the disabled identity. Emphasising the similarities between mental and bodily disablement allowed a broader, more inclusive politics, with neurodiversity proponents straddling the divide between people with medicalised bodies and those with medicalised minds.

这种扩展的广度体现在卡西安·阿萨苏玛苏在 21 世纪初创造的“神经殊异”一词中。对她而言，这指的是任何被认为“偏离典型”的神经功能， 5 无论这种差异是被缺乏包容的社会所残障化，还是诸如癫痫之类的医学状况。阿萨苏玛苏写道，这个概念“特别是一种包容的工具”，可供任何觉得它有用的神经非典型人士使用。虽然这种扩展引发了关于神经多样性框架范围和界限的疑问，但它很重要，因为它帮助了更多人聚集在神经多样性的旗帜下。与此同时，正如史蒂夫·格拉比 6 所观察到的，尽管反精神病学倡导者曾强调他们与身体残障者不同——并且被精神病化的人并非真正残障——但神经多样性的视角却拥抱了残障身份。强调精神与身体残障之间的相似性，促成了更广泛、更具包容性的政治，神经多样性的倡导者跨越了医学化身体与医学化心灵之间的鸿沟。



As the movement grew, the theory of neurodiversity was further developed to fit. Most notably, for me, by 2011, a young autistic scholar called Nick Walker proposed that neurodivergent liberation required not just rights. It also required a mass scientific and cultural paradigm shift. This shift would be away from the dominant ‘pathology paradigm’, which for Walker was defined by highly restricted standards of mental normality and by the default pathologisation and stigmatisation of divergence. Walker drew attention to this as she took it to underpin psychiatric and psychological research and practice, as well as more general societal responses to neurodivergence.

随着运动的发展，神经多样性理论也得到进一步拓展以适应需求。对我而言，最值得注意的是，到 2011 年，一位名叫尼克·沃克的年轻孤独谱系学者提出：神经殊异群体的解放不仅需要权利保障，更需要一场大规模的科学与文化范式转变。这种转变旨在摆脱主流的"病理学范式"——沃克将其定义为对心理正常性设定高度受限的标准，并默认对差异进行病理化与污名化。沃克指出，这种范式不仅支撑着精神病学与心理学的研究实践，更影响着社会对神经殊异性的普遍反应。



In its place, she argued, neurodiversity proponents must build a ‘neurodiversity paradigm’, which would embrace and support a much broader range of cognitive and emotional variation. This prospect offered not just hope to countless neurodivergent people, but also an ideal to collectively work towards. And this was an ideal that, as a philosopher, I would soon dedicate my own efforts towards, since I knew that shifting the paradigm would require more fundamental theoretical work alongside shifting scientific, clinical, and cultural practices.

她主张，神经多样性的倡导者必须构建一个"神经多样性范式"，以接纳并支持更广泛的认知与情感差异。这一愿景不仅为无数神经殊异者带来了希望，也提供了一个值得共同奋斗的理想。作为一名哲学家，我很快便将致力于这一理想，因为我深知，要转变范式，除了改变科学、临床和文化实践外，还需要更根本的理论工作。



My own first exposure to this perspective was in 2012, one year after Walker’s seminal publication. For me, reading Singer, Walker, and other proponents offered a different path to both the pathology paradigm framing and to the anti-psychiatry denialists. What it did was allow me to fully recognise the reality of my disabilities, yet in a way that helped me develop an awareness of the political nature of the kinds of hardship that had structured my whole existence. Through the neurodiversity lens I began to wonder, for instance, whether since the very start, I had been disabled by a neuronormative society. This, I came to see, had hindered my learning, my development, and my prospects right from the beginning of life. I also began to understand my trauma and mental illness as stemming from not just relative poverty and parental neglect but also a structurally ableist world. For me as for so many others, this more nuanced understanding felt liberating, allowing me to make sense of my life anew.

我首次接触这一视角是在 2012 年，即沃克开创性著作发表一年后。对我而言，阅读辛格、沃克及其他倡导者的作品，为我提供了不同于病理学范式框架和反精神病学否定论的路径。它使我能够完全认识到自身残障的现实，同时以一种帮助我理解那些构成我整个生存境遇的困境之政治本质的方式。透过神经多样性的棱镜，我开始思考，例如，是否从一开始，我就被神经规范性社会所残障化。我逐渐认识到，这从生命之初就阻碍了我的学习、发展和前景。我也开始理解，我的创伤和精神疾病不仅源于相对贫困和父母忽视，还源于一个结构性健全主义的世界。对我以及许多人而言，这种更为细致的理解令人感到解放，让我能够重新解读自己的人生。



Just as important, this perspective also helped me develop solidarity with other disabled and chronically ill people, and even a sense of disability pride. Together, all this helped me combat isolation, political inertia, and shame. It also helped me, and so many others, begin to see a way out. It finally suddenly seemed possible for neurodivergent people to collectively change the world – to make it more inclusive for the neurologically weird and disabled. This provided a kind of hope that had never before seemed possible. As such, I threw myself into the movement just as it was beginning to grow rapidly, to an extent and in ways that nobody back then could have predicted.

同样重要的是，这种视角也帮助我与其他残障和慢性病患者建立团结，甚至培养了一种残障自豪感。这一切共同帮助我克服了孤立感、政治惰性和羞耻感。它也帮助我，以及许许多多其他人，开始看到一条出路。神经殊异者似乎终于有可能集体改变世界——让它对神经上的"怪人"和残障者更具包容性。这提供了一种前所未有的希望。因此，我全身心投入到这场运动中，而它当时正开始迅猛发展，其程度和方式都是当时无人能预料的。



THE LIMITS OF LIBERALISM

自由主义的局限



As the movement has grown since 2012, most neurodiversity activism has continued in a liberal, rights-based framework, which focuses on incremental reforms within the current system. Simultaneously there have been huge collective efforts focused on overcoming the pathology paradigm. Through my own period of involvement, I have contributed much time and effort to this dual approach. This was first through blogging and campaigning, next through doctoral research, and since then advocating, teaching, and researching in academia. Yet despite finding the neurodiversity perspective so useful, and despite contributing to efforts to develop this perspective myself, I also began to find the dominant approach to neurodiversity analysis, activism, and advocacy unsatisfying.

自 2012 年以来，随着运动的发展，大多数神经多样性倡导活动仍在自由主义的、基于权利的框架内进行，这一框架侧重于在当前体系内进行渐进式改革。与此同时，也出现了巨大的集体努力，旨在克服病理学范式。在我自己参与的这段时间里，我为这种双重方法投入了大量的时间和精力。最初是通过博客和宣传活动，接着是通过博士研究，之后则是在学术界进行倡导、教学和研究。然而，尽管我发现神经多样性的视角非常有用，尽管我自己也为发展这一视角做出了努力，但我开始对神经多样性分析、行动主义和倡导的主流方法感到不满。



To be sure, I did clearly see first-hand how the liberal approach made important gains in a short time. Given continuous pressure from neurodivergent activists, research has increasingly drawn on neurodiversity theory, cultural representations of neurodivergence have become less stigmatising, and how we design our social world has likewise begun to change. In Britain, to give just a few examples, supermarkets and cinemas often have autism-friendly hours, more airports have sensory rooms for neurodivergent children, and classrooms and workplaces are making increased efforts to become more inclusive in line with new rights legislation.

诚然，我确实亲眼见证了自由主义方法如何在短时间内取得重要进展。在神经殊异活动人士持续施压的背景下，研究日益借鉴神经多样性理论，文化层面对神经殊异性的呈现逐渐去污名化，我们构建社会世界的方式亦随之开始转变。仅以英国为例：超市与影院常设孤独症友好时段，更多机场为神经殊异儿童配备感官安抚室，教室与职场也依据新权利法案持续提升包容性建设。



And yet, over time I increasingly came to see that, despite its very real successes, the liberal, rights-based approach to neurodiversity activism also had significant limitations. Consider some of the following facts. Despite our combined efforts over many years, most research, policy, and practice remained based within the pathology paradigm. Even when it came to autism – where progress has been quickest – the most widely used autism ‘therapy’ was still Applied Behaviour Analysis. This was designed to use a system of punishments and rewards to try to make autistic children more ‘normal’. Despite countless critiques from neurodiversity proponents who see this method as abusive and a form of conversion therapy, this multi-billion-pound international industry continued its growth, only making minor concessions to its critics.

然而，随着时间的推移，我越来越清楚地认识到，尽管基于权利的神经多样性自由主义行动方式确实取得了不少成就，但它也存在显著的局限性。不妨思考以下事实：尽管我们多年来共同努力，大多数研究、政策和实践仍停留在病理学范式之内。即便是在进展最快的孤独症领域，最广泛使用的孤独症"疗法"依然是应用行为分析。这种方法旨在通过惩罚与奖励体系，试图让孤独谱系儿童变得更"正常"。尽管神经多样性倡导者无数次批评这种方法具有虐待性、属于转化治疗的一种形式，但这个价值数十亿英镑的国际产业仍在持续扩张，仅对其批评者作出微不足道的让步。



At the same time, many experts in the old, medicalised paradigm began rebranding as ‘neurodiversity’ experts without significantly changing their approach. Psychiatrists, psychologists, and politicians were adopting the vocabularies of the neurodiversity movement – albeit often incorrectly – and making superficial changes to practice while leaving the logics of the pathology paradigm intact. Neurodiversity activists had referred to this co-option as ‘neurodiversity-lite’, indicating how it leaves the dominant paradigm and political order unchallenged despite the shift in presentation. Yet given their existing positions of power, it was these neurodiversity-lite proponents who were often given the biggest platforms, and who were positioned as exemplars of the neurodiversity approach.

与此同时，许多遵循旧有医学化范式的专家开始将自己重新包装为"神经多样性"专家，却并未显著改变其方法。精神病学家、心理学家和政治人物纷纷采纳神经多样性运动的词汇——尽管常常误用——并对实践进行表面调整，同时保持病理范式的逻辑内核完好无损。神经多样性活动家将这种挪用称为"轻量版神经多样性"，意指其在表现形式转变的同时，并未撼动主导范式和政治秩序。然而凭借其既有的权力地位，正是这些轻量版神经多样性的倡导者往往获得了最大的发声平台，并被塑造为神经多样性方法的典范。



More broadly, regardless of gains in rights and recognition, the apparatus of social forces that disenables and discriminates against neurodivergent people remained intact. Consider, to give just a few of countless potential examples, how around a quarter of prison inmates in the UK still had ADHD;7 how people with intellectual disabilities were still routinely segregated in education and accommodation; or how autistic people in Denmark, purportedly among the happiest countries in the world, were still around three times more likely to die by suicide than members of the general population.8

更广泛地说，无论权利和认可度如何提升，那些阻碍和歧视神经殊异人群的社会力量机制依然根深蒂固。仅举无数潜在例子中的几个：在英国，仍有约四分之一的囚犯患有注意缺陷多动障碍；智力障碍者在教育和住宿方面仍普遍遭受隔离；又或者在据称是世界上最幸福国家之一的丹麦，孤独谱系群体的自杀率仍比普通人群高出约三倍。



None of this was ‘natural’. Rather, it seemed to me, it must be determined by complex and deeper societal power relations, structures, and norms. As such, despite real gains in rights and representation, it was clear that the movement remained far from achieving its long-term goal of liberating neurodivergent people through shifting the paradigm more broadly. If anything, while liberal reformism did help some neurodivergent people, it was mainly those who were already relatively privileged in other ways – white, middle-class, and so on – while leaving multiply marginalised neurodivergents stuck in a variety of carceral systems, homeless, or in other unbearable situations. For me, all this raised the question of exactly what it would take to achieve emancipation, and why gains in rights and recognition had not led to this. It also raised the question of exactly where the pathology paradigm had come from, why it had been able to become so dominant, and how it related to the broader economic and systemic factors that I increasingly saw it as so deeply intertwined with.

这一切都并非“自然”现象。相反，在我看来，它必然是由复杂且深层的社会权力关系、结构和规范所决定的。因此，尽管在权利和代表性方面取得了实际进展，但显然，这场运动距离通过更广泛地转变范式来解放神经殊异者的长期目标仍然遥远。如果说有什么不同的话，那就是自由主义改良主义确实帮助了一些神经殊异者，但主要是那些在其他方面已经相对享有特权的人——白人、中产阶级等等——而让那些遭受多重边缘化的神经殊异者困在各种监禁体系中、无家可归，或处于其他难以忍受的境地。对我而言，所有这些都提出了一个问题：究竟需要什么才能实现解放？为什么权利和认可方面的进展未能带来这一结果？这也引出了另一个问题：病理学范式究竟从何而来？它为何能够变得如此主导？以及它与我日益认为其深深交织在一起的更广泛的经济和系统性因素有何关联？



Through my historical research into the origins of the pathology paradigm, I became more convinced that the problem lay at a deeper level, relating more specifically to underlying social, technological, and economic factors. Because so many of the failures of liberal activism also related to broader economic factors, I began to turn to different frameworks to make sense of the workings of the pathology paradigm. This led me back to an older, more radical tradition that emphasised the role of political economy in social domination. This was the Marxian tradition, as opposed to the liberal political position most neurodiversity advocacy has sat within.

通过对病理学范式起源的历史研究，我愈发确信问题存在于更深层次，更具体地与社会、技术和经济基础因素相关。由于自由主义行动主义的诸多失败同样与更广泛的经济因素有关，我开始转向不同的理论框架来理解病理学范式的运作机制。这使我回归到一个更古老、更激进的传统，该传统强调政治经济学在社会支配中的作用——即马克思主义传统，这与大多数神经多样性倡导所处的自由主义政治立场形成鲜明对比。



This tradition itself was not new to me. Especially given my own experience of poverty and homelessness when young – not to mention poorly paid, precarious work, insecure housing, and much else as an adult – I had long found Marxian analyses of class domination illuminating. And just as a Marxian approach had, since Marx’s time, been further developed in a number of new ways, I suspected it would be useful to develop a similar analysis for neurodiversity. This would be to help position neurodivergent oppression within the broader economic system that had come to dominate the world over the prior centuries, and in turn to help develop a politics of neurodiversity to help resist this.

这一传统本身对我而言并不陌生。尤其考虑到我年轻时曾经历贫困和无家可归——更不用说成年后低薪、不稳定的工作、无保障的住房等诸多困境——我早已发现马克思主义对阶级统治的分析颇具启发性。正如马克思主义方法自马克思时代以来已以多种新方式得到进一步发展，我推测对神经多样性进行类似分析将大有裨益。这将有助于将神经殊异压迫置于过去几个世纪主导世界的更广泛经济体系中定位，进而助力发展神经多样性政治以抵抗这种压迫。



Initially, I struggled with this project, not least since many fundamental commitments of Marxism seemed at odds with the standard liberal neurodiversity approach. I also disliked most Marxian analyses of mental health, since they were grounded more in the anti-psychiatry tradition that I had come to see as reactionary and outdated. Yet as I slowly pieced together such an analysis, drawing on not just Marx but a range of later scholars in the broader Marxian tradition, I increasingly came to see this approach as providing a deeper understanding of neurodivergent disablement and oppression than I had hitherto held. In the end I began to think of this approach as Neurodivergent Marxism. And I came to see this as distinct from, and a challenge to, both liberal neurodiversity and orthodox Marxism.

起初，我对这个项目感到棘手，尤其是因为马克思主义的许多基本主张似乎与主流的自由主义神经多样性路径格格不入。我也不喜欢大多数马克思主义对心理健康的分析，因为它们更多地植根于反精神病学传统，而我认为这种传统是反动且过时的。然而，当我慢慢拼凑出这样一种分析，不仅借鉴了马克思，还借鉴了更广泛的马克思主义传统中的一系列后世学者时，我逐渐认识到，这种方法为我提供了比以往更深入的理解神经殊异者的障碍与压迫。最终，我开始将这种方法视为神经殊异马克思主义。并且我认为，这既不同于自由主义神经多样性和正统马克思主义，也是对两者的挑战。



NEURODIVERSITY AND MARXISM

神经多样性与马克思主义



To clarify Neurodivergent Marxism, as I understand it, it will help to say a bit about Marx’s critique of capitalist domination. At base, this was developed through Marx’s theory of what has been called ‘historical’ or ‘dialectical’ materialism.9 This frames our consciousness, thought, and perception, as significantly constrained by the broader material and economic conditions of the age. In turn, it seeks to navigate the prospects for change in the contradictions that arise from the clash between agency and historical forces. In Marx’s own words, humans ‘make their own history, but they do not make it just as they please; they do not make it under circumstances chosen by themselves, but under circumstances directly encountered, given and transmitted from the past’.10 Vitally, it was this way of viewing history that allowed Marx to develop his historical analysis of capitalism.

要阐明我所理解的神经殊异马克思主义，有必要先简要谈谈马克思对资本主义统治的批判。从根本上说，这一批判是通过马克思所谓的"历史"或"辩证"唯物主义理论发展起来的。 9 该理论认为，我们的意识、思想和感知在很大程度上受到时代更广泛的物质经济条件的制约。相应地，它试图在主体能动性与历史力量冲突所产生的矛盾中探寻变革的可能性。用马克思自己的话说，人类"创造自己的历史，但不是随心所欲地创造；不是在他们自己选定的条件下创造，而是在直接碰到的、既定的、从过去承继下来的条件下创造"。 10 至关重要的是，正是这种历史观使马克思得以发展出对资本主义的历史分析。



Living through the nineteenth century as England was swiftly industrialising, Marx identified capitalism as a system where only a small part of the population owns the means of production, while most of the population is mined for productivity, with capitalists extracting surplus value from their wage-labour. Whereas domination and inequality were previously based on the more direct and violent political power of kings, lords, and so on, in this new system technically free workers were primarily compelled by economic relations. In this, capitalism stratified new classes of people – most notably the bourgeoisie, the workers, and the unemployed surplus – distinguished by objective material relations and positionings within the broader global system.

生活在十九世纪英国迅速工业化的时代，马克思将资本主义界定为一种制度：仅少数人占有生产资料，而大多数人被当作生产力资源开采，资本家从他们的雇佣劳动中榨取剩余价值。以往的统治与不平等主要基于国王、领主等更为直接且暴力的政治权力，而在这一新体系中，形式上自由的工人主要受经济关系驱使。由此，资本主义将人群划分为新的阶级——最显著的是资产阶级、工人以及失业的剩余劳动力——这些阶级由客观的物质关系及其在全球体系中的位置所区分。



Through his historical analysis of capitalism, he came to see this system as bringing both unique benefits and problems when compared to previous economic systems. On the one hand, he saw that its benefits included helping end the more brutal forms of oppression of the feudal era, while simultaneously bringing increased technological progress and greater levels of productivity that had the potential to greatly benefit the population at large. Yet Marx also saw capitalism as containing inherent contradictions that necessitated deep-seated inequality and constant economic crisis.

通过对资本主义的历史分析，他认识到这一制度相较于以往的经济体系既带来了独特的益处，也产生了特有的问题。一方面，他认为资本主义的益处包括帮助终结封建时代更为残酷的压迫形式，同时带来了技术进步和生产力的提升，这些都有可能极大地惠及广大民众。然而，马克思也看到资本主义蕴含着固有的矛盾，这些矛盾必然导致深刻的不平等和持续的经济危机。



Perhaps the most important contradiction, for our purposes, was grounded in his concept of alienation. For Marx, humans are essentially social animals who use our creative potentials for artistic and innovative projects, and our ‘productive forces’ to make the world more habitable for us. Put more concretely, while there is no fixed ‘human nature’, we are at least relatively unique in making tools, building houses, growing crops, painting, writing music, and so forth, in ways that can help us develop, thrive, and prosper.11 This was important for Marx because, if we must use our creative and productive forces not for our individual or collective good, but rather for others to profit, our freedom and developmental potentials are thus simultaneously expanded yet stifled. While some alienation had always existed, since capitalism typically brought longer working hours, heightened divisions of labour, and more gruelling, monotonous work than the feudal age, Marx saw this newer system as leading to increased alienation. This was from our own creative potentials, from the products of our labour, and ultimately from each other, making every aspect of our existence increasingly alienated as the domain and power of capitalism grew.

或许对我们而言，最重要的矛盾根植于他的异化概念。在马克思看来，人类本质上是社会性动物，我们运用自身的创造潜力从事艺术与创新活动，并借助"生产力"使世界更适合人类居住。更具体地说，虽然不存在固定的"人性"，但人类至少在制造工具、建造房屋、种植作物、绘画、谱写音乐等方面具有相对独特性，这些活动能帮助我们发展、繁荣与兴盛。 11 这对马克思至关重要，因为如果我们必须将创造力和生产力不是用于个人或集体利益，而是为他人牟利，那么我们的自由和发展潜力就会在扩张的同时受到压制。虽然异化现象始终存在，但由于资本主义通常带来比封建时代更长的工作时间、更细化的劳动分工以及更繁重单调的工作，马克思认为这种新制度导致了异化的加剧。 这种异化既源于我们自身的创造潜力，也源于劳动产品，并最终导致人与人之间的疏离。随着资本主义的领域和权力不断扩张，我们生存的方方面面都日益异化。



Given this, for Marx, while capitalism did bring greater productive capacity, including for medical technology and support, at a deeper level it was simultaneously harmful to both bodily and mental health. For under capitalism, most of the population are workers who have little control over our prospects. We are effectively forced to constantly use our productive forces, and debilitate our bodies and minds, in the service of capitalists, just to earn enough to survive. In this context, good health becomes ever harder to maintain, even with the many benefits that capitalism brings.

因此，在马克思看来，尽管资本主义确实带来了更强大的生产能力，包括医疗技术和支持，但在更深层次上，它同时对身心健康造成了损害。因为在资本主义制度下，大多数人口都是工人，我们对自己的前景几乎没有控制权。我们实际上被迫不断利用自己的生产力，并在资本家的服务中损耗我们的身心，仅仅是为了赚取足够的生存所需。在这种背景下，即使资本主义带来了诸多好处，保持健康也变得越来越困难。



Looked at this way, for Marx, a key contradiction of capitalism is that, under the ‘mute compulsion’ of capitalist economic power, wealth is produced collectively by the many, who are forced to sell wage-labour to be exploited and alienated. Yet this wealth is then appropriated privately by the few at the expense of the many. It is this contradiction that Marx thought might bring the conflicts that would one day end capitalism, allowing a shift towards a freer, more equal society. Following this, he hoped, such deeply ingrained divisions in social class would be consigned to history.

从这个角度看，对马克思而言，资本主义的一个核心矛盾在于：在资本经济权力的"无声强制"下，财富由广大劳动者集体创造，他们被迫出卖劳动力遭受剥削与异化，而这些财富最终却被少数人私人占有，代价由多数人承担。马克思认为正是这一矛盾可能引发冲突，终将终结资本主义，推动社会向更自由平等的形态转变。他期待随着这种转变，根深蒂固的社会阶级分化终将成为历史陈迹。



While Marx was born in 1818, over two centuries ago, the core of this analysis is no less relevant today. For despite increases in living standards in some times and places, worsening crises continue to send shocks through the global economy, and such inequalities remain deeply entrenched. It is not just that, as my own experience attests, many of us still live in relative poverty even in the wealthiest nations. It is also that globally, as one recent report found, since 1995, the richest 1 per cent have accumulated nearly 20 times more wealth than the poorest 50 per cent.12

尽管马克思出生于两个多世纪前的 1818 年，其分析内核在今日依然振聋发聩。纵然某些时空下生活水平有所提升，但日益恶化的危机仍持续冲击全球经济，不平等现象依然盘根错节。不仅如我亲身经历所印证——即便在最富裕的国家，许多人仍生活在相对贫困中；全球层面更触目惊心：近期报告显示，自 1995 年以来，最富有的 1%人群积累的财富竟是最贫困 50%人口的近 20 倍。 12



It is important to note here that Marx’s analysis has been updated and expanded since his death in 1883, and early orthodox readings of his works have been challenged. Most notably, the rather crass and distorted understanding of Marxism wrongly used to justify Stalinist totalitarianism was hotly contested by Marxist humanists13 and Frankfurt School critical theorists,14 who emphasised that Marx was arguing for a freer society rather than one that was state-controlled. In turn, scholars in the Black Radical tradition have shown how primary racism and colonialism were to the emergence of capitalism as a global system,15 feminist scholarship has examined the ways in which capital continuously extracts unpaid emotional and reproductive work from women,16 disability studies scholars have examined how capitalism disabled us and worsens disability discrimination,17 and environmental scholars and activists have since emphasised how capital will literally destroy our planet and end all human life if it is not stopped.18 All of these accounts update and supplement Marx’s analysis, which had focused primarily on the white, male worker in Europe.

需要指出的是，自马克思于 1883 年逝世后，其分析框架已得到更新与拓展，早期对其著作的正统解读也受到了挑战。尤为显著的是，那种曾被错误用于为斯大林式极权主义辩护的、相当粗陋且扭曲的马克思主义理解，遭到了马克思主义人道主义者 13 和法兰克福学派批判理论家 14 的激烈驳斥，他们强调马克思所主张的是一个更为自由的社会，而非国家控制的社会。与此同时，黑人激进传统中的学者揭示了种族主义与殖民主义对资本主义作为全球体系兴起的关键作用 15 ；女性主义学术研究了资本如何持续从女性身上榨取无偿的情感与再生产劳动 16 ；残障研究学者探讨了资本主义如何使我们陷入残障境地并加剧残障歧视 17 ；环境学者与活动家则强调，若不加以制止，资本将切实摧毁我们的星球并终结全人类生命 18 。所有这些论述都更新并补充了马克思的分析，其原本主要聚焦于欧洲的白人男性工人。



Neurodivergent Marxism continues in this updated Marxian tradition. While my understanding is heavily grounded in and synthesises aspects of this broader Marxian tradition, I go beyond them by providing the first history and politics of neurodiversity from a Marxian perspective. In this, I show how the rise and workings of the pathology paradigm are intimately intertwined with not just the vested interests of various groups or people, but, vitally, the underlying logics of capitalism itself. This thus begins with covering how our current scientific and cultural understandings of neurological disability and normality grew in relation to specific economic conditions, power relations, and ideological landscapes. This then develops into a materialist history of the pathology paradigm, tracing how its ideas arose from and in turn functioned to naturalise the shifting material relations of capitalism as it continually develops.

神经殊异马克思主义延续了这一更新的马克思主义传统。虽然我的理解深深植根于并综合了这一更广泛的马克思主义传统的各个方面，但我超越了它们，首次从马克思主义视角提供了神经多样性的历史与政治分析。在此过程中，我揭示了病理学范式的兴起与运作，不仅与各种群体或个人的既得利益紧密交织，更重要的是，与资本主义本身的底层逻辑密不可分。因此，本书首先探讨了我们当前对神经性残障与常态的科学和文化理解，是如何在特定的经济条件、权力关系和意识形态背景下发展起来的。随后，这发展成对病理学范式的唯物主义历史考察，追溯其观念如何从资本主义不断发展的、不断变化的物质关系中产生，并反过来将这些关系自然化。



In doing this, I also clarify how and why capitalism is so intensely neuronormative, becoming more so with each passing decade. While all societies and economic systems have some standard of what is considered acceptable or valuable mental functioning – and while some mental illness and disability will always exist – I suggest capitalism is disposed to much tighter standards than other modes of production. In this view, neurodivergent oppression and disablement is established as a feature of the system rather than a bug. And in turn, since the pathology paradigm is a product of the broader economic system, overcoming it will require more than a revolution in how we think about neurodiversity. It will also require changing much deeper structures in our society, in ways that are usually left unclarified in existing neurodiversity theory.

在此过程中，我也阐明了资本主义为何如此强烈地奉行神经规范性，且这种趋势随着时间推移日益加剧。尽管所有社会和经济体系都对可接受或有价值的心理功能设定了一定标准——尽管精神疾病和残障总会存在——但我认为资本主义倾向于设定比其他生产方式更为严苛的标准。从这个角度看，神经殊异群体的压迫与残障化被确立为这一体系的固有特征，而非缺陷。相应地，既然病理学范式是更广泛经济体系的产物，要克服它就不仅需要我们对神经多样性的认知进行革命性转变，还必须改变社会中更为深层的结构——这些深层变革在现有神经多样性理论中往往未能得到明确阐述。



While a materialist analysis helps account for restricting neuronormativity, an updated analysis of alienation simultaneously allows us to make sense of rising rates of mental health problems in recent decades. In particular, I am concerned with seemingly rising depression, anxiety, and trauma even in the otherwise neurotypical population. While the kind of alienation Marx detailed in industrial England still remains, it is my contention that as capitalism has intensified, the kind of alienation we experience has shifted. More specifically, many workers today perform cognitive, attentive, and emotional labour more than the manual labour of Marx’s time, while our requirements as consumers and citizens, to have the correct desires, have also been restricted. All this, as we will see, contributes both to tightening neuronormativity, and thus increased disablement, but also to much more widespread mental health problems even for those who fall within the neurological norms of the age.

虽然唯物主义分析有助于解释神经规范性的限制，但关于异化的更新分析同时让我们能够理解近几十年来心理健康问题日益增多的现象。我尤其关注的是，即使在神经典型人群中，抑郁、焦虑和创伤也似乎呈上升趋势。尽管马克思在工业英国时期所描述的异化现象依然存在，但我认为随着资本主义的加剧，我们所经历的异化形式已经发生了变化。更具体地说，今天的许多劳动者更多地从事认知、注意力和情感劳动，而非马克思时代的手工劳动；同时，作为消费者和公民，我们拥有正确欲望的要求也受到了限制。正如我们将看到的，所有这些不仅加剧了神经规范性的收紧，从而增加了残障化，而且即使对那些符合时代神经规范的人来说，也导致了更广泛的心理健康问题。



The implication of this is that, increasingly, new forms of domination often have less to do with social class, which now, to an extent, is more fluid than in the nineteenth century, and much more to do with where each of us falls on the new cognitive hierarchies of capitalism. Of course, this is not to minimise the ongoing significance of class domination, let alone the importance of other intersections. Rather, it is to show how even when traditional forms of domination do lessen to even some small extent, they are merely replaced with increased neuronormative domination instead. Hence a further contradiction of capitalism, for me, is that even when class mobility increases to some extent, a different kind of domination, this time regarding neurodiversity, arises in equal measure. It is in this contradiction, that I take to become more salient as capitalism further intensifies, that I see a key site of struggle, and perhaps emancipation, in the twenty-first century.

这意味着，新的统治形式越来越与我们在资本主义新的认知等级体系中所处的位置有关，而与社会阶层的关联则相对减弱——毕竟，如今的社会阶层在某种程度上比十九世纪时更具流动性。当然，这并不是要淡化阶级统治的持续重要性，更不用说其他交叉性因素的重要性了。相反，这是为了说明，即使传统统治形式在某种程度上有所减弱，它们也仅仅是被日益增强的神经规范性统治所取代。因此，在我看来，资本主义的另一个矛盾在于：即使阶级流动性在某种程度上有所提高，一种不同形式的统治——这次是关于神经多样性的统治——也会以同等程度出现。正是在这个矛盾中，我看到了二十一世纪斗争乃至解放的一个关键场域，而随着资本主义的进一步加剧，我认为这一矛盾将变得更加突出。



THE EMPIRE OF NORMALITY

正常性帝国



This is the first book that provides a history of capitalism that places neurodiversity, rather than class, at its centre. While I do take an intersectional approach that considers class, race, gender, sexuality, and bodily disability, my focus on neurodiversity allows me to trace the emergence of what I call the Empire of Normality. This refers to an apparatus of material relations, social practices, scientific research programmes, bureaucratic mechanisms, economic compulsions, and administrative procedures that emerge from fundamental dispositions of the capitalist system, at least once it reaches a certain stage of development. Together, these bring a much more restricted bodily, cognitive, and emotional normal range than those seen in any previous society. Simultaneously, the framing of this as an empire helps me to emphasise the connection between neurodivergent oppression, colonialism, and imperialism. This in turn should allow us to examine the prospects for developing a politics of neurodiversity that equally helps work towards collective liberation.

这是第一本将神经多样性而非阶级置于核心的资本主义历史著作。尽管我采用了交叉性视角，考量了阶级、种族、性别、性取向及身体残障，但对神经多样性的聚焦使我得以追溯所谓"常态帝国"的兴起。这一概念指涉由资本主义体系根本属性——至少在其发展到特定阶段后——所催生的物质关系网络、社会实践、科研项目、官僚机制、经济强制与行政程序的总和。这些力量共同塑造出比以往任何社会都更为狭隘的身体、认知与情感常态范畴。同时，将这一体系喻为"帝国"，有助于我强调神经殊异群体所受压迫与殖民主义、帝国主义之间的内在关联。由此出发，我们将能更深入地探索发展神经多样性政治的可能性，使其在追求集体解放的道路上发挥同等重要的作用。



For my alternative telling, rather than attempting to provide a comprehensive history, I focus on carefully chosen key thinkers positioned in their broader material context. My aim with this is not to resurrect them as ‘great’ (or not so great) men, but rather to show how the progression of pathology paradigm thinking, especially at key moments, has been significantly determined by material factors in ways that are both guided by and reify capitalist power relations and hierarchies. This allows us to see how the material and the ideological continually interact and mutually reinforce each other even, perhaps especially, through the work of those usually positioned as having helped science progress.

在我的另类叙述中，我并未试图提供一部全面的历史，而是聚焦于精心挑选的关键思想家，并将他们置于更广阔的物质背景之中。我这样做的目的，并非是要将他们复活为“伟大”（或并非那么伟大）的人物，而是要展示病理学范式思维的演进——尤其是在关键时刻——如何显著地受到物质因素的决定，而这些因素既受资本主义权力关系和等级制度的引导，又反过来巩固了这些关系和制度。这使我们能够看到，物质与意识形态如何持续互动、相互强化，甚至——或许尤其——是通过那些通常被认为推动了科学进步的人的工作来实现的。



With this in mind, I begin by covering the work of the ancient Greek Hippocratic doctors as well as other ancient medical approaches across the globe. These tended to view health as a form of harmony or balance, either within the individual or between individual and environment. This only ended, as we will see, with the rise of capitalism, specifically given its emphasis on competition and worker productivity. This new economic system led humans to be reinterpreted as machines, which I explore through the thought of the philosopher Descartes. And in turn it led to the concept of ‘normality’ arising and being utilised to reimagine the nature of health and ability. This, I show, then began being used to rank and control populations in ways that, while bringing scientific progress, nonetheless became increasingly oppressive. In time, the idea of normality entered so deeply into our collective consciousness, it began to seem timeless and objective, thus obscuring its material genesis and contingency.

有鉴于此，我首先探讨古希腊希波克拉底派医者及其他古代全球医疗体系的观点。这些传统往往将健康视为一种和谐或平衡状态——无论是人体内部的平衡，还是个体与环境之间的协调。正如我们将要看到的，这种观念直到资本主义兴起后才发生转变，特别是资本主义对竞争与工人生产力的强调。这种新的经济体系促使人类被重新解读为机器，这一点我将通过哲学家笛卡尔的思想来剖析。随之而来的是“正常”这一概念的诞生，并被用来重塑对健康与能力的理解。我将揭示这个概念如何逐渐被用于对人群进行分级与控制——虽然带来了科学进步，却也日益成为压迫性的工具。久而久之，“正常”的观念深深植入了我们的集体意识，开始显得永恒而客观，从而掩盖了其物质根源与历史偶然性。



Within this context, I trace the pathology paradigm proper in large part to the work of a strange and pioneering scientist called Francis Galton – the half-cousin of Charles Darwin, known today for being the founder of eugenics as well as of many scientific innovations. For our purposes, the most significant thing Galton introduced in the late nineteenth century was a novel way of comparing cognition and measuring biology, which grounded a Darwinian ranking system that naturalised the cognitive hierarchies of industrial capitalism as well as its hierarchies of class, race, and gender. The point of this for Galton was to formalise and amplify the normalising and control of populations, now legitimised as a scientific pursuit. And part of the effect of this was an increased conceptual blending and conflation of normality, productivity, and health.

在此背景下，我将病理学范式的根源很大程度上追溯至一位奇特而开创性的科学家弗朗西斯·高尔顿的工作——他是查尔斯·达尔文的表亲，如今以优生学创始人和多项科学创新者闻名。就我们的目的而言，高尔顿在十九世纪末期引入的最重要贡献，是一种比较认知和测量生物学的新方法。这种方法奠定了一种达尔文式的等级体系，将工业资本主义的认知层级及其阶级、种族和性别层级自然化。对高尔顿而言，此举旨在将人口的规范化与控制形式化并强化，如今这已被合法化为一种科学追求。其部分效果是加剧了正常性、生产力和健康在概念上的混合与混淆。



A key part of my argument is that this paradigm was then taken up and expanded, with great fervour, by influential psychiatrists such as Emil Kraepelin as well as in psychological, psychometric, and biomedical research. In tracing Galton’s influence, I thus cover how a broader eugenic ideology became culturally hegemonic, while his research paradigm simultaneously allowed the cognitive hierarchies of advanced capitalism to become reified through guiding the assumptions, methods, and results of scientific knowledge production. I thus position Galton – rather than Kraepelin, as is typical in histories of psychiatry – as the founder of the currently dominant scientific paradigm used in psychiatry and related fields.

我论证的一个关键部分是，这一范式随后被埃米尔·克雷佩林等有影响力的精神病学家以及心理学、心理测量学和生物医学研究领域以极大的热情采纳并扩展。在追溯高尔顿的影响时，我阐述了更广泛的优生学意识形态如何在文化上取得霸权地位，同时他的研究范式通过引导科学知识生产的假设、方法和结果，使得先进资本主义的认知等级得以固化。因此，我将高尔顿——而非精神病学史中通常强调的克雷佩林——定位为当前精神病学及相关领域主导科学范式的奠基人。



This shines a light on how the ideological biases determined by the material relations of capitalism and imperial Britain – channelled through Galton – have since guided scientific knowledge production, public understanding, policy, and clinical practice relating to neurodiversity to this very day. This has been so even while the old imperial order has crumbled in other important ways. It is this new apparatus of scientific, administrative, cultural, and legal impositions that constitute the Empire of Normality. Long after the British Empire has crumbled, I show, many of its hierarchies and power relations have been maintained, reproduced, and expanded through this apparatus, which has not only survived but grown ever-more hegemonic as capitalism has continued to intensify. Thus, for me, the key problem is not the pathology paradigm alone, but how capitalist logics and the pathology paradigm mutually reinforce each other, leaving no possibility of neurodivergent liberation without deep systemic change.

这揭示了由资本主义和英帝国的物质关系所决定的意识形态偏见——通过高尔顿传递——如何至今仍在引导与神经多样性相关的科学知识生产、公众理解、政策制定及临床实践。即便旧的帝国秩序在其他重要方面已然崩塌，这一影响依然存在。正是这套科学、行政、文化和法律强制的新机制，构成了"常态帝国"。我将表明，在大英帝国崩溃许久之后，其诸多等级制度和权力关系通过这套机制得以维持、复制和扩张；这套机制不仅存续下来，而且随着资本主义的持续强化变得愈发具有霸权性。因此，对我而言，核心问题并不仅仅是病理学范式本身，而在于资本主义逻辑与病理学范式如何相互强化，使得没有深刻的系统性变革，神经殊异者的解放便无从谈起。



My aim is not to develop a set of policy proposals or a political strategy. Rather, it is to help clarify an underlying problem that I see as a deeper, older, and more insidious than the pathology paradigm. Clarifying this problem is just the first step towards what will need to be a much more prolonged, collective effort to combat the Empire of Normality, that is, the apparatus that sits behind and necessitates the pathology paradigm. Only by understanding how the paradigm relates to this broader apparatus and in turn to fundamental dispositions of the capitalist mode of production will we be able to clearly comprehend what neurodivergent liberation would require.

我的目的并非提出一套政策建议或政治策略，而是旨在阐明一个我认为比病理学范式更深层、更久远、也更隐蔽的根本问题。厘清这一问题仅仅是漫长集体斗争的第一步，我们需要共同努力来对抗常态帝国——即隐藏在病理学范式背后并使其成为必要的那套机制。唯有理解这一范式如何与更广泛的机制相联系，进而理解其与资本主义生产方式根本取向的关联，我们才能清晰地认识到神经殊异解放的真正要求。



It is worth emphasising that I also write with some urgency for the current political moment. In the past few years, as recognition and influence of neurodivergent activism has rapidly increased, it is not just that the vocabularies, concepts, and suggestions of neurodiversity proponents have begun being co-opted by clinicians and politicians to maintain the status quo. It is also that countless new diversity and inclusion consultants increasingly charge large sums of money to speak to businesses who then come to see neurodivergent people as new resources to be mined for productivity. In this, we see the rise of what I call neuro-Thatcherism, in which capitalism even subverts attempts to resist its harmful effects, turning these attempts back into new opportunities for the maximisation of profit and productivity. In this, the liberatory potential of this new movement is being stifled just as the movement seems to be gaining power.

值得强调的是，我写作时也带着对当前政治时刻的紧迫感。过去几年，随着神经殊异行动主义的认知度和影响力迅速增长，不仅神经多样性倡导者的词汇、概念和建议开始被临床医生和政治家挪用，以维持现状；还有无数新的多元化和包容性顾问越来越多地向企业收取高额费用进行宣讲，而这些企业逐渐将神经殊异人群视为可挖掘生产力的新资源。在此过程中，我们看到了我称之为“神经撒切尔主义”的兴起——资本主义甚至颠覆了抵抗其有害影响的尝试，将这些尝试转化为最大化利润和生产力的新机遇。如此一来，这场新运动的解放潜力正被扼杀，尽管运动本身似乎正在获得力量。



At the same time, the anti-psychiatry movement, which waned towards the end of the twentieth century, is now growing in popularity again. In contrast to my analysis, this tradition sees psychiatry itself, and belief in the concept of ‘mental illness’, as the core problem. Although not all anti-psychiatrists took this position, this approach, which stems from the work of the right-wing libertarian Thomas Szasz, has perhaps been the most influential in offering an alternative story to mainstream psychiatry.

与此同时，在二十世纪末逐渐式微的反精神病学运动如今再度兴起。与我的分析不同，这一传统将精神病学本身以及对"精神疾病"概念的信仰视为核心问题。尽管并非所有反精神病学家都持此立场，但源自右翼自由主义者托马斯·萨兹著作的这一路径，或许在为主流精神病学提供替代性叙事方面产生了最具影响力的作用。



Importantly, while my analysis may have some superficial overlap with Szasz, I wholly resist the idea that this means the various things we currently call autism, ADHD, or so forth are not ‘real’ disabilities. I also forcefully resist the Szaszian claim that mental illness is a ‘myth’. While I do critique the foundations and effects of the dominant psychiatric paradigm, my critique is of how the concept of health has been conflated with normality and productivity, and of how disablement and illness have actually increased, under the material relations of capitalism. It is not a rejection of recognising mental illness or disability as such. Indeed, as we will see, I argue that anti-psychiatry is part of the problem, not the solution. For despite looking different on the surface, in fact, it reinforces rather than challenges the logics of the pathology paradigm and the broader apparatus of normality.

重要的是，虽然我的分析可能与萨斯在某些表面上有重叠，但我完全反对这样一种观点，即这意味着我们目前称之为孤独谱系、注意力缺陷多动障碍等等的各种情况不是“真实的”残障。我也强烈反对萨斯关于精神疾病是一种“神话”的主张。虽然我确实批判主流精神病学范式的基础和影响，但我的批判是针对健康概念如何被混同于正常性和生产力，以及残障和疾病如何在资本主义的物质关系下实际上有所增加。这并非拒绝承认精神疾病或残障本身。事实上，正如我们将看到的，我认为反精神病学是问题的一部分，而非解决方案。因为尽管表面上看起来不同，实际上它强化而非挑战了病理学范式的逻辑以及更广泛的正常性机制。



By contrast, in tracing the rise of the neurodiversity movement, I synthesise the work of seminal neurodiversity theorists Judy Singer and Nick Walker with my Marxian approach. This is important as it allows me to clarify as-yet unidentified contradictions of capitalism that show the futility of neuro-Thatcherism. The most important of these regards a tendency towards a neuronormative double-bind that increasingly traps each of us, regardless of whether we are closer or further from the neurotypical ideal. Those aspects of our species-wide neuro-cognitive diversity that it cannot currently use are disenabled, devalued, and discriminated against; while those it can use are ruthlessly exploited and thus made unwell. Either way, I argue, all human minds and selves are estranged from one another through the psychic hierarchies this produces. This leads to a situation where we all become sick or disabled, or at the very least where wellbeing is elusive for most of us. On this view, then, it is not the neurotypical who oppresses the neurodivergent, but capitalist domination that, in a certain sense, creates and harms both neurotypicals and neurodivergents, albeit in slightly different ways depending on any given individual’s proximity to the norm.

相比之下，在追溯神经多样性运动的兴起时，我将先驱神经多样性理论家朱迪·辛格和尼克·沃克的研究与我的马克思主义方法相结合。这一点至关重要，因为它使我能够阐明资本主义中尚未被识别的矛盾，这些矛盾揭示了神经撒切尔主义的徒劳。其中最重要的矛盾涉及一种神经规范性双重束缚的趋势，这种趋势日益将我们每个人困住，无论我们距离神经典型理想更近还是更远。那些目前无法被利用的、我们人类物种范围内的神经认知多样性特征被剥夺能力、贬低价值并遭受歧视；而那些可以被利用的特征则被无情剥削，从而导致身心失调。我认为，无论哪种情况，所有人的心智与自我都因这种体系所产生的心理等级制而彼此疏离。这导致了一种局面：我们所有人都变得病态或残障，或者至少对大多数人而言，福祉变得遥不可及。 因此，从这个视角看，压迫神经殊异者的并非神经典型者，而是资本主义的支配——在某种意义上，这种支配既塑造又伤害了神经典型者与神经殊异者双方。尽管具体方式会因个体与规范的接近程度而略有不同。



Indeed, as already alluded to, part of what I seek to show is that while capitalist societies have allowed some degree of mobility regarding social class, this has only meant that domination shifts more towards neurodivergence rather than diminishing overall. This, I argue, undermines the last promise of capitalism, which purports to help us approach a meritocracy where free individuals are valued not by their inherited status but by their virtues and how hard they work.

诚然，正如前文所暗示的，我试图揭示的部分内容是：尽管资本主义社会在社会阶层方面允许了一定程度的流动性，但这仅仅意味着支配更多地转向了神经殊异性，而非整体上的削弱。我认为，这破坏了资本主义的最后一项承诺，即声称帮助我们接近一个精英统治的社会，在那里自由个体不是因其继承的地位，而是因其美德和努力程度而受到重视。



It is not just that this is untrue at the national level, where class still significantly constrains individual economic outcomes, or at the global level, since the wealth of the Global North precisely relies on the relative poverty of the global south. It is also, I argue, that even where capitalism does bring limited advances that allow increased mobility in social class, we simply switch more traditional forms of domination for neuronormative domination relative to the increasingly intense cognitive needs of capital. Thus, there seems to be only a very limited possibility of liberation under capitalism, and only an offer of different forms of domination and alienation depending on where we are positioned. It is this, I argue, that grounds the need for a more radical politics of neurodiversity, directed against the Empire of Normality itself.

这不仅在国家层面不属实——在那里，阶级仍然显著制约着个人的经济结果——在全球层面也不属实，因为全球北方的财富恰恰依赖于全球南方的相对贫困。我认为，即使资本主义确实带来了有限的进步，允许社会阶层流动性增加，我们也只是用更传统的支配形式，换成了相对于资本日益增长的认知需求而言的神经规范性支配。因此，在资本主义制度下，似乎只有非常有限的解放可能性，并且根据我们所处的位置，只提供了不同形式的支配和异化。我认为，正是这一点，奠定了需要一种更激进的神经多样性政治的基础，以直接对抗常态帝国本身。



---

Empire of Normality



Empire of Normality

正常帝国



Neurodiversity and Capitalism

神经多样性与资本主义



Robert Chapman

罗伯特·查普曼
